# Editora

A keyboard-driven, cross-platform programmer's text editor. JDK 25 + JavaFX 26 +
Maven, modular (JPMS, module `com.editora`).

## Commands

- Run the app: `mvn javafx:run`
- Run tests: `mvn test`
- Build app image / native installer: **`mvn clean -Pdist package`** (`clean` is REQUIRED, not optional).
  - Produces `target/dist/Editora.app` (macOS); OS profiles auto-select DMG/MSI/DEB.
  - Quick unpackaged bundle: `mvn clean -Pdist -DskipTests -Djpackage.type=APP_IMAGE package` ⇒ `target/dist/Editora.app`.
  - **Always package from a clean `target/`.** The dist JAR (jlink's input for the `com.editora` module)
    is built from `target/classes`; an **incremental** compile does **not** regenerate a synthetic
    `$SwitchMap` inner class (e.g. `KeyDispatcher$1`, `QuickOpen$1`, `MarkdownViewToggle$1`, emitted for a
    `switch` over an *external* enum) once it's missing — javac sees the `.java` as up-to-date and skips
    it. Anything that leaves `target/classes` inconsistent — a background **jdtls/Eclipse** compiler
    writing there, an interrupted build, a partial clean — then makes `-Pdist package` ship a jimage
    **missing that class**, and the packaged app throws `ClassNotFoundException` on the **first keypress**
    (dead keyboard). A `clean` regenerates every class and avoids it. `release.yml`'s `-Pdist` step runs
    `clean` for this reason. (`mvn javafx:run` and the fat jar are immune — they don't jlink a stale JAR.)
  - **Both** also run the AOT-cache training step (a GUI window flashes for ~2.5 s, then the build
    injects `editora.aot`) — see the AOT-cache note under *Conventions → performance*. It's
    failure-tolerant, so on a display-less machine it just skips the cache.
- Build a runnable fat jar: `mvn -Pfatjar package` ⇒ `target/Editora-<version>.jar`, run with
  `java -jar`. It bundles JavaFX (classes + natives) for **the build host's platform only** and runs
  from the classpath via the non-`Application` `com.editora.Launcher` main class. A single
  all-platforms jar is impossible (JavaFX's macOS/Linux x64 and arm64 natives share filenames and
  collide), so the release CI builds one fat jar per runner.
- Cut a release: set `<version>` in `pom.xml` to the release version, i.e. **drop the `-SNAPSHOT`** (the pom is the **single** source — `AppInfo.VERSION` derives from it via Maven-filtered `build-info.properties`, so no other file needs the number; update `CHANGELOG.md` too), push a `vX.Y.Z` tag (`-rcN` ⇒ pre-release). **Between releases `master` sits on `X.Y.Z-SNAPSHOT`** — `release.yml`'s final `bump` job reopens it at the next patch `-SNAPSHOT` automatically after a non-rc release (idempotent: it bumps only when the pom still reads the version just released), so the step above is the only manual version edit. The suffix makes a build **self-identifying**: `AppInfo.isSnapshot()` shows a **`snapshot` toolbar badge** beside the `--dev` one, and the suffix appears in `--version`/About/Welcome — so a test build off `master` is never mistaken for a release. Anywhere a version must be a plain dotted number uses **`AppInfo.releaseVersion()`** (the versioned docs URL in `CommandPalette`, which would otherwise 404) or the pom's **`jpackage.publicVersion`** — each OS profile's antrun strips `-SNAPSHOT` into it and derives `jpackage.appVersion` from that (mac additionally bumps a leading `0.`→`1.`), because **jpackage rejects a non-numeric app-version**; `aot_build.java` writes `publicVersion` into the macOS `Info.plist`. See [docs/release.md](docs/release.md).

Run Maven from the project root (`/Users/adriandeleon/src/adl/Editora-V2`).

## Worktrees — one per task (important)

This repo is worked on by multiple Claude Code sessions. **Each task gets its own
`git worktree`** so sessions don't share a single working tree (which previously caused commits to
land on the wrong branch when a parallel session ran `git checkout` in the shared checkout).

- **Start a task:** `scripts/worktree.sh new <branch>` (e.g. `feat/foo`, base defaults to
  `origin/master`). It creates an isolated checkout at `../Editora-V2-worktrees/<slug>` on a new
  branch; `cd` into it and do the work there. `list` shows all worktrees; `rm <branch>` removes the
  worktree + branch after merging; `prune` cleans stale metadata.
- **Never `git checkout` a different branch in the main checkout** (`/Users/adriandeleon/src/adl/Editora-V2`)
  while other sessions may be active — switch by creating/entering a worktree instead. Keep the main
  checkout on `master`.
- **Subagents:** spawn them with the Agent tool's `isolation: "worktree"` so background work can't
  disturb the main checkout.
- **A session/terminal does not "move into" a worktree by creating one.** A session is anchored to
  the directory it launched in; a worktree is just a separate folder. To actually *work inside* one
  interactively, open a **new terminal / Claude Code session** in that directory
  (`cd ../Editora-V2-worktrees/<slug>`). A long-running session pinned to the main checkout (e.g. the
  one whose terminal sits on `master`) instead operates on a worktree **by path** — absolute paths for
  edits, `cd <worktree> && ./mvnw …` for builds — and stays on `master`; commit/merge from there but
  **never `git checkout` another branch in the main checkout**. (Claude's Bash tool also resets its
  working dir to the project root after each command, so it can only reach a worktree by path, not by
  persistently `cd`-ing in.)
- Worktrees live in the sibling `../Editora-V2-worktrees/` dir (outside the repo), so nothing needs
  to be gitignored. They share the same `.git`, so all branches/commits are visible everywhere.

## Release pipeline

`.github/workflows/release.yml` runs on a `v*` tag (or manual dispatch for a dry run): a 5-way
matrix (linux x64/arm64, macOS x64/arm64, windows x64 — **Windows arm64 is omitted: a hosted
runner now exists (`windows-11-arm`, GA Jan 2026), but OpenJFX 25 publishes no `win-aarch64` native
jar on Maven Central (see [JDK-8314064]), so a native ARM64 build can't link — Windows-on-ARM users
run the x64 installer under x64 emulation. Revisit when JavaFX ships win-aarch64 natives.** macOS x64
uses the `macos-15-intel` runner — the last Intel x86_64 image (good through ~Aug 2027) — since the
old `macos-13` Intel runner was retired Dec 2025;
each on its own GitHub-hosted runner) builds the native
installer via the existing `-Pdist` profile — there is **no cross-building** (jpackage + JavaFX are
host-specific), so each runner builds for itself. Each runner also builds a per-platform runnable
fat jar via `-Pfatjar` (`Editora-<version>-<target>.jar`). **Linux also ships two portable formats built
from the same AOT-trained app-image the `.deb`/`.rpm` are wrapped from (`target/aot-image/Editora`, so no
second `-Pdist` build):** a single-file **`.AppImage`** (`scripts/build-appimage.sh`) and an extract-and-install
**`.tar.gz`** (`scripts/build-tarball.sh`) whose bundled `packaging/linux/tarball-install.sh` installs the
image to `/opt/editora` (root) or `~/.local/editora` (user) with an `editora` command + a `.desktop`
(`StartupWMClass=com.editora.App`), supporting `--system`/`--user`/`--prefix`/`--uninstall`. Both reuse the
jpackage `APP_IMAGE` output (= jlink + the native launcher + `lib/app/editora.aot`, `$APPDIR`-relative so it's
relocatable); both release steps are `continue-on-error` so a hiccup can't sink the installers. The
`.tar.gz`/`.AppImage`/`.rpm` are attached to the GitHub release via `jreleaser.yml`'s file globs. Installers are renamed to
`Editora-<version>-<target>.<ext>` per target (the Stage step preserves the compound `.tar.gz`
extension) — one consistent `Editora-<version>-<target>` prefix
across all artifacts (jpackage's DMG/MSI names omit the version + arch; the
version comes from a `Resolve version` step — the tag minus `v`, else the pom version) and uploaded as
artifacts alongside the fat jar. **macOS pre-1.0 app-version:** jpackage's `--app-version` (which becomes
`CFBundleVersion`/`CFBundleShortVersionString`) rejects a version whose first number is zero/negative, so a
`0.x.y` `pom.xml` version fails jpackage on macOS only (Linux/Windows accept it fine) — the `os-mac` profile
computes a bundle-metadata-only `jpackage.appVersion` via a `maven-antrun-plugin` execution (Ant
`loadresource`/`propertyresource`/`tokenfilter replaceregex`, `initialize` phase, `exportAntProperties`)
that bumps a leading `0.` to `1.` (`0.9.0`→`1.9.0`); `os-windows`/`os-linux` just alias it to
`${project.version}`. Both jpackage invocations — the `jpackage-app-image` execution and
`aot_build.java`'s later DMG-wrap call — read `${jpackage.appVersion}` for their `--app-version` flag
(confirmed empirically: the DMG-wrap bundler enforces the same zero/negative-first-number rule even in
`--app-image <path>` mode, so the placeholder is unavoidable on *both* calls). But the placeholder must
never reach the delivered app: `aot_build.java`'s **`fixMacBundleMetadata`** (which already rewrites
`CFBundleDocumentTypes` for "Open With" — see below) also rewrites `CFBundleVersion`/
`CFBundleShortVersionString` back to the TRUE version (passed as a separate `publicVersion` argument,
`${project.version}`, distinct from the `appVersion` placeholder) right after the app-image build,
*before* the DMG wrap runs — confirmed empirically that jpackage's DMG-wrap does **not** re-touch an
already-correct `Info.plist` (it only uses `--app-version` for its own CLI validation and to name the raw
`.dmg` file, which the `Resolve version`-based rename above replaces anyway), so the delivered `.app`'s
Finder "Get Info" / `mdls` / System Settings, plus the in-app `--version`/About dialog, all show the real
semver — never the placeholder. A final job
hands them to **JReleaser** (`jreleaser.yml`, via `jreleaser/release-action`) which creates the
GitHub release with all installers + fat jars + `checksums.txt` + a changelog. JReleaser only *orchestrates the release* — it does not
build (the `dist` profile is reused as-is) and there is **no `pom.xml`/Maven change**, so the normal
build is unaffected. Installers are currently **unsigned** (signing/notarization is a follow-up).
**Linux `.deb` PATH command + menu/icon registration:** jpackage installs everything under
`/opt/editora/` (launcher at `bin/Editora`, the `.desktop` + the 512×512 `Editora.png` at
`lib/editora-Editora.desktop`/`lib/Editora.png`) and relies on its **own generated `postinst`** to
register the `.desktop`/icon system-wide (via `xdg-desktop-menu`). The **`.deb`** ships a custom **jpackage resource dir** (staged by
**the DEB wrap of `scripts/aot_build.java`** into `target/dist/jpackage-deb-resources` = the
`packaging/linux` files + `branding/editora.png` staged as `Editora.png` — DEB-only; the RPM bundler
uses a `.spec` and ignores these overrides, so `.rpm` users run `/opt/editora/bin/Editora`) carrying
three overrides: **(a)** Debian maintainer scripts `postinst`/`postrm`, **(b)** the menu-entry
template **`Editora.desktop`** (jpackage substitutes the `APPLICATION_*` placeholders in a
resource-dir `<launcher>.desktop` exactly like its bundled `template.desktop`) — ours adds
**`Exec=… %F`** (without it GNOME launches the app *without* the opened file; the path arrives as
argv → `App.fileTargets`), **`MimeType=text/plain;`** (registers Editora as a text-file handler so
GNOME Files offers it under "Open With" and it can be made the default editor via `xdg-mime default
editora-Editora.desktop text/plain`; GIO follows shared-mime-info subclassing, so `text/plain`
covers markdown/python/json/…), **`StartupWMClass=com.editora.App`** (the real `WM_CLASS`, verified
via `wmctrl -lx` — JavaFX derives it from the module main class, *not* the app name; without it the
*running* window can't be matched to the entry), and real `Categories` (jpackage emits `Unknown`) —
and **(c)** the **icon `Editora.png`**: the wrap **regenerates `lib/<name>.png` in the DEB payload
from its own resources**, ignoring `--icon` *and clobbering the app image's already-fixed icon*
(verified empirically: the wrapped `.deb` shipped a byte-identical copy of jpackage's bundled 32×32
`JavaApp.png` despite the pre-wrap overwrite), so the icon **must** be supplied as a resource-dir
override — the pre-wrap `aot_build.java` overwrite of `<imageRoot>/lib/Editora.png` (Linux-only,
guarded) still matters, but only for the deliveries built directly from the app image (APP_IMAGE /
`.tar.gz` / `.AppImage`). **Because the maintainer-script override *replaces* jpackage's generated
scripts, it must reproduce their registration or the launcher is never installed into
`/usr/share/applications` and the app shows the generic Java icon.** So `postinst` (`configure`):
(1) symlinks `/usr/bin/editora` → the launcher (found via the `/opt/*/bin/Editora` glob, since
jpackage lowercases the install dir); (2) **copies the bundled `.desktop` into
`/usr/share/applications/editora-Editora.desktop`** (the template already carries
StartupWMClass/MimeType/`%F`, so the copy takes the verbatim fast path; an awk StartupWMClass
injection remains as a fallback — the menu icon itself comes from the `.desktop`'s already-absolute
`Icon=/opt/editora/lib/Editora.png`); (3) **derives a second menu entry
`/usr/share/applications/editora-Editora-expert.desktop`** ("Editora Expert Mode") from the
just-registered primary via `sed` — `Exec=… --expert --single-window %F`, `StartupWMClass`
**dropped** (both entries launch the same `WM_CLASS` `com.editora.App`; only the primary may claim
it or GNOME binds the running window/dock icon to an arbitrary entry), and a `MimeType` listing the
concrete text types; and (4) **registers Expert Mode as the system-wide default text editor** by
merging a `[Default Applications]` `type=editora-Editora-expert.desktop` line per type into
`/usr/share/applications/mimeapps.list` (the freedesktop mime-apps mechanism GIO honors for system
defaults; idempotent across re-runs, drops a competing default for the same type, preserves
unrelated entries). The type list is the **canonical shared-mime-info names** (verified via
`xdg-mime query filetype` on Debian 13): the `text/*` source/config types plus the `application/*`
text formats (json/yaml/toml/xml/sql/x-shellscript/x-ruby/x-php/x-perl); anything unlisted still
reaches Editora via GIO's `text/plain` **subclass fallback** (a type with its own explicit default
elsewhere doesn't fall back — that's why the explicit list exists). **`text/html` and
`image/svg+xml` are deliberately excluded** (browser / image viewer keep those), and a user's own
`~/.config/mimeapps.list` choice still wins over the system default (deliberate, per Debian
convention — postinst runs as root and must not rewrite per-user config). Then
`update-desktop-database`. Verify a real `.deb`'s icon by
`sha256sum`-ing `/opt/editora/lib/Editora.png` against `branding/editora.png` — they must match.
`postrm` (remove/purge) removes all of it: the symlink, both `.desktop` entries, and the
expert-default lines from `mimeapps.list` (deleting that file only when nothing but section headers
remains, i.e. postinst created it). DEB-only — the RPM bundler ignores the resource-dir maintainer
scripts, and the `.tar.gz`'s `tarball-install.sh` installs its own single `.desktop`. **Device-test on Linux** (install the `.deb`: `which editora`
works + the app shows our icon in the menu and dock; then remove: both are gone) — the macOS dev box and
the `os-linux` profile can't exercise this. *(If a terminal-launched window's dock icon is still generic,
the real `WM_CLASS` differs from `Editora` — check `xprop WM_CLASS` and fix the injected value.)*
Uses the BellSoft **Liberica** JDK 25 in CI for full arch coverage (incl. linux aarch64).

## Architecture

Single module `com.editora` (see `src/main/java/module-info.java`). `App` is the
JavaFX entry point: it loads the **shared** config (`config/SharedConfig`), localizes the UI, applies
the theme + keymap, then hands off to **`ui/WindowManager`** which builds the window(s) — **the app is
multi-window** (each project opens in its own top-level window; see the `ui/`/`config/` bullets). `App`
also pins a classloader before building any window: `FXMLLoader.setDefaultClassLoader(...)` +
`Thread.currentThread().setContextClassLoader(...)`, because on macOS the FX/AppKit thread's context
classloader can be null, which would otherwise NPE inside `FXMLLoader.load()` when a window is built at
runtime (and break lazy class loading on that thread). `WindowManager.buildWindow` is the per-window
construction (extracted from `App.start`): it loads config, builds the command + keymap system, installs
the key dispatcher on the scene, applies the theme, and loads `ui/main.fxml`. It
wraps the FXML root in a `StackPane` so a floating overlay can sit on top — used by
`MainController.installZenOverlay` for the **Zen-mode exit button** (a small floating "Z",
`Icons.zen()`, styled `.zen-exit` like the Markdown preview controls, shown top-right only while
`WorkspaceState.isZenMode()` — toggled in `applyChromeVisibility` via `updateZenButton` — and
clicking it runs `setZenMode(false)`). `updateZenButton` also drops the Z below the Markdown preview
controls (a larger top margin) when the active buffer is Markdown, since those also float top-right; it
re-runs on tab switches so the offset tracks the active file. **Expert mode** is Zen's near-twin
(`WorkspaceState.expertMode` + `preExpertToolWindows`; `setExpertMode`/`toggleExpert`; command
`view.toggleExpert` = `C-c C-e`; Settings → Interface → Modes checkbox): it's a *lighter* focus mode that strips only the surrounding window
chrome (toolbar/tab bar/breadcrumb/tool stripes + whitespace guides) and **keeps the whole editor view**
(line numbers, status bar, minimap, column ruler, current-line highlight), via `Chrome`'s `focusMode`
(= `zen || expert`) param on the items both hide while `statusBar`/`lineNumbers`/`columnRuler`/`lineHighlight`/
`minimap` stay keyed on the real `zen` flag. It has its
own floating **"E"** exit button (`Icons.expert()`, `.expert-exit`, `updateExpertButton`) and the two modes
are **mutually exclusive** (entering one exits the other). `installZenOverlay` also creates a second
floating button, the **toolbar-restore "Tool" button** (`Icons.tools()`, styled `.toolbar-restore` like
the Zen "Z", also `Pos.TOP_RIGHT` — it never coexists with the "Z", which only shows in Zen mode), shown by `updateToolbarRestoreButton` (called from
`applyChromeVisibility`) only when the toolbar is hidden and not in Zen (`!isShowToolbar() && !isZenMode()`);
clicking it runs `toggleToolbar()` (which also `settingsWindow.syncToolbarCheck()`s), so a user who hides
the toolbar (Settings checkbox or the `view.toggleToolbar` palette command) can always bring it back. The
**toolbar's state-aware edit icons** (Save/Undo/Redo/Cut/Copy/Paste) are kept enabled/disabled by
`refreshEditState()` (save←dirty, undo/redo←`area.isUndoAvailable/isRedoAvailable`, cut←selection+editable,
copy←selection — all disabled on a non-buffer/Welcome tab) and `refreshPasteState()` (paste←editable +
`Clipboard.hasString()`, kept off the per-keystroke path: run on tab switch, window focus-regain, and after
cut/copy). `refreshEditState` runs on tab switch and the active buffer's edit/selection/dirty pulses;
disabling is cosmetic only — the `C-s`/`C-z`/… keymap commands still work. The toolbar's **Find in Files**
icon (`Icons.findInFiles()`, `onFindInFiles → openSearchInFiles`) sits beside the in-file Find icon.

- `command/` — the keyboard-driven core.
  - `Command` / `CommandRegistry`: every action is a registered `Command` (id + title + runnable). The registry feeds both keybindings and the palette.
  - `KeymapManager`: maps chord sequences (e.g. `C-x C-s`) to command ids; `loadNamed(name)` loads the bundled `resources/com/editora/keymaps/<name>.json`, then `applyOverrides` layers user (and plugin) overrides. **Five bundled keymaps** via the static ordered `KeymapManager.AVAILABLE` (id→display name): `emacs` (default), `cua`, `sublime`, `vscode`, `intellij` — the four non-Emacs ones are **non-modal** (just different chord→command maps over the existing command ids, so they fit the flat resolver; the commands are all palette-reachable, so a keymap only changes accelerators and never strands functionality). **Per-OS files:** each GUI keymap ships a base `<name>.json` (Ctrl-based, Win/Linux) **and** a complete `<name>.mac.json` (Cmd-based) — `loadNamed` prefers the `.mac` variant on macOS (full replacement, not a merge, so no Ctrl-shadowing or modifier token-order bug); Emacs is single-file (Control on every platform). Chord tokens are exactly what `KeyDispatcher.chord()` emits, modifiers in canonical order `C- M- Cmd- S-`; **function keys work via the `keyName` fallback** (`KeyCode.F5`→`"f5"`), so VSCode/IntelliJ F-key bindings need no engine change. **Live switching:** the Settings → Keymaps picker (the formerly-placeholder category) + the `keymap.select` palette command (`MainController.chooseKeymap`→`applyKeymap`) set `Settings.keymap`, then `WindowManager.reloadSharedKeymap()` rebuilds the **single shared** `KeymapManager` (base→user overrides→enabled plugins' `manifest.keymap`, mirroring `applyPlugins`) and `broadcastSettingsApplied()`s — every window's `KeyDispatcher` reads the same instance, so the switch is instant with no restart (a stale mid-chord prefix self-cancels on the next key). Each window's `reapplyAfterSharedSettingsChange` then **refreshes every chord-derived hint** so none stays frozen to the old keymap: **toolbar tooltips** (`setupButton(button, icon, tip, commandId)` → `applyToolbarTip`/`refreshToolbarTooltips` strip the chord baked into the `tooltip.*` i18n string — `"Save (C-x C-s)"` → `"Save"` — and append the live `invertBindings().get(id)`), the **command palette** (`CommandPalette.refreshBindings()`), the **tool-window stripe tooltips** (`ToolWindowManager.refreshTooltips()`), and the **Welcome shortcut labels** (`WelcomePane.refresh()`'s `shortcutFor`). The status-bar read-only/git-switch tooltips had their baked Emacs chords stripped from i18n. `KeymapsTest` guards all bundled keymaps (parse, valid command ids vs the `command.*` i18n keys, canonical token order, base↔`.mac` same-command-set parity). **Keybinding editor (fully configurable shortcuts):** Settings → Keymaps (below the theme combo) lists every command (from `CommandRegistry.all()`) with its current chord and a filter; a **Record** button turns a row into a live capture field (`KeyDispatcher.chord(e)` is now `public`; space-joins multi-key sequences, Esc cancels), **Reset** restores one command's default, and **Reset all** clears every override. The mutation logic is the pure, unit-tested **`command/KeybindingEdits`** (`rebind`/`clear`/`reset` over `(baseMap, overrides)`): a rebind drops the command's prior user entries, suppresses each base default via the **`KeymapManager.UNBIND`** sentinel (a blank override value → `applyOverrides` *removes* that chord), then binds the new chord; `reset` removes the command's user entries + its default-suppressors. `MainController` wires the editor (`SettingsWindow.ShortcutActions`/`Shortcut`): `shortcutRows()` (registry + `invertBindings`), `baseBindings()` (a fresh `KeymapManager.loadNamed` with no overrides), conflict check via **`KeybindingEdits.conflicts(keymap.bindings(), proposed, forCommand)`** — not just the exact `commandFor` match (which missed the footgun where recording a lone `C-x` silently killed every `C-x …` binding): it reports whole-token **prefix** collisions both ways (SHADOWS a longer chord / an existing chord makes the new one UNREACHABLE) so `rebindWithConflictCheck` warns and lists the affected shortcuts — and `rebindShortcut/resetShortcut/resetAllShortcuts` → persist the running platform's override map + `reloadKeymap()` (live, all windows; overrides layer on top of the active theme). **Overrides are stored per platform (#439):** `Settings.keybindings` holds the Ctrl-based (Windows/Linux) map and `Settings.keybindingsMac` the Cmd-based (macOS) one, read/written via `Settings.keybindingsFor(KeymapManager.isMac())` / `setKeybindingsFor(...)` — because a chord is modifier-specific and a rebind's `UNBIND` suppressor keys to the *resolved* chord, so a single shared map double-binds a rebound command on a config synced across OSes (a mac-written `Cmd-S UNBIND` doesn't suppress the `Ctrl-S` default on Windows, leaving it live beside the new, platform-neutral chord). Every apply site (`App`, `WindowManager.reloadSharedKeymap`, `MainController.reloadKeymap`) + the editor's rebind/reset use `keybindingsFor(isMac())`. Schema 80→81 (`ConfigMigrations.splitKeybindingsByPlatform`, pure core `splitKeybindings(node, mac)`): the existing single map moves into the slot of the platform running the migration and the other slot is cleared, so a later load on the other OS starts from defaults (no leak); `Settings.resetToDefaults` preserves both maps. The recorder runs in the Settings window's own scene (no `KeyDispatcher` there), so capture is clean. **New editor commands** `edit.selectAll` + the pure/unit-tested **`editops/LineOps`** (`duplicateLine`/`moveLineUp`/`moveLineDown` → an `Edit{from,to,replacement,caret}`, mirroring `Transposer`; applied by `MainController.lineOp(...)` guarded by `activeEditable()`) are bound in the GUI keymaps (Ctrl/Cmd-A, Alt/Option-Up/Down, etc.; Emacs leaves them palette-only since `C-a` is `nav.lineStart`). **Extended Emacs editing/movement commands** fill the remaining gaps vs. a standard Emacs `global-map`, via two more pure/unit-tested helpers in `editor/`: **`EmacsEdits`** (each returns an `Edit{from,to,replacement,caret}` applied by `MainController.emacsEdit(...)`/`emacsCaseRegion(...)`, guarded by `activeEditable()`) — `backward-kill-word` (`M-DEL`), `upcase`/`downcase`/`capitalize-word` (`M-u`/`M-l`/`M-c`) + region `upcase`/`downcase` (`C-x C-u`/`C-x C-l`), `delete-indentation`/join-line (`M-S-6` = `M-^`), `delete-horizontal-space` (`M-\`), `just-one-space` (`M-SPC`), `delete-blank-lines` (`C-x C-o`), `open-line` (`C-o`), `kill-whole-line` (`C-S-DEL`), and `zap-to-char` (`M-z`, the target char captured by a one-shot `KEY_TYPED` filter on the focused area, AceJump-style; the span is the pure `EmacsEdits.zapToChar`); and **`SexpNav`** (bracket/string/symbol-aware structural navigation) — `forward`/`backward-sexp` (`C-M-f`/`C-M-b`), `mark-sexp` (`C-M-SPC`), `kill-sexp` (`C-M-k`), heuristic `beginning`/`end-of-defun` (`C-M-a`/`C-M-e`, column-0 defun-start lines — approximate in a language-agnostic editor), and `paragraphBounds` for `mark-paragraph` (`M-h`). `mark-whole-buffer` reuses `edit.selectAll` (now bound `C-x h` in Emacs); `move-to-window-line-top-bottom` (`M-r`, `MainController.moveToWindowLine` cycling center/top/bottom of the viewport) rounds it out. All are palette-discoverable `edit.*`/`nav.*` commands, Emacs-keymap-bound, and i18n'd in all six catalogs; like transpose they don't fan out to multiple carets, and these edits clear the Emacs mark. *Deferred: the **kill ring** (so `M-y` yank-pop, and consecutive-kill accumulation — `C-w`/`M-w`/`C-y` still use the system clipboard, and the "kill" commands above just delete); modal **Vim** (needs a normal/insert/visual mode state machine, operator-pending, counts, registers, `:` command line — the flat resolver can't express it); the keybinding recorder allows a modifier-less chord (can shadow typing) and multi-line-selection block move/duplicate (v1 acts on the caret's line).*
  - `KeyDispatcher`: a scene-level `KEY_PRESSED` filter that builds chord tokens and resolves them, holding a pending-prefix buffer for multi-key Emacs chords. Lone unbound keys are *not* consumed, so normal typing works. **Windows/Linux Alt menu-mode fix (confirmed via on-device key logging):** on Windows a bare `Alt` **or an unbound `Alt+<key>`** is treated by the OS as menu/mnemonic activation, which puts the native window into "menu mode" — that freezes `KEY_TYPED` app-wide (mouse still works, restart required) and breaks the many `M-` chords (`M-x`, `M-g`, `M-1`…`M-9`, …). So on non-macOS `handle()` consumes **(a)** a bare `Alt` press and **(b)** any *unbound* key while plain Alt is held, and `install()` adds a `KEY_RELEASED` filter that consumes the bare `Alt` release. Bound `M-` chords still run+consume normally. The plain-vs-AltGr test is the pure, unit-tested **`plainAltActive(isMac, altDown, controlDown)`** = `!isMac && altDown && !controlDown` — **AltGr** (reported as Ctrl+Alt) and Ctrl+Alt chords are deliberately **not** consumed, so international layouts keep composing characters. macOS is unaffected (Option = Meta). *(Note: a global hotkey manager on the user's machine — e.g. XKeymaps — can still grab a specific chord like `Alt+X` before Editora sees it; that's external, not an Editora bug.)*
- `editor/` — `EditorBuffer` wraps a RichTextFX `CodeArea` (line numbers + fold chevrons via `FoldManager`, debounced highlighting). **Bookmarks**: a per-buffer `BookmarkManager` (analogous to `FoldManager`) holds line→`Bookmark` (record `line/note/lineText` in `config`), tracks lines through edits via `plainTextChanges` so bookmarks **follow their content** with forward/"sticky" gravity — inserting at a bookmarked line's start pushes it down (pure, column-aware `BookmarkManager.shift(...)` is unit-tested). Because `shift` only runs for edits made *inside* the app, on open each bookmark is **re-anchored to its saved `lineText`** (pure, unit-tested `BookmarkManager.reanchor(...)`: keeps an exact match in place, else moves it to the *nearest* line whose stripped text matches — downward-first on ties — bounded by `MAX_REANCHOR_SCAN`; an empty/vanished `lineText` stays at its clamped stored line), so bookmarks survive **external** edits to the file. `restore(...)` returns whether anything moved and `BookmarkCoordinator.restoreBookmarks` then calls `persistBookmarks` to self-heal the saved indices once (later opens hit the exact-match fast path, no save). The gutter draws a `.bookmark-marker` glyph (wired through `FoldManager.setBookmarkHooks`, refreshed per-line via `recreateParagraphGraphic`) — **display only: the gutter is not clickable**. A whole-gutter click used to toggle a bookmark, which misfired constantly on the narrow breakpoint strip / Run ▶ sitting inside the same gutter (a slightly-off click added a stray bookmark instead of setting a breakpoint or running the file), so adding/removing is done from the palette (`bookmarks.toggle`, `C-c m`) or the **editor right-click menu** (`editmenu.addBookmark`/`removeBookmark`, acting on the right-clicked line, `MenuIcons.bookmark()`), which routes through `EditorBuffer.setBookmarkToggleRequest` → `BookmarkCoordinator.onBookmarkToggleRequest` (adds silently, confirms a removal). Only the individual gutter slots — breakpoint, Run, blame, fold chevron — handle clicks, each on its own glyph/strip. Bookmarks live in their own `bookmarks.json` (`config/BookmarkStore`) — kept out of `WorkspaceState` so they're all in one easy-to-find file — but **scoped per project**: the store is `Map<projectKey, Map<path,List<Bookmark>>>` (`byProject`; `projectKey` = `""` for the no-project/global session, else the project id). `ConfigManager.getBookmarks()` returns the **active** project's bucket, chosen by `currentBookmarkKey()` (derived from the active `workspaceStateFile`: `workspace-state.json` → `""`, `projects/<id>.json` → `<id>`), so switching a project (`setWorkspaceStateFile`/`useDefaultWorkspaceStateFile`) automatically swaps which bookmarks are visible — `MainController.activateSession` already calls `bookmarksPanel.refresh()`. `saveBookmarks()` writes the whole `bookmarks.json`; `BookmarkCoordinator.persistBookmarks`/`restoreBookmarks` call `saveBookmarks()` — *not* `save()`. On first run, `ConfigManager.loadBookmarks()` does a one-time migration: it pulls bookmarks previously embedded in `workspace-state.json` (→ the `""` bucket) and each `projects/<id>.json` (→ that project's bucket), strips the legacy `bookmarks` node from those files, and writes `bookmarks.json` (created even when empty) so the migration runs once. Deleting a project also drops its bookmarks (`MainController.deleteProject` → `ConfigManager.deleteBookmarksForProject(id)`). The `BookmarksPanel` **groups by project** — it reads the *whole* store (`BookmarkCoordinator.scope()` → `ConfigManager.getAllBookmarks()` + `currentProjectKey()` + a key→name resolver, packaged as `BookmarksPanel.Scope`), always shows the **General** (`""`) group and the **current project** group ("… (current)"), and a **"Show all projects" `ToggleButton`** reveals every other project too (grouping order via the pure/unit-tested `ui/ScopeGroups.visibleKeys`), so bookmarks no longer appear/disappear when switching projects (#565). Reordering (drag / Alt+Up-Down / menu) is confined to the current project's group (the only editable bucket); file rows use the real `FileIcons` glyph and project-group headers read accent-colored. It includes closed files and routes edits back through the controller (open buffer's manager, else the map). **Order is user-controlled, not sorted**: the panel renders the bucket's map order (files) and each file's list order (bookmarks) verbatim, and the `M-g b` jump picker (`allBookmarkEntries`) reads the same order — so the two always agree. Reorder a bookmark within its file or a whole file group via **Alt+Up/Down**, a right-click **Move Up/Down**, or **drag-and-drop** (bookmark onto a sibling, file header onto another; disabled while a filter is active), routed through `Actions.moveBookmark`/`moveFile` → `BookmarkCoordinator.moveBookmark`/`moveBookmarkFile` (mutate the bucket + `saveBookmarks`; the panel reselects the moved row after refresh). The drag uses the **same visuals as the tab strip**: a translucent `setDragView` snapshot follows the cursor, the dragged `.tree-cell` dims (`.bookmark-dragging`), and an accent insertion line shows on the target row's top/bottom edge (`.bookmark-drop-above`/`.bookmark-drop-below`, mirroring `.tab-drop-before/after`); `BookmarksPanel.insertIndex` (pure/unit-tested) maps the drop side to the post-removal insert index. Because an open buffer's `BookmarkManager.snapshot()` is line-ordered, `persistBookmarks` runs the pure, unit-tested `BookmarkStore.mergePreservingOrder(previous, snapshot)` to keep the custom order across edits (matching bookmarks by line, else by captured `lineText` so the order follows content through line shifts). Commands: `bookmarks.toggle` (`C-c m`), `bookmarks.next`/`previous` (`C-c ]`/`C-c [`, within-file), `bookmarks.jump` (`M-g b`, cross-file picker), `editNote`/`clearFile`. The window wiring lives in **`ui/BookmarkCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `BookmarksPanel` + the jump picker + the per-buffer persist/restore + the `bookmarks.*` flow, reaching the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension for open-path / navigate-to-line / open-buffer-for-path / note-prompt / the `bookmarks.json` map; bookmarks are always on, so there's no support gate); `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` (built with `bookmarkCoordinator.panel()`), the rename-migration call (`migrateKey`), and wires `addBuffer`'s bookmark hooks + the `bookmarks.*` commands to the coordinator. **Markdown preview**: an IntelliJ-style per-buffer 3-mode view (`EditorBuffer.MarkdownViewMode` EDITOR/SPLIT/PREVIEW) driven by a floating `MarkdownViewToggle` overlaid top-right of the editor for Markdown files (the same 3-mode toggle **every** previewable file type reuses; two file-type-agnostic palette commands flip the active buffer's mode for any file with `hasPreview()` — **`view.togglePreview`** = Editor ⇄ full Preview, **`view.toggleSplitPreview`** = Editor ⇄ Split, both backed by `MainController.togglePreviewMode(target)`, which collapses to Editor when already in the target and so also flips Split ⇄ Preview between the two commands; these replaced the former per-type `view.toggle*Preview` palette commands — each preview type's *support* is still a Settings → Editor checkbox); `MarkdownRenderer` parses CommonMark+GFM (commonmark-java, all proper JPMS modules — `requires org.commonmark.*`, no moditect) **off-thread** then builds native JavaFX nodes **on the FX thread** under a stale-gen guard (the `highlightExecutor` idiom), debounced via `multiPlainChanges().successionEnds(250ms)`, only while SPLIT/PREVIEW (≥5 MB files render once). The mode is persisted per file in `WorkspaceState.markdownViewModes` (`MainController.persistMarkdownMode`/`restoreMarkdownMode`), mirroring folds. Preview colors use AtlantaFX semantic CSS (`.markdown-preview`/`.md-*` in `app.css`) so they track the theme without per-theme overrides. **Independent light/dark preview theme**: the preview can be themed separately from the app/editor theme via a floating sun/moon button added to the `−`/`+` zoom control (top-left). Persisted globally in `Settings.markdownPreviewTheme` (`""` = follow the app theme until first toggled, then `"light"`/`"dark"`; schema bumped 2→3, additive identity migration). `MainController.toggleMarkdownPreviewTheme` (also the palette `view.toggleMarkdownPreviewTheme`) flips the effective theme — seeded from app brightness via `appThemeDark()` (`Themes.backgroundFor`) — saves, and `applyMarkdownPreviewTheme()` pushes it to every open buffer. `EditorBuffer.applyPreviewTheme(mode, appDark)` adds `md-light`/`md-dark` to the preview `ScrollPane`, which **redefine the looked-up `-color-*` vars for the whole preview subtree** so the existing `.md-*` rules re-resolve to a fixed GitHub-style palette (no rule duplication), and refreshes the toggle glyph (sun while dark → switch to light, moon while light → switch to dark). The toggle is injected via `setPreviewThemeToggle` (like the snippet/completion providers — `editor` can't depend on `ui`). No Settings-window entry. For readability the content is a **centered, width-capped column** (`MAX_CONTENT_WIDTH`≈860; `renderDocument` wraps the `.markdown-preview` VBox in a centering `StackPane` `.markdown-preview-wrap` that clamps to the viewport when narrower) with GitHub-like margins + vertical rhythm (padding/spacing/line-spacing tuned in `app.css`). **Keyboard scrolling** in the preview: Space/PageDown page down and Backspace/PageUp page up via a `KEY_PRESSED` filter on the preview `ScrollPane` (`scrollPreviewPage`; the pane is focused on entering PREVIEW + on click). **SPLIT-mode scroll sync** (`EditorBuffer.installSplitScrollSync` + the preview `vvalueProperty` listener in `previewPane()`): in SPLIT the editor and preview track each other by scroll **fraction** (editor `estimatedScrollY`/(`totalHeightEstimate` − viewport height) ↔ preview `vvalue` fraction), so they stay aligned despite differing content heights. The gate is which pane is **hovered** (`previewPane.isHover()` — the wheel target), so the pane the mouse is over drives the other; the mouse is over at most one pane, making the sync one-directional at any moment so it **can't oscillate** — the same RichTextFX `estimatedScrollY`-refinement feedback trap `DiffViewerPane.syncScroll` guards against (hover is used here rather than focus because a wheel over the `CodeArea` doesn't reliably focus it). A `syncingScroll` re-entrancy flag wraps each programmatic set as a second guard, and entering SPLIT aligns the preview to the editor via a one-shot `Platform.runLater(syncPreviewToEditorScroll)`. **The hover gate is not sufficient on its own (#605):** a `ScrollPane`'s `vvalue` also moves when the pane **re-anchors to content that resized**, which `isHover()` cannot distinguish from a wheel — and a preview that renders **progressively** (typst pages, Mermaid diagrams, images resolving) resizes many times over a second or two, so each growth arrived as a fake scroll and dragged the editor with it: measured at **~80 viewport moves over ~2 s, the editor drifting ~100 lines down and back**, with the mouse merely *resting* over the preview and long after first paint (the same file in EDITOR mode moved twice — the initial layout — which is what isolated it). So the preview→editor listener tracks the preview's content height and, within a **250 ms settle window** after a resize (the pure, unit-tested `EditorBuffer.previewHeightChanged`/`previewSettling` — a *window*, not a single-pulse check, because the provoked `vvalue` changes don't all land on the resize pulse), treats the move as layout and **re-anchors the preview to the editor** instead, the editor being the source of truth. Genuine scrolling past that window syncs as before. **Diagnosing this needed per-pulse instrumentation**; three plausible-sounding culprits — the restore scroll, `goToStart`, the font-zoom re-layout — were all wrong, and the tail-render they *did* fix turned out to happen while the area still had **zero height**, i.e. invisible. **Two traps when instrumenting a RichTextFX viewport, both of which produced wrong conclusions here:** (a) **`firstVisibleParToAllParIndex()` forces a `VirtualFlow` layout** (`getCellIfVisible` → `layoutChildren`) and *itself moves `estimatedScrollY`* — polling it every pulse perturbs the very thing being measured, so probe **`estimatedScrollYProperty().getValue()`** instead (a plain property read); (b) a **per-pulse poll can only correct a reset one frame late**, turning a jump into a bounce — to catch the frame, hook the change, not the pulse. **A restored file's viewport is collapsed to the top by *two* distinct mechanisms, both of which must be defended:** (1) documented under `setStyleSpansPreservingScroll` in `EditorBuffer` — **`setStyleSpans` can collapse the flow's scroll to the top** (measured `estimatedScrollY` 184 → 0 on the first highlight pass after a session restore, a couple of pulses after the file had already painted at its saved caret), so the span apply restores the scroll when — and only when — it collapsed; and (2) the **virtual flow re-anchors itself during a plain layout pass** (`Parent.layout → VirtualFlow.layoutChildren → Navigator.fillViewportFrom → `CellListManager.cropTo`, with **no app code in the stack**), which `MainController.scrollRestoredCaretIntoView` defends with a listener that puts the offset back **in the same pulse** for a bounded settle window. **Correcting it a pulse later — the obvious poll — only converts the jump into a bounce**, which is what two earlier attempts shipped-and-reverted did. The guard is deliberately narrow (only a drop *to the top*, only while a non-zero offset was wanted) so it can't fight legitimate scrolling. Rides existing scroll listeners — no new per-keystroke/per-pulse work. The preview `ScrollPane` also has a **right-click menu** (`setOnContextMenuRequested`→`showPreviewContextMenu`): **Select All** / **Copy** (both → `copyPreviewToClipboard` → `MarkdownRenderer.plainText(getContent())`, the commonmark `TextContentRenderer` rendering of the source = the visible text with markup stripped; a diagram copies its source) + **Export to PDF** / **Print** (injected `setPreviewExportPdfHandler`/`setPreviewPrintHandler` → `MainController.exportPreviewPdf`/`printPreview`). The native preview nodes aren't selectable, so copy is **menu-driven** (no drag-highlight). While `C-v`/`M-v` (→ `nav.pageDown`/`nav.pageUp`) page the preview through `EditorBuffer.pagePreview` / `MainController.pageActivePreview` when the preview is the active scroll target (PREVIEW mode, or a focused SPLIT preview) and otherwise fall back to paging the editor. Rendering aims to match **GitHub**: GFM task items render as real checkboxes (the `TaskListItemMarker` is the `ListItem`'s **first child**, not nested in its paragraph — `firstTaskMarker`), inline `code` is a `Label` "pill" with a rounded gray background (a `Text` can't carry a background), `#`/`##` headings get an underline rule, and links aren't permanently underlined. **Fenced code blocks are syntax-highlighted** (`highlightedCodeBlock`): a block with a language info string renders as a `TextFlow` shown immediately as plain text, then tokenized **off the FX thread** on a daemon `md-code-highlight` executor (tm4e access must not run on the FX thread — it contends/deadlocks with the editor's background highlighters) and the styled `Text` runs are filled in on the FX thread when ready (the `MermaidImages` placeholder-then-fill pattern). The runs carry the same `.text.<class>` token classes the editor uses, so it tracks the active editor theme; the info string maps to a grammar via `forLanguageName` then a `forFileName("x.<ext>")` fallback over an alias map (`INFO_EXT`: `js`/`ts`/`py`/`rb`/`sh`/…). Untokenized runs get a `.md-code-block .text { -fx-fill: -color-fg-default }` fallback in `syntax.css` (same specificity as the token rules, placed *before* them so tokens win on source order; scoped to the preview, never the RichTextFX area, so the per-node-cache/scroll concern doesn't apply). No language / an indented block / a >50k-char block / a tokenize failure falls back to the plain `codeBlock` `Label`. **The token colors follow the preview's independent light/dark theme, not the editor's:** `syntax.css` pins a fixed GitHub palette per preview brightness via `.md-light .md-code-block .text.<class>` (Primer Light) / `.md-dark .md-code-block .text.<class>` (Primer Dark) — specificity (0,4,0), above the editor-theme override's (0,2,0) — so code stays readable when the preview is forced opposite the editor. In "follow app" mode no `md-*` class is present, so the code tracks the editor theme (already consistent); plain-run `-color-fg-default` + log-token `-color-*` vars adapt for free. Images render via `ImageView` (`imageNode`, capped to `MAX_IMAGE_WIDTH`, alt/title tooltip); a paragraph that is just an image becomes a **block** image, `http(s)`/`file`/`data:` URLs load directly and relative paths resolve against the file's folder (`resolveUrl`, `baseDir`). Loading goes through **`PreviewImageLoader`** (`editor/`): off the FX thread it fetches the bytes (URLConnection with a timeout; `data:` decoded inline) and, crucially, **rasterizes SVG** — which JavaFX's decoder can't read — via **JSVG** (`com.github.weisj.jsvg`, a small modular SVG lib; `requires com.github.weisj.jsvg` + `java.desktop`, no moditect) into a `BufferedImage` (`LoaderContext.createDefault()` denies external resource loads → no SVG-based SSRF) then copies it to a JavaFX `WritableImage` via a `PixelWriter` (no `javafx.swing`); non-SVG bytes decode with JavaFX. This is what makes **shields.io / GitHub badges** (served as `image/svg+xml`) show in the preview. Results are cached per URL and recent failures are remembered for `FAILURE_TTL_MS` so a re-render doesn't hammer an unreachable host; only the final `setImage` touches the FX thread. The pure `looksLikeSvg(bytes)` sniff is unit-tested. (JSVG can't render a nested SVG-in-SVG, e.g. a badge's embedded logo glyph — harmless; its logger is quieted to `SEVERE` so that per-render WARNING isn't spammed.) **Crucial macOS guard:** because SVG rasterization touches `java.awt`/Java2D, **`App.main` sets `java.awt.headless=true` as its very first statement**. On macOS the AWT/Java2D *native* pipeline (AppKit/Metal) otherwise contends with JavaFX's Glass/Prism for the single AppKit run loop — an **intermittent deadlock/hang** that grows likelier the more SVG badges are rasterized (i.e. the more Markdown previews are open). Headless Java2D rasterizes to a `BufferedImage` purely in software (no AppKit), so badges still render while the conflict disappears. Keep it first in `main` (before any AWT class loads); it covers every entry point (`javafx:run`, fat-jar `Launcher`, jpackage module all route through `App.main`). **Read-only / View mode**: `EditorBuffer.setViewMode/isViewMode` is a user toggle *separate* from the huge-file `setReadOnly` — `applyEditable()` sets `area.setEditable(!hugeFile && !viewMode)` and tags the surface `.read-only`, but View mode keeps highlighting/minimap/undo (unlike huge-file mode). `isEditable()` is the single source of truth. `setEditable(false)` blocks typing; the app's own edit commands are guarded by `MainController.activeEditable()` (checked in `withArea` + `onCut`/`onPaste`/`chooseLineEndings`). Command `view.toggleReadOnly` (`C-x C-q`); the state persists per file in `WorkspaceState.readOnlyFiles` (`persist/restoreReadOnly`, mirroring markdown mode), and `restoreReadOnly` also auto-enables it for files not writable on disk (pure/unit-tested `MainController.shouldOpenReadOnly`). The status bar shows a read-only **toggle** segment — "Read-Only" (amber/`.active`) ⇄ "Editable" (muted), click to flip either way — and the tab gets a `.read-only` class. `getNode()` returns an outer `BorderPane` whose top is an MS-Word-style **"View Mode" banner** (`.view-mode-bar`, shown by `updateViewModeBar()` only while `viewMode && !hugeFile`) with the navigation hint and an **Enable Editing** button — visible only when the file is writable (else a "read-only on disk" note); the button runs `onEnableEditing` (wired by `MainController.addBuffer` to `enableEditing(buffer)` → off + persist + refresh). **Save as Administrator** (Linux & macOS): the pure **`process/ElevatedSave`** (`supportedOnOs`/`isLinux`/`isMac`, `pkexecArgv`, `osascriptArgv`, `elevatedArgv`, `isCancellation` — unit-tested) writes a non-writable file (e.g. under `/etc`) via the OS auth agent, which prompts for the password itself (Editora never handles it): **`pkexec`/polkit** on Linux, **`osascript` `do shell script … with administrator privileges`** (native Touch ID / password prompt) on macOS. Both run `cat source > target` as root — an in-place truncate+rewrite that preserves the target's owner/mode; the macOS path passes the two paths as `osascript` argv and shell-escapes them via AppleScript `quoted form of` (never interpolated). Gated by `Settings.adminSave` (default off, schema 46→47; Settings → Editor → Saving + palette `view.toggleAdminSave`); `MainController.applyAdminSaveSupport()` (init + settings apply, the `applyRipgrepSupport` idiom) marks the tool available immediately on macOS (osascript always present) or probes `pkexec --version` off-thread on Linux, then pushes `EditorBuffer.setAdminEditAvailable(...)` so a non-writable file's banner shows **"Edit as Administrator"** (relabels the Enable-Editing button; enabling editing then routes Save through the elevated write) instead of the dead-end note. `save()` routes to `saveAsAdmin(buffer)` when `adminSaveApplicable(path)` (enabled + tool found + local + exists + `!isWritable`); `saveAsAdmin` writes `saveBytes` to a 0600 temp file then runs `ElevatedSave.elevatedArgv(os, …)` off-thread via `ProcessRunner`, applying the result on the FX thread (`onAdminSaveDone`: 0 = markClean+refresh, `ElevatedSave.isCancellation(os, exit, stderr)` = cancelled — pkexec 126 / osascript `-128`/"User canceled" — else failed). Palette command `file.saveAsAdmin`. Windows isn't supported (falls back to the plain read-only note; `save()` returns false for the async elevated path, so a save-before-run/quit re-prompts). While read-only, an `area`-level `KEY_PRESSED` filter (`addViewModePaging`, installed on `area`/`area2`) makes unmodified **Space page down / Backspace page up** (pager-style); it runs before RichTextFX's own no-op handling and only acts when `viewMode` is on. The pure, toolkit-free text-editing operation cores — `Indenter`, `AutoClose`, `BraceMatcher`, `Commenter`, `Transposer`, `LineOps`, `EmacsEdits`, `SexpNav`, `Filler`, `LineIndent`, `StringCase`, `LineTransforms`, and `TagRename` (each returning a small `Edit`/decision record or transformed text, no FX) — live in their own **`com.editora.editops`** package (internal, no `module-info` change), with their unit tests under `com.editora.editops`; `EditorBuffer`/`MainController` import them. **String manipulation** (the JetBrains String-Manipulation-plugin family): pure, unit-tested **`StringCase`** (`words`/`to(Style)`/`detect`/`cycle`/`swapCase`/`tokenAt` — camelCase/PascalCase/snake_case/SCREAMING_SNAKE_CASE/kebab-case/dot.case; `cycle` steps a token camel→snake→SCREAMING→kebab→Pascal→camel; `tokenAt` grabs the letters/digits/`_`/`-` run at the caret, dots excluded) and **`LineTransforms`** (`lineBounds` — full-line extension of a selection, a column-0 end excluding that line — plus `sortAscending`/`sortDescending` (the `NATURAL` numeric-aware case-insensitive comparator, case-sensitive tiebreak), `sortByLength`, `reverse`, `shuffle(text, RandomGenerator)` (randomness injected for tests), `removeDuplicates` (first occurrence kept), `removeEmpty`, `trimTrailing`; each preserves a single trailing newline so a whole-buffer slice never grows a phantom sorted-to-top empty line). `MainController.caseOp` (selection, else `tokenAt` fallback) and `lineTransform` (selection extended via `lineBounds`, else the whole buffer) apply one op as a single undoable `replaceText` guarded by `activeEditable()`, re-selecting the result so `edit.case.cycle` can be pressed repeatedly; a no-op echoes `status.stringops.noChange`. Commands: `edit.case.cycle`/`camel`/`pascal`/`snake`/`screamingSnake`/`kebab`/`dot`/`swap`, `edit.sortLinesAsc`/`Desc`/`ByLength`, `edit.reverseLines`, `edit.shuffleLines`, `edit.removeDuplicateLines`/`removeEmptyLines`, `edit.trimTrailingWhitespace` — all palette-discoverable/key-bindable — plus **`edit.stringOps`** (`C-c x`, Emacs-bound), a `QuickOpen` picker over the whole set (the plugin's Alt+M popup; labels/details from the command title/desc i18n keys). *Deferred: escape/encode (Java/JSON/XML/HTML, URL/Base64, unicode escapes, diacritics→ASCII), align-by-separator, keep/remove lines by pattern, increment/sequences, multi-caret fan-out.* **Auto/smart indentation**: the pure, unit-tested `Indenter` (per-language `Style` BRACES/XML/PY/SHELL/RUBY/LUA/PLAIN via `styleFor`) computes Enter indentation — inherit the current line's indent, +1 level after a block opener, and a matching-pair split (`{}`/`()`/`[]`/`<a>|</a>`); `EditorBuffer.addAutoIndent` (a `KEY_PRESSED` Enter filter + a `KEY_TYPED` filter on `area`/`area2`, same pattern as the pager/snippet keys) inserts it, consuming Enter so RichTextFX's plain newline doesn't also run. Typing a closer (a `)]}` bracket alone on a line, or a completed keyword `end`/`fi`/`done`/… via `completesCloserKeyword`) re-aligns the line to its opener via `Indenter.closerAlignIndent` (nearest shallower previous line) — done on the completing keystroke, not on Enter, so it never over-dedents. Indent unit (tab vs `tabSize` spaces) is inferred from the file (`detectUnit`), from the first indented line — **defaulting to spaces** when the file has no indentation at all (VSCode/IntelliJ's "spaces unless detected as tabs"). **Smart backspace**: a `BACK_SPACE` `KEY_PRESSED` filter (also in `addAutoIndent`) does a one-press indent delete when the caret is in leading-only whitespace — pure/unit-tested `Indenter.smartBackspaceCount(beforeCaret, afterCaret, hasPreviousLine)`: on a **blank (auto-indented) line** it removes the indent **and the preceding newline** (so one press jumps back to the end of the previous line — "back to where you hit Enter"), on an **indented content line** it clears the indent only, and returns 0 elsewhere. The filter consumes only when the count is >1 so a normal single-char Backspace runs everywhere else. Inert while a snippet session is active or in read-only mode. **Markdown lists:** the same Backspace filter first checks `MarkdownLines.emptyMarkerDeleteLength(line, col)` (pure/unit-tested) — when the caret is at the end of a line that is only an empty list/blockquote marker (`- `/`1. `/`> `/`- [ ] `), one press deletes the whole marker back to the line start (→ a blank line), the SDD "smart backspace" helper; otherwise it falls through to the indent dedent above. **Auto-close & matching brackets**: pure, unit-tested `AutoClose` (decision for a typed char → INSERT_PAIR/SKIP_OVER/WRAP_SELECTION/NONE; quotes aren't paired next to a word char) and `BraceMatcher` (`match(text, caret, maxScan)` → the two offsets to highlight, nearest bracket left-of-caret first). `EditorBuffer.addAutoClose` (a `KEY_TYPED` filter + a Backspace `KEY_PRESSED` filter on `area`/`area2`, **registered before `addAutoClose`/`addAutoIndent` order matters** — auto-close runs first and only consumes when it acts, leaving a plain closer for the indent dedent) inserts pairs / types over / wraps / clears empty pairs. Brace matching runs off the caret listener via `scheduleBraceMatch` (coalesced to one per pulse) → `updateBraceMatch`, which adds a combinable `brace-match` style class to the two bracket chars (`.text.brace-match` in `syntax.css`, a semi-transparent box so it keeps the token color and needs no per-theme override); the syntax highlighter overwrites it on re-highlight, so the highlight apply re-calls `scheduleBraceMatch`. Off in large-file mode. **Auto Rename Tag** (VS Code parity, gated by `Settings.autoRenameTag`, default on, schema 50→51 additive-identity; Settings → Editor checkbox + palette `view.toggleAutoRenameTag`): editing an HTML/XML tag *name* renames the paired open/close tag live — the pure/unit-tested `TagRename.mirror(text, changePos, removed, inserted, html)` finds the tag-name region around the change (bounded backwalk to `<`/`</`), reconstructs the **old name** by reverting the change, then pairs tags by **same-name depth counting** over one forward lex (only tags bearing the old name participate, so unclosed optional-close elements — `<li>`/`<p>`/… — with other names can't misalign the match; skips comments/CDATA/doctype/PI/quoted attribute values/self-closing tags; HTML mode treats void elements as self-closing and jumps over `<script>`/`<style>`/`<textarea>`/`<title>` raw content; HTML names compare case-insensitively, XML case-sensitively) and emits a `Mirror{from,to,name}` for the tag returning the same-name depth to zero (forward for an opener, backward for a closer) — the pair bears the old name by construction, so a half-typed brand-new tag never renames an unrelated closer; docs over `MAX_DOC` (2M chars) aren't scanned. `EditorBuffer.maybeMirrorTagRename` (an immediate `plainTextChanges` subscription; first checks are two boolean/string compares for non-html/xml buffers) applies it as one `replaceText` on the focused area, restores the caret/anchor (replaceText moves the caret to the mirror), is guarded re-entrantly (`applyingTagRename`) and **suppressed during undo/redo** (`UndoManager.isPerformingAction`, both views — undoing the user edit and the mirror separately must not re-mirror); off in large/huge-file mode; `applyViewSettings` pushes `setAutoRenameTag`. *Deferred: JSX/TSX, surviving a fully-emptied name, single-undo-step mirroring.* **Auto Close Tags** (VS Code parity, gated by `Settings.autoCloseTags`, default on, schema 51→52 additive-identity; Settings → Editor checkbox + palette `view.toggleAutoCloseTags`): typing the `>` that completes an HTML/XML open tag inserts `</name>` after the caret (caret stays between the tags) — the pure/unit-tested **`TagAutoClose.closer(beforeCaret, html)`** decides over a bounded pre-caret window (`MAX_TAG_SCAN`) with one forward pass whose quote state applies only *inside* tags (so text apostrophes and `>`/`<` inside closed attribute strings can't derail it), returning null for closers/`/>`/doctype/comment/PI/HTML-void elements (`TagRename.VOID_ELEMENTS`, now package-shared) or a `>` inside an open attribute string. Wired as the first branch of `EditorBuffer.applyAutoCloseTyped` (before the `AutoClose` bracket logic), so the live KEY_TYPED filter **and macro replay** (`typeChar`) share it; per-buffer `setAutoCloseTags` pushed from `applyViewSettings`; inert for non-html/xml buffers at the cost of one boolean+string check. *Deferred: `</` closing-tag name completion.* **Comment/uncomment**: pure, unit-tested `Commenter` (`styleFor(language)` → `CommentStyle(line, blockStart, blockEnd)`; `toggle(text, selStart, selEnd, style)` → an `Edit`); a single line uses the line comment (else block), a multi-line selection uses the block/region comment (else line-comments each line), preserving indentation and toggling off when already commented. Command `edit.toggleComment` (`M-;`, Emacs comment-dwim) in `MainController.toggleComment`, guarded by `activeEditable()`. **Transpose**: pure, unit-tested `Transposer` (`transposeChars`/`transposeWords`/`transposeLines` → an `Edit{from,to,replacement,caret}`, or null for a no-op) implements the Emacs transpose commands; `MainController.transpose(op)` applies it to the active `CodeArea` (guarded by `activeEditable()`). Commands `edit.transposeChars` (`C-t`), `edit.transposeWords` (`M-t`), `edit.transposeLines` (`C-x C-t`). **Fill** (Emacs fill commands): pure, unit-tested **`Filler`** (`fillParagraph(text, caret, fillColumn, lineComment)` / `fillRegion(text, selStart, selEnd, fillColumn, lineComment)` → an `Edit{from,to,replacement,caret}`) re-wraps a blank-line-bounded paragraph to the fill column — joins its lines, collapses whitespace, greedily packs words (never breaking a word longer than the column), and repeats the paragraph's **fill prefix** (leading indent + an optional comment/quote marker — the language line-comment via `Commenter.styleFor(...).line()`, or `>`/`*`) on every wrapped line. `MainController.fillParagraph`/`fillRegion`/`applyFill` apply it guarded by `activeEditable()`; `setFillColumn` (`C-x f`) prompts via `promptText` and persists `Settings.fillColumn` (default `Filler.DEFAULT_FILL_COLUMN` = 70; schema 25→26 additive-identity; Settings → Editor spinner). Commands `edit.fillParagraph` (`M-q`), `edit.fillRegion`, `edit.setFillColumn` (`C-x f`) — Emacs-keymap-bound, palette-discoverable. *Deferred: Auto Fill mode (break-as-you-type), justification, sentence double-spacing, `fill-individual-paragraphs`.* **Spell checking**: Apache **Lucene Hunspell** (pure Java; `requires org.apache.lucene.analysis.common`/`.core`, real JPMS modules → no moditect). `SpellDictionaries` builds + caches one `Hunspell` per language **lazily/off-thread** from bundled `resources/com/editora/dictionaries/<id>/index.{aff,dic}` (in-memory `ByteBuffersDirectory`); ships `en_US`/`en_GB` (SCOWL, permissive), `es` (Spain) + `es_MX` (Mexico) — both the RLA/LibreOffice Spanish dictionary, used under MPL-1.1 — and `fr` (MPL-2.0). German is GPL-only upstream, so it's not bundled. Add a language by dropping `<id>/index.{aff,dic}` under `dictionaries/` and adding the id to `SpellDictionaries.AVAILABLE` (+ NOTICE). `SpellChecker` wraps the engine + the shared user dictionary + a per-session ignore set: pure/unit-tested `wordSpans(line)` (letter runs with intra-word apostrophes) and `skip(word)` (≤1 char / digits / ALL-CAPS / camelCase) gate which words are checked; `isMisspelled`/`suggest` defer to Hunspell. Rendering is a mouse-transparent `SpellCheckOverlay` (a `Canvas`, **mirrors `WhitespaceOverlay`**) that draws red wavy underlines for visible misspelled words — decoupled from `setStyleSpans`, coalesced per pulse, visible-paragraphs only, off in large-file mode. Eligibility by applied style: prose buffers (`isProse()` = plaintext/markdown) check all words except `code`; code buffers only `comment`/`string`. The editor right-click menu (`installContextMenu`) prepends suggestions (replace the word) + **Add to Dictionary** (`ConfigManager.addUserWord` → `dictionary.txt`, then `MainController.addUserWordAndRefreshAll` → **`WindowManager.broadcastUserDictionaryChanged()`** re-runs the spell pass in *every* window's tabs, not just this one — the dictionary is shared app-wide, so another window's buffers otherwise kept the stale squiggle on the just-added word until they applied a setting (#443); mirrors `broadcastSettingsApplied`/`broadcastMacrosChanged`; the global word list is also editable in **Settings → Spell Check → Personal Dictionary** (`SettingsWindow.dictionaryEditor`: a list + add/remove over `ConfigManager.addUserWord`/`removeUserWord`, the latter rewriting `dictionary.txt` from the in-memory set; palette `spell.manageDictionary` → `showSpellCheck`), with an **Enable personal dictionary** checkbox (`Settings.personalDictionary`, default on, schema 40→41; off gates the user-word check via `SpellChecker.setUserWordsEnabled` pushed by `EditorBuffer.setUserDictionaryEnabled` in the spell apply path; palette `view.togglePersonalDictionary`)) + **Ignore** when over a misspelling. **Technical-terms dictionary**: a bundled list of common programming/web/data/devops words that standard prose dictionaries flag (`config`, `async`, `middleware`, `kubernetes`, …) lives in `resources/com/editora/dictionaries/technical.txt` (one lowercase term per line; `#` comments + blank lines ignored) and is loaded once via the static, cached `editor/TechnicalDictionary.words()` (same module-resource idiom as the keymap — no `module-info` opens). `SpellChecker` treats those terms as correct (a second gate beside the user words: `technicalWordsEnabled && TechnicalDictionary.contains(lower)` in `isMisspelled`), toggled by `setTechnicalWordsEnabled` ← `EditorBuffer.setTechnicalDictionaryEnabled` ← `Settings.technicalDictionary` (default **on**, schema 41→42 additive-identity) pushed in the spell apply path. **Settings → Spell Check** has an "Enable technical dictionary" checkbox above the personal-dictionary one; palette `view.toggleTechnicalDictionary` (+ `SettingsWindow.syncTechnicalDictionaryCheck`). The page also has two file links (injected via `SettingsWindow.setDictionaryActions`): "View bundled technical terms…" (`MainController.openTechnicalDictionary` opens the classpath `technical.txt` in a read-only buffer) and "Open dictionary.txt…" (`MainController.openPersonalDictionary` opens `ConfigManager.getDictionaryFile()`, creating it empty if absent). `TechnicalDictionary` loading is unit-tested (`TechnicalDictionaryTest`) (`spellHitAt` via `area.hit`). Toggle `view.toggleSpellCheck` (`Settings.spellCheck`, default on); per-file language `spell.setLanguage` (`QuickOpen` over `SpellDictionaries.available()`, persisted in `WorkspaceState.spellLanguages`, default `Settings.spellLanguage`). `SettingsWindow` also has an "Enable spell check" checkbox and a default-language `ComboBox` (friendly names via `spellLanguageName`), applied live through the standard `apply()`/`applyViewSettingsToAllBuffers` path. Syntax highlighting uses **TextMate grammars** via tm4e: `GrammarRegistry` (singleton) maps a file extension to a bundled `.tmLanguage.json` grammar under `resources/com/editora/grammars/`; `TextMateHighlighter` tokenizes the document line-by-line (carrying grammar state across lines) and maps each token's TextMate scope to a CSS class themed in `styles/syntax.css`. Files without a bundled grammar are left unstyled. `LanguageRegistry` is now only an extension→language-name resolver used by `FoldRegions`/`FoldManager` (fold strategy) and the File Information panel — it no longer does highlighting. **Grammar resources live in the `com.editora.grammars` package, which `module-info.java` must `opens ... to org.eclipse.tm4e.core`; without that, JPMS encapsulation makes tm4e's `Class.getResourceAsStream` return null at runtime (module path) and grammars silently fail to load even though classpath tests pass.** **CSV/TSV** (`.csv`/`.tsv` → language `csv`, scope `source.csv`, authored `grammars/csv.tmLanguage.json`) get a **delimiter-agnostic** grammar: quoted fields → `string` (with the `""` RFC-4180 escape), bare numeric fields → `number`, and the separators (`,`/`;`/tab/`|`) → a muted `.text.csv-delimiter` (a CSV-specific branch in `TextMateHighlighter.classify`, styled in `syntax.css`). TextMate can't count columns, so *column-position* tinting is left to a future editor overlay. The file already carries the `table` `FileIcons` glyph. The pure, toolkit-free **`csv/CsvParser`** (`detectDelimiter` — comma/semicolon/tab/pipe, auto-detected from the first non-blank line; `fieldCount`/`fieldIndexAt` — RFC-4180-quote-aware single-line field counting for the status readout; `parse` — full RFC-4180 record/field parse into `List<List<String>>`, reused by the grid preview; records end on **LF, CRLF, or a lone CR** (classic-Mac) — a bare `\r` used to be dropped as content, fusing two records (`a,b\rc,d` → `[[a,bc,d]]` vs Python csv's `[[a,b],[c,d]]`, #478); an EOL inside quotes is preserved as a multi-line field; `columnCount`; all unit-tested in `CsvParserTest` — record-separator cases verified against Python's `csv`) backs the CSV editor features: the **status bar shows a "Field N of M" segment** for `.csv`/`.tsv` buffers (`EditorBuffer.isCsv()`; computed in `StatusBar.refresh` from two cheap single-line scans — the header row for the column count and the caret's line up to the caret for the field index — negligible next to the O(n) file-size formatting already done there; hidden in Simple mode; clicking it copies the file as a Markdown table), and the command **`csv.copyAsMarkdownTable`** (`MainController.csvCopyAsMarkdownTable`) copies the whole buffer to the clipboard as a GFM table via the existing `markdown/MarkdownTable.fromCsv`. **CSV grid preview**: an IntelliJ-style **Editor/Split/Preview** view of the active `.csv`/`.tsv` buffer embedded *in the editor* — **mirroring the Markdown preview, not a tool window** (the old bottom `csvGrid` stripe + `tool.csvGrid` were retired). A CSV buffer becomes previewable (`EditorBuffer.hasPreview()` → true once the grid node is injected — the `hasCsvPreview()` gate), so the **same** floating `MarkdownViewToggle` attaches top-right and the `MarkdownViewMode` split/preview layout + per-file persistence (`WorkspaceState.markdownViewModes`, keyed by path, so a CSV path rides the same map — no new field/schema bump) are reused wholesale. The `editor` package stays free of `ui`: `EditorBuffer.setCsvPreviewNode(Node)`/`setCsvPreviewRefresh(Runnable)` inject the grid + its refresh (like `setViewModeControl`), `rebuildViewHost` renders SPLIT as `SplitPane(editor, grid)` and PREVIEW as the grid alone (the toggle overlaid via a `csvPreviewHost` StackPane), and `scheduleRenderPreview` routes a CSV buffer to `csvPreviewRefresh` on the existing debounced (250 ms) preview subscription, skipping the Markdown-only zoom/theme/scroll-sync chrome (the Markdown `previewPane`/`previewHost` are never built for a CSV buffer). The grid is `ui/CsvGridPanel`, a `TableView<List<String>>` with a **"First row is a header" toggle** (drives the column titles + the click→line mapping), a **summary/profiler line** ("N rows × M cols · P number, Q text" from the pure `csv/CsvColumns.inferTypes`, left-aligned so the toggle's top-right corner stays clear), and **double-click / Enter on a cell jumps the editor caret** to that field (`CsvParser.fieldStartOffset`; the data-row→document-line map adds 1 for the header). **`ui/CsvCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` pattern) owns **one `CsvGridPanel` per open CSV buffer** (a Node can't live in two tabs — kept in an `IdentityHashMap`, dropped on tab close via `onBufferClosed`): `ensureCsvPreview(buffer)` (mirrors `ensurePreviewControls`, and is called at the top of it + `restoreMarkdownMode`) injects or clears that buffer's grid per the feature gate, `applySupport()` re-evaluates every open buffer on each settings apply, and `rebuild(buffer)` re-parses the buffer text into *that* buffer's grid; the whole-file `CsvParser.parse` + TableView build is skipped above a 2 MB `MAX_PREVIEW_CHARS` guard (the huge-file idiom) and runs only on the debounced pulse while split/preview is showing, so there's no per-keystroke cost. Gated by `Settings.csvPreview` (default on, schema 47→48 additive; Settings → Editor → CSV checkbox; palette `view.toggleCsvGrid`). No new dependency. **The grid is editable** (the fourth slice) when the buffer is writable and its parsed rows map 1:1 to physical lines (`!CsvParser.hasMultilineField(rows)` — a quoted multi-line field disables editing, since a data row would no longer correspond to one line); then cells are `TextFieldTableCell`s and committing an edit calls `CsvCoordinator.commitCell(dataRow, field, value)`, which rebuilds only that row's physical line — fields re-quoted per RFC-4180 via the pure `CsvParser.formatRow` — and replaces exactly that paragraph with an **undoable** `area.replaceText(start, end, newLine)` (offsets from `getAbsolutePosition`); the ensuing text change fires the debounced re-parse, resyncing the grid. Editing takes the double-click / Enter gestures (a read-only grid keeps them for caret-jump), and the right-click **"Reveal in editor"** jumps in either mode. **Column headers are editable too**: each data column's header is a `.csv-grid-col-header` `Label` graphic that becomes an inline `TextField` on double-click (when editable + a header row exists) and commits the new name to the buffer's **line 0** via `commitCell(-1, field, value)` (the `dataRow == -1` header case). **Spreadsheet polish**: a leading non-editable **"#" row-number gutter** column (`.csv-grid-rownum-cell`, showing 1-based data-row numbers — so the clicked-field index is the visible column *minus one*), **AtlantaFX zebra striping** (the `striped` style class), **bold accent headers**, **numeric columns right-aligned** (via `CsvColumns.inferTypes` per column; `.csv-grid-*` rules in `app.css`), and **content-fit column widths** — each data column's `prefWidth` is sized to the widest of its cells or its header title (pure/unit-tested `CsvColumns.maxContentLengths` → `CsvGridPanel.columnWidthFor(chars)` = `chars·CHAR_PX + CELL_PADDING`, clamped `[MIN_COL_WIDTH=56, MAX_COL_WIDTH=600]` so a long value can't blow the table off-screen), computed once per rebuild, under `UNCONSTRAINED_RESIZE_POLICY` so a user can still drag to resize; the "#" gutter sizes to the largest row number's digit count. `CsvParser.formatRow`/`hasMultilineField` are unit-tested. **Right-click exports**: the grid's context menu offers **Export to PDF** / **Print** (both reuse the Markdown-table → PDF/print pipeline: `MarkdownTable.fromCsv` → `PdfExportService.exportMarkdown` / `PrintService.prepareMarkdown` + `openPrintPreview`), **Export to Excel (`.xlsx`)** (`office/XlsxWriter`, POI XSSF) and **Export to ODF spreadsheet (`.ods`)** (`office/OdsWriter`, a hand-rolled OpenDocument-spreadsheet ZIP mirroring `OdtWriter` — `mimetype` STORED first + `content.xml` + manifest, no ODF-Toolkit dep). Both spreadsheet writers write a cell as a number only when the pure/unit-tested **`office/CsvValues.numericValue`** judges it safe — a leading-zero code (`007`, a ZIP `07030`) or a thousands-separated value (`1,960`) stays text so Excel/Calc don't corrupt it — and bold the header row. The four exports go through `CsvGridPanel.ExportActions` → `CsvCoordinator` → `MainController` (FileChooser + off-thread `OfficeExportService.exportXlsx/exportOds` / `pdfService`/`printService`); each is also a palette command (`csv.exportPdf`/`csv.print`/`csv.exportExcel`/`csv.exportOds`). `OdsWriter.contentXml` + `CsvValues` are unit-tested; POI is the existing office dependency (no new one). This completes the multi-tier CSV feature (grammar/highlighting → column readout + copy → grid preview → editable grid + editable headers + polish + exports [done]). **Rainbow columns** (matching VS Code's Rainbow CSV): when `Settings.csvRainbow` is on (default), a CSV/TSV buffer's editor text is colored **per column** instead of by the `source.csv` grammar. The pure/unit-tested **`editor/CsvRainbow`** (`segments(text, delim, colors)` → `{length, code}` runs — column-index-mod-8 for a field, `DELIMITER`/`PLAIN` for separators/newlines, RFC-4180-quote-aware; `buildSpans` wraps it as RichTextFX `StyleSpans` with `.text.csv-col-<k>`/`.text.csv-delimiter` classes) drives it. `EditorBuffer.applyHighlighting` branches to `applyCsvRainbow()` (a cheap O(n) FX-thread whole-document pass on the same debounced pulse — no grammar state) when `csvRainbow && isCsv() && !heavyFile`, else falls through to the TextMate path (so a huge CSV keeps the grammar's delimiter highlighting). `EditorBuffer.setCsvRainbowEnabled` (pushed from `applyViewSettings`) re-highlights on change; eight fixed hues in `syntax.css` (`.text.csv-col-0..7`) read on both light and dark themes. Schema 48→49 additive; Settings → Editor → CSV "Rainbow columns" checkbox + palette `view.toggleCsvRainbow`. **Grid sort / filter / inconsistent-column diagnostics**: `CsvGridPanel` wraps each parsed row in a `record Row(int index, List<String> cells)` so the view order can diverge from file order while edit-commit + caret-jump still resolve back to the physical line via `Row.index`. A **filter field** in the top bar live-filters rows (lowercase substring over any cell, applied through `applyView()`), the **column context menu** sorts the focused column ascending/descending or clears the sort (numeric-aware comparator seeded by `CsvColumns.inferTypes`; the sorted header shows a ▲/▼ via `refreshHeaderArrows`), and **ragged (inconsistent-width) data rows are tinted** via a `PseudoClass RAGGED = "csv-ragged"` on a custom `TableRow` factory (`.csv-grid-table .table-row-cell:csv-ragged` in `app.css`), the summary line appending "· N inconsistent" from the pure/unit-tested `CsvColumns.expectedColumns`/`raggedRowCount`. **Column align / shrink** (Rainbow-CSV's Align/Shrink): the pure/unit-tested **`csv/CsvAlign`** (`align(text, delim)` pads every field with trailing spaces so a column's delimiters line up in a monospace editor; `shrink(text, delim)` strips that padding back to bare fields — each reversible by the other, and both trim, so `align(align(x))==align(x)` and `shrink(align(x))==shrink(x)`). Both operate line-by-line via the quote-preserving `splitFieldsRaw` (keeps quotes/`""` escapes, unlike `CsvParser.parse`), leave blank lines + a trailing newline intact, and measure widths in chars. `MainController.csvAlign`/`csvShrink` → `csvReformat(align)` guard on `isCsv()` + `activeEditable()`, detect the delimiter, **refuse when `CsvParser.hasMultilineField`** (a wrapped record would split across lines — reports `status.csv.multiline`), then whole-document `area.replaceText` (undoable); a no-op transform reports "already aligned"/"nothing to remove". Palette-only commands `csv.align`/`csv.shrink` (no keybinding). *Deferred: delimiter/encoding pickers, editing multi-line-field files.*
