- `snippet/` — VS Code/TextMate **snippets**. `SnippetParser` (pure/unit-tested) parses a body into a `ParsedSnippet` (literal `text` + `TabStop`s with relative offset ranges): `$1`/`${1:default}`/`$0`, mirrors (repeated number), `${1|a,b|}` choices (captured per stop; `SnippetSession` shows a `ContextMenu` dropdown when the field is entered, first option is the default text; the dropdown is driven by the same chords as autocomplete — `C-n`/`C-p` move (= Down/Up), `Tab` accepts (= Enter), `C-g` cancels, via a `KEY_PRESSED` filter on the popup scene that re-dispatches to the menu's native handler (`installChoiceKeys`/`redispatch`)), `$VAR`/`${VAR:default}` resolved by `VariableResolver` (`TM_FILENAME`/`TM_FILENAME_BASE`/`TM_DIRECTORY`/`TM_FILEPATH`, selection, `CLIPBOARD`, date/time, line vars), `\$ \} \\` escapes; transforms `${1/re/fmt/}` are parsed-and-ignored. `SnippetManager` loads bundled `resources/com/editora/snippets/<lang>.json` + `global.json` and user `<configDir>/snippets/<lang>.json` (user overrides bundled by prefix; language overrides global), cached until `reload()`. **Bundled snippets cover 21 languages** (the languages added later for their LSP — PHP, Lua, Dockerfile, Terraform, TOML — have highlighting + folding but no bundled snippet yet) — 15 vendored unmodified from the MIT [friendly-snippets](https://github.com/rafamadriz/friendly-snippets) collection (attributed in `NOTICE`), the other 6 (xml/batchfile/groovy/json/yaml/ini) + `global` written for Editora. The Jackson reader is **lenient for real-world VS Code files**: `FAIL_ON_UNKNOWN_PROPERTIES=false` (ignores `scope`), and `prefix`/`body`/`description` each accept a string *or* an array (array `prefix` registers every trigger). **No `module-info` opens needed for the resources** — our own code reads them via `getResourceAsStream` (same module), like the keymap; only the Jackson DTO needs `opens com.editora.snippet to com.fasterxml.jackson.databind`. `SnippetSession` (in `editor`, bound to the `CodeArea`) inserts the expansion (re-indenting continuation lines to the caret's indent), tracks absolute field ranges through edits via a `plainTextChanges` subscription using the pure `SnippetSession.shift(...)`/`reindent(...)` (mirror of `BookmarkManager.shift`), mirrors the active field live (an `applying` reentrancy guard), and steps stops with Tab/Shift-Tab to `$0`; `$0` is tracked as a shifting range so it lands correctly after earlier-field edits. **A typed edit into a mirrored field is one undo unit (#415):** `SnippetSession.replaceInActiveField(from,to,replacement)` — called from an `EditorBuffer` `KEY_TYPED` filter for a printable char when the active field has ≥2 occurrences — reconstructs the whole span from the first to the last occurrence (each occurrence → the field's new text, literals between copied verbatim) and applies it as **one** `area.replaceText`, so a single Ctrl-Z reverts the field + all its mirrors together instead of the old half-reverted `x = ;`; ranges are then re-derived with the same pure `shift` arithmetic. (A single `replaceText` is used, not `createMultiChange`, because the fork's `MultiChangeBuilder.replaceMulti` applies its replacements sequentially against the progressively-edited document — finicky about order — whereas the span reconstruction is trivially one change.) `onChange` also cancels the session when `area.getUndoManager().isPerformingAction()` (an undo/redo is rewriting the document), so a revert leaves the document consistent and never fires a re-entrant mirror mid-undo. A non-mirrored field — or a newline/paste/other path — falls through to the normal insert + reactive `mirrorActive`, already one undo unit when there's nothing to mirror. *(Deferred: making the session **survive** an undo with its ranges intact — it currently ends cleanly on undo; a merged multi-char undo makes correct range restoration hard.)* `EditorBuffer` holds the session, installs `addSnippetKeys` (Tab/Shift-Tab/Escape filter on `area`/`area2`, only consuming Tab when a session is active or a prefix matched — else indent). **`expandPrefixAtCaret` tries the whole non-whitespace token before the identifier run** (bounded by `MAX_SNIPPET_PREFIX`), because plenty of prefixes aren't identifiers — `#inc`/`#ifndef` (c/cpp), `!` (the emmet html skeleton), `?xml`, `---` (yaml), `->` (ruby), `[PSCustomObject]`; scanning back over `[A-Za-z0-9_]` only, it looked up "inc" at `#inc` and left **42 bundled snippets** unreachable from the keyboard. The identifier fallback keeps every previously-working expansion. *(The completion **popup** now matches snippets on the wide token too, so a `#inc`-style snippet surfaces in the popup, not only via Tab (#446): `updateCompletion` computes the identifier `prefix` (for words/LSP) **and** the wider `snippetTokenStart`→`wideToken` (for snippets), passes both to `CompletionEngine.complete(snippetLang, dictLang, prefix, snippetPrefix, prose)` — snippets match `snippetPrefix`, words/keywords match `prefix` — and when `wideStart < identifierStart` stamps a `ReplaceStart` (`a.offsetToPosition(wideStart)`) on the snippet-kind items so `acceptCompletion` replaces `[wideStart‥caret]` (the whole `#inc`, never `##include`). Pure-symbol snippets with no identifier part (`!`, `->`) stay Tab-only — their identifier prefix is empty, gated by `MIN_PREFIX`. **LSP completion accept also honors a replace range**: `Completion` carries an optional `ReplaceStart` (the LSP `textEdit.range.start`, populated by `CompletionMapper.replaceStartOf`), and `acceptCompletion` replaces `[ReplaceStart‥caret]` when present; for an `insertText`-only item whose insert begins with the non-identifier trigger the identifier walk stopped at (phpactor's `$`, shell vars) it consumes the pure `CompletionEngine.prefixOverlap` so accepting `$user` after typing `$` yields `$user`, not `$$user` — #445.)*, and gets the lookup via an injected `setSnippetProvider` (decoupled from `SnippetManager`, like `setGutterBlameClick`). Commands `snippets.insert` (`C-c i`, `QuickOpen` picker), `snippets.reload`, `snippets.editUser`. **Settings → Snippets management UI** (`SettingsWindow.snippetsEditor`, injected `setSnippetManager`): a master-detail page — an editable language picker (`global` + the bundled languages + any existing user languages), the snippets for that language on the left, and a name/trigger/description/body form on the right. The list is the **merged** view: the **bundled (shipped) snippets** (`SnippetManager.bundledSnippets(lang)` reads only the classpath resource) shown read-only with a `(bundled)` tag, with any **user file entries overriding** the bundled one of the same name + net-new user snippets appended (`mergedSnippetsForCurrentLang` rebuilds the `snippetUserNames` set of writable names). Editing a bundled snippet flips it to a user override (its name joins `snippetUserNames`, the tag drops); `saveSnippets` writes **only** user-owned names via `SnippetManager.saveUserSnippets(lang, list)` (`<configDir>/snippets/<lang>.json`, VS Code shape, atomic temp+move, then cache clear) — the shipped snippets are never copied into the user file. Add appends a new user snippet; Remove (disabled for a pristine bundled row) deletes a user entry/override and re-derives (a removed override reverts to its bundled snippet). `SnippetManager.userSnippets`/`userSnippetLanguages` also back the page; palette `snippets.manage` opens Settings focused there (`showSnippets`).
- `template/` — **File Templates** (always-on; "New File From Template"). A thin layer over the snippet engine: substitution is exactly `${var}`/`${var:default}`/`$0`, so the engine reuses `SnippetParser`. **`Template`/`TemplateFile`** are pure model records — a template is single-file (`fileName` pattern + `body`) or multi-file (`files:[{path,body}]`). **`TemplateRegistry(ConfigManager)`** mirrors `SnippetManager`: bundled `resources/com/editora/templates/<id>.json` enumerated by a bundled `index.json` (a classpath/JAR dir can't be listed) + user `<configDir>/templates/*.json` (user id overrides bundled), lenient Jackson DTO (string-or-array bodies), cached until `reload()`. Bundled: `java-class`/`java-compact`/`html-page`/`markdown-doc`/`python-script`/`shell-script`/`zsh-script` (single) + `html-bundle` (multi). **`TemplateVariableResolver implements SnippetParser.Variables`** (pure, fixed-clock): wizard answers → template built-ins (`author` from `Settings.getAuthorName()` defaulting to the OS user, `projectName`, `packageName`, `fileName`/`baseName`/`extension` — **null when no file name so a `${baseName:default}` falls back**, `date`/`year`/`time`) → a wrapped `VariableResolver` (TM_/CURRENT_/SELECTION/CLIPBOARD) → null; the static `isBuiltIn(name)` is shared with discovery. **`TemplateEngine`** (pure, unit-tested): `discoverVariables(...)` (the named, non-built-in vars to prompt for, with their defaults), **`discoverVariablesForNewFile(fileNamePattern, body…)`** (same, but a file-identity built-in — `fileName`/`baseName`/`extension` — used **in the file-name pattern** *is* prompted, since there's no source file to derive it from when creating a new file; the same name used only in the body stays auto-derived — this is why `${baseName:Main}.java` now asks for the name instead of silently using its default; the answer feeds both the file-name expansion and the body because the resolver checks wizard answers before its built-ins), `substitute(body, vars)` (**rewrites `${cursor}` → `$0`** then `SnippetParser.parse`), `expand(pattern, vars)` (file names; it also **collapses a doubled trailing extension** via the pure `collapseDuplicateExtension` — `${baseName:document}.md` + a user `baseName` that already ends in `.md` would otherwise yield `x.md.md`; only *identical* adjacent extensions collapse, so `types.d.ts`/`foo.tar.gz`/`app.min.js` are left alone, and only the final path segment is touched), `resolveTargetPath(dir, pattern, vars)` (mandatory `startsWith(dir)` traversal guard). **Flow** (UI in `MainController`): a `QuickOpen<Template>` picker → an `OverlayInput` wizard (one field per discovered var, pre-filled with defaults) → apply. The **untitled-buffer path** (`template.new`, single-file) creates an `EditorBuffer`, `setDisplayName(fileName)`, and `EditorBuffer.applyTemplate(parsed)` starts a `SnippetSession` over `[0,0)` honoring `${cursor}` + any `$1…` stops (path null → Save = Save-As). The **write-to-disk path** (`template.newInFolder`, the ProjectPanel folder right-click `New From Template…`, and any multi-file) substitutes each file, guards the path, refuses to overwrite, `Files.writeString`s, opens the primary (first `files[]` entry) and sets the caret to the captured `$0` offset (`SnippetSession` needs a live area, so disk files honor only the final `${cursor}`, not other stops). Commands `template.new` (`C-c C-n` + toolbar `Icons.fileSheet()` + palette), `template.newInFolder`, `template.reload`, `template.editUser`; `Settings.authorName` (Settings → Application → Templates; schema 17→18 additive-identity). **Settings → Templates management UI** (`SettingsWindow.templatesEditor`, injected `setTemplateRegistry`, mirrors the Snippets page): a master-detail list = `TemplateRegistry.bundledTemplates()` (read-only, `(bundled)` tag) overridden by `userTemplates()` of the same id + net-new user templates (`mergedTemplates` rebuilds the `templateUserIds` set of writable ids). The form edits id/name/description/language/fileName/body; editing a bundled template flips it to a user override and `TemplateRegistry.saveUserTemplate(t)` writes `<configDir>/templates/<id>.json` (one file per id, atomic temp+move, cache cleared). Add appends a user template; Remove (disabled for a pristine bundled row) `deleteUserTemplate(id)`s and re-derives. **Multi-file templates are display-only** in the form (a note points to `template.editUser`). Palette `template.manage` opens Settings focused there (`showTemplates`). `module-info` `opens com.editora.template to com.fasterxml.jackson.databind`. **No new dependency.** *Deferred: project (whole-tree) templates, downloadable/plugin packs, string transforms — the two-source registry generalizes to N sources.*
- `completion/` — **autocomplete**. Source-agnostic core (pure, unit-tested): `Completion` (record: `label`/`insert`/`Kind {SNIPPET, WORD}`/`detail`/nullable `Snippet`), and `CompletionEngine.complete(snippetLang, dictLang, prefix, prose)` which merges sources, de-dupes by `insert` (snippet wins), ranks (exact-case prefix first, then "very close" matches — the prefix plus at most one char — then alphabetical; snippets ahead of words) and caps at `MAX` (12). **`rankCompare` must stay antisymmetric** — deciding the very-close tier from one operand made it self-contradictory, so the ranking depended on the snippet file's declaration order (and a ≥32 same-prefix run risked TimSort's contract `IllegalArgumentException`); won't trigger below `MIN_PREFIX` (2). Two sources: **snippets** — `CompletionEngine.snippetCompletions(...)` filters `SnippetManager.forLanguage(lang)` to prefix matches; accepting one starts a full `SnippetSession` (tab stops) rather than inserting literal text. **dictionary words** (prose buffers only) — `DictionaryWords` parses the bundled Hunspell `.dic` base word list (same `resources/com/editora/dictionaries/<id>/index.dic` the spell checker uses — **no new resources**), **off-thread + cached** per language (mirrors `SpellDictionaries.ensureBuilt`), into a sorted `String[]`; `startingWith(...)` is a case-insensitive binary-search range merged with the user dictionary. Pure `parseDic`/`matchPrefix`/`sortedUnique` are unit-tested. **Two presentations**: **code** buffers use the popup `editor/CompletionPopup` (a **focus-less** `Popup` + `ListView<Completion>`, caret-anchored, styled `.completion-*` in `app.css`; kept in `editor` so the package stays independent of `ui`) — ↑/↓ move, **Enter/Tab accept**, Esc/caret-move dismiss. **Prose** buffers (`isProse()`) instead use **inline "ghost text"**: a muted, mouse-transparent, unmanaged `Label` (`.completion-ghost`) added to the view's `root`/`root2` AnchorPane and free-positioned at the caret (screen→local via `getCharacterBoundsOnScreen`), showing the single best WORD suffix; **Tab** accepts (`acceptGhost` inserts the suffix), Esc/typing/caret-move/scroll clears it. Ghost is shown only when the caret is at end-of-line content (no overlap with following text); `bestGhostSuffix` picks the first WORD completion the pure/unit-tested **`CompletionEngine.ghostSuffix(word, prefix)`** accepts — since only the *suffix* is inserted and the typed prefix is kept, the word must be cased compatibly with what was typed (its own casing, `app`→`apple`, or a sentence-start capitalization, `App`→`Apple`); a case-insensitive match that appended the dictionary's tail regardless spliced `APP` + `le` into `APPle`. `EditorBuffer` wires both: injected `setCompletionProvider` (decoupled, like `setSnippetProvider`); `addCompletionKeys` is registered **last** (so its KEY_PRESSED filter runs first — handles ghost first, then the popup); `installCompletionTrigger` debounces auto-trigger via `multiPlainChanges().successionEnds(280ms)` and adds caret/scroll listeners that clear the ghost. Accept replaces `[wordStart,caret]` (popup) or inserts the suffix at the caret (ghost); a snippet completion starts a `SnippetSession`. **For an LSP item the accept honors the server's replace range** (`Completion.ReplaceStart` = the `textEdit.range.start`, filled by `CompletionMapper.replaceStartOf`; `acceptCompletion` replaces `[ReplaceStart‥caret]`) and, for an `insertText`-only item whose insert begins with the non-identifier trigger the walk stopped at (phpactor's `$`, shell vars), consumes the pure `CompletionEngine.prefixOverlap` — so accepting `$user` after typing `$` yields `$user`, not `$$user` (#445). **Post-accept suppression is stamped, not a boolean**: each accept (and the Tab LSP re-indent) sets `suppressCompletionAtVersion = docVersion` *after* its edit, and `updateCompletion` skips a non-manual pass while `docVersion == suppressCompletionAtVersion` — so the trigger the accept's own edit schedules is swallowed but the user's next edit re-enables it. A plain flag cleared in `Platform.runLater` (the previous shape) was useless: it dropped ~264 ms before the debounce it gated, so accepting a word instantly re-offered a completion on it. **`EditorBuffer.docVersion()`** (a `long` bumped from an immediate `plainTextChanges` subscription — one `++` per edit, covering both views since they share the document) is the general "has the document moved under me" stamp for the deferred/async paths: `requestLspCompletion` drops a response whose `docVersion` changed (caret equality alone can't tell — an edit can land the caret back on the same offset), and `LspCoordinator.autoImportAccept` captures it before the `completionItem/resolve` round-trip and drops the resolved `additionalTextEdits` if the document moved (else undoing the accept mid-resolve inserts the import anyway/in the wrong place). **That guard is not enough on its own:** even with the document untouched since, those positions were computed against the document as it stood *before* the accept, while they are applied *after* it — so a multi-line accepted insert (a snippet, or an `insertText` carrying newlines) has moved everything below the caret and the import lands on the wrong line, silently (#410). `acceptCompletion` therefore **measures its own edit** (the replaced range's pre-accept line/col + where that range's end sits afterwards, derived from the net length change so the snippet path is covered too) into a `pendingCompletionShift`, and the resolve callback goes through **`EditorBuffer.applyCompletionAdditionalEdits`** → the pure, unit-tested **`editor/LspEditShift.shift`**, which translates each position across that change (at-or-before the range: untouched — the common import-above-the-caret case; after it: line delta, plus the column delta when it shares the range's last line; strictly inside it: dropped, since the text it addressed is gone). `applyLspEdits` itself stays verbatim — Format Document's edits *are* computed against the current document. Inert when not editable / a snippet session is active / huge-file / toggled off. In the popup, ↑/↓ **and `C-n`/`C-p`** move the selection — while it's open the area sets the `editora.ownsKeys` property so `KeyDispatcher` leaves those editor-context chords to the popup instead of moving the caret (released on hide). **Esc or `C-g` cancels** either presentation: the popup catches both in its own filter (it owns keys); for the ghost, `C-g` (=`edit.cancel`) is routed through `MainController.cancel()` → `EditorBuffer.cancelCompletion()` (guarded by `completionShowing()`), and Esc is caught in the buffer filter. The popup is sized to exactly fit up to 9 rows (no scrollbar unless it overflows; the horizontal scrollbar is suppressed). Manual trigger = command `edit.completion` (`C-M-i`/`M-/`) → `EditorBuffer.triggerCompletion()`. Palette toggles: `view.toggleAutocomplete` (master), `view.toggleAutocompleteProse`, `view.toggleAutocompleteSnippets` (each flips the setting, re-applies, re-syncs the Settings window via `SettingsWindow.syncAutocompleteChecks()`, and reports status). Gated by `Settings.autocomplete` (master) + per-source `Settings.autocompleteProse`/`autocompleteSnippets` (Settings → Editor, all default **on**; the sub-checkboxes disable when the master is off, and more sources can be added later). `MainController.applyAutocomplete()` (mirrors `applyGitSupport`, called at init + every settings apply) pushes all three to each buffer via `EditorBuffer.setAutocomplete(enabled, prose, snippets)`; `updateCompletion` gates by source (`isProse() ? autocompleteProse : autocompleteSnippets`). **IntelliJ-style popup presentation**: the `Completion` record carries a display **`CompletionIconKind`** (in `completion/`, distinct from the behavioral `Kind`), `sortText`/`preselect`, a `deprecated` flag, and an opaque `resolveToken` (the LSP `CompletionItem`, kept as `Object` so `editor`/`completion` stay lsp4j-free). `CompletionMapper` (the only place touching lsp4j's `CompletionItemKind`/tags) populates them — `iconKindOf`, `detailText` (right column, enriched from `labelDetails.description`), `isDeprecated`. The cell renders **`editor/CompletionIcons.forKind(...)`** (a package-local glyph map mirroring `MenuIcons`/`FileIcons`, `.completion-icon`) + a `TextFlow` label whose matched runs (pure/unit-tested **`completion/MatchHighlighter.matchRanges`** — contiguous substring else camelCase subsequence; it indexes the label **directly**, folding case per char, because `toLowerCase` isn't length-preserving ("İ"→2 chars) and ranges taken from a lowercased copy drift past such a char — mis-bolding, and overrunning the label the cell substrings) get `.completion-match` (bold accent) + an ellipsized `.completion-detail`; deprecated rows strike the label. LSP results are ordered by **`CompletionEngine.sortLspByRelevance`** (preselect → `sortText` nulls-last → label; pure/unit-tested) before merging the local snippets, and the popup pre-selects the server's preselect index. **Documentation side-popup** (`editor/CompletionDocPopup`, IntelliJ "quick doc"): on selection change `EditorBuffer` debounces (~180 ms, generation-guarded) and calls the injected `setCompletionDocResolver` → `LspManager.resolveCompletionDoc(file, token, cb)` (short-circuits if the item already carries docs, else `completionItem/resolve`, delivered on the FX thread), renders the markdown (signature header from `detail` + the doc body) via `MarkdownRenderer`, and shows it to the **right** of the list (flipping left at the screen edge). It auto-shows when `Settings.completionDoc` (default on, schema 28→29) is set and **`C-q`** (`edit.completionDoc`, handled in `addCompletionKeys` while the popup owns keys; palette-discoverable) toggles it for the session; it tears down with the list (`hidePopup` + the popup's `setOnHidden`). `PAGE_UP`/`PAGE_DOWN` page the popup. **No new dependency / `module-info` change.**
- `pdf/` — **Export to PDF** via Apache **PDFBox 3.x** (`pdfbox`/`pdfbox-io`/`fontbox` are **automatic modules**; `commons-logging` 1.3.5 is a real multi-release module. `module-info` `requires org.apache.pdfbox`). **jlink/moditect (critical):** all three pdfbox-family modules log via `commons-logging`, but jdeps reports `commons-logging` "not found" (it isn't on moditect's jdeps path) and the global `--ignore-missing-deps` then **drops the `requires`** — so jlink silently prunes `commons-logging` and **all PDF export dies on the packaged build** with `NoClassDefFoundError`/`IllegalAccessError: org/apache/commons/logging/LogFactory`. So the `dist` profile gives pdfbox/pdfbox-io/fontbox **hand-written `<moduleInfoSource>`** descriptors (not jdeps-generated `<moduleInfo>`) that explicitly `requires org.apache.commons.logging` (fontbox also `requires org.apache.pdfbox.io`); the export lists come from jdeps' generated set. This was latent — packaged PDF export never worked until device-tested. Belt-and-suspenders: `PdfExportService` (and `PrintService`/`OfficeExportService`) catch **`Throwable`**, not just `Exception`, and log via j.u.l — their `exec.submit(...)` tasks otherwise swallow an `Error` into the `Future` and hang the "Exporting…"/"Preparing…" status forever with no error. Output is **light-theme** regardless of the app/editor theme and is generated **off the FX thread** on a daemon executor. `PdfExportService` (the `GitService`/`MermaidService` idiom: single `pdf-export` daemon thread + `Platform.runLater` callbacks returning a `Result{ok,message}`) has `exportCode(...)` (tokenizes off-thread via `GrammarRegistry.shared().forFileName` + `TextMateHighlighter.compute` when highlighting is on — no grammar ⇒ plain text — then `CodePdfWriter.write`) and `exportMarkdown(...)` (`MarkdownPdfWriter.write`). **`PdfTheme`** is the single Primer-Light palette: a `class→Color` `TOKEN` map mirroring `syntax.css` plus `colorFor`/`bold`/`italic` decisions for a TextMate scope-class collection. **`PdfText`** is the pure/unit-tested code-layout core: `splitIntoLineRuns(text, spans, tabSize)` → per-line styled `Run{text,color,bold,italic}` (tab-expanded, `\r`-dropped, same-style merged) and `wrap(line, maxCols)` for monospace column wrapping. **`CodePdfWriter`** embeds the four JetBrains Mono TTFs, computes char/gutter/column metrics, paginates, and draws the optional right-aligned muted line-number gutter (blank on wrapped continuations) + colored runs + a centered page number; missing glyphs degrade to `?` (`safeShowText`). **`MarkdownPdfWriter`** is a second CommonMark-AST backend beside `MarkdownRenderer` (reuses `MarkdownRenderer.parseToDocument`), emitting **native vector text** via a `Cur` cursor (embedded+subset **Inter** for prose — matching the on-screen preview on every platform, and giving full Unicode coverage WinAnsi Helvetica lacked — plus embedded JBMono for code; `Cur.embed(doc, relPath)` loads each as a `PDType0Font`): headings (sized + underline rule), inline-run paragraphs (bold/italic/`code`/links), bullet/ordered lists, block quotes, fenced/indented code blocks, thematic breaks, and GFM tables (measured columns, header shading, cell wrap, greedy `flow` wrapping with automatic page breaks). Images resolve like the FX renderer (`data:`/http/file/relative-to-`baseDir`) and embed via `PDImageXObject`; a ` ```mermaid ` block renders to a PNG through `Mermaid.renderPng` and embeds (degrades to a code block when no `mmdc` command is supplied); unfetchable images fall back to alt text — image failures never abort the PDF. Page size is `letter`/`a4` (`pageRectangle`). **Settings** (`pdfLineNumbers`/`pdfSyntaxHighlighting` default on, `pdfPageSize` default `letter`; schema 5→6 additive-identity) surface in **Settings → Editor → Export & Print** (the section is shared with printing — see `print/`). `MainController.exportCodePdf`/`exportPreviewPdf` (mirror `exportMermaid`: FileChooser `*.pdf` defaulting to `<base>.pdf`, "exporting…" status, success/error via `reportPdf`) back commands `editor.exportPdf` + `preview.exportPdf` (the preview one gated to `EditorBuffer.hasPreview()`, routing `.mmd`→`mermaidService.export` and Markdown→`pdfService.exportMarkdown` with `mmdc` only when Mermaid is enabled). ***Snapshot preview export (every preview has an Export-to-PDF):** the image/tree previews that aren't a Markdown/CSV document — **SVG** (rasterized via `PreviewImageLoader.svgToPng`), **Markwhen** timelines, and the **JSON/YAML/TOML + XML trees** — export to PDF by *snapshotting the rendered preview*. `EditorBuffer.snapshotPreviewChunks()` (FX thread) off-screen-renders the full content (the trees via `StructuredTree.printableRows`/`XmlTree.printableRows` — the whole, fully-expanded tree as flat indented `TextFlow` rows, **not** the virtualized `TreeView`, captured in bounded `ROWS_PER_CHUNK`=250 chunks / `MAX_PRINT_ROWS`=4000 so a big tree can't build a giant texture), snapshots each chunk to PNG (`PreviewImageLoader.imageToPng`), and `PdfExportService.exportImages(List<byte[]>,…)` → **`pdf/ImagePdfWriter`** scales each to page width and slices tall images across pages (pure `fitScale`/`rowsPerPage`, unit-tested; end-to-end `PreviewSnapshotPdfFxTest`). `MainController.exportPreviewPdf` dispatches by type: Markdown→`exportMarkdown`, Mermaid→`mermaid.exportDiagram`, DOT/PlantUML→`diagram.exportToPath` (both were previously **mis-routed to the Markdown renderer**), SVG/Markwhen/trees→the snapshot path; the trees host their own right-click menu (`showTreePreviewContextMenu` on `structuredContentHolder`, since they aren't in `previewPane`). **The same snapshot path also drives Print** — `print/PrintService.prepareImages(List<byte[]>)` decodes the PNGs and its `Paginator` slices each across `ImageView` pages (sharing the now-`public` `ImagePdfWriter.fitScale`/`rowsPerPage`); `printPreview` dispatches by type exactly like `exportPreviewPdf` (Mermaid→`prepareMermaid`, DOT/PlantUML→`printDiagramViaImage` = CLI-render to a temp PNG → `prepareImages`, SVG/Markwhen/trees→snapshot→`prepareImages`), and the tree/Markwhen right-click menus gained a **Print** item beside Export-to-PDF. **A snapshot PDF/print is forced to a light theme** — `snapshotNodePng(node, lightUa)` sets the off-screen scene's user-agent stylesheet to `Themes.lightUserAgentStylesheet()` (Primer Light), so the `-color-*`-based tree/timeline colors resolve to an ink-friendly light palette regardless of the app theme (Markdown/CSV stay native-vector). Deferred: headers/branding, watermarks, TOC/bookmarks, password protection, a native-vector (non-raster) tree/timeline export.*
- `office/` — **Markdown preview → MS Word (`.docx`) + OpenDocument Text (`.odt`) export.** Walks the same CommonMark AST as the PDF/preview renderers (`MarkdownRenderer.parseToDocument`) via the shared, pure, unit-tested **`InlineRun`** (`flatten(node)` → styled runs: bold/italic/strikethrough/underline/inline-code + link `href`; soft/hard breaks → `"\n"`, inline images → alt text) and **`OfficeImages`** (resolve a Markdown image to raster bytes — local-relative-to-`baseDir`, `data:` URI, or `http(s)` fetch; **SVG rasterized to PNG** via the preview's `PreviewImageLoader.svgToPng` so shields.io/GitHub badges embed; PNG/JPEG/GIF/BMP sniffing for POI type + ODT media-type/extension — plus `renderMermaid(mmdc, src)`→PNG via `mmdc` and `renderMath(latex, display)`→PNG via JLaTeXMath). Block-level `$$…$$` display math (`InlineRun.soleDisplayMath`) (which spans soft line breaks, so a multi-line `$$` block on its own lines is detected) and ` ```mermaid ` fences (`InlineRun.isMermaidInfo`) embed as images in both formats (degrading to a code block / alt text when the tool is unavailable). **Inline `$…$` math** also embeds in all three exporters: a non-code text run is split via `editor/MathSpans.segments` and each math span renders to a PNG (`OfficeImages.renderMath` / `MathImages.renderPng`) placed inline — DOCX via a picture `XWPFRun` (`DocxWriter.embedInlineMath`), ODT via an as-char `<draw:frame>` (`OdtWriter.mathFrame`; the `Embedded` `images` list is threaded through `inline`/`paragraph`/`tableXml`), PDF via an image `Word` drawn baseline-aligned in the flow (`MarkdownPdfWriter.addInlineText`/`mathWord`). Each falls back to literal `$latex$` text when render fails / math is off. **`DocxWriter`** uses Apache **POI** XWPF (headings via `Heading*` style + sized bold runs, paragraphs, bullet/ordered lists prefix-marked + indented to dodge the heavy XWPF numbering API, block quotes indented, fenced/indented code as monospace per-line paragraphs, GFM tables via `XWPFTable`, thematic breaks as bottom-bordered paragraphs, hyperlinks via `createHyperlinkRun`, and local/`data:` images via `addPicture`+`Units.toEMU`). **`OdtWriter`** is **hand-written** (a ZIP of XML via `java.util.zip` — `mimetype` STORED first, then `content.xml`/`styles.xml`/`META-INF/manifest.xml`/`Pictures/`): the pure, unit-tested **`contentXml(...)`** emits ODF (`<text:h>`/`<text:p>` with nested `<text:span>` style runs `TBold`/`TItalic`/`TStrike`/`TUnderline`/`TCode`, `<text:a>` links, `<text:list>` bullet/number `L1`/`L2`, `<table:table>`, `Preformatted_20_Text` code paragraphs with `<text:s>`/`<text:tab/>`, `Quotations`, `Horizontal_20_Line`, `<draw:frame>` images), with paragraph/heading/list styles in `styles.xml`. **ODF Toolkit (odfdom) is deliberately NOT used** — its transitive Apache **Jena** + **xercesImpl** deps break the modular/jlink build (xerces split-packages with `java.xml`), so ODT is hand-rolled with zero new deps for that half. **`OfficeExportService`** (the `PdfExportService` idiom: a single `office-export` daemon thread + `Platform.runLater` → `Result{ok,message}`) runs both off the FX thread. `MainController.exportPreviewDocx`/`exportPreviewOdt` (mirror `exportPreviewPdf`: FileChooser, "exporting…" status, success/error via `reportOffice`) back commands `preview.exportDocx`/`preview.exportOdt` (palette + the preview right-click menu, Markdown buffers only — diagrams aren't supported); wired into `EditorBuffer` via `setPreviewExportDocxHandler`/`setPreviewExportOdtHandler`. `module-info` `requires org.apache.poi.ooxml`/`org.apache.poi.poi`. **`-Pdist` jlink:** POI 5.4.x + xmlbeans + commons-compress/io/codec already ship real module descriptors and link directly; only the four automatic leaf deps — **SparseBitSet** (`com.zaxxer.sparsebitset`), **commons-math3** (`commons.math3`), **commons-collections4** (`org.apache.commons.collections4`), **curvesapi** (`com.github.virtuald.curvesapi`) — get moditect `add-module-info` descriptors (names matching POI's own `requires`). POI's optional batik/bouncycastle/santuario/xmlgraphics/pdfbox-graphics2d deps are `requires static`, so jlink doesn't pull them. **Device-tested**: the packaged macOS app image (`-Pdist`, jlink + AOT) exports a `.docx` (re-openable; 3 embedded `word/media` images) and `.odt` (mimetype-first ODF zip; 3 `Pictures/`) with the math/mermaid/badge all rendered. NOTICE updated (Apache-2.0). *Deferred: Windows/Linux dist device-test.*
- `print/` — **Printing** via **`javafx.print`** (no AWT — `java.awt.print` would throw `HeadlessException` under `App.main`'s `java.awt.headless=true` SVG guard; `javafx.print` is in `javafx.graphics`, already required, **no `module-info`/dependency change**). Mirrors the PDF feature and reuses its layout core; output is always **light**, paper size comes from the print **dialog** (not `pdfPageSize`). **Preview-first flow:** `PrintService` (the `PdfExportService` idiom: single `print` daemon thread + `Platform.runLater`) does the off-thread *prepare* and returns a **`Paginator`** (`paginate(PageLayout)→List<Node>`, a layout-agnostic recipe) inside a `Prepared{paginator,error}`: `prepareCode(...)` tokenizes off-thread (`GrammarRegistry`+`TextMateHighlighter`, null grammar ⇒ plain) → `PdfText.splitIntoLineRuns` → a paginator over `CodePrintLayout`; `prepareMarkdown(...)` off-thread `MarkdownRenderer.parseToDocument` → paginator over `MarkdownPrintLayout`; `prepareMermaid(...)` runs `Mermaid.renderPng` (mmdc) off-thread → paginator yielding a scaled `ImageView` page. The same paginator drives both the on-screen preview and the final print, so **what you preview is what prints**. The static `PrintService.printPages(pages, layout, job)` does the actual `printPage`/`endJob` on the FX thread. **`CodePrintLayout`** is the JavaFX analog of `CodePdfWriter`: reuses `PdfText.wrap` + `PdfTheme` (its `java.awt.Color`→JavaFX `Color`), builds one `VBox` of `TextFlow` rows per page (optional muted right-aligned line-number gutter), paginating by **whole lines**; pure `columns(printableWidth,charWidth)`/`linesPerPage(printableHeight,lineHeight)` are unit-tested. **`MarkdownPrintLayout`** renders the preview (light `md-light` + `app.css`/`syntax.css`), measures each top-level block offscreen (`measureBlockHeights`), and does **block-aware pagination** via the pure/unit-tested `packBlocks(heights,pageHeight)` — greedily packs whole blocks so nothing splits across a page edge; a single block taller than a page gets its own page, uniformly scaled to fit. **The measure scene is created at a definite width (`new Scene(root, pw, ph)`), *not* wrapped in a `Group`:** a `Group` shrink-wraps to its child's intrinsic width, which collapses a **percent-width table `GridPane`** to a few characters — wrapping every cell and grossly over-measuring the table's height, so even a small table got bumped to its own page (the print preview didn't match the on-screen preview). A fixed-width scene gives the columns a real width to distribute; `measureBlockHeights` is FX-harness-tested (`MarkdownPrintLayoutFxTest`). `MainController.printCode`/`printPreview` create a `PrinterJob` (no dialog yet), call the matching `prepare*` ("preparing…" status), then `openPrintPreview` opens **`ui/PrintPreview`** — a modal window showing each page on a scaled white "paper" sheet (◀/▶ navigation, "Page N of M") built via the paginator for the default page layout. Its **Print…** button shows the native `showPrintDialog(stage)`, **re-paginates for the chosen `PageLayout`** (fresh nodes — also avoids re-using preview nodes already in a scene), prints, and reports via `reportPrint`; **Close** cancels. These back **palette-only** commands `editor.print` + `preview.print` (no keybinding — `C-p` is Emacs `nav.lineUp`). Print reuses the PDF settings `pdfLineNumbers`/`pdfSyntaxHighlighting` (the relabeled **Export & Print** section); **no new Settings field, no schema bump**. *Deferred: page-setup dialog, headers/footers / page numbers on printed output, a toolbar Print button / keybinding, print-selection / custom page ranges.*
- `search/` + in-editor find — **Search**. The pure, unit-tested **`editor/SearchMatcher`** is the shared core: `matches(text, query, caseSensitive, regex, wholeWord)` → `List<int[]>` non-overlapping ranges (literal via `regionMatches`, regex via `Pattern` with `\b…\b` wrapping for whole-word; bad regex → empty, `regexError(query)` reports it) plus `nextIndex`/`indexAt` navigation. **Full (length-changing) case folding in literal mode (#444):** `regionMatches` folds *per character*, so it matches `é`↔`É` but never `ß`↔`SS` or `ﬁ`↔`FI` — a case-insensitive `STRASSE` missed `Straße`. The pure, unit-tested **`editor/CaseFold`** closes that: `mayExpand(s)` decides whether either side contains one of the 102 code points whose fold changes length (all BMP, U+00DF…U+FB17, none ASCII or supplementary — derived from the running JDK's tables on first use, not hardcoded, so a Unicode bump can't rot it), and only then does `literalMatches` take the folding path, so ordinary code pays one comparison per char and nothing more. **The fold is applied on the fly, per source code point** (`CaseFold.matchAt` walks the original text comparing against the pre-folded query) rather than by searching a folded copy: a folded copy needs the copy *plus* an index array — roughly 3× the document in transient allocation **per search**, on a path the find bar runs as you type — and then an offset map to translate back. Folding in place allocates nothing, keeps the existing O(n·m), and yields original offsets directly, which is what makes the *replace* path safe (it splices at those offsets, so an off-by-one on a `ß` corrupts the file rather than merely missing a hit). It also makes alignment free: a match consumes **whole** code points, so searching `S` can never report "half of the `SS` that `ß` folds to" — exactly the case a folded-copy offset map has to special-case. Folding is `toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT)` per code point (upper-casing is where Java exposes the length-changing mappings, and it unifies both directions since `ss`→`SS` too; ROOT keeps the Turkish dotted/dotless `i` out). **Two limits, both measured rather than assumed:** the **regex** path is deliberately *not* fixed — the issue claimed `UNICODE_CASE` already handled these, but Java's `CASE_INSENSITIVE | UNICODE_CASE` is *simple* folding, so `STRASSE` doesn't match `Straße` there either; folding the haystack would break user patterns and offsets, so it needs a different regex engine, not a flag. And the **ripgrep** backend keeps rg's own semantics (rg 14 is likewise simple-folding: `rg -i STRASSE` finds `Strasse` but not `Straße`), so Find in Files gets full folding for open buffers and the Java-walker fallback but not the rg-accelerated on-disk half. **In-file** `ui/FindReplaceBar` (top of the editor, `C-s`/`C-r`/`M-S-5`; a repeated `C-s`/`C-r` **cycles** to the next/previous match, `C-g` closes the bar; the bar's actions are also **palette commands** `find.next`/`find.previous`/`find.replaceCurrent`/`find.replaceAll`, which open the bar if it's closed) delegates to it: **incremental** (debounced 150 ms search-as-you-type), case/regex/**whole-word** toggles, a "{n} of {total}" count, and **highlight-all** via **`editor/SearchHighlightOverlay`** (a mouse-transparent `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`: amber wash on every visible match + an orange box on the active one; visible-only, coalesced, off in large-file mode; wired through `EditorBuffer.setSearchMatches`/`clearSearchMatches`). The bar takes a `Supplier<EditorBuffer>` (not just the `CodeArea`) so it can drive the overlay. **Seed from selection**: opening the bar (`FindReplaceBar.show`→`seedFromSelection`) or Find in Files (`MainController.openSearchInFiles`→`selectedLineForSearch`→`SearchPanel.setQuery`) pre-fills the query with the editor's selection when it's non-empty and on a single line (multi-line selections are left alone — they aren't sensible find terms), the VS Code convention. **Multi-file** lives in `com.editora.search`: pure **`MultiFileSearch`** (`matchesInText` → per-line 1-based `LineMatch{line,col,length,lineText}`; `replaceAll(text,query,replacement)` → spliced text + count, both unit-tested) and **`SearchService`** (the `GitService` idiom: daemon executor + generation guard) which walks the active project root (`ProjectManager.active()`, skipping dot-dirs / oversize / binary) **plus open buffers' in-memory text** (so unsaved edits win, and open files outside the root are included), capped, posting an `Outcome` on the FX thread. **Ripgrep backend (optional, auto-detected accelerator):** when `rg` is on PATH, `SearchService` runs the on-disk half of Find in Files through ripgrep instead of the Java walk — much faster and **`.gitignore`-aware** (rg's default; the walker now honors it too — see below). Pure `search/RipgrepArgs` (`SearchQuery`→flags) + `search/RipgrepOutput` (parse `rg --json`; rg's **byte** submatch offsets → Java **char** columns via `charIndexForByteOffset`, multibyte-safe; both unit-tested) + the `search/Ripgrep` facade (`command`/`detect`, the `mermaid/Mermaid` idiom). `SearchService.setBackend(useRipgrep, rgCommand, respectGitignore)` selects it; it **falls back to the walker** on an rg pattern/IO error (exit 2), a remote (non-`Vfs.isLocal`) root, or rg absent — and **open buffers always overlay** via `MultiFileSearch` (unsaved text wins, open files outside the root included). **`.gitignore` exclusion** (`Settings.searchRespectGitignore`, default **on**, schema 42→43; palette `view.toggleSearchGitignore`; Settings → Search): on ⇒ rg uses its native gitignore handling and the walker filters through the pure, unit-tested **`search/GitignoreFilter`** (parses the project-root `.gitignore` — comments, `!` negation/last-match-wins, `dir/` directory-only, root-anchored vs. base-name patterns, `*`/`**`/`?`/`[...]`; the walker `SKIP_SUBTREE`s ignored dirs like `target/`/`node_modules/` and skips ignored files like `*.log`); off ⇒ rg gets `--no-ignore` and the walker skips the filter. Reads only the root `.gitignore` (nested ones / `.git/info/exclude` are rg-only — the walker is the no-tools fallback). The **Project tool window's filter box** honors the same `Settings.searchRespectGitignore` (pushed via `MainController.applyProjectSupport` → `ProjectPanel.setRespectGitignore`, default on): its BFS filename search (`ProjectPanel.search`, unit-tested) skips `.gitignore`d files/subtrees (`target/`, `node_modules/`, `*.log`, …) via a `GitignoreFilter` loaded off-thread from the root, so the full lazy tree still shows everything but filtering hides ignored files. (Opening the Project window also focuses the filter field — `focusFirstItem` — with Down/Enter moving into / opening the results, via the shared `ui/FilterFieldNav.install(field, tree, onEnter)` bridge; the **Structure**, **Bookmarks**, and **Personal Notes** tool windows use the same helper + focus-the-filter-on-open, so all four filterable tool windows behave alike.) Gated by `Settings.ripgrepSearch` (default **on**) + `ripgrepCommand` (blank ⇒ `rg`); `MainController.applyRipgrepSupport()` (init + every settings apply, mirroring `applyMermaidSupport`) detects off-thread then `setBackend`s; **Settings → Search** page (toggle + path + found/not-found status) + palette `view.toggleRipgrep`/`search.setRipgrepCommand`; schema 36→37 additive-identity; no new dependency (rg resolved on PATH like git/mmdc). **`ui/SearchPanel`** ("Find in Files"; a `ToolWindowContent`, `tool.search` on `M-6`, `Icons::find`, registered `Side.RIGHT` — a *default* that respects each window's persisted `WorkspaceState.toolWindowSides`, so existing sessions keep BOTTOM) shows results grouped file→match (Emacs nav `C-n`/`C-p`/`C-f`/`C-b`) with a query/replace box; **`search.inFiles`** (`C-S-f`) opens+focuses it. **Selection opens the match** (mirroring `StructurePanel`): a `selectedItemProperty` listener (guarded by `suppressNavigation` during `setResults`' root swap) **previews** on single-click / keyboard selection — `Actions.openMatch(file, line, col, focusEditor=false)` jumps there but `SearchPanel.focusResults()` keeps focus in the tree so the user can keep arrowing — while **double-click / Enter activates** (`openMatch(…, true)`, focus into the editor). `MainController.openMatch` opens the path then `gotoInFile(file, line, col, focusEditor)` (the new overload only `requestFocus`es the area when `focusEditor`). **Panel extras:** a top **"Searching in:" scope row** (`.search-scope-*`, `SearchPanel.setScope(display, fullPath)`) shows the folder being searched — `MainController.searchScopeRoot()` = this window's project root, else the active file's parent folder ("Current Folder"), else null (open buffers only); home-collapsed display + full-path tooltip, pushed by `refreshSearchScope()` from `setWindowContext` / tab switch / `openSearchInFiles` / each search. That same `searchScopeRoot()` is now the scope passed to `searchService.search(...)`, so a **non-project window searches the current file's folder on disk** (previously it matched only open buffers). file-header rows are **bold** (`.search-file-row`); a **ripgrep badge** (`.search-backend-badge`, `SearchPanel.setBackendActive`, pushed from `applyRipgrepSupport`'s effective flag) shows when rg is the active backend; the query field is an **editable `ComboBox<String>`** bound to the persistent **search history** (`config/SearchHistory` → `search-history.json`, schema `ConfigSchema.SEARCH_HISTORY`, capped/deduped, most-recent-first; `Actions.recordSearch` on each run, `setHistory` binds the dropdown); and two **include/exclude glob fields** (comma-separated, parsed by pure `search/Globs.split`) flow through the widened `Actions.search(query, include, exclude)` → `SearchService.search(…, include, exclude, cb)` → ripgrep `-g`/`-g !` (`RipgrepArgs.build`) **and** the walker/open-buffer overlay (`Globs.accept` over the root-relative path, reusing `editorconfig/EditorConfigGlob.matches`). **Replace-in-files** (`MainController.replaceInFiles`): a confirm dialog, then open buffers are edited in-memory (undoable) and closed files rewritten on disk (UTF-8, EOL preserved since it lives in the text) via `MultiFileSearch.replaceAll`, then the search re-runs to refresh the panel. **Regex capture groups in replace:** in regex mode `replaceAll` routes through `Matcher.replaceAll` (shared `SearchMatcher.compileRegex`, so `$1`/`${name}` work; a bad group ref is a graceful no-op), while literal mode still splices `$` verbatim. **AceJump** (avy-goto-char): `nav.aceJump` (`M-g j`) → `EditorBuffer.startAceJump()` → **`editor/AceJumpOverlay`** takes the keys (`editora.ownsKeys` + `KEY_TYPED`/`KEY_PRESSED` filters on `area`, blocking insertion), the next typed char labels its visible occurrences with the pure/unit-tested **`editor/AceLabels`** (1-char while they fit, else uniform 2-char, capped at alphabet²), and typing a label jumps the caret; `Esc`/`C-g` (or scrolling) cancels. **Line-mode** (avy-goto-line): `nav.aceJumpLine` (`M-g L`) → `EditorBuffer.startAceJumpLine()` → `AceJumpOverlay.startLine()` labels every visible line at once (no char step) and typing a label jumps to that line's first non-whitespace character. **`M-g` closes a focused tool window** (any tool window, not just search) — a generic `KeyDispatcher` pre-dispatch hook (`setPreDispatch`) wired in `MainController.setKeyDispatcher` → `ToolWindowManager.toolWindowOf(target)` + `close` + refocus the editor. **No new dependency / `module-info` change.** The Find-in-Files window wiring lives in **`ui/SearchCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `SearchService` + the `SearchPanel`, the scope/`runFileSearch`/`replaceInFiles`/`openToggle`/selection-seed logic, and the ripgrep/walker backend selection (`applyRipgrepSupport`/`probeRipgrep`), reaching the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension for project root / open-match / tool-window toggle / open-buffer-for-path / search-history / rg-status); `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` (built with `searchCoordinator.panel()`), the search-history store, and the `search.*`/ripgrep command registrations (routing their apply through `applyRipgrepSupport`, their action through `openToggle`), and the MCP `findInFiles` bridge reuses `searchCoordinator.service()`. **Find-in-Files popup** (`search.inFilesPopup`, palette-only, no replace): a keyboard-first in-scene overlay `ui/SearchInFilesPopup` (modeled on `QuickOpen`/`CommandPalette`, shown via the shared `OverlayHost`, `editora.ownsKeys`, `Esc`/`C-g` dismiss) — a query field + case/regex/whole-word toggles (+ the same `ripgrep` backend badge as the panel, `setBackendActive` pushed from `applyRipgrepSupport` via the coordinator's `applyBackendBadge`) + an **editable search-folder field** over a grouped file→match result `ListView` (bold file headers with a match count, indented match rows with a muted line number + preview; `.fif-*` in `app.css`). Typing runs a debounced (150 ms) search through the same `SearchService` (via `SearchCoordinator.showFindInFilesPopup` + a small `SearchInFilesPopup.Ops` for the default root / async search / open-match / history); `↑↓`/`C-n`/`C-p` move, Enter jumps to the match (a header opens the file) and closes, run queries are recorded into the shared search history. The **root field seeds** from `searchScopeRoot()` (project root in a project window, else the active file's folder) and is user-editable (`~` expanded; a blank field or a non-directory ⇒ open-buffers-only, with a "folder not found" hint when non-blank); the pure `SearchInFilesPopup.displayPath(root, file)` (unit-tested) relativizes header paths. *Deferred: search-in-selection, a replace preview/diff.*
- `todo/` — **TODO / highlight patterns** (IntelliJ-style "TODO" patterns; **on by default**, gated by `Settings.todoHighlight`). User-configurable regex patterns are highlighted everywhere they match in the editor and listed in a tool window. Pure, unit-tested core: **`TodoPattern`** (Jackson POJO `name`/`pattern`(regex)/`color`(web hex)/`caseSensitive`/`enabled`, persisted in `settings.toml` as `todoPatterns`, an array of tables — `opens com.editora.todo to jackson.databind`), **`TodoPatterns`** (`compile(list)` → `Compiled{name,color,Pattern}` skipping disabled/blank/invalid-regex; `defaults()` = the standard keyword set **TODO/FIXME/HACK/NOTE/XXX + DONE** (the mark-done state), case-sensitive `\bWORD\b`, each a distinct color; `DONE_KEYWORD`="DONE"), **`TodoScanner.scan(text, compiled)`** → `TodoMatch{start,end,line,col,lineText,patternName,color,parsed}` in document order (mirrors `MultiFileSearch.matchesInText`; matches **anywhere**, zero-length-safe). **Structured "Comment Manager" format** (IntelliJ [TODO Highlighter & Comment Manager](https://plugins.jetbrains.com/plugin/32376)): pure/unit-tested **`TodoComment.parse(lineText, kwStart, kwEnd)`** splits a match into `{keyword, tag, priority, description}` + each part's line offsets — an optional `[tag]` then optional `(priority)` (critical/high/medium/low, case-insensitive) right after the keyword (a `TODO:` colon tolerated), the rest is the description. **Two things are deliberately *not* part of the parse, because `TodoEdit.rebuild` re-emits everything after the keyword canonically and would corrupt them:** a `[label](url)` **Markdown link** is never a tag (a `]` followed by `(` breaks the tag branch — claiming it re-emitted `[label] (url)` and broke the link, on a plain Mark Done in a TODO.md), and a trailing **block-comment terminator** (`*/`, `-->`) is split off by the shared **`TodoComment.closerStart`** and re-appended by `rebuild` — it used to land in the description, so editing the description of `/* TODO: x */` emitted an unterminated comment and silently commented out the rest of the file; carried on `TodoMatch.parsed` (a back-compat `TodoMatch` ctor omits it, so it's null-safe). **`TodoColors`** (pure): the default per-priority + tag part colors; the user-configurable set is the pure/unit-tested **`TodoPartColors`** (`of(tag,critical,high,medium,low)` falling back to the `TodoColors` default for a blank field), built by `TodoCoordinator` from `Settings.todoTagColor`/`todoPriority{Critical,High,Medium,Low}Color`. **In-editor highlight**: `editor/TodoHighlightOverlay` (a mouse-transparent `Canvas` mirroring `SearchHighlightOverlay`: visible-only, coalesced, 1×1 when empty, off in large-file mode) washes **each parsed part** in its color — keyword in its pattern color, `[tag]` in the tag color (with an underline), `(priority)` in its level color — fed neutral `editor/TodoMark{start,end,colorWeb, tag/pri absolute spans + colors}` via an injected `editor/TodoMatcher` (keeps `editor` free of `todo`/`config`); `EditorBuffer.setTodoMatcher`/`setTodoHighlightEnabled` recompute on the existing debounced (300 ms) edit pulse. **`TodoService`** (the `SearchService` idiom: daemon executor + generation guard) scans the active project root (skipping dot-dirs/oversize/binary, and — when `Settings.searchRespectGitignore` is on, via `setRespectGitignore` + the shared `search/GitignoreFilter`, mirroring Find in Files — `.gitignore`d paths like `target/`/`node_modules/`) **plus open buffers' live text**, capped, posting an `Outcome` on the FX thread. **`ui/TodoPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent`; id `todo`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.todo`/`M-g o`, `Icons::todo`) is the Comment-Manager list: a **"Group by" selector** (File/Priority/Tag/Keyword, via the pure/unit-tested **`todo/TodoGrouping`** — priority groups ordered by urgency with the no-priority bucket last, tag/keyword ordered with the catch-all last, file keeps active-file-first) over a tree whose match rows render the structured parts colored in a `TextFlow` (`KEYWORD [tag] (priority) description` + a muted `— file:line`); Enter / double-click → `gotoInFile`, `C-n`/`C-p` nav; a Refresh button; auto-scoped (project root if a project is open, else open files). **Editable from the panel** (right-click a match): **Mark Done** (rewrites the keyword to `DONE`) / **Reopen** (a *submenu* of the configured keywords — mark-done overwrites the keyword and nothing records what it was, so assuming `TODO` silently downgraded every FIXME/HACK/XXX that was ever marked done and reopened; `TodoCoordinator.applyHighlight` pushes the names via `TodoPanel.setKeywords`), a **Priority** submenu (critical/high/medium/low/none), and **Edit Description…** — each rebuilds the comment line via the pure/unit-tested **`todo/TodoEdit`** (preserves the indent + comment opener, re-emits `KEYWORD [tag] (priority) description` canonically) and applies it through `TodoCoordinator.Ops.applyLineEdit` → `MainController.applyTodoLineEdit`, which opens the file, verifies the target line still matches the scan snapshot (else a status + re-scan), then replaces exactly that paragraph via an **undoable** `replaceText` (marks the buffer dirty; guarded by `activeEditable()`), and the panel re-scans. **The active file's group sorts to the top** (IDE convention) via `TodoPanel.setActiveFile(normalizedPath)`, pushed on every tab switch by `TodoCoordinator.setActiveFile` (the shared pure `ui/ActiveFileOrder`; as-walked path form to match the scan keys). A top **"Scanning in:" scope row** (`TodoPanel.setScope(display, fullPath)`, reusing the Find-in-Files `.search-scope-*` styling) shows that scope (home-collapsed + full-path tooltip; "open files only" when no project), pushed by the coordinator's `refreshScope()` from `runScan()`. **`ui/TodoCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `TodoService` + the `TodoPanel`, reaching the window via the shared host plus a small `Ops` extension for the project root / open-match / tool-window toggle / home-collapsed path): `applyHighlight()` (init + every settings apply) compiles the patterns into a `TodoMatcher` and pushes it + the on/off to every buffer (`toTodoMarks` maps scanner→marks); `runScan()` drives the panel; `refreshPanelIfOpen()` re-scans when patterns change. It registers `tool.todo` (toggle + scan), `todo.refresh`, and `todo.addPattern` (palette quick-add: name → regex prompt), and `todo.next`/`todo.previous` (`M-g ]`/`M-g [` — move the caret to the next/previous TODO match in the active file, wrapping, via `EditorBuffer.jumpToNextTodo`/`jumpToPreviousTodo` over the buffer's live `TodoMatcher` marks); `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` (built with `todoCoordinator.panel()`), calls `applyToBuffer`/`applyHighlight` from `addBuffer`/init/settings-apply, and keeps the `view.toggleTodoHighlight` command (the generic `toggleSetting`, delegating its apply to the coordinator). **Overview stripes** (IntelliJ-style, mirroring the LSP diagnostic stripes): `editor/TodoStripe` — a thin per-match stripe docked over the scrollbar (generic colored marks + click-to-jump + a line-text hover tooltip, the `DiagnosticStripe` idiom; positioned beside it via `EditorBuffer.updateTodoStripe`, shifted left by `DiagnosticStripe.WIDTH` when LSP is also active so they don't overlap) — plus **left-edge ticks on the `Minimap`** (`setTodoMarks`/`setTodoEnabled`, drawn on the left so they never clash with the right-edge diagnostics). Both are fed the same `List<TodoMark>` from `EditorBuffer.refreshTodoMarks` (so `TodoMark` carries the 0-based `line` + `lineText` alongside the offsets); inert/empty when off or huge-file. **Settings → Editor → TODO Highlighting**: an enable checkbox + a per-pattern editor (enabled / name / regex / a real **`ColorPicker`** / case + add/remove; text fields commit on Enter/blur, the picker + checkboxes immediately) + a **TODO Part Colors** section with five `ColorPicker`s (tag + the four priority levels) writing `Settings.todoTagColor`/`todoPriority*Color` live; the palette `todo.setPartColor` (pick a part → `#RRGGBB` prompt) mirrors it and re-syncs the Settings pickers. `Settings.todoHighlight` (default true) + `todoPatterns`; schema 32→33 (todoHighlight/todoPatterns), **49→50**, 55→56 (todoGroupBy), **57→58** (the five part colors) (`ConfigMigrations.growTodoDefaultKeywords` grows an existing user's `todoPatterns` to include the new HACK/NOTE/XXX/DONE defaults, keeping custom entries + never duplicating). CSS `.todo-panel`/`.todo-file-row`/`.todo-run`/`.todo-row-location`/`.todo-color-tag`/`.todo-stripe-tooltip` (the editor highlight + stripes + structured rows are inline-colored). i18n in all six catalogs (`todo.groupBy.*`/`todo.menu.*`/`todo.priority.*`). **No new dependency.** *Deferred: comment/string-only matching (TextMate-scope-aware).*
- `externaltool/` — **External Tools** (IntelliJ-style user-defined CLI commands, always available; the tool list is empty by default so it's inert until configured; **disabled in Simple UI mode**). Pure, unit-tested core: **`ExternalTool`** (Jackson POJO mirroring `todo/TodoPattern`: `name`/`command`/`arguments`/`workingDir`/`StdinSource {NONE,SELECTION,BUFFER}`/`OutputTarget {CONSOLE,REPLACE_SELECTION,REPLACE_BUFFER,INSERT_AT_CARET}`/`enabled`; static `commandIdFor(name)` → `externalTool.run.<slug>`, `slug` copied from `MacroService`), **`ToolContext`** (record captured from the active buffer: filePath/fileDir/fileName/baseName/selectedText/1-based line+column/projectFileDir/bufferText), **`ToolMacros.expand(template, ctx)`** (pure `$Name$` expander over `$FilePath$ $FileDir$ $FileName$ $FileNameWithoutExtension$ $SelectedText$ $LineNumber$ $ColumnNumber$ $ProjectFileDir$`; unknown `$X$` left literal, `$$`→`$`), **`ToolInvocation.of(tool, ctx, defaultDir)`** (argv = the **tokenized template with each token macro-expanded** — `tokenize` *then* `expand`, so one macro is always exactly one argv element; expanding first tokenized the user's own data, splitting a `$FilePath$` with a space into two args with no quoting able to fix it, and dropping an empty `$SelectedText$` entirely; workingDir = expanded or default; stdin per source; `displayCommand`). The impure **`ExternalToolService`** (the `MermaidService` idiom: single daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`) runs an invocation off-thread via **`ProcessRunner.run(workingDir,timeout,argv,env,stdin)`** — a **new stdin overload** on the single subprocess chokepoint that writes the buffer/selection to the child's stdin on a daemon thread then **closes** it (so `jq`/`wc` see EOF); 2-min `DEFAULT_TIMEOUT`. **`ui/ExternalToolPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `RunPanel` minus Stop/stdin — runs are one-shot; id `externalTool`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `Icons::tools`, `tool.externalTools`; reuses the `run-*` CSS + the package-private `RunPanel.installLinkClicks` so output paths are clickable). **`ui/ExternalToolCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern, like `HttpClientCoordinator`) owns the `ExternalToolService` + the console panel + the run/output logic + the `externalTool.*` commands, reaching the window via the shared host plus a small `Ops` extension (`projectRoot()`/`openConsole()`/`onOutputLink(link)`); `MainController` keeps only the `externalToolToolWindow` (built with `externalToolCoordinator.panel()` as content; **registered default-hidden** via `toolWindows.register(tw, false)` — the stripe is off until enabled via `tool.externalTools` / the `externalTool.run` picker / Settings → Tool Windows), its availability gating, the `tool.externalTools` toggle, and a thin `refreshExternalToolCommands()` delegate (the `WindowManager` broadcast contract). The coordinator's `buildContext()`/`defaultDir()` read the active buffer + window project; `run(tool)` → `ExternalToolService.run` → `applyResult` on the FX thread — CONSOLE opens the panel always; REPLACE_*/INSERT apply stdout **only when `r.ok() && !r.out().isEmpty()`** (mirrors `format-runner-plugin`), stripping one trailing newline for selection/caret inserts, else surfacing stderr in the panel + status; `REPLACE_BUFFER`→`area.replaceText(out)` (whole-document undoable, as `ActiveEditor.setText`), `REPLACE_SELECTION`→`replaceSelection`, `INSERT_AT_CARET`→`insertText`. **Dynamic commands** mirror the macro pattern: `registerExternalToolCommands`/`refreshExternalToolCommands` register one `externalTool.run.<slug>` per *enabled* tool (title = tool name, so it's palette- + keybinding-editor-visible and key-bindable), re-synced across windows via `WindowManager.broadcastExternalToolsChanged()` from `onSettingsApplied`. Static commands `externalTool.run` (`QuickOpen` picker), `externalTool.rerunLast`, `externalTool.clearOutput` (`ExternalToolPanel.clearConsole`), `tool.externalTools`. **Gating** = `externalToolsEnabled() = !simpleModeActive()`; the palette predicate hides `externalTool.*`/`tool.externalTools` in Simple mode and `runExternalTool` early-returns. **Persistence**: `Settings.externalTools : List<ExternalTool>` in `settings.toml` (default empty; `opens com.editora.externaltool to jackson.databind`; schema 35→36 additive-identity). **Settings → External Tools** is a **master-detail** page (left `ListView` of tool names + Add/Remove; right form: name/command/arguments/working-dir/stdin combo/output combo/enabled, localized enum `StringConverter`s + a `$Macros$` help note) reusing the `todoRow` commit idiom (combos/checkbox apply immediately, text fields on Enter/blur → `setExternalTools` + `apply()`). i18n in all six catalogs. **No new dependency.** *Deferred: live-streamed console output (v1 is one-shot capture), per-tool timeout/env, output-to-new-file, `$Prompt$`.*
- `macro/` — **keyboard macros** (Emacs-style record/replay, always on). Pure, unit-tested model + engine: **`MacroStep`** (a record `{kind,value}` with `kind ∈ command|text|**key**`; the `is*` accessors are `@JsonIgnore`d so the boolean getters don't pollute `macros.json` or break record deserialization), **`Macro`** (`name` + ordered `List<MacroStep>`), **`MacroRecorder`** (accumulates the interleaved stream; `recordCommand`/`recordChar`, consecutive chars coalesced into one TEXT step; no-op unless `start()`ed), **`MacroPlayer`** (`play(macro, times, runCommand, typeText)` dispatches each step in order N times; a single `playing` re-entrancy guard makes a self-referential / bound-to-itself macro run once, not recurse). **`MacroService`** (per-window coordinator over `ConfigManager`; depends only on config + the pure model) owns the recorder/player + the just-recorded "last" macro, exposes `start/stopRecording`, the recording hooks `onCommand`/`onTypedChar` (both short-circuit on `!isRecording()` — the idle hot path — and ignore replay), `replayLast`/`run`, `saveLast`/`saved`/`delete`, and the static `commandIdFor`/`slug`. **Capture** is three hooks fed in FX-event order so commands, typed text and bare keys interleave correctly: `CommandRegistry.setExecutionListener(Consumer<String>)` (fires after the **outermost** `run(id)` — a `runDepth` counter means a command that synchronously delegates to another via `registry.run(...)` records only what the user invoked, not the internal decomposition, and never in reverse order (#449); a command that throws is never recorded; `onCommand` ignores the `macro.*` **control** commands + `palette.show` — but **not** `macro.run.*`, which is a real action: macro composition is the point, and recursion is the player's guard's job), `KeyDispatcher.setTypedListener(Consumer<Character>)` (each real, non-consumed `KEY_TYPED` char), and **`KeyDispatcher.setKeyListener(Consumer<String>)`** — the **bare editing/navigation keys** (Backspace/Delete/arrows/Home/End/PageUp/Down), captured at `handle()`'s *unbound-key fall-through*, because the area handles them natively and **no bundled keymap binds them**, so neither other hook can see them (Backspace is 0x08, below `isRecordableChar`'s printable floor; arrows emit no `KEY_TYPED` at all) — without it a recorded macro silently omitted every Backspace and arrow. The value is a pure/unit-tested **`macro/MacroKey`** token (`BACK_SPACE`, `S-DOWN`, `C-LEFT` — modifiers ride along since the area acts on those variants too; reaching the fall-through *means* unbound, so a bound chord still goes down the command path), replayed by **`EditorBuffer.pressKey`**, which **re-dispatches a real `KEY_PRESSED` at the focused area** (the only faithful option — this behavior lives in the area's own InputMap + the Backspace filters, so there's no `apply*` to reuse as `typeChar` does). **All three hooks are gated by `KeyDispatcher.setRecordTarget(Predicate<EventTarget>)`** (→ `EditorBuffer.ownsKeyTarget`): they're **scene** filters, so they otherwise saw — and recorded — everything typed into the command palette / find bar / any picker, which replay then typed into the document. **Replay of TEXT steps** routes through **`EditorBuffer.typeChar/typeString`**, which reuses the *same* assists the live key filters use — extracted into `applyEnter` (Markdown-list/`Indenter` auto-indent), `applyAutoCloseTyped` (`AutoClose` pair/skip/wrap), `applyCloserDedent`, and `applySmartTab` — so a replayed `(` pairs and a replayed newline re-indents exactly as hand-typed (no synthetic `KeyEvent`s, which would re-enter `KeyDispatcher`). COMMAND steps replay via `registry::run`. **Persistence** is app-global `config/MacroStore` (`schemaVersion` + `List<Macro>`, `put`/`find`/`remove`) in `macros.json`, owned by `SharedConfig` (`getMacroStore`/`saveMacros`, loaded via `ConfigMigrations.readVersioned(..., ConfigSchema.MACROS)`) and delegated by `ConfigManager`; `opens com.editora.macro to com.fasterxml.jackson.databind` (the records). **Each saved macro is registered as a synthetic command `macro.run.<slug>`** (explicit title = the macro name) so it appears in the palette and the Settings → Keymaps keybinding editor and is **bindable to a key** like any command; `MainController.refreshSavedMacroCommands` drops stale `macro.run.*` then re-registers the current set, and `WindowManager.broadcastMacrosChanged()` runs it in every window after a save/delete (mirroring `broadcastSettingsApplied`). The window wiring lives in **`ui/MacroCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern): it owns the per-window `MacroService`, the capture hooks (`onCommand`/`onTypedChar`, fed from `CommandRegistry.setExecutionListener` + `KeyDispatcher.setTypedListener`), and the `macro.*` commands, reaching the window via the shared host plus a one-method `Ops` extension (`refreshAllWindows`, which needs `WindowManager`); `MainController` keeps only a thin `refreshSavedMacroCommands()` delegate (the `WindowManager` broadcast contract) + `refreshSavedMacroCommandsAllWindows()`. Commands (registered by the coordinator): `macro.startRecording` (`F3`), `macro.stopRecording` (`F4`), `macro.replayLast` (`C-x e`; auto-finalizes if still recording), plus palette-only `macro.replayLastN` (count prompt), `macro.nameAndSave`, `macro.runSaved` (`QuickOpen` picker), `macro.deleteSaved`. Status echoes via `setStatus` (`status.macro.*`). Bound only in `emacs.json` (Emacs has no `.mac` variant); i18n in all six catalogs. **No new dependency.** **Settings → Macros management page** (`SettingsWindow.macrosEditor`, `Category.MACROS` under the System group): a master-detail editor over `config.getMacroStore().macros` — list saved macros, **rename** (with keybinding migration old→new id), **edit the steps** (a `MacroStep` list with Add Command / Add Text / reorder ▲▼ / Remove + an editable value field for the selected step), **delete**, and **assign a keybinding inline** (reuses the Keymaps `ShortcutActions` rebind/reset + the shared `rebindWithConflictCheck`, capturing chords via `KeyDispatcher.chord`; binds the macro's `macro.run.<slug>` command). Persists via `config.saveMacros()` then the injected `setMacrosChangedHandler` (→ `MainController.refreshSavedMacroCommandsAllWindows`) re-registers the commands in every window. *Deferred: import/export, a persistent "● REC" status segment, scripting overlay/picker input during replay.*
- `build/` + `maven/` — **Build-tool support** (IntelliJ-style per-tool toolbar icon + actions popup + streaming console; on by default, self-gating — each tool's button stays hidden until its marker file is detected; **disabled in Simple UI mode** and for remote/SFTP files). A generic, tool-agnostic framework in **`com.editora.build`** with one instance per tool: **Maven** (`pom.xml`), **npm** (`package.json`), **Cargo** (`Cargo.toml`), **Go** (`go.mod`/`go.work`), and **Gradle** (`build.gradle[.kts]`). **Adding a tool = a new `BuildTool` enum constant + its `*ActionsProvider` + an `Icons` glyph + `Settings` fields + i18n — no `MainController`/coordinator change.**
  - **`BuildTool`** (enum, the single per-tool descriptor): id, display name, a command example (Settings prompt), marker file(s) (**no `.git` fallback** — we want the build file, not the repo root), the `view.toggle<Tool>Support` command id, `Settings` enable/command get+set accessors (`Predicate`/`Function`/`BiConsumer<Settings,…>`), an `OutputStyle`, and two abstract per-constant behaviors: **`parse(root)`** → a `Detected{BuildActionsProvider provider, String label}` (throws on a malformed marker; the coordinator distinguishes found-but-malformed from absent) and **`executable(root, isWindows, override)`** → the launch argv prefix. `BuildTool.enabled()` is the wired-in list (MAVEN, NPM, CARGO, GO, GRADLE). Maven/Gradle's executable prefers the project wrapper (`./mvnw`/`./gradlew`), else `mvn`/`gradle` — via the shared `BuildTool.wrapperArgv`, which **requires the wrapper to be `isExecutable`, not merely present** (a non-`+x` `mvnw` from a Windows clone/unzip otherwise won a preference it couldn't honor and every build died `error=13 Permission denied` instead of falling back) and hands back an **absolute** path on Windows (a bare `mvnw.cmd` is neither on PATH nor resolved against the child's working dir; `./mvnw` is kept on Unix, where the forked child chdirs before exec); npm's is the detected package manager (npm/yarn/pnpm/bun); Cargo/Go run `cargo`/`go`. Two optional default methods support a DSL tool whose task list can't be statically parsed: **`taskLoadLabel()`** (the i18n key of a "Load all tasks…" popup action, present only for Gradle) and **`loadTasks(root,…)`** (enumerates task names on a short-lived process — Gradle runs `gradle tasks --all` via `ProcessRunner`, parsed by the pure `GradleTasks`).
  - **Action model** (pure): `BuildAction.{Section, Task, Toggle}` produced by a **`BuildActionsProvider.sections(activeToggleIds)`** (re-queried on every toggle flip, so Maven can reveal a checked profile's nested goals) + **`toggleArgs(activeToggleIds)`** (extra argv, e.g. Maven's `-Pa,b`). Run argv = `executable + task.args + toggleArgs`. **`BuildExecutable.resolve(wrapperArgv, override, defaultCommand)`** is the shared executable chooser; **`OutputStyle`** classifies a console line's color (Maven reclassifies its `[INFO]`/`[ERROR]`/`BUILD …` prefixes; npm/others pass through). **`BuildService`** mirrors `run/RunService`'s streaming shape (daemon pump threads + a monotonic generation guard) keyed on an explicit working-directory `Path` (a build always runs at the marker root); one instance **per tool** so a polyglot repo can run e.g. Maven + npm at once — and they stream into **one shared tabbed "Build Output" window**, a tab per tool (see the `ui/BuildOutputPanel`/`BuildCoordinator` bullet below), not a console each.
  - **Maven** (pure `com.editora.maven`, unchanged by the generalization): **`PomModel`** (groupId/artifactId/version/packaging + top-level `List<Plugin>`/`List<Profile>`; `Execution{id,phase,goals}`; a profile holds its own `<build>/<plugins>` **not merged** into the top-level list), **`PomParser.parse/parseFile`** (JDK `javax.xml.parsers` DOM, XXE-hardened — DOCTYPE disallowed, external entities/DTD off; **not** an effective pom: no default-lifecycle bindings, `<pluginManagement>` skipped), **`MavenPluginPrefix.derive`** (Maven's CLI-prefix convention), **`MavenLifecycle.PHASES`** (the fixed clean…deploy list). **`build/MavenActionsProvider`** maps a `PomModel` into Lifecycle (a Task per phase) + Profiles (a Toggle per `<profile>`, `activeByDefault` noted) + Plugins (a Task per explicitly-bound `<execution>` goal, `<prefix>:<goal>`, phase/execution-id tooltip) + a nested per-checked-profile Plugins section; active profiles merge into `-Pa,b`.
  - **npm** (pure): **`NpmProject.parse`** (Jackson `readTree` → name + `scripts` names in order + the `packageManager` field; no POJO binding → no `module-info` `opens`), **`NpmPackageManager.detect`** (packageManager field → lockfile → `npm`, pure — the caller probes lockfiles), **`build/NpmActionsProvider`** (a Task per script `<pm> run <name>`, portable across managers, + a Common section: `install`; `ci` only for npm). No toggles.
  - **Cargo** (pure): **`CargoProject.parse`** (`TomlMapper` `readTree` → `[package] name` + `[[bin]]`/`[[example]]` target names; a virtual `[workspace]` has no package name), **`build/CargoActionsProvider`** (a Commands section of the standard subcommands, a Targets section of additive `run --bin X`/`run --example Y` — never replacing the plain `run`, and a `--release` `Toggle` whose `toggleArgs` appends `--release`).
  - **Go** (pure): **`GoProject.parse`** (a single regex over the `go.mod` `module` line → the module path label; `go.work` has none), **`build/GoActionsProvider`** (a static Commands section — `build ./...`/`test ./...`/`vet`/`fmt`/`mod tidy`/… over the whole module; no toggles).
  - **Gradle** (the DSL can't be statically parsed): **`build/GradleActionsProvider`** (a static Common section — build/clean/test/assemble/check/jar/run/bootRun — plus an All-tasks section populated on demand via the interface's **`addLoadedTasks`** hook, deduped against the common set), and the pure **`GradleTasks.parse`** (the task names out of `gradle tasks --all` output — a **whole-line name match**: a task with no description prints as a *bare name* (the norm for "Other tasks" and any `tasks.register` that sets none), so requiring `" - desc"` silently dropped them while the status echoed the undercount as success; bare section headers ("Rules", "Other tasks") are told apart by the `-----` rule Gradle underlines every header with. **The loaded tasks are cached per root in `BuildCoordinator`** and re-applied in `applyDetected` — `GRADLE.parse` builds a *fresh* provider and detect re-runs on tab switch/focus/**every save**, so a `C-s` used to throw away the ~90 s enumeration; and the load is generation-guarded like `refresh()`, without which switching projects mid-load merged one project's tasks into another's tree). The label is the marker directory's name.
  - **UI**: **`ui/BuildCoordinator`** (one per tool, the `CoordinatorHost` pattern generalized from the old `MavenCoordinator`) owns the tool's `BuildService`, streaming into its own tab of the **shared `ui/BuildOutputPanel`** "Build Output" window (a `TabPane` `ToolWindowContent` **owned by `MainController`, one for all five tools**; each tab is a per-tool **`BuildToolPanel`** console — a `VBox` modeled on `RunPanel` minus stdin, reusing the `run.*` CSS/i18n). **Console keyboard scrolling** rides the shared **`ui/ConsoleNav`** — the `CodeArea` analogue of `command/TextInputKeymap`, installed on the Build Output, Run, External Tools and Debug consoles: these panels mark themselves `editora.ownsKeys`, so `KeyDispatcher` deliberately leaves every `nav.*`/`edit.*` chord to the focused panel (`isEditorContext`) — but a console had nothing to hand them to, so the configured scroll chords (Emacs `C-n`/`C-p`, `C-v`/`M-v`, `M-<`/`M->`) were silently swallowed and only the raw arrows/PageUp/PageDown RichTextFX handles natively worked. A `KEY_PRESSED` filter (ahead of RichTextFX's own InputMap) rebuilds the dispatcher's chord token, resolves it through the shared `KeymapManager` (`TextInputKeymap.sharedKeymap()`), and runs the motion + `requestFollowCaret()`; only **single-key** chords resolve (a console has no use for `C-x …` prefixes) and an unmapped key falls through untouched, so native arrows and mouse selection are unaffected. Motions are **caret moves**, not raw scrolling, so selection/copy stay coherent — a console that hides its caret still scrolls, since `requestFollowCaret` moves the viewport either way. **Auto-follow is conditional**: RichTextFX's `appendText` always leaves the caret at the end, so each panel captures the caret *before* appending and `ConsoleNav.afterAppend(console, caretBefore, follow, maxChars)` (shared trim + follow-or-restore tail) either scrolls to the new end or puts the caret back where the user left it — without which scrolling back through a *running* build was useless, the next output line yanking the view to the tail again. `BuildOutputPanel` is **owner-routed**: `started(owner, toolName, header, style, onStop)` lazily creates the tool's tab (titled `toolName`) + selects it, and `appendOutput`/`finished`/`failed(owner, …)` route to that owner's console — so two concurrent builds stream into separate tabs without interleaving;
