tabs persist for the session (bounded, ≤5) so finished output stays readable) + the primary **`BuildActionsTree`** (an IntelliJ-style `ToolWindowContent`: a mini icon toolbar — Run selected / Reload / Stop / Run custom…, plus Gradle's "Load all tasks…" — over a `TreeView` of the provider's sections; a `Task` is a runnable leaf (double-click / Enter / the Run button), a `Toggle` is a checkbox leaf that re-queries `provider.sections(active)` so a checked toggle reveals extra rows and contributes `toggleArgs`; `.build-tasks-*` CSS) + a searchable **`BuildActionsPopup`** kept for the command palette (`<id>.showActions`, shown **centered** via `OverlayHost.show(content, true, …)` now that there's no toolbar button; checkable toggles, a "Run custom…" row, and the same Gradle secondary "Load all tasks…" — the coordinator runs `tool.loadTasks(...)` off-thread, then `provider.addLoadedTasks(...)` once and re-renders **both** the tree (`refreshFromProvider()`) and the popup (`rerender()`)). `contextPath()` picks the active local file else the project root; `refresh()` walks up via `lsp/RootResolver.findMarkerRoot(context, tool.markers(), /*filesOnly*/ true)` and parses off-thread (generation-guarded) — **`filesOnly`** matches a marker only as a regular *file*, since every build marker is a file (`pom.xml`/`package.json`/`go.mod`/…), so a *directory* merely named like one up the tree must not root the tool there (it would then fail to parse and show a bogus "can't read the build file" error); the 2-arg `findMarkerRoot` (files-or-dirs) is kept for LSP callers whose markers include real directories (`.git`/`.terraform`) (#451). Then `applyDetected` pushes the provider into the tree (`tree.setProvider`) and flips the **tasks-tree stripe's availability** (`Ops.setToolWindowsAvailable`, which also re-derives the **shared console's** availability from `MainController.anyBuildDetected()` — an OR across all tools) on the same cadence as Git (startup, tab switch, focus-regain, save, every settings apply). Strings are **generic** (`status.build.*`/`buildpopup.*`/`buildtree.*`/`dialog.buildCustom.*` parameterized by the tool's display name; Maven's provider keeps `mavenpopup.lifecycle/profiles/plugins/…`), so the coordinator has no per-tool code. Registers per-tool `tool.<id>` (opens the **tasks** window) + `<id>.showActions/runCustom/stop/rerunLast/refresh`. **`MainController`** holds `List<BuildCoordinator>` + one `Map<BuildTool,ToolWindow>` (the per-tool **tasks** windows, `register(tw, true)` then `setAvailable(false)` — stripe appears when the marker is detected) **plus a single shared Build Output console** (`buildOutputPanel`/`buildOutputToolWindow`, id `buildOutput`, `register(false)` default-hidden, `Icons::terminal`, title `toolwindow.buildOutput` = "Build Output", auto-opens on a run, available once any tool is detected; its `tool.buildOutput` toggle command is registered once by `MainController`, not per tool). Refresh/overlay/shutdown/`view.toggle<Tool>Support` iterate the coordinator list; the console font is set once on the shared panel. There is **no** longer a per-tool main-toolbar button (the FXML `buildToolsSeparator` + `setupBuildToolButtons` were removed). The palette gate hides `tool.<id>` + `<id>.*` for a disabled tool (the shared `tool.buildOutput` isn't tool-scoped, so it's not gated).
  - **Workspace trust (#412)**: a build tool may launch a script the **repository** supplies — Maven's `./mvnw`, Gradle's `./gradlew` — as `argv[0]`, so a malicious repo ships a trojaned wrapper and the first build hands it code execution with the user's privileges (the `npm run dev` → repo-controlled devDependency class). **`BuildTool.repoWrapper(root, isWindows)`** is the single source of truth for "would this run repo-controlled code?": it shares `wrapperFile(...)` with `wrapperArgv`, so a non-null result is **exactly** the case where `BuildExecutable.resolve` prefers the wrapper — which it does even over a Settings command override, so an override must not silently disarm the gate (`BuildToolRepoWrapperTest` pins that agreement). Only MAVEN/GRADLE override it; every other tool returns null and is never gated, so the common path costs one `Files.isRegularFile`. **`BuildCoordinator.allowRun(root)`** gates on it: no wrapper ⇒ straight through; wrapper + untrusted ⇒ the modal `Ops.confirmTrust` prompt (implemented by `MainController.confirmTrustFolder`, the `confirmEnableMcp`/`confirmEnablePlugin` shape, default button Cancel so dismissing never grants trust) ⇒ `Ops.trust` persists it. The prompt lives on `Ops`, not in the coordinator, so the FX test can answer it without a real dialog. **Two gates are required, not one:** `launch(...)` **and** `loadAllTasks()` — Gradle's "Load all tasks…" runs `./gradlew tasks --all` through `BuildTool.loadTasks` on its own thread, bypassing `launch` entirely. Declining **does not fall back to the PATH `mvn`/`gradle`**: a hostile `pom.xml`/`build.gradle` executes code through those too (build plugins and Gradle scripts run in-process), so "no" has to mean no build rather than a quieter one. Trust lives in **`config/TrustStore`** (`trusted-folders.json`, `ConfigSchema.TRUST`; keys are `PathKeys.canonical` symlink-resolved absolute paths) and is **inherited by subfolders** (VS Code semantics — a multi-module repo asks once), with containment decided on `Path` components, never key strings (`~/src/app2` must not inherit `~/src/app`'s trust). Untrusted is the default *and* the failure mode: `readVersioned` fails open to defaults, which here means nothing trusted. Revocation is Settings → Workspace → **Trusted Folders** (list + Remove/Remove All, injected via `SettingsWindow.TrustActions`) plus the palette `workspace.manageTrust`/`workspace.revokeTrust` — the latter reports "still trusted through a parent folder" rather than claiming a revoke an ancestor entry still overrides. **No new dependency / `module-info` change.** *Deferred: the broader surface — `mvn`/`gradle`/`make`/`npm run` on a hostile build file are repo-controlled **content** even when `argv[0]` is the user's own tool; gating those means trusting a folder for any build at all, a much larger behavior change than #412 scoped. Run/Debug are unaffected: `RunCoordinator.buildRunCommand` always emits a PATH interpreter (`java`/`python3`/`bash`/`make`) as `argv[0]`.*
  - **Settings/gating**: a `<tool>Support`/`<tool>Command` pair per tool (`maven`/`npm`/`cargo`/`go`/`gradle`, all default **true**, inert until the marker is found; schema 65→69 additive — one identity step per new pair). A **data-driven** Settings → Languages & Tools → **Build Tools** page (one section per `BuildTool.enabled()`: enable checkbox + command-override field + a found/not-found status reading the coordinator's cached detection — no subprocess probe). Palette gating is generic: `Chrome.PaletteGates.disabledBuildToolIds` (a `Set<String>`) hides any `<id>.`/`tool.<id>` command whose tool is off, so future tools need no `Chrome` change. Stripe glyphs: Maven feather + npm from Simple Icons (CC0), and Cargo/Go/Gradle from Material Design Icons (Apache-2.0) — box/running-figure/layers (both in NOTICE). *(The original Simple-Icons Cargo/Go/Gradle brand logos were dropped: their SVGO-compact **packed elliptical-arc flags** — e.g. `a1 1 0 000-.5` — fail JavaFX's stricter `SVGPath` parser ("invalid boolean flag"), so they rendered blank. `IconsFxTest` guards that every build-tool glyph parses to a non-empty shape.)* **No new dependency / `module-info` change** (Cargo rides the existing `TomlMapper`, Go/Gradle are a regex + static lists; Maven keeps `requires java.xml`). *Deferred: full effective-pom resolution (default-lifecycle bindings, parent inheritance, `<pluginManagement>`); a Cargo `--release`-only subset (the global toggle can combine with `fmt`/`update`); a per-root cache for Gradle's loaded tasks; a persistent run-configuration list; clickable console links stay Maven/JVM-only.*
- `git/` — **native-CLI Git integration** (no JGit; we shell out to the user's `git`). `ProcessRunner` is the *only* place Editora runs a subprocess: `ProcessBuilder` + concurrent stdout/stderr drainers (**both** on side threads — draining stdout inline on the caller made the timeout *unreachable*, since `waitFor(timeout)` only ran once the drain hit EOF, i.e. once the child had already exited) + a hard timeout (`killTree` on expiry) + a 10 MB capture cap. **When there's no stdin to feed, the child's stdin is closed anyway** — otherwise anything that reads it (`grep`/`jq`/`sort`) blocks on input that can never come, never exits, never closes stdout, and wedges the caller forever, `LC_ALL=C` and `GIT_OPTIONAL_LOCKS=0` for stable parsing and lock-free status. `GitService` is the facade: every command runs on a single daemon executor (the `highlightExecutor` idiom) and posts results to the FX thread via `Platform.runLater`; `git --version` presence and `rev-parse --show-toplevel` repo roots are cached, and `refresh(contextPath, diffFile, cb)` (status `--porcelain=v2 --branch` + `diff -U0 HEAD -- file`) carries a generation guard so stale results are dropped. Two **pure, unit-tested** parsers feed the UI: `StatusParser` (porcelain-v2 → `GitStatus`{branch, upstream, ahead/behind, `FileEntry`s with porcelain index/worktree letters + rename `origPath`}) and `DiffParser` (hunk headers → `LineChange`{0-based startLine, count, `ChangeType` ADDED/MODIFIED/DELETED}; pure-insertion `b==0`→ADDED, pure-deletion `d==0`→a single DELETED marker on the following line, else MODIFIED — a v1 approximation). **`ChangeType.cssClass()`** maps to `git-added`/`git-modified`/`git-deleted`. *Caution:* a static `Path.of(...)` sentinel must not contain a NUL — `NO_ROOT = Path.of("")` (empty path, never returned by rev-parse, compared by identity). **Gutter change bars** (in `editor/`): `EditorBuffer.setChangeBars(Map<line,cssClass>, Map<line,hunkText>)` stores both maps (null = not tracked) and `FoldManager` (via `setChangeHook(enabled, classFor, tooltipFor)`) reserves a fixed `CHANGE_SLOT_WIDTH` stripe at the gutter's inner edge on every row while tracking is on (so a bar appearing/vanishing never shifts text indent), repainting only changed lines (`recreateParagraphGraphic`); colors are AtlantaFX semantic (`.git-change-bar.git-*` in `app.css`), off in large-file mode. **Hovering a change bar** shows that hunk's unified diff (the `-`/`+` lines) in a monospace `.git-diff-tooltip` — the per-line hunk text comes from `DiffParser.parseToHunkText` (pure, unit-tested; same `git diff -U0 HEAD` output that feeds the bars) carried on `GitService.GitDiff`/`RepoState.hunks`. **UI**: `StatusBar.setGitBranch(branch, ahead, behind)` shows a clickable `⎇ branch ↑a↓b` segment (`git.switchBranch`) **only when the active file is inside a repo** — a null/blank branch hides the segment entirely (centralized in `StatusBar.applyGitVisibility`: visible iff `gitFeatureEnabled && gitInRepo && !simpleMode`, so it's gone for files outside any repo and on the no-file Welcome tab). To keep that accurate per active file, `MainController.refreshGit()` short-circuits to `RepoState.NONE` when `gitContextPath()` is null (no file + no project), instead of falling back to the process working directory's repo. The **Commit** tool window is shown only inside a repo via **`ToolWindowManager.setAvailable(tw, inRepo)`** — a *transient* hide (distinct from the persisted `setVisible`; guarded by `shouldShowButton = isVisible && !unavailable`) so it never clobbers the user's show/hide preference; driven from `applyGitState`. The Commit + Git Log setters (`setCommitWindowAvailable`/`setGitLogWindowAvailable`) additionally **`&& activeBuffer() != null`**, and `updateBufferToolWindows()` force-hides both on a non-buffer tab — they act on the active file, so they vanish on the Welcome tab even inside a repo. `GitPanel` (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `BookmarksPanel`) groups Staged/Changes/Untracked with stage/unstage/discard + a commit box (Ctrl/Cmd+Enter), routing mutations through an `Actions` callback. The whole integration is **gated by `Settings.gitSupport`** ("Enable Git", Settings → Git, default **on** — self-gating, inert until `git` is on PATH): `MainController.applyGitSupport()` (mirrors `applyProjectSupport` — called at init + on every settings apply) disables the status-bar segment (`StatusBar.setGitEnabled`), hides the Commit window (`setAvailable(false)`), clears every open buffer's gutter bars, and the **`ifGit(...)`** wrapper makes each Git command/keybinding a no-op; `git.*`/`tool.commit` are filtered from the command palette + tool-window picker, and `refreshGit()` early-returns when off. `MainController` owns the wiring: it keeps `currentRepoRoot`, runs `refreshGit()` on tab switch / window focus-regain / save / auto-save / project switch (all coalesced by the service's generation guard), and `applyGitState(RepoState)` updates the status bar + `GitPanel` + active buffer's change bars in one pass. After a **git mutation** (commit/stage/unstage/discard/checkout/pull/push/refresh) it instead calls **`afterGitMutation()`**, which does `refreshGit()` *plus* re-diffs every **other open buffer in the same repo** (via `GitService.diff`) so a commit clears the gutter bars on background tabs too, not just the visible one. Git command **failures** are shown via **`gitError(summary, detail)`** — a scrollable error dialog (the often-multiline git stderr is unreadable in the one-line status bar) plus a short status summary. **The Git mutation operations live in `GitCoordinator`** alongside the engine (it already owned `GitService` + repo state): `gitOp`/`gitCommit`/`discardChanges`, `checkoutBranch`/`checkoutRemoteBranch`/`newBranch`, `gitSync`/`gitPush`, the stash commands (`gitStash`/`gitStashPop`/`gitUnstash`/`gitStashDrop`), the active-file `gitStageActiveFile`/`gitUnstageActiveFile`/`gitDiscardActiveFile`, `gitCommitFocus`, the `gitError` dialog, and **`git.clone`** (`GitCoordinator.cloneRepo` — the URL+destination `OverlayInput` form → `GitService.clone` → `openClonedEntry` opens a file from the clone; the pure/unit-tested folder-name deriver is `GitCoordinator.repoNameFromUrl`, named `cloneRepo` to avoid clashing with `Object.clone()`) — all running through its own `service()`/`repoRoot()`/`afterMutation()`; `MainController` keeps the `GitPanel`/`GitLogPanel`/`BranchPopup` + tool windows + `git.*` command registrations + the Git-Log/blame flows (their `Actions`/callbacks delegate to `git.*`; the clone callbacks — the `git.clone` command, the empty-`GitPanel` button, and the `BranchPopup` No-VCS action — delegate to `git::cloneRepo`), plus the `WindowOps` the coordinator drives (commit-message clear/focus, open Commit window, `checkExternalChanges`, `reloadAllFromDiskSilently`, the clone form's `keymap`/`openPath`). Commands (all no-op with a clear status when git is absent / not a repo): `git.commit` (`C-x g`, opens the Commit tool window + focuses the message), `git.stageFile` (+ the symmetric `git.unstageFile`/`git.discardFile` on the active file — `gitUnstageActiveFile`/`gitDiscardActiveFile`; discard confirms first), `git.switchBranch` (**toggles** `BranchPopup` — clicking the git status segment opens the dropdown, clicking again closes it; `MainController.chooseBranch` early-returns when `branchPopup.isShown()`/`justHidden()`, a `lastHiddenAt` guard absorbing the autoHide-then-click race like the message-log popup — an IntelliJ-style dropdown anchored above the status-bar branch segment via `StatusBar.gitSegmentNode()`: a search field over actions (New Branch/Pull/Fetch/Push/Commit) + Local/Remote branch sections from `GitService.branches`→`Branches{local:List<BranchInfo>, remote:List<String>}` (one `for-each-ref` with `%(upstream:short)`+`%(upstream:track)`, parsed by the unit-tested `GitService.parseTrack`); the header shows the **remote URL** (`Branches.remoteUrl` — origin's, else the first remote's); each local row shows its **upstream** + **incoming/outgoing** (`↓behind`/`↑ahead`) badge + tooltip ("Git Branch: … / N incoming commits"); local rows → `checkoutBranch`, remote rows → `checkoutRemoteBranch` (`checkout --track`)) and `git.newBranch`, `git.fetch`/`git.pull`/`git.push` (`runNetwork`, longer timeout; **`gitPush()`** uses `--set-upstream origin <branch>` when the branch has no upstream, else plain `push`), `git.refresh`, and `git.clone` (an `OverlayInput` form asks for **URL + destination directory** — a Browse button plus directory auto-fill to `<home>/<repo>` from the URL via the pure/unit-tested `GitCoordinator.repoNameFromUrl`; `GitService.clone` runs in the destination's parent; then `openClonedEntry` opens a file from the clone — its README if present — so Git activates **without** creating a project; clone/Projects are independent — also offered via a button in the empty `GitPanel`; the form + clone live in `GitCoordinator.cloneRepo`); the **Commit** tool window (id `commit`, title "Commit") is `tool.commit` (`M-4`) — the name "git" is intentionally left free for future use. Branch switch / pull / push call `reloadAllFromDiskSilently()` to refresh unmodified open buffers whose files changed on disk. **No new dependency / `module-info` change** — it's pure CLI. The diff viewer (below) reuses this facade — `GitService.showBytes(root, spec, cb)` fetches a blob's **raw bytes** via `git show HEAD:/:/<ref>:rel` (so the diff can decode it with the file's real charset — a BOM, else the file's `.editorconfig` `charset`, else UTF-8 — rather than force-decoding as UTF-8, which mojibaked a Latin-1/UTF-16 tracked file's HEAD side and showed the whole file as one spurious change; `ProcessRunner.runBytes`→`BytesResult` is the bytes-returning subprocess core the String `run` also delegates to), `log(root, file, max, cb)` lists commits (pure `parseLog`), and `repoRelative(root, file)` builds the `git show` spec — it **symlink-resolves both sides** (`toRealPath`, ancestor-walk fallback for a not-yet-saved file), because `rev-parse --show-toplevel` returns the real root while the buffer's file is as-opened, so a repo reached through a symlink (macOS `/tmp`, a symlinked work dir) otherwise mismatched and every path-based op reported "not in repo"; `GitCoordinator.rel` delegates to it. **History / Log, blame, and stash** (IntelliJ/VSCode-parity "Core trio", all `ifGit`-gated): `GitService` adds `blame(root, file, cb)` (`git blame --line-porcelain` → the pure, unit-tested `BlameParser` → `BlameLine{hash, author, epochSeconds, summary, uncommitted}`; all-zero sha ⇒ uncommitted), `commitFiles(root, hash, cb)` (`git diff-tree --no-commit-id --name-status -r -M` → the pure `parseNameStatus` → `CommitFile{status, path, origPath}`), `stashList(root, cb)` (`git stash list` → the pure, unit-tested `StashParser` → `StashEntry{index, ref, branch, subject}`), and reuses `run(...)` for the mutations (stash push/pop/apply/drop; `checkout`/`reset --soft|--mixed|--hard`/`revert --no-edit`/`cherry-pick <hash>`). The pure `RelativeTime.of(epoch, now)` buckets an age into `(Unit, value)` for blame labels (unit-tested). **Git Log tool window** (`ui/GitLogPanel`, a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `GitPanel`; id `gitLog`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.gitLog`/`M-g h`, `Icons::gitLog`, `setAvailable(inRepo)` from `applyGitState`): a commit `ListView` over the selected commit's changed files; selecting a commit fetches its files (`commitFiles`), double-clicking a file opens a **read-only** diff (commit~1 vs commit via `openDiff`), and a commit's context menu offers Copy Hash / Checkout / Soft·Mixed·Hard Reset / Revert / Cherry-Pick / New Branch (each → `MainController.gitMutate` → `gitService.run` → `afterGitMutation` + reload log). The same operations are also **palette commands** `git.log.checkout`/`newBranch`/`revert`/`cherryPick`/`reset`/`copyHash` that act on the panel's selected commit (`MainController.withSelectedCommit` over the new `GitLogPanel.selectedHash()`, reusing the stored `gitLogOps` `Actions` instance; `git.log.reset` prompts soft/mixed/hard via a `ChoiceDialog`). Whole-repo log = `tool.gitLog`; the active file's history = `git.fileHistory` (also the tab context menu's "Show File History"); `loadGitLog(file)` caps at 200 commits. **Blame annotations** (IntelliJ-style "Annotate" gutter column, all lines): a leftmost fixed-width gutter slot built by `FoldManager` (via `setBlameHooks(enabled, infoFor, columnWidth, onClick)` + `buildBlameSlot`, mirroring the breakpoint/bookmark/change-bar slots — so toggling it shifts the editor right as a block and line numbers stay aligned) shows per-line `author` (left, ellipsized) + `date` (right) with an **age-heatmap** background tint, a hover tooltip (full commit: author / date / relative time / summary / short hash), and click → that line's commit diff. `EditorBuffer.setBlame(List<editor/BlameInfo>)` stores the list, measures the (fixed) column width from the widest author+date in the editor font, and rebuilds the gutter; `blameHashAt(line)`/`blameHashAtCaret()`/`isBlameOn()` keep `editor` git-free (the neutral `BlameInfo{author, date, tooltip, bg, hash}` is mapped from git blame by `GitCoordinator.toBlameInfos`). The heatmap is the pure/unit-tested `git/BlameHeatmap.intensity(epoch, min, max)` (0=oldest → 1=newest across the file's committed lines) → a theme-aware rgba tint (`heatmapColor(intensity, dark)`); the date is ISO `yyyy-MM-dd` and the tooltip's relative time uses `RelativeTime` via i18n. The blame subprocess runs **once per file** (off-thread, re-run only on the coarse `applyGitState` events — tab switch / focus / save / mutation) and only the active buffer is annotated; there is no per-keystroke/per-caret work (the old per-caret `BlameOverlay` canvas was removed). **The whole inline-blame feature lives in `GitCoordinator`** — the engine (`applyBlame`/`refreshBlame`/`toBlameInfos`) *and* the UI (`toggleBlame`/`blameShowCommit`/`onGutterBlameClick`); `MainController` just registers the commands (delegating to `git::toggleBlame`/`git::blameShowCommit`) and wires the gutter click (`buffer.setGutterBlameClick(git::onGutterBlameClick)`). The two surfaces the UI touches outside the coordinator route through `WindowOps`: `syncBlameCheck()` (the Settings checkbox) and `openCommitFileDiff(hash, repoRel)` (the line's commit diff — through the window to reach `DiffCoordinator` without a circular dependency). Gated by `Settings.gitBlameInline` (default off; schema 20→21 additive-identity; `git.toggleBlame`/`M-g a`; Settings → Git checkbox + `SettingsWindow.syncGitBlameCheck`). `git.blameShowCommit` opens the caret line's commit diff; clicking any line's annotation opens that line's. CSS `.blame-slot`/`.blame-author`/`.blame-date`/`.blame-tooltip` in `app.css` (semantic colors, theme-tracking). **Stash** commands (`git.stash` with an optional message prompt, `git.stashPop`, `git.unstash`/`git.stashDrop` over a `QuickOpen<StashEntry>` picker) plus **Stash/Unstash** rows in the `BranchPopup` actions list. All gated by `gitEnabled()` (so disabled in Simple UI mode); `git.*`/`tool.gitLog` are palette-filtered when Git is off. *Deferred (later phase): a richer log graph/filtering, live-as-you-type gutter diff vs the HEAD blob, interactive rebase/merge/tag UIs.*
- `github/` + `ui/GitHubCoordinator` — **GitHub integration via the `gh` CLI** (on by default, gated by `Settings.githubSupport`; also off in Simple UI mode). The native-CLI analogue of `git/`: Editora shells out to the user's installed **`gh`** through `ProcessRunner` (the single subprocess chokepoint) and parses `gh … --json` with the already-required Jackson — **no GitHub API client, no OAuth, no new Maven dependency**. **Self-gating on four independent checks:** `Settings.githubSupport` (default on, inert-until-detected) → `gh --version` on PATH → `gh auth status` exit 0 → the repo remote being a GitHub host (the cheap pre-filter `github/GitHubRemote.isGitHub`; gh is the authority). It **rides on the Git integration**: every `gh` call runs with cwd = the git repo root (`GitCoordinator.repoRoot()`, else the active file's folder), so `gh` resolves owner/repo from the remote itself — GHES included, no host config in Editora. **Security: Editora never handles a token** — `gh` holds the user's GitHub credentials and Editora only shells out, exactly the native-CLI Git trust boundary; `gh auth login` is deliberately out-of-app (the Settings page says so). **`github/GitHubService`** is a `GitService` structural clone: one `github-service` daemon executor, QUICK(10s)/NETWORK(120s) timeouts, `Platform.runLater` callbacks, an `AtomicLong` generation guard on list refreshes, and a cached one-shot `Availability(found, authenticated, version)` probe. Its `GH_ENV` forces `GH_PROMPT_DISABLED`/`GH_NO_UPDATE_NOTIFIER`/`GH_PAGER=cat`/`NO_COLOR` so `gh` never prompts, pages, or colorizes (and `ProcessRunner` closes the child stdin, so a would-be prompt EOFs). Pure, unit-tested parsers (Jackson `readTree`, tolerant/throw-free → **no `module-info` opens**): **`GitHubRemote`** (`isGitHub`/`hostOf` over https/ssh/scp URLs), **`PrListParser`** (`gh pr list --json` → `PullRequest`), **`IssueListParser`** (→ `Issue`), **`PrViewParser`** (→ `PrDetail`), **`ChecksParser`** (`gh pr checks --json` → `CheckRun`s + a `ChecksSummary`/`Overall` roll-up — **parsed regardless of exit code**, since `gh pr checks` exits 1/8 when failing/pending with the JSON still on stdout), and **`PrCreateArgs`** (the `gh pr create` argv — a blank body still passes `--body ""` so gh never opens an interactive editor). **`ui/GitHubCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern) owns the flows, reaching the window via the shared host plus a small `WindowOps` (reload-from-disk / check-external-changes / keymap / tool-window availability+toggle / status-bar checks). Every flow runs through a `ready(Consumer<Path>)` guard that echoes the precise reason (disabled / gh missing / not authenticated / no repo). **Slice 1 flows:** **PR checkout** (`github.checkoutPr` — a `QuickOpen<PullRequest>` picker → `gh pr checkout <n>` → `GitCoordinator.afterMutation()` + `reloadAllFromDiskSilently()`, the branch-switch choreography), **PR diff review** (`github.viewPrDiff` — picker → `gh pr diff <n>` → the pure `diff/PatchParser` → **read-only text/text tabs via `DiffCoordinator.openDiff` with `EditableSide.NONE`**, so no new diff code; a multi-file PR opens a **`ui/PrReviewPane`** — a GitHub-"Files changed"-style review tab (a `TabContent` built like `WelcomePane`) with a PR-meta header (number/title/author, `head → base`, state, `+adds −dels`) + a collapsible **Markdown-rendered PR description** (the `gh pr view` body via `MarkdownRenderer`, a few lines with a Show more/less toggle when long — pure/unit-tested `PrReviewSummary.isLongDescription`/`collapseDescription`) + Open-on-GitHub / Open-all (the guarded `MAX_OPEN_ALL_WITHOUT_CONFIRM`=12 confirm) / Refresh links over clickable file rows (status letter + `FileIcons` glyph colored via `.git-status-*` + path + per-file `+a −d`), each row opening that file's read-only base↔head diff; the pane fetches `gh pr diff` + `gh pr view` concurrently off-thread, keeps **one tab per PR** (keyed by number — re-review re-selects + refreshes in place, disposed via `MainController.disposeViewerTab`), and a single-file PR opens the diff directly. Per-file counts come from the pure, unit-tested `github/PrReviewSummary` + `diff/PatchParser`'s new per-file `additions`/`deletions` (the tagged `+`/`−` lines — `oldLines`/`newLines` also carry context, so their sizes are *not* the stat)), **open-on-GitHub** (`github.openOnGitHub` — `gh browse --no-browser <rel>:<line> --branch <b>`, routed through gh for GHES/renamed-default-branch/permalink correctness), **create PR** (`github.createPr` — an `OverlayInput` form title/body/base/draft → `gh pr create`; base blank ⇒ gh's default branch), **submit review** (`github.submitReview` / the review pane's *Submit review…* link — a form picks approve / request-changes / comment + an optional-for-approve, required-otherwise body → `gh pr review`, argv from the pure/unit-tested `github/PrReviewArgs`), **`github.refresh`**, and the master **`view.toggleGithub`** — palette-gated by `Chrome.PaletteGates.github` (hides `github.*`/`tool.github` when off; `view.toggleGithub` uses the never-gated `view.` prefix). **Slice 2 — PR/issue tool window** (`ui/GitHubPanel`, a `GitLogPanel`-modeled `ToolWindowContent`; id `github`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `Icons::github`, `tool.github` (Emacs `M-g p`), **registered default-hidden**, shown only when the repo is a GitHub repo **and has at least one open PR or issue** (nothing to review ⇒ no stripe; both the remote-host classification and the open-activity probe `GitHubService.hasOpenActivity` — a `gh pr list`/`gh issue list --limit 1` check — are cached per repo root and re-gate on completion). It's **repo-scoped, not buffer-scoped** (unlike the Commit/Git Log windows): `setGitHubWindowAvailable` no longer ANDs an open buffer, so the stripe stays visible across tab switches within a project window (incl. the Welcome tab), re-derived through `updateBufferToolWindows`→`refreshAvailability`; `github.refresh` invalidates both per-root caches so the stripe re-evaluates after the repo's first PR/issue is opened): a segmented **Pull Requests | Issues | Runs** list (double-click/Enter reviews a PR's diff or opens an issue on GitHub; a row's context menu offers check-out / review-diff / open-on-GitHub / copy-URL), fed off-thread via the coordinator's `fetchPrs`/`fetchIssues` + the by-number `checkoutNumber`/`reviewPrNumber`; the window lazy-loads its current mode on open (the `gitLogToolWindow` state-listener pattern). **Slice 4 — GitHub Actions runs:** the panel's third segment lists recent workflow runs (`gh run list --json …` → the pure, unit-tested **`github/RunListParser`** + its nested **`RunState`** enum, which collapses gh's `status`×`conclusion` pair into one display state — deliberately *not* `ChecksParser.Overall`, a multi-check roll-up that lacks the per-item CANCELLED/SKIPPED and QUEUED-vs-RUNNING distinctions the row actions gate on; note `databaseId` is a **`long`** — run ids are past `Integer.MAX_VALUE`). A row shows a state glyph (`.github-run-*`) + workflow + title; its menu offers view-failure-log / rerun / rerun-failed / cancel / open / copy-URL, gated by `RunState.failed()`/`active()`. **The headline path — a failed run's log → the code:** double-clicking a failed run runs `gh run view <id> --log-failed` (one-shot, *not* streamed — a finished run's log never grows; capped twice: `ProcessRunner`'s 10 MB then a tail-trim to the last 3 000 lines **off the FX thread**) and pipes it into the **shared Build Output console** on its own owner-routed **"CI" tab** (owner = the `GitHubCoordinator`, so it never fights the Maven/npm tabs), styled by the new `OutputStyle.ci()` (`##[error]`/`##[warning]` + `LogPatterns` levels). Its stack frames are clickable because **`run/RunnerPaths`** (pure/unit-tested) maps the *runner's* paths onto the local checkout: a CI log prints `/home/runner/work/<repo>/<repo>/src/…` (or `D:\a\repo\repo\src\…`, or a repo-relative path), none of which exists locally, so it generates progressively shorter repo-relative **suffixes** (longest first, bounded to 12 trailing segments — a runner prefix is ~5 and a deep Java path 8+, so a tighter cap would silently never emit the suffix that resolves) which `MainController.resolveRunLinkFile` tries under the project root; a `..` segment is rejected outright so a log line can never escape the root. Commands `github.showRuns` + `github.viewRunLog` (a picker over the failed runs, falling back to all). Runs also count toward the stripe's `hasOpenActivity` probe (checked last so the `||` short-circuits) — a trunk-based repo with no PRs/issues but a red CI run is exactly what the tab is for. *Deliberate non-goals: live streaming/`gh run watch` (violates the no-polling invariant; a completed run's log is static), job-level drill-down, artifact download, pagination, and a status-bar run glyph (the checks segment already covers the current PR).* **Slice 3 — status-bar CI checks:** `StatusBar` gained a GitHub-checks segment (`✓/✗/○` + fail count, `setGitHubChecks(ChecksSummary)`, hidden in Simple mode), populated by the coordinator's `refreshChecks` on `github.refresh` + after a PR checkout (**no background polling** — `gh pr checks` with no number resolves the current branch's PR). **Settings → Version Control → GitHub** page (`Category.GITHUB`): enable checkbox + `gh` path field + a green/red found/authenticated/not-found status row (mirrors the Git/Mermaid pages; `GitHubService` injected via the `SettingsWindow` ctor). `Settings.githubSupport`/`ghPath` (schema **81→82** additive-identity); i18n in all six catalogs. **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change.** *Deferred (the `gh` ceiling): threaded/inline review comments + "suggested changes" (no `gh` subcommand — needs `gh api graphql`); notifications; per-file server-side diff retrieval (`gh pr diff` is all-or-nothing, binaries are stubs); selected-row palette commands.*
- `diff/` — **Diff viewer + merge-conflict resolution** (SDD-driven). Pure, unit-tested core on **java-diff-utils** (`io.github.javadiffutils`, an automatic module — moditect injects a descriptor for the jlink dist, like pdfbox; deps only `java.base`, not signed so no strip). No diff-match-patch: its Maven artifact isn't a reliable JPMS module, so intra-line word highlighting is done in-house. **`DiffEngine.compute(left, right)` → `DiffModels.DiffModel`** walks the java-diff-utils `Patch` deltas into aligned **side-by-side rows** (`Row{type EQUAL/ADDED/REMOVED/MODIFIED, left, leftLine, right, rightLine, leftWordRanges, rightWordRanges}` — a CHANGE delta is paired line-by-line into MODIFIED rows + filler for the longer side) plus derived **unified rows** and `changeBlockStarts` (prev/next nav); `lines(text)` normalizes CRLF + drops one trailing newline. **`compute(left, right, DiffOptions{ignoreWhitespace, wordLevel})`** is the options overload (drives the File History tool window's inline-diff toggles): `ignoreWhitespace` runs the Myers diff over whitespace-normalized lines but — since normalization is strictly 1:1 per line — the delta positions still index the originals, so every `Row` renders the **original** text (only equality changes); `wordLevel=false` skips the per-line `InlineDiff` (whole-line highlight). `DiffService` gained a matching options overload. **`InlineDiff`** tokenizes a changed line into word/non-word runs, diffs the token lists, and maps changed tokens back to `[start,end)` char ranges (word-level emphasis, no second lib). **`ConflictParser`** parses Git markers (`<<<<<<<`/`|||||||`/`=======`/`>>>>>>>`) → ours/**base**/theirs segments (the 3-way `|||||||` common-ancestor region is **captured** when present — i.e. `diff3`/`zdiff3` `merge.conflictStyle`; empty under Git's default `merge` style, gated via `Conflict.hasBase()`/`ConflictFile.hasBase()`) + `resolve(file, choices)` (OURS/THEIRS/**BASE**/BOTH/UNRESOLVED-keeps-markers, where UNRESOLVED round-trips the captured base region verbatim). **`PatchWriter.unifiedDiff`** → a `.patch` via `UnifiedDiffUtils`; the reverse direction, **`PatchParser.parse(text)`**, is a pure/unit-tested parser that reconstructs each file section's old/new line sequences from a unified diff (tolerant of a bare `diff -u` file, a git `diff --git`/`index`/rename preamble, several files back to back, `/dev/null` add/delete sides, and a `\ No newline at end of file` marker; a hunk's declared `@@ -a,b +c,d @@` line counts gate exactly how many lines are consumed as content, so a removed/added line that happens to start with `---`/`+++` is never mistaken for the next file's header). The reconstructed lines feed straight back into `DiffEngine.compute` — no new row type needed. **`DiffCoordinator.openPatchFile(buffer)`** opens the active `.patch`/`.diff` buffer's first file-section as a read-only structured diff tab this way (via the tab-menu **"Open in Diff Viewer"** item — shown only for a `.patch`/`.diff` file — or the palette-only `diff.openPatchFile`); it parses the buffer's own live text (not a re-read from disk), so unsaved edits to the patch are reflected, and reports a status note when the patch has more than one file (v1 shows just the first). **`DiffService`** runs `DiffEngine` off the FX thread (the `GitService` idiom; posts `null` past a 60k-line guard). **UI** (`ui/`): **`DiffViewerPane implements TabContent`** — side-by-side (default) is two read-only `editor-area` `CodeArea`s with synced vertical scroll (guarded `estimatedScrollYProperty` listeners; aligned row counts mean equal line heights), per-side original-line-number gutters (`setParagraphGraphicFactory`), TextMate syntax (`TextMateHighlighter.compute`) **overlaid** with intra-line `.diff-word` spans (`StyleSpans.overlay`), and per-line diff backgrounds via `setParagraphStyle` (`.diff-added/-removed/-modified/-filler`); a toolbar toggles **unified** (one CodeArea, `+/−` gutter), navigates prev/next change (single-key **`n`**/**`p`** in a read-only diff — a `root` KEY_PRESSED filter gated on `EditableSide.NONE` so it never eats typing in an editable apply-change diff), and exports the patch. The toolbar's view-toggle / apply-all / prev / next actions are also **palette commands** `diff.toggleView`/`diff.applyAll`/`diff.nextChange`/`diff.previousChange` (via `DiffCoordinator.withActiveDiff` over the active tab's `DiffViewerPane`; `applyAllChanges()` no-ops on a read-only diff). **`MergeViewerPane implements TabContent`** lists each conflict (ours/theirs `TextArea`s — plus a middle **base** column with an **Accept Base** button when the conflict `hasBase()`, styled `.merge-base`) with Accept Ours/Theirs/Both + a resolved-count toolbar; Save routes the resolved lines back (replaces the active buffer text, undoable). **`Icons.diff()`/`merge()`** + `.diff-*`/`.merge-*` CSS in `app.css`. **The whole diff/merge feature lives in `ui/DiffCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `DiffService`, `openDiff`/`refreshOpenDiffs`/`withActiveDiff`, the `applyToLocal`/`undoLocal`/`saveLocal` "apply change" flow, `worktreeText`, `exportPatch`, the compare entry points, and `resolveConflicts`; git-backed diffs reach the repo via the shared `GitCoordinator` passed in; reaches the window via an `Ops` extension for add-diff-tab / open-buffer-for-path / open-background-buffer / save-buffer / the open-&-active diff-pane lookups / finder-start-dir). `computeDiff` + `applyToLocal`/`undoLocal`/`saveLocal` are **package-visible** so the Local File History tool window (`FileHistoryPanel`, via `HistoryCoordinator`) reuses them for its inline revision diff + per-hunk chevrons, and `applyToLocal` also lets History's `restoreHistory` write a restored revision through the same undoable-buffer path. **The Local File History feature itself lives in `ui/HistoryCoordinator`** (the same `CoordinatorHost` pattern) — it owns the `HistoryService` (off-thread snapshot/blob engine) + the `FileHistoryPanel`, the record hooks (save/autosave/external/pre-delete), the per-file + folder-history views, the label / recent-changes pickers, and the revision diff/restore (via the shared `DiffCoordinator`), reaching the window via an `Ops` extension (the `history/index.json` bucket maps + save / blobs dir / the File History tool-window availability+open / open-path / tree-refresh / current-text). **The revision diff lives inline in the tool window** (there is no separate history window — the old `ui/LocalHistoryWindow` was folded in): `FileHistoryPanel` is a horizontal `SplitPane` — the revision `ListView` (+ label/reason/time filter) on the left, and on the right a **live** side-by-side diff of the *selected* revision (before) vs the current file (after), rebuilt on selection by re-diffing off-thread via the injected `FileHistoryPanel.DiffSupport` (→ `DiffCoordinator.computeDiff`) into a reused `DiffViewerPane` (its own toolbar keeps side-by-side/unified + prev/next). A right-pane toolbar shows the revision-timestamp header, an **N-differences** count (`model.changeBlockStarts().size()`), **Ignore whitespace** / **Highlight words** `ToggleButton`s (both `recompute()` via `DiffEngine.DiffOptions`), and a **Revert** button (→ `restoreHistory`, undoable). The diff's current-file (RIGHT) side is **editable**, so the IntelliJ-style **per-hunk apply chevrons** do selective restore (a fragment from the snapshot into the file through the undoable buffer, via `DiffSupport.applyToLocal`/`undoLocal`/`saveLocal`); after an apply/undo the panel re-baselines (`currentText`) and re-diffs so the remaining chevrons update (`reDiffAfterEdit`). No diff runs until a revision is selected (nothing when the window is closed / no selection), and the right pane resets to a "select a revision" prompt on tab switch / new file. `DiffSupport` is injected once by `HistoryCoordinator.setDiffSupport` (delegating to `historyService.content` / `diff.*` / `ops.currentTextOf` / `host.settings` / `restoreHistory`); folder-history mode keeps the tree on the left with the right pane disabled (its revisions belong to different files). `MainController` keeps the File History `ToolWindow` (built with `historyCoordinator.panel()`) + the `history.*`/`tool.fileHistory` command registrations + the project-tree "Show Local History" item (delegating to the coordinator). `MainController` keeps the `diff.*`/`merge.resolve` command registrations + the tab-menu / Git-panel / project-tree / Git-log entry points (delegating to the coordinator), and calls `diffCoordinator.refreshOpenDiffs()` on window focus-regain + in `afterGitMutation`. Entry points: `diff.vsHead` (`C-x v =`; tab menu "Compare with HEAD"; Git-panel "Show Diff" → `diffGitPanelFile(rel, staged)` = staged: index↔HEAD, unstaged: working↔index), `diff.compareWith` (FileFinder picks the second file — **ungated**), `diff.vsCommit` (`QuickOpen` over `GitService.log`), `merge.resolve` (opens the merge view when `ConflictParser.hasConflictMarkers`). Git-backed diffs are `ifGit`-gated; the working side uses the open buffer's live text when the file is open (canonical-path match), else disk (`worktreeText`, which decodes a closed file's bytes with the same charset rules as the blob side, not force-UTF-8). **Both a blob and a closed working file decode with the file's real charset** (`EditorConfigCharset.resolveName(bytes, ops.editorConfigCharset(file))` → `decode`: a BOM wins, else the file's `.editorconfig` `charset`, else UTF-8 — mirroring how the editor reads the file), so a Latin-1/UTF-16 tracked file shows real text and only genuine edits differ instead of UTF-8 mojibake + a spurious whole-file change (#435). **Live refresh**: each side is a re-fetchable `DiffSide` (a `Consumer<Consumer<String>>` — a `git show` blob via the `blobSide(root, spec, file)` helper, or `worktreeText`), and `openDiff` installs a `DiffViewerPane.refresher` that re-fetches both + `pane.updateContent(...)` **only when the content changed** (`pane.matches(l,r)` guard, so an unchanged refresh keeps the view + scroll); `refreshOpenDiffs()` (iterates tabs whose `userData instanceof DiffViewerPane`) runs on **window focus-regain** (a compared file changed on disk) and in **`afterGitMutation`** (a commit/stage/checkout moved HEAD/index/working). **Apply change** (IntelliJ's hunk-accept arrow): `DiffViewerPane.setEditable(EditableSide, onApply)` marks which side is the writable local file (RIGHT for vs-HEAD/vs-commit/unstaged, LEFT for compare-with, NONE for staged index↔HEAD); that side's gutter then shows apply chevrons (`.diff-apply`): a **single chevron on every changed row** (per-line / sub-hunk — `applyRow` → `computeApplied(i,i+1)`) and a **double chevron at each change block's first row** (whole hunk — `applyBlock(start)` → `computeApplied(start, blockEndFrom(start))`), both over the pure aligned rows; an **Apply-all** toolbar button (`Icons.check()`, shown only when a side is editable) replaces the editable file with the other side wholesale. Both hand the new full text to `DiffCoordinator.applyToLocal(target, text)` — which routes through an **undoable editor buffer** (`bufferForApply`: the open buffer, else one opened in the **background** via `addBuffer(buffer, false)` so the diff stays focused), `replaceText`s it (marks dirty), then `refreshOpenDiffs()` re-diffs. The toolbar's **Undo** (`undoLocal` → the buffer's `undo()`) and **Save** (`saveLocal` → `save(buffer)`) act on that buffer, so applies are revertible and persisted explicitly. **Apply-all** confirms first (it replaces the whole file). (`setEditable` rebuilds the view so the arrows + Undo/Save/Apply-all toolbar buttons appear, since it runs after construction.) **One new dependency + its moditect entry; no `module-info` opens / Settings / schema change.** *Deferred: a **computed** 3-way merge — fetch base/ours/theirs (the conflicted index stages `:1:`/`:2:`/`:3:` via `GitService.show`, or `git merge-base` + blobs outside a conflict) and run a diff3 engine that auto-resolves non-conflicting hunks and surfaces only true conflicts, independent of the user's `conflictStyle` (the base **column** itself already ships — see `MergeViewerPane`/`ConflictParser` — but it's only populated for `diff3`/`zdiff3` markers); in-diff editing, gutter-arrow stage/revert hunks, the SDD's standalone Diff Model persistence, multi-file `.patch` tabs (one tab per file section).*
- `process/` + `mermaid/` — **Mermaid diagram support** (on by default — inert until the `mmdc` CLI is detected — gated by `Settings.mermaidSupport`). The generic subprocess runner `ProcessRunner` lives in **`com.editora.process`** (moved out of `git/` so Git and Mermaid share it; `GitService` passes `GIT_OPTIONAL_LOCKS=0` through the new `run(dir,timeout,cmd,extraEnv)` overload, and `LC_ALL=C` is always set). **GUI-launch PATH fix (important):** a Finder-launched `.app` (or a `.desktop`) inherits a stripped `PATH` (`/usr/bin:/bin:…`) without Homebrew/npm/Node dirs, so `mmdc`/`npx`/`maid` (and a Homebrew `git`) wouldn't be found — `ProcessRunner` builds an **augmented PATH** = the inherited PATH **+ the user's login-shell PATH + the usual install dirs**, then rewrites a bare command name to its absolute path against it before launching (Java's Unix `ProcessBuilder` resolves the executable against the JVM's own stripped PATH, not the child env, so both steps are needed). The **login-shell PATH** (`ProcessRunner.loginShellPath()`) is the crucial part for version managers: it runs the user's `$SHELL -l -i -c 'printf …$PATH…'` **once** (stdin `/dev/null`, stderr discarded, 5 s timeout, markers fence the PATH off from any rc banner — the pure marker parse `extractMarked` is unit-tested; the VS Code `resolveShellEnv` approach) and folds its entries in. This recovers bin dirs that are **version-specific and so can't be hardcoded** — e.g. **nvm**'s `~/.nvm/versions/node/<ver>/bin` (where npm-global servers like `typescript-language-server`/`pyright-langserver`/`yaml-language-server` live), fnm/asdf/volta, and a profile-set Homebrew. The hardcoded `EXTRA_PATH_DIRS` (`/opt/homebrew/bin`, `/usr/local/bin`, `/opt/local/bin`, `~/.local/bin`, `~/go/bin`, `~/.cargo/bin`, …) remain as a fallback. `augmentedPath()` is cached after the first call, and `LspManager`'s constructor **warms it off-thread** (the probe spawns a process) so neither detection nor `session.start()` blocks — and `session.start()` itself (the process fork + `PATH` scan + ledger write) now runs on `LspManager`'s `lsp-start` daemon pool, off the FX thread (#407); the session is cached synchronously and the caller's `didOpen` queues via `whenReady` until the async `initialize` completes (`start()` is deliberately **not** `synchronized`, so the fork never blocks `whenReady`'s monitor on the FX thread). Windows yields no login-shell PATH (no POSIX convention). A Settings absolute path still overrides. `com.editora.mermaid.Mermaid` is the static CLI facade over **mmdc** (mermaid-cli; renders/exports) and **maid** (`probelabs/maid`; a fast pure-JS linter): `renderPng(mmdc,source,dark)` (writes a temp `.mmd`, runs `mmdc -i -o -t default|dark -b transparent -s 2`, reads the **PNG** — *not* SVG, because JavaFX/JSVG can't apply mermaid's embedded `<style>` CSS or render its `<foreignObject>` HTML labels, so SVG comes out all-black/textless; mmdc rasterizes faithfully via headless Chromium), `exportTo(...)` (format by the chosen file extension — SVG/PNG/PDF, mmdc writes it directly), `validate(maid,source)` (runs `maid --format json`, parsed by the pure, unit-tested `MaidOutput` → `Diagnostic{line,column,severity,code,message}`; JSON with a text fallback). `MermaidService` (UI-owned, mirrors `GitService`: daemon executor + `Platform.runLater` + cached availability probe) backs the export command + the Settings detection status. Because `MarkdownRenderer` is synchronous/pure but mmdc is a multi-second subprocess, the editor-side **`MermaidImages`** static façade (like `PreviewImageLoader`: daemon pool + cache, configured via `configure(enabled,mmdcExe,maidExe,dark)` injected from `MermaidCoordinator.applySupport`) returns a placeholder `StackPane` immediately and fills it async — decoding mmdc's PNG with a JavaFX `Image` (logical width = pixels ÷ `RENDER_SCALE`) into an `ImageView` sized by a caller-supplied `DoubleUnaryOperator` (embedded Markdown blocks clamp to the content column; a standalone `.mmd` multiplies by the preview zoom so zoom actually resizes the image) — **cached by `sha-256(source+theme)`** so the debounced whole-document re-render never re-invokes mmdc for unchanged diagrams; on failure it shows `maid`'s precise line/column diagnostics (else mmdc's stderr) in a `.mermaid-error` label. (No JSVG/AWT in the Mermaid path — PNG decodes natively.) `MarkdownRenderer` special-cases a fenced block whose info string is `mermaid` (`isMermaidInfo`) → `MermaidImages.node(...)`, else the usual `codeBlock`. Standalone **`.mmd` files** (TextMate grammar `grammars/mermaid.tmLanguage.json` → `source.mermaid`, `LanguageRegistry` `mmd`→`mermaid`) get the same 3-mode preview: `EditorBuffer.isDiagram()`/`hasPreview()` generalize the markdown gating, and `scheduleRenderPreview` branches to render the whole buffer as one diagram. **Markwhen timelines** (`.mw`/`.markwhen` → language `markwhen`, scope `source.markwhen`, authored `grammars/markwhen.tmLanguage.json`) get the same 3-mode preview via the identical seam: the pure, JavaFX-free **`com.editora.markwhen`** package (`MwDate` — ISO + English month-name dates as half-open `[start,endExclusive)` intervals; sealed `MwNode` `Event`/`Group`; `Timeline`; tolerant line-based `MarkwhenParser.parse` — frontmatter `title:`/`#Tag: color`, `#`-header sections nested by level like Markdown, single/range events split on a whitespace-surrounded `-`/`/`, `//` comments — all unit-tested) parses the buffer **off-thread on `PREVIEW_POOL`** (a fourth `scheduleRenderPreview` branch beside `isMarkwhen()`, `previewGen` stale-guard) and **`editor/MarkwhenTimeline.build(model, zoomScale, viewportWidth)`** renders it on the FX thread as a **node-based `Pane`** (time axis + tick gridlines, one row per event/group, range→rounded `Region` bar / point→`Circle`, `#`-section bands, hover tooltips, `#tag` colors from the frontmatter else a fallback palette; capped at 500 events → placeholder), themed via `.markwhen-*` AtlantaFX looked-up colors in `app.css` (no per-theme override). Folding reuses the Markdown heading-level algorithm (`FoldRegions.markwhen`, `headingLevel` ignores space-less `#tag:` decls); `Commenter` `//`; `FileIcons` `table` glyph; horizontal zoom scales the axis width (re-render via `applyPreviewScale`). **A second renderer — `editor/MarkwhenCalendar` (month-grid: a vertical stack of Sun–Sat month cards, tag-colored event chips on each covered day, capped at 120 months) — is toggled per file** (`EditorBuffer.MarkwhenView` TIMELINE/CALENDAR, `toggleMarkwhenView`, persisted in `WorkspaceState.markwhenViews`; the render branch picks the renderer); both share `editor/MarkwhenPaint` (tag→color). The Markwhen preview right-click menu (and palette `markwhen.exportJson`/`markwhen.toggleView`) offers **Export to JSON** (`markwhen/MarkwhenJson.toJson` — a clean pretty-printed tree of title/tagColors/nested nodes, not `@markwhen/parser`'s schema) and **Switch to Calendar/Timeline View**, plus **Export to PDF** and **Print** (both a light raster snapshot of the timeline/calendar — the shared preview→PDF/print snapshot path, see the *snapshot preview export* note in `pdf/` above). Word (docx/odt) stays markwhen-unsupported (`isMarkdown()`-only). Deferred: relative/human-fuzzy dates, recurrence, times/timezones, lane-packing, and a markwhen CLI (none renders to an image like `mmdc`). Command `mermaid.export` (`FileChooser` SVG/PNG/PDF → `MermaidService.export`). Each tool is run as a **tokenized command** (`Mermaid.command(configured, default)`, whitespace-split) so a bare binary *or* an npx invocation works: defaults are `mmdc` (a binary; the user installs mermaid-cli) and **`npx -y @probelabs/maid`** (maid is normally run via npx, not a global bin — `MermaidService.DEFAULT_MMDC`/`DEFAULT_MAID`). maid emits its JSON report on stdout regardless of exit code, so `validate` always parses it (doesn't gate on success); the real shape is `{errors:[{line,column,message,severity,code,hint}], …}` — locked in by a `MaidOutputTest` case. Settings → **Mermaid** page: enable checkbox + `mmdc`/`maid` command fields (Browse; blank = the defaults above) + a live found/not-found status (`detect` counts any clean launch, not just exit 0). **`ui/MermaidCoordinator`** (a feature coordinator extracted from `MainController`, the `LogViewerCoordinator` pattern — owns the `MermaidService` + the detected-tool `Availability` + the apply/gating/export logic, reaching the window only through a shared `CoordinatorHost` interface; `MainController` keeps one-line delegations and a fake `Host` makes it unit-testable, see `MermaidCoordinatorFxTest`): `applySupport()` (mirrors `applyGitSupport`, init + every settings/theme apply) configures the façade + service + re-renders open previews, then detects the tools and gates lint/autocomplete; the `export` command no-ops when off (`ifEnabled`) and `mermaid.*` is filtered from the palette. The mermaid reads other features need are exposed as coordinator methods: `mmdcCommandOrNull()` (PDF/print embedding), `effectiveAutocomplete()` (the completion config), `exportDiagram()` (PDF diagram export), and `service()` (the Settings → Mermaid detection-status row). **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (grammar rides the existing `opens com.editora.grammars`; mmdc/maid are external CLIs the user installs via npm). **Live linting**: `.mmd` buffers run **maid** debounced (~450 ms) while typing via `MermaidService.validate(source, cb)` (async, gen-guarded) injected into `EditorBuffer.setMermaidValidator`; `MermaidLintOverlay` (a `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`) draws red wavy underlines at each diagnostic's `line/column/length` (visible paragraphs only, coalesced), and an `area` `MOUSE_MOVED` handler shows the maid message in a tooltip over a squiggle. Gated by `EditorBuffer.setMermaidLintEnabled` (controller sets it = mermaid on && maid detected, re-applied after the async `detect`). **Autocomplete**: `.mmd` buffers get Mermaid keyword completions (`completion/MermaidKeywords`, merged in `CompletionEngine.complete` when `snippetLang == "mermaid"`) + bundled `snippets/mermaid.json`, gated by `Settings.autocompleteMermaid` (Settings → Editor, default on; `view.toggleAutocompleteMermaid`) — **effective only** when the master autocomplete is on, Mermaid is enabled, and mmdc is detected (`MermaidCoordinator.effectiveAutocomplete()`; `EditorBuffer.updateCompletion` routes diagram buffers through this flag). `MaidOutput.Diagnostic` carries `length` for the underline span. *Deferred (per the SDD): a Markdown→HTML/PDF export pipeline (none exists to hook "render before export" into), a Mermaid LSP (no LSP layer exists), and block-at-caret export from Markdown.*
- `diagram/` — **Diagram-as-code preview** (Graphviz DOT + PlantUML; on by default, gated by `Settings.diagramSupport` — self-gating, inert until `dot`/`plantuml` are detected). A **generic, Mermaid-independent** seam that mirrors the Mermaid pattern (`process/`+`mermaid/`) without touching its shipped path. Pure package **`com.editora.diagram`**: **`DiagramKind`** (enum DOT/PLANTUML — each maps a buffer `languageId` → default command + temp-source extension + a pure `args(cmd,in,out,fmt,dark)` argv builder; `fromLanguage(lang)`; a `themeSensitive` flag, false for both today so the render cache omits the theme bit → a theme toggle is a cache hit, not a re-render), **`DiagramRenderer`** (the synchronous CLI facade — the `mermaid/Mermaid` generalized: `renderPng`/`exportTo`/`detect`/`command`, writing the temp source to `diagram.<ext>` and reading back **whatever the tool actually produced** (`producedFile`, globbing the single-use temp dir): **PlantUML names its output after the *diagram***, so `@startuml myclassdiagram` writes `myclassdiagram.png` — reading a fixed `diagram.<fmt>` made every *named* diagram render as "render failed" and made its export report success while writing nothing; `exportTo` moves it to the chosen dest; DOT/PlantUML both **rasterize PNG natively — no headless browser**, unlike mmdc/D2; pure `formatFor`/args unit-tested in `DiagramRendererTest`), and **`DiagramService`** (UI façade, the `MermaidService` idiom: one `diagram-service` daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`, per-kind path map + cached `Availability`(`Map<DiagramKind,Boolean>`) probe + async `export`). **`editor/DiagramImages`** is the async render engine (a near-copy of `MermaidImages`: 2-thread `diagram-render` daemon pool, LRU cache keyed by `kind+sha256((theme?)+source)`, placeholder→fill; `.md-diagram`/`.diagram-placeholder`/`.diagram-error` CSS mirroring `.md-mermaid`; `configure(enabled, Map<DiagramKind,List<String>>, dark)` injected from the coordinator — the editor package stays free of `ui`). **`EditorBuffer`** mirrors the Mermaid gating: `diagramKind()`/`isRenderedDiagram()`, a broadened `hasPreview()` (`|| (isRenderedDiagram() && DiagramImages.isEnabled())`), a new `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch (whole buffer → one async image via `DiagramImages.node(kind, text, lw->lw*zoom)`, right after the Mermaid `isDiagram()` branch), and the zoom re-render. The floating 3-mode toggle attaches automatically (it keys off `hasPreview()`). **`ui/DiagramCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern, alongside `MermaidCoordinator`): `applySupport()` (init + every settings/theme apply — configure `DiagramImages` + refresh previews + detect tools) and `export()` (active DOT/PlantUML buffer → SVG/PNG/PDF FileChooser → `DiagramService.export`); `MainController` keeps a `diagram` field with one-line delegations at the same sites as `mermaid` (init/settings-apply/theme-apply/dispose) + the palette gate (`Chrome.PaletteGates.diagram`, filtering `diagram.*`). **Registration:** `LanguageRegistry` (`dot`/`gv`→dot, `puml`/`plantuml`/`pu`/`iuml`→plantuml), authored `grammars/dot.tmLanguage.json` (`source.dot`) + `grammars/plantuml.tmLanguage.json` (`source.plantuml`) in `GrammarRegistry` (`scopeToResource`+`mapExtensions`, riding the existing `opens com.editora.grammars`), `Commenter` (DOT `//`+`/* */`, PlantUML `'`+`/' '/`), `FoldRegions` (DOT brace folding). **Settings → Languages & Tools → Diagrams** page (enable checkbox + `dot`/`plantuml` path fields + a green/red found/not-found status, the Mermaid-page shape; `DiagramService` threaded into `SettingsWindow` as a ctor arg). Commands `diagram.export`, `view.toggleDiagramSupport`, `diagram.setDotCommand`, `diagram.setPlantumlCommand`; `Settings.diagramSupport`/`dotPath`/`plantumlPath` (schema 62→63 additive-identity); i18n ×6. **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (grammars ride the existing opens; dot/plantuml are external CLIs the user installs). *Deferred: PlantUML `@start/@end` block folding, a themed (dark) render (the `themeSensitive` flag is ready), live linting (no `maid`-equivalent), the in-app installer, autocomplete, and the browser-raster diagram tools (D2, WaveDrom — their clean raster needs a headless Chrome like mmdc).*
- `typst/` — **Typst document support** (3-mode preview + export; on by default, gated by `Settings.typstSupport` — self-gating, inert until the `typst` CLI is detected). A `.typ` buffer gets the same Editor/Split/Preview view as Markdown, but rendered by the external **typst** CLI to **stacked page images** (a Typst document paginates — the multi-page analogue of `diagram/`, which is why it's its own seam, not a `DiagramKind`). Pure package **`com.editora.typst`**: **`TypstRenderer`** (the synchronous CLI facade — `renderPages(cmd, source, fileDir, root[, displayName])` rasterizes one PNG per page at `96×RENDER_SCALE` PPI and returns the ordered bytes; `exportTo` writes PDF (single file) or PNG/SVG (one numbered file per page, `report-1.png`…); `command`/`detect` mirror `DiagramRenderer` — a configured path that *is* a file is taken whole so a home dir with a space doesn't split, and a multi-token wrapper's exit code gates detection; the pure `renderArgs`/`exportArgs`/`exportOutput`/`exportedFiles`/`effectiveRoot`/`sortPageFiles`/`formatFor`/`friendlyMessage` are unit-tested). **Relative-path root:** typst commonly `#image("logo.png")`/`#import`s a sibling, resolved against the project **root**, so the live text is written to a throwaway `.editora-typst-<uuid>.typ` **inside** the saved file's folder and compiled with `--root <fileDir>` (or a higher project root via the injected `rootResolver`); the throwaway is always deleted (`finally`). An untitled/remote buffer uses an isolated temp dir (relative refs won't resolve — acceptable for a scratch doc). A compile error's temp filename is rewritten to the buffer's display name (`friendlyMessage`, #462). **`TypstService`** is the UI façade (the `MermaidService`/`DiagramService` idiom: one `typst` daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`, cached `detect` probe, async `export`/`renderPages`). **`editor/TypstImages`** is the async render engine (a near-copy of `MermaidImages`/`DiagramImages`, but each cache entry is a **list** of page images stacked in a `VBox`): a 2-thread `typst-render` daemon pool, retain-last-image per surface (`LAST_GOOD`, so live editing updates in place without a placeholder flash + a compile error keeps the last good pages under a non-destructive banner), a page-count-bounded LRU (`MAX_CACHED_PAGES`, #461 — each page pins a GPU texture, so bounding by entry count let a 40-page doc retain ~570 MB), and `configure(enabled, command)` injected from `TypstCoordinator.applySupport` (editor stays free of `ui`). **`EditorBuffer`** mirrors the Mermaid/diagram gating: `isTypst()`, `hasTypstPreview()` folded into `hasPreview()`, a `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch (whole buffer → `TypstImages.node(text, sizer, surfaceKey, fileDir, root, displayName)`), and zoom re-render. **`ui/TypstCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern, alongside `DiagramCoordinator`): `applySupport()` (init + every settings apply — configure `TypstImages` + refresh previews + detect) and `export`/`exportPng`/`exportSvg` (FileChooser → `TypstService.export`, reporting the actual `exportedFiles`). **Editing markup:** pure/unit-tested **`typst/TypstMarkup`** supplies the Typst-specific editing pieces (headings `=`/`==`, links `#link("url")[text]`, list markers `-`/`+`/`N.` — deliberately **not** `*`, which is Typst *bold*); inline `*bold*`/`_emph_`/`` `raw` `` reuse the generic `markdown/MarkdownInline.toggle`, and `EditorBuffer`'s markdown menu/format actions dispatch on `isTypst()`. **Registration:** authored `grammars/typst.tmLanguage.json` + `snippets/typst.json` + a `FileIcons` glyph. There's also a **typst LSP** server option (`tinymist`, `Settings.typstLspEnabled`) in the LSP registry. Commands `typst.export`/`typst.exportPng`/`typst.exportSvg` + `view.toggleTypstSupport` + the markup commands; Settings → Languages & Tools → **Typst** page (enable + `typst` path + found/not-found status + Install… button); `Settings.typstSupport`/`typstPath` (schema 66→67 additive); the in-app installer knows typst; i18n ×6. **No new Maven dependency** (typst is an external CLI the user installs). *Deferred: multi-file project root beyond the injected resolver, live linting, a block-at-caret export, incremental/partial-page rendering.*
- `mcp/` — **Model Context Protocol server** (off by default, gated by `Settings.mcpSupport`; **also off in Simple UI mode**). Lets an **external** AI agent drive *this* editor (the inverse of `ai/`, which calls out to a model): a tiny embedded **loopback-only** HTTP server speaking **JSON-RPC 2.0** over MCP's Streamable-HTTP request/response subset (one POST → one `application/json`; no SSE). **`mcp/McpServer`** (modeled on `web/LivePreviewServer`; touches no JavaFX — all editor reads marshal onto the FX thread via the bridge) binds an **ephemeral 127.0.0.1 port** (never the LAN), requires **`Authorization: Bearer <token>`** on every request (the token gates other local processes), and on start writes `<configDir>/mcp-endpoint.json` (url + token) **owner-only (0600)** for client discovery — stamped with the process pid + start instant so a stale file from a crash is reaped at launch (`reapStaleEndpoint`, #464). **`mcp/McpTools`** exposes the tool set (`initialize`/`tools/list`/`tools/call`/`ping`): **`list_open_files`**, **`read_buffer`**, **`get_diagnostics`**, **`find_in_files`**, **`list_commands`**, **`execute_command`** (run any registered `Command`), **`open_file`**, **`edit_buffer`**, **`save_buffer`**, **`get_selection`**, **`document_symbols`**, **`git_status`**, **`todo_scan`** — all editor access flows through **`mcp/McpBridge`** (implemented by `MainController`, which marshals each call onto the FX thread and returns neutral records). The server is **app-wide, single-instance** held in a static field with an `mcpOwner` window; `MainController.applyMcpSupport` starts it when first enabled (that window becomes the bridge) and stops it when disabled. **Closing the owner window re-owns the server to a surviving window** (`McpServer.rebind(bridge)` keeps the same port/token/endpoint so a connected agent isn't dropped; stops only when the last window closes — #463). A **security-notice confirmation** is shown before enabling (from the palette toggle + the Settings checkbox, mirroring the plugin-enable confirm). The status bar shows an MCP-running indicator (`StatusBar.setMcpRunning`). Commands `view.toggleMcp` + `mcp.copyEndpoint` (copies a ready-to-paste `claude mcp add --transport http editora <url> --header "Authorization: Bearer <token>"` command); `Settings.mcpSupport` (default off; schema 27→28 additive; Settings → System → MCP). Batch requests + SSE are unsupported (answered with a clear error, not a hang). **`module-info` `requires jdk.httpserver`** — no new Maven dependency (JSON via the existing Jackson). *Deferred: SSE/streaming transport, a resources/prompts surface, per-tool scoping/permissions, remote (non-loopback) access.*
- `structured/` — **Structured-data preview** (JSON/YAML/TOML tree + OpenAPI/Swagger docs; on by default, `Settings.structuredPreview`). A `.json`/`.yaml`/`.toml` buffer gets the same 3-mode preview as Markdown, via the **render-branch** model (buffer-owned, no coordinator — like Markwhen), but hosting a **self-scrolling node** the CSV-grid way (so the `TreeView` keeps virtualization) rather than inside the preview `ScrollPane`. Pure package **`com.editora.structured`** (the only place that touches Jackson, so `editor` stays Jackson-free): **`StructuredNode`** (neutral tree: key/kind(OBJECT/ARRAY/STRING/NUMBER/BOOLEAN/NULL)/value/children), **`StructuredParser`** (`Format.forLanguage` json/yaml/toml; `parse(text,fmt)` → a `Parsed{root, openApi, error}` via `ObjectMapper`/`YAMLMapper`/`TomlMapper` → one `JsonNode`→`StructuredNode` conversion, capped at `MAX_NODES`=50k so a pathological doc can't build millions of FX nodes), **`OpenApiModel`** + **`OpenApiParser`** (`detect` = a textual `openapi`/`swagger` key; `parse` shallow-walks OpenAPI 3 `servers`/`components.schemas` + Swagger 2 `host`/`basePath`/`definitions` into title/servers/paths(operations→params/responses)/schemas; `$ref`s shown by simple name via `refName`; unit-tested `StructuredParserTest`/`OpenApiParserTest`). **`editor/StructuredTree`** renders the tree as a `TreeView<StructuredNode>` (type-colored `.structured-*` cells, auto-expand depth 1); **`editor/OpenApiDoc`** renders the spec as Redoc-style API docs (title, servers, endpoints with colored `.openapi-method-*` badges + params/responses, schemas) in a self-scrolling `ScrollPane`. Both keep `editor` free of `ui`. **`EditorBuffer`**: `isStructured()`/`structuredFormat()`, `hasStructuredPreview()` (= `structuredPreviewEnabled && isStructured() && !hugeFile`) folded into `hasPreview()`, a `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch (parse off-thread on `PREVIEW_POOL`, build the node on the FX thread under the `previewGen` guard into a stable `structuredContentHolder`), and the `rebuildViewHost` SPLIT/PREVIEW branches use that holder as the preview side (mirroring `hasCsvPreview()`). A **transient** tri-state `structuredShowApiDocs` (`null`=auto: API docs for a detected spec, else tree) drives `toggleStructuredView()`; default view auto-picks docs for an OpenAPI file. `setStructuredPreviewEnabled` is pushed from `MainController.applyViewSettings` (like `setCsvRainbowEnabled`). **Every `set*PreviewEnabled` ends in the shared `reconcilePreviewMode()`** — leave the preview iff `!hasPreview()`. Never re-add a per-format `isX()` test there: one setting backs several formats (XML's tree rides `structuredPreview`, yet `isStructured()` is false for XML → the buffer was **stranded** in PREVIEW, where every `scheduleRenderPreview` branch misses and falls through to the **unconditional Markdown tail**, rendering the source as Markdown, with `hasPreview()`=false also removing the toggle needed to escape), and one file can have two previews (a workflow is YAML → turning off structured **evicted** it from its own still-enabled preview and clobbered the per-file mode persisted in `WorkspaceState.markdownViewModes`) + `ensurePreviewControls` re-attaches the 3-mode toggle. Command `structured.toggleView` (tree ⇄ API docs); preview-*support* setting = Settings → Editor → **Structured data** checkbox (the view is toggled by the shared `view.togglePreview`/`view.toggleSplitPreview`); `Settings.structuredPreview` (schema 63→64 additive); i18n ×6 (`structured.*`/`openapi.*`). **New dependency: `jackson-dataformat-yaml`** (+ transitive `org.yaml:snakeyaml` 2.4 — **both real JPMS modules**, so they link directly under jlink with **no moditect** entry; `module-info` `requires com.fasterxml.jackson.dataformat.yaml`). **XML tree** (a 4th format, added later): `.xml` buffers (excluding `.svg`, which is an image, and `.xhtml`, which maps to `html`→browser) get a **faithful DOM tree** via **`structured/XmlNode`** (element/attribute/text/comment — *not* an XML→JSON shoehorn) + **`structured/XmlParser`** (the JDK DOM parser, **no new dependency**, XXE-hardened exactly like `maven/PomParser`; text-only elements inlined as `tag = "value"`, mixed content kept in document order, `MAX_NODES`=50k) rendered by **`editor/XmlTree`** (`.xml-*` cells). It reuses the same self-scrolling `structuredContentHolder` host and the **same `Settings.structuredPreview` gate** (not a new setting): `isXml()`/`hasXmlPreview()` + a `hasTreePreview()` (=`hasStructuredPreview() || hasXmlPreview()`) drives the shared host wiring in `hasPreview()`/`rebuildViewHost`/the mode-setter tail; a separate `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch parses off-thread → `renderXml`. Unit-tested `XmlParserTest` (incl. an XXE-blocked case). *Deferred: GeoJSON map (an offline vector plot — Editora ships no network tiles), specialized XML-dialect renderers (RSS/Atom feed view, like `OpenApiDoc` for JSON), jump-from-tree-node-to-source-line (needs Jackson/DOM location tracking), per-file view persistence (`WorkspaceState`), expand/collapse-all, and editing (read-only preview).*
- **SVG image preview** (`editor/SvgImages`; on by default, `Settings.svgPreview`, schema 64→65). A `.svg` file stays a normal XML **text** buffer (so it keeps XML highlighting + the lemminx LSP — `LanguageRegistry` still maps `svg`→`xml`), but gains a rendered-image preview in the same 3-mode view as Markdown. `EditorBuffer.isSvg()` is an **extension check** (not a language change, to avoid disturbing XML LSP/folding), `hasSvgPreview()` (= `svgPreviewEnabled && isSvg() && !hugeFile`) folds into `hasPreview()`, and a `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch renders it exactly like the Mermaid/diagram image branch (image node in the preview `ScrollPane`, zoom scales fit width). **`editor/SvgImages`** is the async engine — a near-copy of `MermaidImages`/`DiagramImages` but **in-process** (no CLI/theme): a `svg-render` daemon pool + LRU cache keyed by `sha256(source)`, rasterizing via **`PreviewImageLoader.rasterizeSvg(bytes)`** (JSVG → JavaFX `Loaded`; the same rasterizer already bundled for Markdown badge images, so **no new dependency**). `setSvgPreviewEnabled` pushed from `MainController.applyViewSettings` + `ensurePreviewControls` (like the structured gate); preview-*support* setting = Settings → Editor → **SVG** checkbox; `.md-svg`/`.svg-error` CSS mirroring `.md-diagram`; i18n ×6 (`svg.*`). `PreviewImageLoader.svgToPng`/rasterization unit-tested (`PreviewImageLoaderTest`, headless Java2D). First of the "reuse-existing-deps" preview cluster (next candidates: PDF via PDFBox, Excel/ODS via POI, XML tree, font specimen, archive contents). *Deferred: export-as-PNG from the preview, a checkerboard backdrop for transparent SVGs.*
- `cron/` + **crontab schedule preview** (`editor/CrontabPreview`; on by default, `Settings.crontabPreview`, schema 65→66). A `crontab`/`*.cron`/`*.crontab`/`cron.d/*` file (language `crontab` via `ConfigFileType`, already syntax-highlighted via the `text.crontab` grammar) gains the same 3-mode Editor/Split/Preview view as Markdown, decoding each job into plain English + the next fire times. Pure, java.base-only, unit-tested **`com.editora.cron`** package: **`CronField`** (parses one field — `*`, `,` lists, `a-b` ranges, `*/n`/`a-b/n` steps, JAN–DEC/SUN–SAT names, 7=Sunday wrap — into an expanded value set + structure for describe; range/out-of-range → a `ParseException` with a user-facing message), **`CronExpression`** (5-field + the `@reboot @yearly @annually @monthly @weekly @daily @midnight @hourly` macros; `parse` returns a `Parsed{expr,error}` — field-level error text, never throws — so the preview red-flags the exact bad line; `describe()` → English ("At 02:30, Monday through Friday", "Every 15 minutes", "At midnight"/"noon" special-cased); `nextRuns(from,n)` minute-steps forward, budgeting `MAX_SCAN_MINUTES` ≈ 4 years **per result** (the scan counter resets after each hit) so a sparse schedule whose period exceeds 4 years — a leap-day `0 0 29 2 *`, a yearly `0 0 1 JAN *` — still returns all `n` runs, while an impossible spec like Feb 31 still terminates (a full scan with no hit ends the loop); it was one shared budget across all `n`, which found only the first occurrence of such a schedule (#477); **`matches`** implements the classic Vixie **day-of-month/day-of-week OR-rule** — when *both* fields are restricted (neither literal `*`), a time fires if *either* matches. **`describe()` must gate on that same `isStar()` predicate and join the two day parts with "or"** — it used `coversAll()` + " and ", so `0 0 13 * 5` read as "day 13 **and** Friday" (= Friday the 13th — the very gotcha the OR-rule *is*) and `0 0 1-31 * 5` dropped the day-of-month and claimed "on Friday" while firing **daily**, all while the next-run times beside it in the preview said otherwise. Day-of-week parses over **0-7** and folds `7`→`0` only *after* a range is expanded (Vixie's order): folding first turned the canonical weekend `6-7` into `lo=6, hi=0` → "range start after end" for a schedule real cron runs. `CronExpressionTest` pins all three, and `nextRuns` is diff-tested clean against **croniter** over 21 expressions), and **`Crontab`** (splits a file into `Assignment`s (`NAME=value`, quote-unwrapped), `Job`s (5-field or `@macro` + command, tolerant of tabs/extra whitespace), dropping comments/blanks). **`editor/CrontabPreview`** (in `editor`, no `ui` dep) renders it as a self-scrolling node (header + assignments + per-job command/English-schedule/next-runs, red row for a parse error). `EditorBuffer` mirrors the structured/SVG gates: `isCrontab()` (= `"crontab".equals(language)`), `hasCrontabPreview()` (= `crontabPreviewEnabled && isCrontab() && !hugeFile`) folded into `hasPreview()` **and `hasTreePreview()`** (so it reuses `structuredContentHolder` + `rebuildViewHost` + the mode-setter tail with zero new host plumbing), a `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch (parse off-thread on `PREVIEW_POOL` with the "now" captured on the FX thread, `previewGen`-guarded), and `setCrontabPreviewEnabled` pushed from `MainController.applyViewSettings`. Snapshot **Export-to-PDF/Print** rides the existing tree-host path (`snapshotPreviewChunks` gained a crontab branch → `CrontabPreview.content(...)` → `snapshotNodePng`, forced light). Preview-*support* setting = Settings → Editor → **Crontab** checkbox; `.crontab-*` CSS (AtlantaFX semantic colors, theme-tracking); i18n ×6 (`crontab.*`). **No new dependency / `module-info` change** (rides the existing crontab grammar + the structured preview host). *Deferred: 6-field cron (seconds/year), Quartz `L`/`W`/`#` modifiers, a 24h×7d heat-grid view, timezone-aware next-run display.*
- `fstab/` + **fstab mount preview** (`editor/FstabPreview`; on by default, `Settings.fstabPreview`, schema 67→68). An `/etc/fstab` file (language `fstab` via `ConfigFileType`, already syntax-highlighted via the `source.fstab` grammar) gains the same 3-mode Editor/Split/Preview view, decoding each mount line into plain English — the crontab-preview pattern applied to fstab's columns.
