Pure, java.base-only, unit-tested **`com.editora.fstab`** package: **`FstabEntry`** (record of the 6 columns — spec/mountPoint/fsType/options/dump/pass — with a nullable `error` + `isSwap()`), **`Fstab`** (`parse(text)` → `List<FstabEntry>`, dropping comments/blanks; 4–6 whitespace columns, dump/pass default 0, `<4`/`>6`/non-numeric dump-or-pass → an entry with an `error`), and **`FstabDescribe`** (the decode: `device(spec)` — `UUID=`/`PARTUUID=`/`LABEL=`/`PARTLABEL=`, `//host/share`→SMB/CIFS, `host:/export`→NFS, `/dev/*`, and the `proc`/`sysfs`/`tmpfs`/`none` pseudo-FS keywords; `summary(entry)` — "Mount … at … as ext4" or "Swap space on …"; `options(entry)` — a per-option dictionary mapping the boolean flags (`noatime`→"access times not updated", `nofail`→"boot continues even if the device is missing", `nosuid`/`noexec`/`nodev`/`_netdev`/`discard`/`bind`/…) and the `key=value` opts (`uid=`/`gid=`/`umask=`/`size=`/`errors=`/`commit=`/`compress=`/`subvol=`/`data=`), unknown tokens passing through verbatim; `checkLine(entry)` — "fsck-checked first (root) · not backed up"). **`editor/FstabPreview`** (in `editor`, no `ui` dep) renders a self-scrolling node (header + per-entry mount-point/summary/options/fsck-note, red row for a malformed line). `EditorBuffer` mirrors the crontab gates exactly: `isFstab()` (= `"fstab".equals(language)`), `hasFstabPreview()` folded into `hasPreview()` **and `hasTreePreview()`** (reuses `structuredContentHolder` + `rebuildViewHost`), a `scheduleRenderPreview()` branch (parse off-thread on `PREVIEW_POOL`, `previewGen`-guarded), `setFstabPreviewEnabled` from `applyViewSettings`, and a `snapshotPreviewChunks` branch for snapshot Export-to-PDF/Print (forced light). Preview-*support* setting = Settings → Editor → **fstab** checkbox; `.fstab-*` CSS; i18n ×6 (`fstab.*`). **No new dependency / `module-info` change** (rides the existing fstab grammar + the structured preview host). *Deferred: btrfs subvolume tree, per-option man-page links, a fstab-vs-currently-mounted diff.*
- `systemd/` + `sshconfig/` + `dockerfile/` — **three more config-file previews** (`editor/SystemdPreview`/`SshConfigPreview`/`DockerfilePreview`; all on by default — `Settings.systemdPreview`/`sshConfigPreview`/`dockerfilePreview`, one schema bump 73→74). Each decodes an already-recognized config language into plain English in the same 3-mode view, following the crontab/fstab pattern (pure package + `editor/*Preview` node into the shared self-scrolling `structuredContentHolder`; `is*()`/`has*Preview()` folded into `hasPreview()`+`hasTreePreview()`; off-thread `scheduleRenderPreview()` + `snapshotPreviewChunks()` branches; `set*PreviewEnabled` from `applyViewSettings`; a preview-*support* Settings → Editor checkbox each (the view is toggled by the shared `view.togglePreview`/`view.toggleSplitPreview`); i18n ×6). **`com.editora.systemd`** (language `systemd`, the `.service`/`.timer`/`.socket`/… extensions): **`SystemdUnit`** (INI parse → ordered `Section`/`Directive`, keeping duplicates + `\`-continuations), **`SystemdCalendar`** (the crown jewel — parses `OnCalendar=`: the `minutely`/`hourly`/`daily`/`weekly`/`monthly`/`yearly`/`quarterly`/`semiannually` shorthands + the general `[weekdays] [y-m-d] H:M[:S]` form with `*`/list/`a..b` range/`start/step` per field; `describe()` → English ("At 02:30, Monday through Friday", "Daily at 02:00", "Every 15 minutes"), `nextRuns(from,n)` minute-steps bounded ~4 years, `parse` returns a field-level error not a throw), **`TimeSpan`** (systemd time spans "1h 30min"/"15min"/bare-seconds → total seconds + English, for the `On*Sec=` monotonic timers + `RestartSec=`), and **`SystemdDescribe`** (`kind()` from the type-specific section + a per-directive `gloss()` dictionary — ExecStart/Type/User/Restart/After/Wants/WantedBy/ListenStream/OnCalendar/On*Sec/…, unknown key → null so the preview shows raw `Key=value`). The preview shows each directive's gloss above the raw line + `OnCalendar` next-runs. **`com.editora.sshconfig`** (language `ssh-config`): **`SshConfig`** (parse into a `global` block + `Host`/`Match` blocks of `Keyword value` options, `=`-or-space-separated, quote-stripped; `effective(blocks, host, key)` applies ssh's **first-obtained-value-wins** rule across the whole file — `global` matches every host, a `Host` block matches per `SshPattern` — and `isConcreteHost(argument)` tells a single concrete host name from a wildcard/multi-pattern line) + **`SshPattern`** (OpenSSH `Host` glob matching — whitespace-separated patterns, `*` spans dots, `?` = one char, `!`-negation disqualifies the line, **case-sensitive**; all verified against `ssh -G`) + **`SshConfigDescribe`** (`summary(blocks, block)` → "Connects to <HostName> on port <Port> as <User>, key <IdentityFile>, via jump host <ProxyJump>"; for a **concrete-host** block the values are *resolved across the file* so an earlier `Host *` overriding `User`/`Port` is reflected — matching what `ssh` actually does, not the block's own line, which previously stated the opposite (#476); a wildcard/multi-pattern block describes a class of hosts, not one connection, so its own declared values are shown. Plus a per-option `gloss()` — ForwardAgent/ProxyJump/ServerAliveInterval/…). **`com.editora.dockerfile`** (language `dockerfile`): **`Dockerfile`** (parse into build `Stage`s split on `FROM … AS name`, `\`-continuations, `ARG` before the first FROM = global) + **`DockerfileDescribe`** (`title(stage)` + `summaryLines(stage)` — a curated digest: exposed ports/workdir/user/env-count/volumes/entrypoint/cmd/healthcheck/build-step-count, not a gloss of every instruction). All three reuse the existing grammars (`source.systemd`/`source.ssh-config`/`source.dockerfile`); **no new dependency / `module-info` change**. *Deferred: systemd second-granularity next-runs + `.network`/`.link` specifics, ssh `Match`/`Include` resolution, Dockerfile ARG-substitution in image names.*
- `ghactions/` + **GitHub Actions workflow preview** (`editor/GithubActionsPreview`; on by default, `Settings.githubActionsPreview`, schema 74→75). The first **content-detected YAML-dialect** preview: a workflow file stays language `yaml` (keeps YAML highlighting + the yaml LSP), but its buffer is recognized as a workflow by **content** (not path/extension) and routed to a specialized digest instead of the generic YAML tree. Pure, unit-tested **`com.editora.ghactions`**: **`GithubActions.looksLikeWorkflow(text)`** — the sniff (a top-level `on:` **and** `jobs:` key, iterated line-by-line via `indexOf` without splitting the whole string, bounded to the first 400 lines), and **`Workflow.parse(text)`** — reads the YAML via the existing `YAMLMapper` into a `JsonNode` (no new dep, no `module-info` opens — like `structured/`) and walks it into a toolkit-free model: `name`, human trigger phrases from the `on:` key (**handles the YAML-1.1 `on`→boolean-`true` key gotcha** by checking both `"on"` and `"true"`; `push`/`pull_request` → "push to main, dev"/"pull request to main" from the `branches`/`tags`/`paths` filters, `workflow_dispatch` → "manual dispatch", `release`(types), and a **`schedule:` cron decoded via `com.editora.cron.CronExpression`** → "on a schedule (…Monday through Friday)"), and each `Job` (id/name/`runs-on`/`needs`/`if`/matrix + `Step`s whose `label()` = the step name, else the short action name — `actions/checkout@v4`→"checkout" — else `run: <first line>`). `EditorBuffer.isGithubActions()` = `"yaml".equals(language)` + `GithubActions.looksLikeWorkflow(area.getText(0, min(len, 65536)))` (a **bounded head read**, so a large non-workflow YAML doesn't cost a full `getText()` per `hasPreview()` call); `hasGithubActionsPreview()` folded into `hasPreview()`+`hasTreePreview()`, and its `scheduleRenderPreview()`/`snapshotPreviewChunks()` branches **precede the structured (YAML tree) branch** so a workflow wins — turning the feature off falls back to the YAML tree (`setGithubActionsPreviewEnabled` only forces the editor when `!hasPreview()`). Preview-*support* setting = Settings → Editor → **GitHub Actions** checkbox; `.ghactions-*` CSS; i18n ×6 (`ghactions.*`). **No new dependency / `module-info` change** (reuses the yaml + cron support). *Deferred: a workflow⇄YAML-tree toggle (like OpenAPI's tree⇄docs), composite `action.yml`, and the next YAML dialects (docker-compose, Kubernetes manifests).*
- `lsp/` — **Language Server Protocol** support (off by default, gated by `Settings.lspSupport`). **Servers: Java** (Eclipse **JDT LS**, `jdtls`), **TypeScript/JavaScript** (`typescript-language-server --stdio`, serving js/ts/jsx/tsx), **Python** (`pyright-langserver --stdio`), **XML** (`lemminx`, serving the `xml` language id — xml/xsd/xsl/svg/fxml/pom/…), **JSON** (`vscode-json-language-server --stdio`), **Bash/Shell** (`bash-language-server start`, serving the `shell` language id — sh/bash/zsh; its diagnostics come from `shellcheck` when that's on PATH), **YAML** (`yaml-language-server --stdio`), **Go** (`gopls`, root markers `go.mod`/`go.work`), **Rust** (`rust-analyzer`, root marker `Cargo.toml`), **PHP** (`phpactor language-server`, root marker `composer.json`), **Ruby** (`ruby-lsp`, root markers `Gemfile`/`.ruby-version`), **C/C++** (`clangd` — one server serving both the `c` and `cpp` language ids, root markers `compile_commands.json`/`CMakeLists.txt`/…), **HTML** (`vscode-html-language-server --stdio`), **CSS** (`vscode-css-language-server --stdio`), **Kotlin** (`kotlin-language-server`), **Lua** (`lua-language-server`), **Dockerfile** (`docker-langserver --stdio`), **SQL** (`sqls`), **Terraform** (`terraform-ls serve`, root markers `.terraform`/lock file), **TOML** (`taplo lsp stdio`), and **C#** (`csharp-ls`, root markers `global.json`/`.git`) — **twenty-one servers** total. Most already had highlighting + folding, so each was just a registry/Settings entry; the five with **no grammar** (PHP, Lua, Dockerfile, Terraform, TOML) each got a bundled `*.tmLanguage.json` (PHP `source.php` from VS Code MIT; Lua/Dockerfile/Terraform/TOML `source.lua`/`source.dockerfile`/`source.hcl.terraform`/`source.toml` from the shiki tm-grammars collection — see NOTICE) + `LanguageRegistry`/`FoldRegions`/`Indenter`/`Commenter` entries, like the JS/TS case. **Dockerfile** is matched by **filename** (extension-less `Dockerfile`/`Containerfile`, or a `Dockerfile.<tag>` suffix) via a special case in both `LanguageRegistry.forFileName` and `GrammarRegistry.scopeForFileName`; TOML moved off the borrowed INI grammar onto its own `source.toml`. **Adding a server = one `ServerDef` in `LspServerRegistry` + its id in `MainController.LSP_SERVER_IDS` + the served language id(s) in `EditorBuffer.LSP_LANGUAGES` + a Settings command/enable pair** (the Settings → LSP page is **data-driven** over a `SettingsWindow.lspServerUis()` descriptor list, so a new server is one entry there too) — `LspManager.configure(enabled, Map<serverId,command>)` is map-based so it never needs a signature change. The registry is **server-centric**: `LspServerRegistry` lists each server with the language ids it serves + its root markers (Java: `pom.xml`/`build.gradle`/…; TS: `tsconfig.json`/`jsconfig.json`/`package.json`/`.git`), so `LspManager` keys **one session per `(serverId, root)`** and js/ts/jsx/tsx in one project share a single `tsserver`. Each server has its own configurable command (`Settings.javaLspCommand`/`typescriptLspCommand`; blank ⇒ default) + its own cached availability probe; `MainController` detects each independently and gates each buffer by *its* server's availability and the file's language id (`EditorBuffer.getLanguage()`, which here doubles as the LSP languageId: `java`/`javascript`/`javascriptreact`/`typescript`/`typescriptreact`/`python`/`xml`/`json`/`shell`/`yaml`/`go`/`rust`/`php`/`ruby`/`c`/`cpp`/`html`/`css`/`kotlin`/`lua`/`dockerfile`/`sql`/`terraform`/`toml`/`csharp`). **JS/TS also get syntax highlighting** — bundled `typescript.tmLanguage.json` (`source.ts`) + `typescriptreact.tmLanguage.json` (`source.tsx`) grammars from VS Code (MIT, see NOTICE); `.ts/.mts/.cts/.js/.mjs/.cjs`→`source.ts`, `.tsx/.jsx`→`source.tsx` (the TS grammar tokenizes plain JS, so no separate JS grammar), with the extensions registered in `LanguageRegistry`/`FoldRegions`/`Indenter`/`Commenter`. **Auto-imports**: accepting an LSP completion runs an optional `Completion.onAccept` hook (`CompletionMapper.map(items, onAcceptFor)`); for an item that `mayHaveAdditionalEdits` (carries resolve `data`), `MainController.autoImportAccept` → `LspManager.resolveCompletion` (`completionItem/resolve`) and applies the resolved `additionalTextEdits` (e.g. a TS `import` line) via `EditorBuffer.applyLspEdits(List<editor/LspTextEdit>)` (offset-mapped, sorted ascending + overlap-skipped, then committed as **one `MultiChangeBuilder` commit** so a multi-line Format Document / an auto-import's edits are a **single undo unit** rather than one Ctrl-Z per edit — #415's Format-Document sub-item; a lone edit stays a plain `replaceText`; the `LspTextEdit` record keeps `editor` lsp4j-free). Uses **LSP4J** (`org.eclipse.lsp4j` + `.jsonrpc`, automatic modules → moditect-patched in the `dist` profile like tm4e/pdfbox; jsonrpc reuses the existing `gson`). `module-info` **`opens com.editora.lsp;`** (unqualified, **not** qualified-to-jsonrpc) because Gson reflectively reads our `@JsonNotification("language/status")` param DTO (`LanguageServerSession.LanguageStatus`) and, under `mvn javafx:run`, runs in the **unnamed** module — a qualified opens to `org.eclipse.lsp4j.jsonrpc` alone leaves it unable to set the DTO fields accessible. **`LanguageServerSession`** runs one external server process per workspace root over stdio: it launches via `ProcessBuilder` reusing `ProcessRunner.resolveExecutable`/`applyStandardEnv` (the GUI-launch PATH augmentation, so a Finder-launched `.app` finds `jdtls`), drives it with an LSP4J `Launcher` on a daemon executor, implements `LanguageClient` (receives `publishDiagnostics`/log/show-message), does `initialize`/`initialized` + client capabilities, full-text document sync (`didOpen`/`didChange`/`didSave`/`didClose`), the request subset (completion/hover/definition/references), **queues requests until initialize completes**, and `shutdown`+`exit` on dispose. **The server's stderr is drained on a daemon thread** (`LanguageServerSession.drainStderr`, capped, into the Debug Log so a failed launch surfaces *why* — missing JDK, lock, bad command) — it **must** be consumed: leaving it a PIPE lets a chatty server (jdtls logs heavily) fill the ~64 KB OS pipe buffer and block mid-startup (LSP traffic is on stdout). (The standalone DAP adapters still `Redirect.DISCARD` their stderr instead.) **Dispose kills the whole descendant process tree** via **`process/ProcessRegistry.killTree`**, not just the launcher: jdtls (and others) is a wrapper script (Homebrew `jdtls` → python → java), so destroying only the wrapper **orphans the real server JVM**, which keeps running and holds its Eclipse workspace `.lock` — the next session for the same root then can't acquire the lock and hangs (no diagnostics/completion). **Per-project jdtls workspace:** to avoid that lock contention up front, jdtls is launched with **`-data <configDir>/jdtls-workspaces/<sha256(root)>`** (`LspServerRegistry.withDataDir`/`workspaceDirName`, pure/unit-tested; base dir injected via `LspManager.setJdtlsWorkspaceBase` from `applyLspSupport`) so each root gets its own Eclipse workspace instead of the single shared default (which deadlocked when two roots — or a leaked run, or another editor — contended for it, leaving `initialize` unresolved → loading bar spinning forever + dead completion). The workspace persists across sessions (jdtls's index is reused); a user-supplied `-data` in the configured command is respected (`withDataDir` no-ops then). **`com.editora.process.ProcessRegistry`** is the central lifecycle owner for *every* spawned external server (LSP **and** DAP — `LanguageServerSession.start` and `DapClient.connectStdio`/`setAdapterProcess` call `ProcessRegistry.track(process)`): (1) **`killTree(process)`** destroys the descendant tree (children first so the wrapper can't reparent-orphan its child), then escalates to a **force-kill after a `GRACE_MS` grace period** if SIGTERM is ignored — **non-blocking** (a daemon scheduler), so it's safe on the FX thread during a window close; (2) a **JVM shutdown hook** (`installShutdownHook`, called from `App.main`) force-kills every tracked tree on exit — covering a normal quit *and* SIGTERM/`kill`/OS-quit/most crashes, the paths that bypass the window-close teardown and used to leak servers; (3) a small on-disk **ledger** (`<configDir>/spawned-servers.txt`, set via `setLedgerFile`) records each spawned root pid + start-time + executable, and **`reapOrphans()`** (called once from `App.start` *before* any window builds) kills any server **leaked by a previous run that died too hard for the hook** (SIGKILL / power loss). The pure `LedgerEntry` parse/format + `shouldReap(...)` decision (reap only when pid **and** start-instant **and** executable all match — so it can never kill an unrelated reused PID) are unit-tested (`ProcessRegistryTest`). `untrack` + an `onExit` self-clean keep the live set/ledger accurate; only long-lived servers are tracked (short-lived start-then-destroy probes aren't). Uses only `java.base` — no dependency / `module-info` change. **`LspManager`** is the UI-facing facade (mirrors `MermaidService`: one session per `(lang, root)`, cached async `detect()`, request `CompletableFuture`s marshaled to the FX thread via `Platform.runLater`, neutral `Target(file,line,char)` results, mapped-diagnostics callback, `shutdownAll`). Pure/unit-tested helpers: **`LspServerRegistry`** (language→spec + command tokenization; `java`→`jdtls`, root markers `pom.xml`/`build.gradle`/…), **`RootResolver`** (active project → nearest build file → file's dir), **`LspPositions`** (offset↔LSP line/char), **`DiagnosticMapper`** (LSP `Diagnostic`→`editor/LspDiagnostic`), **`CompletionMapper`** (`CompletionItem`→`completion/Completion`; snippet-format items fall back to the label so `$0` placeholders aren't inserted). **Diagnostics UI** (`editor/`): `LspDiagnostic` (range+severity record) + `LspDiagnosticOverlay` (a `Canvas` mirroring `MermaidLintOverlay`, multi-line/range-aware, severity colors, visible-paragraphs + coalesced, `CanvasGuards`). **Diagnostic stripes** (IntelliJ-style, fed by the same `setLspDiagnostics`, both gated on `lspActive`): the **minimap** edge stripes (`Minimap.setDiagnostics`/`setDiagnosticsEnabled` — errors-on-top; the LSP setters only repaint stripes over an *already-cached* snapshot and **never** force a `renderContent()`/`snapshot()`, since a synchronous snapshot during the editor's first layout blanks the surface until a relayout), plus an always-on thin **`editor/DiagnosticStripe`** docked over the vertical scrollbar that maps the whole document to its height by the editor's real content metrics (`totalHeightEstimate` ÷ paragraph count, read lazily at draw time — **no listener**, which would force eager re-computation and starve repaints) so marks sit at the actual on-screen line; mouse-transparent until it has marks, hover shows the message, click jumps via `EditorBuffer.jumpToLine`; releases its canvas to 1×1 when empty. `EditorBuffer` mirrors the mermaid hooks — `setLspActive`/`setLspDiagnostics`/`setLspChangeListener` (debounced `multiPlainChanges`→didChange)/`setLspCompletionProvider` + an `installLspHover` diagnostic tooltip — kept decoupled (`editor` imports nothing from `lsp`; `isLspLanguage()` checks a hardcoded set of the served languages, kept in sync with `LspServerRegistry`). `ui/ProblemsPanel` (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `SearchPanel`; id `problems`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.problems`/`M-8`) groups diagnostics **by programming language → file → diagnostic** (language via `LanguageRegistry.forFileName`, a friendly `.problem-lang-row` header). **The active file sorts to the top** (IDE convention): `ProblemsPanel.setActiveFile(canonicalPath)` — pushed on every tab switch via `LspCoordinator.setProblemsActiveFile` — orders the active file's language group first and, within it, the active file first, re-sorting the cached tree without needing fresh diagnostics (pure/unit-tested `ui/ActiveFileOrder`, shared with the TODO window; the caller passes the canonical path so it matches the LSP diagnostic keys). **`MainController`** owns the manager + an `lspProblems` map **scoped to open files** — a server publishes diagnostics project-wide (jdtls especially), so `onLspDiagnostics` drops any file without an open tab to keep the Problems window from filling with whole-workspace noise; the open-tab lookup (`tabForPath`) matches by **canonical (symlink-resolved) path** via `MainController.canonicalPath` (`Path.toRealPath`, falling back to `toAbsolutePath().normalize()`) — a server reports diagnostics under the file's *real* URI (e.g. `/private/tmp/…` for a `/tmp/…` symlink on macOS, or any symlinked project dir) while a buffer keeps the path as opened, so plain `normalize()` matching silently **dropped every diagnostic** (no squiggles, empty Problems) — the unit-tested fix. **The `problems` map is itself keyed by the canonical path** (`LspCoordinator.onDiagnostics`/`clearDiagnostics` run the file through `Ops.canonicalize` → `MainController.canonicalPath`) so the server-reported key agrees with `setProblemsActiveFile` (given the canonical active path) and the tab-close clear — otherwise the active file's group never sorted to the top of Problems for a symlinked file, since `ActiveFileOrder.isActive` compares with `normalize()`, which doesn't resolve symlinks (#470; FX-tested with a real symlink). `applyLspSupport()`/`applyLspGating()`/`ifLsp()` mirror `applyMermaidSupport` (configure → async detect → per-buffer `syncBufferLsp` open/activate/close), run at init + every settings apply; lifecycle: open on `addBuffer`/save-as, didChange (debounced in the buffer), didSave from `writeBuffer`, didClose on tab removal, `shutdownAll` when disabled. **A server starts only for a buffer whose tab has actually been shown** — `wireBuffer` (and `applyGating`) call **`syncBufferWhenShown`**, which syncs the active buffer immediately and parks the rest in a weakly-keyed `deferredLsp` set that **`onBufferShown`** (wired into `MainController`'s tab-selection listener, beside `setRenderingActive`/`onTabShown`) drains on first switch. `wireBuffer` runs for *every* restored tab, so a session of N files used to fork up to N servers during launch — **measured on an 8-file session: 4 extra server processes (including jdtls, a second JVM plus its Eclipse indexing), ~2× the CPU Editora itself burns while starting, ~225 MB.** Deferring costs the opened file nothing (it's the active buffer) and is invisible except that a background file's diagnostics appear when you first visit it rather than at startup; the disable/close path, capability pushes and gating are unchanged, since a deferred buffer just runs the same `syncBuffer` later. Commands (all `ifLsp`-gated, palette-filtered when off): `lsp.gotoDefinition` (`M-.`), `lsp.findReferences` (`M-?`, ≥2 results → the **References tool window**; a lone result jumps straight there), `lsp.gotoSymbol` (**Go to Symbol in Workspace** — palette-only), `lsp.hover` (`C-c h`, hover markdown via `MarkdownRenderer` in a tooltip), `lsp.restartServers`, `lsp.formatDocument` (whole-file `textDocument/formatting`, palette-only: `LspManager.formatDocument` → `LanguageServerSession.formatting` → `EditorBuffer.applyLspEdits` (undoable); gated by `LspManager.supportsFormatting` reading the `documentFormattingProvider` capability — which **vscode-json/css/html-language-server** only advertise when passed VS Code's `provideFormatter` flag: `LspManager.initOptionsFor(serverId, debugBundles)` (pure/unit-tested, the per-server `initialize.initializationOptions` chooser — java autobuild-off + java-debug bundles, gopls `semanticTokens`) sends `{provideFormatter: true}` for json/css/html, which flips their advertised capability false→true so Format Document works on a `.json`/`.css`/`.html` (they implement the handler but hid it; verified by driving the real servers — the flag flips the capability, #468); `FormattingOptions` from `Settings.tabSize` + `EditorBuffer.detectInsertSpaces`), `tool.problems` (`M-8`), `view.toggleLsp`. **The entire LSP integration lives in `ui/LspCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern). It owns: the nav/format flows (`gotoDefinition`/`findReferences`/`showHover`/`formatDocument` + the hover popup); diagnostics routing (the per-open-file `problems` map + the `ProblemsPanel` + the `onDiagnostics` callback — compact-source-noise filter + open-files scoping); and the **configure/detect/gating + per-buffer lifecycle** — `applySupport()` (mirrors `MermaidCoordinator`; sets the jdtls workspace base, `lspManager.configure(...)`, gates the Run affordance, then per-`SERVER_IDS` detect → `applyGating()`), the per-server `serverEnabled`/`serverCommand`/`setServer*` switches, `serverAvailable` (read by DAP's `debugEffectiveFor` via `lspCoordinator.isServerAvailable("java")`/`serverEnabled("java")`), `syncBuffer()` (open/activate/close + push trigger-chars/format/range-format/semantic flags), `updateStatusBar()` (the `LSP:` segment + Problems availability), `requestStructureSymbols()`, `requestSemanticTokens()`/`applySemanticHighlight()`, `onServerStatus()` (the ready event → refresh capabilities + pull diagnostics + structure), `restartServers()`, `notifyDocumentSaved()`, `wireBuffer()` (the addBuffer hook set: didChange/pull-diagnostics/semantic/completion/doc-resolver/range-formatter/nav-actions + `syncBuffer`), and the `lsp.toggleServer`/`lsp.setServerCommand` pickers. It reaches the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension (open-and-goto / active-editable / lsp-feature-enabled / set-loading-bar / buffer-for-path / set-status-bar-LSP / set-problems-available / set-structure-symbols / refresh-run-button / jdtls-workspace-base / lsp-project-root). The `lsp.*` commands + `buffer.setLspNavActions` delegate to it, and the MCP bridge reads `lspCoordinator.problems()`. The `LspManager` stays owned by `MainController` (Debug layers on the jdtls session, the MCP bridge reads its diagnostics) and is passed to the coordinator as a ctor arg; its `publishDiagnostics`/`status` callbacks route through thin `MainController.onLspDiagnostics`/`onLspServerStatus` method-ref delegates (to dodge an illegal forward reference at the manager's field initializer). `MainController` keeps `lspEnabled()` (used widely by Run/Debug gating), the `ifLsp`/`toggleLsp` command glue, the Problems `ToolWindow` (built with `lspCoordinator.problemsPanel()`), and `canonicalPath`/`tabForPath`. The first three are also prepended to the **editor right-click menu** while `EditorBuffer.isLspActive()` (gated to LSP-on + a managed buffer of a served language); the menu items move the caret to the click offset first so they target the right-clicked symbol (labels reuse the `command.lsp.*` titles — no new i18n keys). **Ctrl/Cmd-click go-to-definition:** the same `EditorBuffer` `MOUSE_PRESSED` filter that opens a Markdown link on Ctrl/Cmd-click also, in a code buffer with `isLspActive()`, moves the caret to the clicked symbol, focuses the area, and fires `lspGotoDefinitionAction` (deferred via `Platform.runLater` so focus/caret settle first) — the IDE go-to-definition gesture, reusing the existing `gotoDefinition` flow (no new command/i18n). It only consumes the click for a served buffer, so a non-LSP file's normal click (and the multi-caret gestures) are untouched. **Format Document** joins that menu only when the server advertises formatting (`EditorBuffer.setLspFormatAvailable`, pushed from `syncBufferLsp` + the ready event like `setLspTriggerChars`). **Tab line re-indent**: in a buffer whose server advertises **range** formatting (`documentRangeFormattingProvider` via `LspManager.supportsRangeFormatting`, pushed to `EditorBuffer.setLspRangeFormatAvailable` alongside the format flag at `syncBufferLsp` + the ready event), plain Tab re-indents the current line to the server's convention — **indentation only**, not a full line reformat. `EditorBuffer.tryLspReindentLine` (in the `addSnippetKeys` Tab branch, after snippet-prefix expansion and before `applySmartTab`) requests `textDocument/rangeFormatting` over the line via the injected `setLspRangeFormatter` (→ `LspManager.rangeFormatting` → `LanguageServerSession.rangeFormatting`), then the pure/unit-tested `editops/LineIndent.formattedIndent` computes the formatted line's leading whitespace and `applyLspLineIndent` applies only that (async, generation-guarded + line-unchanged check). It returns false (→ normal smart-Tab) for a selection, a blank line (formatters strip blank-line whitespace, so a fresh line keeps the local indent), non-LSP buffers, or servers without range formatting; completion-accept / snippet-tab still take Tab first. The status bar shows an **`LSP: <server>`** segment (`StatusBar.setLsp`, `MainController.updateLspStatusBar`) for managed files, clickable → Problems, plus an indeterminate **loading bar** while a server starts (`StatusBar.setLspLoading`) — kept determinate (a fixed value) when idle so its animation timeline can't keep pulsing the scene and starving repaints; flipped indeterminate only during the load. The bar is **cleared when the `initialize` handshake resolves** — `LanguageServerSession` emits a synthetic `onStatus("ServiceReady", null)` on success / `("Error", null)` on failure (null message ⇒ no echo write), which `onLspServerStatus` turns into `setLspLoading(false)`. This is **universal** across every server and a clean file that never publishes a diagnostic — earlier the bar only stopped on incoming diagnostics or jdtls's vendor-specific `language/status`, so a no-diagnostic file (or any non-jdtls server) left it spinning forever. lsp4j's "Unsupported notification method" log noise (JDT LS's `language/status` etc.) is quieted via `App`'s `org.eclipse.lsp4j` logger set to SEVERE. **LSP completion** is an async source merged into the existing `CompletionPopup` for code buffers (`EditorBuffer.requestLspCompletion`/`mergeCompletions`, generation-guarded; LSP items first, then local snippets). **Completion fires on the server's advertised trigger characters**, not just `.`/a word prefix: `LanguageServerSession.capabilities()` carries the `initialize` result, `LspManager.triggerCharacters(file)` (pure `triggerCharsOf(ServerCapabilities)`, unit-tested) reads `completionProvider.triggerCharacters`, and `MainController` pushes the set into `EditorBuffer.setLspTriggerChars` (in `syncBufferLsp` + refreshed on the `onLspServerStatus("ready")` event, since capabilities are only known post-`initialize`); `EditorBuffer.endsWithLspTrigger` checks that set. So `<` in HTML, `:` in CSS, etc. pop the completion (the trigger was previously hardcoded to `.`, so HTML/CSS completion effectively never fired even though the server returns 100+ tag/attr items — confirmed by driving the real `vscode-html-language-server`). **Pull diagnostics** (LSP 3.17 `textDocument/diagnostic`): the client declares `DiagnosticCapabilities`, and for a server advertising a `diagnosticProvider` (vscode-html/css/json, …) `LspManager.pullDiagnostics(file)` requests diagnostics and routes the report through the **same** `onDiagnostics` path as pushed `publishDiagnostics` (`DiagnosticMapper.mapReport` maps a full report, returns null for an "unchanged" report — both unit-tested). No-op for push-only servers (jdtls/Pyright/tsserver have no `diagnosticProvider`). Pulls are debounced on the existing 300 ms didChange pulse (`EditorBuffer.setLspDiagnosticsRequester`, fired *separately* from `lspChangeListener` so a completion-keystroke flush doesn't trigger a pull) + once on save + once when the server reports ready (initial diagnostics). **Settings → LSP** page (enable checkbox + a server-command field **per server** (all twenty-one) with Browse + a live found/not-found status row each via `LspManager.detect(serverId, …)`; **data-driven** — the page, `load()`, `refreshLspStatus()`, and `updateLspRowsEnabled()` all loop over `lspServerUis()` descriptors keyed into `lspEnableChecks`/`lspCommandFields`/`lspStatusLabels` maps, so adding a server is one descriptor; `syncLspCheck` for the palette toggle). `Settings.lspSupport` + a per-server `…LspCommand` + `…LspEnabled` pair for each of the twenty-one server ids (`java`/`typescript`/`python`/`xml`/`json`/`bash`/`yaml`/`go`/`rust`/`php`/`ruby`/`clangd`/`html`/`css`/`kotlin`/`lua`/`dockerfile`/`sql`/`terraform`/`toml`/`csharp`; default on, only effective under the global enable; `MainController.serverEnabled` gates `syncBufferLsp` and `applyLspSupport` calls `LspManager.shutdownServer(serverId)` for a disabled server — **preceded by `clearDiagnosticsForServer(serverId)`** (clears every open buffer served by that id: its Problems-map entry + editor overlay, and closes the document), because *after* the shutdown `isManaged` is false so `syncBuffer`'s else-branch clear (guarded on `isManaged`) is skipped, and with no server left to re-publish an empty list the Problems window would otherwise strand that server's diagnostics forever (#469; FX-tested)). The `configure(...)`/migration maps use `Map.ofEntries` (>10 servers exceed `Map.of`'s overloads). Schema 7→8→9→10→11→12→13 (additive-identity migrations). The Settings → LSP page's per-server **found/not-found** status is colored green/red (`settings-git-found`/`settings-git-missing`, like the Git page). Servers are **auto-detected, never bundled** (`jdtls`/`typescript-language-server`/`pyright-langserver`/`lemminx`/`vscode-json-language-server`/`bash-language-server`/`yaml-language-server`/`gopls`/`rust-analyzer`/`phpactor`/`ruby-lsp`/`clangd`/`vscode-html-language-server`/`vscode-css-language-server`/`kotlin-language-server`/`lua-language-server`/`docker-langserver`/`sqls`/`terraform-ls`/`taplo`/`csharp-ls` on PATH; Settings override). **Document symbols / Structure outline**: `LanguageServerSession.documentSymbol(uri)` (`textDocument/documentSymbol`) + `LspManager.documentSymbols(file, cb)` (capability-gated by the pure/unit-tested `documentSymbolProvider(ServerCapabilities)`) map the response — modern hierarchical `DocumentSymbol` or legacy flat `SymbolInformation` — via `lsp/DocumentSymbolMapper` into the neutral, lsp4j-free `lsp/SymbolNode` tree (`kindName` lowercases the `SymbolKind`; `descendInto` keeps children **only for type-like containers** (class/interface/enum/struct/namespace/module/package/object); every callable (method/function/constructor) is a leaf, so a server reporting method-body internals as children — jdtls emits locals/lambdas/anonymous-class methods, which showed as "methods inside methods" — is flattened away. Nested functions in Python/JS therefore appear flat too). `MainController.requestStructureSymbols(buffer)` pushes it into `ui/StructurePanel.setLspSymbols(buffer, syms)` for the **active** buffer on tab switch, the debounced didChange pulse, and the `onLspServerStatus("ready")` event; the panel renders an LSP-precise hierarchy with per-kind icons (`ui/StructureIcons`); method/function/constructor rows append the server's signature (`SymbolNode.detail`, e.g. `(String x) : void`) in a muted `.structure-detail` colour beside the name — or `()` when there's no detail **and** the label doesn't already carry its own param list (jdtls names methods like `setX(Foo)`, so `StructurePanel.StructureCell.signature` suppresses the redundant `()` to avoid `setX(Foo)()`); plus a **sort** selector (Position/Name/Kind) and a **kind filter**, falling back to the fold-region/TextMate heuristic for non-LSP/remote files, LSP-off, or an empty result (`setLspSymbols(buffer, null)`). Each row also shows its **leading doc comment** as a hover tooltip via the pure/unit-tested `ui/StructureDoc.commentAbove(lines, declLine)` (Javadoc/JSDoc/PHPDoc + plain `/* */` blocks, and `//`/`#`/`--` line-comment runs above the declaration, skipping intervening annotation/decorator lines, capped) — `StructurePanel.attachDocs` reads it from `buffer.getContent()` for both the LSP and heuristic outlines. **Go to Symbol in Workspace** (`workspace/symbol`): `LanguageServerSession.workspaceSymbol(query)` (client capability declared via `WorkspaceClientCapabilities.setSymbol`) + `LspManager.workspaceSymbols(anchorFile, query, cb)` (maps both the legacy flat `SymbolInformation` and modern `WorkspaceSymbol` shapes — the latter's URI-only range-less location → line 0 — into the neutral `WorkspaceSymbolMatch{name, container, kind, file, line, character}`; capability-gated by the pure/unit-tested `workspaceSymbolProvider(ServerCapabilities)`). `LspCoordinator.gotoSymbolInWorkspace` opens **`ui/WorkspaceSymbolPopup`** — an incremental in-scene overlay (modeled on `SearchInFilesPopup`: `OverlayHost`, `editora.ownsKeys`, `Esc`/`C-g` dismiss) whose query field re-runs `workspace/symbol` on the active file's server debounced (150 ms, stale-generation-guarded) as you type; `↑↓`/`C-n`/`C-p` move, Enter jumps to the symbol via `ops.openAndGoto` (cross-file), the query seeded from a single-line selection. Command `lsp.gotoSymbol` (palette-only, no keybinding); reports `status.lsp.workspaceSymbolsUnsupported` when the server lacks the capability. **References tool window**: `lsp.findReferences` (`M-?`) now routes ≥2 results into **`ui/ReferencesPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `ProblemsPanel`; id `references`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `Icons::find`, `tool.references`, **registered default-hidden** — the coordinator `open`s it on demand) — a `TreeView` grouped **by file → reference** (`line:col preview`), Enter / double-click jumps (`ReferencesPanel.Actions` → `ops.openAndGoto`); a **lone** reference jumps straight there (no window). `LspCoordinator` owns the panel (`referencesPanel()`, like `problemsPanel()`) + `previewLine(target)` — the one-line preview comes from the file's **open buffer** when a tab holds it (cheap, FX-safe, reflects unsaved edits), else empty (closed files show just the line number — no disk I/O on the FX thread); the `references` window's availability is gated alongside Problems (`Ops.setProblemsAvailable`), opened via `Ops.openReferencesWindow`. *Deferred: previews for closed files (off-thread read), more languages, on-type formatting, rename/code actions/quick fixes, incremental sync, a TOML-driven server registry.*
- `run/` — **Run a file from a gutter ▶**, **gated by the LSP feature** (`EditorBuffer.setRunEnabled`, pushed = `Settings.lspSupport` from `MainController.applyLspSupport` on init + every settings apply; off ⇒ no gutter glyph / menu item / Run window). **Runnable files**: a **Java 25 compact source file** (JEP 512) — detected by the pure, unit-tested **`editor/CompactSource`** (a `.java` with a `void main(` at **brace depth 0** after blanking comments/string/char/text-block literals length-preservingly; `mainLine(source)` is the glyph line) — **any Python script** (`language == "python"`; the glyph sits on the `if __name__ == "__main__":` guard via `EditorBuffer.pythonRunLine`, else the first line) — **or a shell script** (`language == "shell"`, glyph on line 0/the shebang) **but only when the Bash LSP server is enabled** (`EditorBuffer.setShellRunEnabled`, pushed = `lspSupport && Settings.bashLspEnabled` from `applyLspSupport`/`addBuffer`; a per-buffer gate *separate* from `setRunEnabled` so Java/Python are unaffected — they need only the global LSP feature) — **or a GNU Makefile** (`language == "makefile"`, `EditorBuffer.isMakefile()`): unlike the single-entry script types, **every rule target gets its own gutter ▶** (the `.http` multi-glyph model), and clicking it runs `make -f <file> <target>` in the file's dir. The pure/unit-tested **`run/MakefileTargets.parse`** extracts each runnable target's name + 0-based line (skipping recipe lines, variable assignments `:=`/`?=`/…, directives, `%` pattern rules, `.PHONY`/dot targets, and `$var` names), stored as a line→name map that `recomputeRun` fills alongside the `.http` request-line set (both set `runnable=true` + `runLine=-1`); the generic **"Run File"** / `file.run` runs the **default goal** (bare `make`). `RunCoordinator.runMakeTarget(buffer, target)` saves first then streams via `RunService` (`-f <basename>` so a `build.mk`/`Makefile.inc` buffer runs *itself*, not the dir's default Makefile); `MainController` wires `setMakeRunHandler`. Rides the same Run-feature gate as Java/Python — **no `make`-on-PATH detection** (a missing `make` surfaces as a clear `onError` in the Run console). **Shebang language detection** (pure/unit-tested **`editor/Shebang`**): when a file's extension resolves to plaintext, `EditorBuffer.maybeApplyShebang` (run at the top of `recomputeRun`) promotes it to the language named by a first-line interpreter shebang — direct path (`#!/bin/bash`), `env` lookup (`#!/usr/bin/env python3`), or `env -S` with args — reducing the interpreter to its basename (version-stripped: `python3.12`→python), mapping it to a **representative extension**, and resolving language+grammar through the normal `forFileName("shebang.<ext>")` path so highlighting/folding/run/LSP all follow (shell for bash/zsh/sh/dash/ksh/…, python, javascript for node, typescript for deno/bun/ts-node/tsx, ruby, php, lua, groovy, powershell). A `java --source N` shebang → Java compact source: `getShebangJavaSource()` widens `recomputeRun`'s compact-source branch (via `CompactSource.hasTopLevelMain`, no `.java` needed) and feeds `RunCoordinator.buildRunCommand` a `java --source N <file>` argv (an extensionless file needs the flag). It never overrides a real extension or the user's status-bar language pick (`setLanguageOverride` sets a `languageUserOverride` guard). *(jdtls keys off `.java`, so an extensionless Java shebang file gets highlighting/run but likely no jdtls LSP; python/shell LSP work since the languageId is sent explicitly. The tab file-icon stays generic — it's filename-based.)* `EditorBuffer.recomputeRun` caches `runnable`/`runLine` (recomputed on load, Save-As, and the debounced 150 ms edit pulse; skipped for large files), fires `onRunnableChanged`, and exposes `isRunnable()`/`isPython()`/`isShell()` + `setRunHandler` (→ controller `runActiveFile`). **Gutter affordance**: `FoldManager.setRunHooks(enabled, isRunLine, onRun)` reserves a fixed `RUN_SLOT_WIDTH` slot **just left of the line number, only while runnable** (so other files' gutters are unaffected and the glyph never shifts text), drawing a clickable green play glyph (`FoldManager.runGlyph()`, `.run-marker`, right-aligned) on the entry line; the same glyph is the **right-click "Run File"** item. **`run/RunService.run(file, argv, listener)`** streams a launched program — `[java, <file>]` (JDK source-file launcher; needs JDK 25 on PATH, no `--enable-preview` since JEP 512 is final in 25), `[python3, <file>]`, or `[bash, <file>]` (the controller picks by `isPython()`/`isShell()`, else java) — via `ProcessBuilder` reusing `ProcessRunner.resolveExecutable`/`applyStandardEnv`, two daemon reader threads posting stdout/stderr to the FX thread (generation-guarded), `stop()` kills it; **`sendInput(line)`** writes one line to the process's stdin off-thread (so `IO.readln`-style console programs work) and **`detectJavaMajor(cb)`** probes `java -version` once (cached; the pure `javaMajorOf` parse handles the legacy `1.8` scheme — tested) so `runActiveFile` can **preflight** a java run and report a clear "needs JDK 25 — found Java N" instead of a cryptic launcher error. **Program arguments**: per-file args persist in `WorkspaceState.programArgs` (path → raw string; additive field), tokenized by the pure/unit-tested **`run/ProgramArgs.tokenize`** (quote-aware) and appended to the run argv; **the same stored args feed debug launches** (`DapManager.setProgramArgs` before `startLaunch` — sticky across `restart()`; `LaunchConfig.launch` already took java args, `program(...)` gained an args overload for debugpy/js-debug). Commands `file.runWithArgs` (prompt pre-filled via `promptText`, saved per file) and `run.rerun` (re-runs the last file+argv). **Clickable stack traces**: the pure/unit-tested **`run/StackTraceLinks.parse(line)`** recognizes Java (`(File.java:12)`), Python (`File "/path", line N`), and Node (`/path/x.js:12:5`) frames; double-clicking such a console line (the shared `RunPanel.installLinkClicks`, also installed on the Debug console) resolves the file (absolute path → direct; bare Java name → open tabs → the run file's dir → the project root) and jumps via `openAndGoto`. **jdtls noise filter**: for a compact buffer (`language==java && isRunnable()`), `onLspDiagnostics` drops implicit-class complaints from a server whose compliance predates JDK 25 (pure `MainController.isCompactSourceNoise`, tested) while real errors still surface. Bundled `snippets/java.json` gained `cmain` (compact main skeleton) + `ioprintln`/`ioreadln` (JEP 512 final dropped the implicit static IO import, so bodies use `IO.println`). **`ui/RunPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent`; tool id `run`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.run`/`M-9`, `Icons.run()`) is a read-only monospace console (output capped) with Stop/Clear + a run-state header. The window wiring lives in **`ui/RunCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `RunService` + the `RunPanel`, the `runActiveFile`/`rerunLast`/`launchRun`/`buildRunCommand`/`stopRun` flow + the `lastRun` file/argv, reaching the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension for open-tool-window / save-buffer / program-args get+set / stack-trace-link jump): `runActiveFile` saves first (dirty → save; untitled → Save-As), opens the Run window, then streams. `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` (built with `runCoordinator.panel()`), `updateRunButton` (gates the Run stripe on `isRunnable()`), the `programArgsFor` helper (shared with debug launches), and the shared `openRunLink` stack-trace resolver (which reuses `runCoordinator.lastRunDir()`); `buffer.setRunHandler` and the `file.run`/`run.*` commands delegate to the coordinator. Commands `file.run` (`C-c r`), `run.stop`, `run.clear` (`RunPanel.clearConsole`), `tool.run` (`M-9`) — palette-discoverable, localized in all six catalogs. **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (`com.editora.run` is internal to the module). *Deferred: running regular (non-compact) Java / other languages, a configurable run command per language, run configurations.*
- `test/` — **IntelliJ-style Test Runner** (a dedicated **Test Results** tool window; on by default, `Settings.testRunner`, suppressed in Simple UI mode). When a build tool's **`test`** task runs — from the actions tree/popup, the toolbar icon, or the palette (`test.run`) — the run is **intercepted, not duplicated**: `BuildCoordinator.launch` keeps running the same single `BuildService` process and, when the pure/unit-tested **`test/TestRunRecognizer.isTestRun(tool, taskArgs)`** matches, forwards its `onOutput`/`onExit` stream to an optional **`ui/TestRunHook`** (the raw console still streams to Build Output). Covers **all five build tools** via a common **`test/TestResultParser`** seam + a per-tool factory `TestResultParsers.forTool`: **Maven + Gradle** parse authoritative **JUnit XML** (`test/JUnitXmlParser`, XXE-hardened like `maven/PomParser`) — the coordinator **polls the reports dir** (`test/JvmReportDirs` → `target/surefire-reports`/`target/failsafe-reports`, `build/test-results/test`, + a bounded reactor-module walk) every ~750 ms parsing mtime-advanced files, with a **final full sweep on exit**; **Go** augments the argv with `-json` (`TestRunRecognizer.augmentArgv`) and folds the event stream (`test/GoTestJsonParser`, whose `consoleLine` decodes `-json` back to readable text so Build Output stays legible); **Cargo** parses libtest text (`test/CargoTestParser`, best-effort) and **npm** parses **TAP** when `TapParser.looksLikeTap` (else a "structured results unavailable — see Build Output" banner node — best-effort, no universal format). All parsers emit neutral **`ParsedSuite`/`ParsedTest`** records merged idempotently into a mutable **`TestNode`** tree by **`TestTreeBuilder.merge`** (upsert-by-id: JVM re-reads + streaming deltas both converge; a later detail-less delta never wipes a captured failure). **`TestStatus`** rolls up by severity (`worst`: a failure surfaces over a still-running sibling; running dominates a passed sibling), **`TestCounts`** drives the header. **`test/TestRun`** holds the session (tool/workingDir/task+toggle args/timing) + pure `failedTestFilters()` per tool (Maven `-Dtest=`, Gradle `--tests`, Go `-run`, Cargo name filters; npm → full rerun). **`ui/TestRunCoordinator`** (CoordinatorHost pattern, implements `TestRunHook`) owns the panel + parser + the JVM poll thread + an elapsed-time `Timeline`, coalescing tree merges to one panel refresh per FX pulse (never rebuild per line); **`ui/TestRunnerPanel`** (`ToolWindowContent`) is a header (status + `ProgressBar` + pass/fail/skip chips + elapsed) + a small toolbar (rerun / rerun-failed / stop / show-passed toggle) over a `TreeView<TestNode>` (status-icon + name + muted duration cell) split with a reused read-only detail `CodeArea` (failure message/stack + captured stdout/stderr, clickable frames via `RunPanel.installLinkClicks`). **Double-click / Enter on a test → jump to source**: a failure prefers its exact stack-trace frame (`run/StackTraceLinks` → `MainController.openRunLink`), else `MainController.jumpToTestSource` derives the file from the class name (`test/TestSourceLocator.fileHint`), opens it (open-tab / project-tree walk), and text-searches the method. **`MainController`** keeps the `testResultsToolWindow` (Side.BOTTOM, `Icons::testResults`, `tool.testResults`/`M-g e`, `register(false)` + available-on-first-run), injects the coordinator as the hook into every build coordinator, and registers `test.run`/`test.rerun`/`test.rerunFailed`/`test.stop` + `view.toggleTestRunner` (generic `toggleSetting`); palette-gated via `Chrome.PaletteGates.testRunner`. Icons `testResults`/`testPassed`/`testFailed`/`testSkipped`/`testRunning` (+ `.test-icon-{pass,fail,skip}` semantic colors in `app.css`); i18n ×6 (`testrunner.*`/`command.test.*`/`command.tool.testResults`/`toolwindow.testResults`/`status.testrunner.*`). **No new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (JUnit XML via `java.xml`, Go JSON via the existing Jackson). **Window fronting:** a *claimed* test run shows the Test Results window (the hook opens it) and `BuildCoordinator.launch` **skips `ops.openConsole()`** for a claimed run — else Build Output, on the same one-window bottom stripe, would displace it (its tab is still fed, one stripe-click away). **Poller correctness:** the JVM poller runs `baselineReports` on the poll thread **before the first tick** to snapshot pre-run report mtimes, so a leftover `TEST-*.xml` from a prior run (esp. after `-Dtest=Foo`) is never merged; the final sweep runs **off the FX thread** (`poller.execute` → `sweepReports` → `Platform.runLater(completeRun)`) and a `runGeneration` guard drops a late tick from a superseded run (`seenMtimes`/`baselineMtimes` are poll-thread-confined). **Detail pane** shows the selected test's **fully-qualified name** + status/duration, its failure block, and its captured output — falling back to the owning **class's** `system-out`/`system-err` when the test has none (a passing JVM test usually doesn't: Surefire writes `system-out` at the *class* level, which is why a pass used to render as just "Passed"); `JUnitXmlParser` now also captures a per-`<testcase>` `system-out`/`system-err`, which it previously dropped. A suite adds a counts summary, and the **run summary shows when nothing is selected** (`showRunSummary`). **Row context menu** (`installContextMenu`): *Go to Test/Class* (the existing activate → stack-frame or name-based jump), *Rerun This Test/Class* (`TestRunRecognizer.singleTestTask` → `Ops.runTest`), and — only when `Ops.debugAvailable()` (Java debugging configured) — *Debug This Test/Class*, which runs it via the pure **`test/TestDebug.debugTaskArgs`** (Maven `-Dmaven.surefire.debug`, Gradle `--debug-jvm`) so the tool forks the test JVM **suspended**, then watches the stream for the JDWP banner (`TestDebug.jdwpPort`, checked *before* the file-based early-return since for Maven/Gradle the console is the only place it appears) and attaches via `DebugCoordinator.attachToPort`. The attach flag is armed **after** `ops.runTest` returns — that call re-enters `onTestRunStart` synchronously, which resets per-run state and would otherwise wipe it. **Gutter ▶ on JUnit tests:** the pure/unit-tested **`test/JavaTestScanner.scan`** (length-preserving blank-comments/literals + brace-depth walk; `@Test`/`@ParameterizedTest`/`@RepeatedTest`/`@TestFactory`/`@TestTemplate`, JUnit 4/5, simple or FQ; skips `@Nested`-inner methods) yields a class-decl target + a per-method target; `EditorBuffer` reuses the run-slot machinery (`setTestGutterEnabled`/`setTestRunHandler`/`testTargetAtCaret`, additive to the compact-source ▶, distinct `.test-run-marker` accent glyph via the widened `FoldManager.setRunHooks(...,extraClassFor)`) gated by `MainController.applyTestGutter` (Test Runner on + not Simple mode + local + a detected Maven/Gradle project, re-pushed on detect/settings). Clicking runs one class/method via **`TestRunRecognizer.singleTestTask(tool, className, methodName)`** (Maven `-Dtest=Class#method -DfailIfNoTests=false`, Gradle `--tests FQN.method`; JVM only) → `BuildCoordinator.runTask` → the hook → Test Results; palette commands `test.runAtCaret`/`test.runClassAtCaret`. Each blue ▶ carries a hover tooltip explaining what it runs (`testrunner.gutter.runClass`/`runMethod`, via the widened `FoldManager.setRunHooks(…, tooltipFor)` + `EditorBuffer.runGlyphTooltip`), and a test file's editor right-click menu shows **"Run Tests"** with the blue glyph (running the whole class via `EditorBuffer.testClassTarget()`) instead of the generic green "Run File". **IntelliJ-style pending pre-seed:** for an **unfiltered** JVM run (`!TestRunRecognizer.isFilteredRun`), the coordinator walks the project's Java **test sources** off the poll thread at start (bounded/capped `seedFromSources`), `JavaTestScanner.scan`s each, and seeds the whole expected list **greyed-out (RUNNING)** via the pure **`TestPlan.seed`** → **`TestTreeBuilder.seed`** (create-missing-only: never downgrades a result that already arrived), so tests show as pending and **flip to green/red** as reports land instead of popping in per finished class. Only plain `@Test` methods are seeded (the `JavaTestScanner.TestTarget.dynamic` flag skips the `@ParameterizedTest`/`@RepeatedTest`/`@TestFactory`/`@TestTemplate` family, whose runtime case ids don't match the method name); `TestNode.pruneRunning()` on finish drops any still-pending seed (parameterized placeholders, filtered-out/abstract classes). Go already streams a RUNNING node per test as it starts (`go test -json` `run` events); Cargo/npm still pop in (no upfront enumeration). **Track running test:** the coordinator remembers the run's *frontier* (`followTarget` — the newest merged result; the pending pre-seed deliberately doesn't move it, or the view would jump to the bottom before anything ran) and `TestRunnerPanel.update(run, follow)` scrolls it into view while the run is live, so a long run reads as real-time progress. A `followToggle` (the `Icons.arrowDown()` Follow button, like the log viewer's) governs it: on by default, re-armed by each `startRun`, and **auto-disabled the moment the user selects a row** (they're inspecting — don't yank the view). `TreeView.scrollTo` only moves when the row isn't already visible, so a steady run doesn't jitter. *Deferred: a "Run Tests" toolbar split-button, richer npm reporters, per-run history, source nav for closed non-JVM files, `@Nested`/nested-class gutter runs, go/cargo in-file test gutters.*
- `http/` — **HTTP Client for `.http`/`.rest` files** (on by default, gated by `Settings.httpClientSupport`). Runs requests with the **built-in JDK `java.net.http.HttpClient`** (no external tool — `ijhttp` was tried first but it's a CI test-runner: slow JVM startup + a progress report instead of the response body). **`http/HttpFile`** (pure, unit-tested) parses a file into `Request{startLine,endLine,method,url,name,block}` (requests split on `###`) and one request's `block` into `Parsed{method,url,List<String[]> headers,body,…,warning}` (`parseRequest`; merges indented URL-continuation lines, stops the body at a `>`/`<>` response-handler line). A header line is only taken as a header when its name is a valid RFC 7230 field-name token (`isHeaderFieldName`); a non-blank line in the header block that isn't — almost always a **request body written without the blank line before it** (a common typo where a colon-bearing body like `{"a": 1}` used to be split into a bogus header and the POST sent empty) — sets `Parsed.warning` instead, which `HttpClientService` threads into `HttpResult.warnings` so it renders atop the report. No body is sent without the blank separator (spec-compliant, per the JetBrains `.http` convention) rather than guessing where the body starts (#441). `requestIndexAt(text,line)` maps a clicked line; `fileVariablePairs(text)` returns the `@name = value` declarations. **`http/HttpEnv`** (pure) reads environment names + one environment's variable map from `http-client.env.json`. **`http/HttpVars`** (pure, unit-tested) substitutes `{{name}}` from a resolved map + dynamic built-ins (`{{$uuid}}`/`{{$timestamp}}`/`{{$randomInt}}`/`{{$isoTimestamp}}`); `resolve(env, fileVars, clock)` layers the file's `@vars` over the env vars (each resolved against the accumulating map). **`http/HttpClientService`** (UI façade, daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`) executes a `Parsed` request via the shared `HttpClient` (`run`, and `runAll` for the whole file) — substitutes url/headers/body, times it, returns an **`HttpResult`** (status/headers/body/contentType/elapsed/size/error/**warnings**). **`HttpHeaders.partition`** (pure) prepares the headers: it **trims every value** (spec-safe OWS strip — a token pasted with a trailing `\r\n` the JDK would reject is now sent, not silently dropped; only `Authorization` was trimmed before, via `HttpAuth.normalizeHeaders`) and **surfaces** any header still un-sendable (a restricted name, or an embedded control char = header-injection) as an `HttpResult.warnings` line atop the report, instead of the old silent `catch (IllegalArgumentException)` skip that turned a dropped auth header into a mystery `401`. **`http/HttpResponseFormat`** (pure, unit-tested) renders a readable report: status line + headers + blank + body (**pretty-printed JSON** by content type) + a `status · ms · size` footer. **Gutter ▶ per request**: `.http` reuses the run-slot — `FoldManager.setRunHooks`'s `onRun` was generalized from `Runnable` to `IntConsumer onRunLine` (the clicked line); `EditorBuffer.recomputeRun` marks **every** request start line runnable for an http buffer (`isHttpFile()` + `setHttpEnabled`, a gate *separate* from the LSP-gated `setRunEnabled`), and `onRunGlyph(line)` dispatches to the injected `httpRunHandler` (→ `HttpClientCoordinator.runRequest`). Syntax highlighting via a bundled authored `grammars/http.tmLanguage.json` (`source.http`, ext `http`/`rest`; registered in `GrammarRegistry` `scopeToResource` **and** `mapExtensions` — both needed; plus `LanguageRegistry`/`Commenter` `#` entries). **The response viewer is the `.http` buffer's *preview*, not a tool window** — an Editor/Split/Preview view of the request file, **mirroring the CSV grid** (`CsvCoordinator`) rather than the old right-side dock. **`ui/HttpClientPanel`** (a plain `VBox`; no longer a `ToolWindowContent`) shows the rendered response in a read-only monospace area with an **environment `ComboBox`** (names from `HttpEnv`, persisted in `WorkspaceState.httpEnvironment`), **Save response** (FileChooser), and Clear. It's injected per buffer via `EditorBuffer.setHttpPreviewNode(Node)`, and **non-null doubles as the enablement gate** (`hasHttpPreview()` = `isHttpFile() && httpPreviewNode != null`) folded into `hasPreview()`, so the floating `MarkdownViewToggle` attaches automatically. `rebuildViewHost` routes it through the extracted `previewModeHost()`/`previewSplitSide()` helpers (PREVIEW wraps it in `httpPreviewHost()` so the toggle can overlay it; SPLIT hands the bare node), and it joins the **self-scrolling** class in `setMarkdownViewMode`'s paging/scroll-sync skip guard (`!hasCsvPreview() && !hasHttpPreview() && !hasTreePreview()`) since the panel scrolls its own body. **It is the one preview not rendered from the buffer text** — `scheduleRenderPreview()` carries an explicit early-return branch for it (re-rendering on the debounced edit pulse would be meaningless, and firing requests catastrophic); only a completed run repopulates it. **That branch must stay**, or the buffer falls through to the Markdown tail and renders its own source as Markdown. Running a request from the gutter ▶ while in EDITOR calls `EditorBuffer.revealHttpPreview()` (EDITOR → SPLIT only; a buffer already in SPLIT/PREVIEW is left alone so the persisted per-file mode wins) — the in-editor replacement for the tool window's auto-open. **`ui/HttpClientCoordinator`** (extracted from `MainController` — the shared-`CoordinatorHost` pattern plus a small `WindowOps` extension for the tab / run-gating / environment persistence) owns **one panel per open `.http` buffer** (a Node can't live in two tabs — an `IdentityHashMap`, so the `onBufferClosed` hook is **required**, unlike the old weak-keyed set): `ensureHttpPreview(buffer)` attaches/detaches per the gate and is called from **both** `ensurePreviewControls` and `restoreMarkdownMode` *before* they read `hasPreview()` (for a node-gated preview the node **is** the gate), plus `refreshFor(active)` on tab switch; `runRequest(buffer,line)` parses the request, builds the variable map (the selected env's public+private env-file vars overlaid with the file's `@vars`) from **that buffer's own** picker, runs it off-thread and renders into **that buffer's** panel; `applySupport()` (init + every settings apply) pushes `setHttpEnabled(on)` + re-runs the attach on every buffer + refreshes each panel's font (no external detection); the commands no-op when off (`ifHttp`) and `http.*` is filtered from the palette. Commands `http.runRequest` (run the request at the caret), `http.runFile` (all requests sequentially), `http.selectEnvironment` (reveals the preview + focuses its env picker), `http.importCurl`, `http.copyAsCurl`, `http.openResponseInTab`. *(There is no `tool.http` / `M-0` / `Icons.httpClient()` any more — the view is toggled by the shared `view.togglePreview`/`view.toggleSplitPreview`, and `M-0` is free.)* `Settings.httpClientSupport` (Settings → **HTTP Client**, just an enable checkbox; schema 18→19 additive-identity). **`module-info` `requires java.net.http`** — no new Maven dependency (env JSON uses the existing Jackson; the grammar rides `opens com.editora.grammars`). **File references are contained (#412):** every path a request names — the `< ./body.json` external body, a multipart file part, and the `>>` response redirect — goes through the pure, unit-tested **`http/HttpPaths.contained(baseDir, ref)`**, which resolves against the request file's own folder and returns null for an absolute path or a `../` escape. A `.http` is *content*, routinely shipped inside a repo the user merely opened, so an unguarded `< /etc/passwd` or `< ../../.ssh/id_rsa` body exfiltrates to the request's own host — and the request being user-initiated is exactly what makes the read look legitimate. The write side (`>>`) had always been contained; the two **read** sides were not, and that asymmetry is what this closed. Containment is lexical (`startsWith` on normalized `Path` components, so a sibling `api-secrets/` can't pass on a shared string prefix); a refused body reports it in the response report rather than failing silently. *Deferred: response-handler JS scripts (`> {% %}`) + cross-request captured variables (a request needing an earlier one's token can't run in isolation), request history, multipart/file bodies, a form/structured response viewer.*
- `web/` — **HTML Live Preview** (on by default, gated by `Settings.htmlPreviewSupport`). A floating "open in browser" globe overlaid top-right of any `.html`/`.htm`/`.xhtml` editor (mirroring the Markdown preview toggle) opens the current file in a **detected desktop browser** over a tiny embedded HTTP server, with **live-as-you-type reload**. **`web/LivePreviewServer`** wraps one JDK `com.sun.net.httpserver.HttpServer` bound to `127.0.0.1:0` (**loopback only**, never the LAN). `setPreview(file, Supplier<String> liveText)` makes the file's parent dir the document root; the previewed file is served from the buffer's **live in-memory text** (so unsaved edits show), assets (CSS/JS/images) from disk; a `/__editora_livereload` **long-poll** endpoint holds the request until `bumpVersion()` advances a `volatile long` (or a ~25 s timeout), and a small **injected `<script>`** (spliced before `</body>`, appended if none) reloads the page on a `200`. Pure/unit-tested helpers: `injectReloadScript`, `contentType` (extension→MIME), `safeResolve` (path-traversal guard rejecting escapes outside the doc root). A cached daemon thread pool backs it so held polls don't starve serving. **`web/Browsers`** (pure/unit-tested) detects installed browsers per-OS — macOS app bundles (`Safari.app` always; `Google Chrome.app`/`Firefox.app`/`Microsoft Edge.app` in `/Applications` + `~/Applications`, launched `open -a`), Linux PATH binaries (via `ProcessRunner.resolveExecutable`, launched `[bin, url]`), Windows Program Files exes (`cmd /c start`) — plus a **System Default** entry routed through `HostServices.showDocument`; the OS + filesystem/PATH probes are injected so detection + `launchArgv` are testable. **`web/HtmlPreviewService`** (UI-owned, the `MermaidService` idiom: single daemon executor + `Platform.runLater` + cached `detectBrowsers`) owns the one server per window; `preview(file, liveText, browser, cb)` (re)binds the doc root, launches the browser **detached** (fire-and-forget, so a foreground browser process can't stall the executor) or via the system opener, and posts a `Result`; `notifyChanged()` → `bumpVersion()`; `stopServer()` (feature disabled) vs `shutdown()` (window close). **`EditorBuffer`** (editor pkg, no `ui` dep): `isHtml()`, an injected `setHtmlPreviewControl(Node)` overlaid via the same code-pane top-right anchoring as the Markdown toggle (`attachControlToCodePane` generalized to place either the markdown `viewModeControl` *or* the `htmlPreviewControl` — mutually exclusive, a buffer is one or the other), and `setHtmlPreviewDirtyListener` fired from the **existing debounced** `multiPlainChanges` 250 ms pulse while `isHtml()` (no new per-keystroke work). **`ui/HtmlPreviewToggle`** (a `Button`, `Icons.htmlPreview()` globe, `.html-preview-toggle`) drops a `ContextMenu` of detected browsers (+ System Default) on click, **each menu item with its own recognizable glyph** (`HtmlPreviewToggle.iconFor(id)` → `Icons.browserSafari/Chrome/Firefox/Edge` — a Material compass for Safari + the Simple-Icons monochrome single-path logos for the rest; System Default / unknown falls back to the globe; Simple Icons is CC0, attributed in NOTICE). **`ui/HtmlPreviewCoordinator`** (a feature coordinator extracted from `MainController`, the `LogViewerCoordinator` pattern — owns the `HtmlPreviewService` + the detected-browser list + the browser picker, and reaches the window only through a shared `CoordinatorHost` interface; `MainController` supplies an anonymous `Host` adapter and keeps one-line delegations, and a fake `Host` makes it unit-testable — see `HtmlPreviewCoordinatorFxTest`): `applySupport()` (init + every settings apply, mirrors `applyMermaidSupport`) (un)attaches the globe on local HTML buffers + async-detects browsers, or `stopServer()`s when off; `ensureControl` gates on `isEnabled() && isHtml() && host.isLocalBuffer` (remote SFTP excluded — the server reads sibling assets from disk); `previewActive` requires a saved file (so assets resolve), remembers the last-used browser in `Settings.htmlPreviewBrowser`; `onBufferEdited` reloads the served file on the debounced edit pulse; the `open`/`openIn` commands no-op when off (`ifEnabled`) and `htmlPreview.*` is palette-filtered. Commands (palette-only, no keymap binding — like preview/print): `htmlPreview.open` (last-used/default browser), `htmlPreview.openIn` (`QuickOpen` browser picker), `view.toggleHtmlPreview` (master toggle → `SettingsWindow.syncHtmlPreviewCheck`). `Settings.htmlPreviewSupport`/`htmlPreviewBrowser` (Settings → **HTML Preview**, enable checkbox; schema 24→25 additive-identity). **`module-info` `requires jdk.httpserver`** — **no new Maven dependency, no moditect** (a JDK module jlink bundles automatically); no `opens` (the last-used-browser is a plain `Settings` string). *Deferred: in-app WebView render (Editora ships no `javafx.web`; external browsers are the explicit design), remote (SFTP) HTML preview, multi-file concurrent previews (v1 serves one active file + its dir), a configurable server port, project-root document root.*
- `dap/` — **Multi-language debugging (Debug Adapter Protocol)** for **Java**, **Python**, and **JavaScript (Node)**, off by default (gated by `Settings.debugSupport`). Three transports, abstracted in `dap/DapClient`: **Java** is **layered on the jdtls LSP session** (not a standalone server) — jdtls is started with the Microsoft **java-debug** plugin jar in `initialize.initializationOptions.bundles`, which registers `vscode.java.*` debug commands; at debug time `LspManager.executeCommand(file, "vscode.java.startDebugSession")` returns a **TCP port** and `DapClient.connect(port, "java")` opens a socket. **Python** is **debugpy over stdio** — `DapManager` spawns `<python> -m debugpy.adapter` and `DapClient.connectStdio(proc, "python")` wires DAP to the process's stdin/stdout. **JavaScript** is **vscode-js-debug over a socket** — `DapManager` allocates a free port, spawns `node <dapDebugServer.js> <port>`, and `DapClient.connect(port, "pwa-node")` connects. All speak DAP via **`org.eclipse.lsp4j.debug`** (`DSPLauncher`). The standalone adapters' stderr is `Redirect.DISCARD`ed (undrained PIPE deadlocks, like the LSP servers), and `DapClient.dispose()` kills the adapter subprocess **tree** (descendants first, then root) so a wrapper script can't orphan the real adapter. **`dap/DapServerRegistry`** (pure, unit-tested) is the language→adapter spec: `java`→`Kind.JDTLS`, `python`→`Kind.STDIO` (launch `type="python"`, default interpreter `python3`, adapter args `-m debugpy.adapter`), `javascript`→`Kind.SOCKET` (launch `type="pwa-node"`, interpreter `node`); `languageIdsForDebug()`={java,python,javascript} gates the breakpoint gutter + debug commands; `interpreterArgv(lang, command)` tokenizes the configured interpreter (blank ⇒ default). The **LSP bridge** (`lsp/`, java only): `LanguageServerSession` gained an optional `initializationOptions` (jdtls gets `{"bundles":[<jar>]}` only when debugging is on) + `executeCommand`; `LspManager` gained `setDebugBundles`/`executeCommand`/`restartServer("java")` — toggling debug **restarts jdtls** so it reloads with the bundle (via `restartServer` → `shutdownServer`, whose scan prefix must agree with `LspManager.sessionKey`'s `SESSION_KEY_SEP` — they silently didn't, so it was a no-op). **`dap/DebugAdapterLocator`** (pure, unit-tested) finds each adapter: `locate(...)` the java-debug jar (`com.microsoft.java.debug.plugin-*.jar` from a configured path / VS Code `vscjava.vscode-java-debug-*` / mason / `~/.editora[-dev]/plugins/dap/java/`, newest wins); `locateJsDebugServer(...)` the preferred `dapDebugServer.js` (config path / `~/.editora[-dev]/plugins/dap/javascript/` / mason `js-debug-adapter` / VS Code `ms-vscode.js-debug-*`) via the pure `selectPreferredEntry`: **Editora's own `plugins/dap/` install wins unconditionally** (`isEditoraOwned` — it's the copy the user asked Editora to install, and its path carries no version, so the old newest-by-`pathVersion` rule always lost it to any VS Code dir, #474), and `pathVersion` only breaks ties *within* a class; `locateDebugpy(...)` a `PYTHONPATH` dir containing a `debugpy` package (config path / `~/.editora[-dev]/plugins/dap/python/`, empty ⇒ rely on the interpreter importing debugpy). **`dap/DapClient`** (mirrors `LanguageServerSession`) runs the DAP handshake (`initialize` with the per-transport `adapterId` → on the `initialized` event fire `setBreakpoints`/`setExceptionBreakpoints`/`configurationDone` **without `.join()`** — that callback runs on the reader thread, so blocking deadlocks). `initialized` is the **only** reader of `exceptionFilters`, so once it has fired (tracked by `configured`) a later `setExceptionFilters` must put the request on the wire **itself** — otherwise toggling exception breakpoints mid-session writes a field nothing will read again and silently does nothing while the UI reports success., `launch`/`attach`, and the control + inspection requests; events arrive on the launcher thread and a `Host` (DapManager) marshals to FX. **`dap/DapManager`** (UI facade, mirrors `LspManager`+`RunService`) owns the **single** session and dispatches `startLaunch(file, language, picker)`: `java` → the jdtls flow (`resolveMainClass` → pick → `resolveClasspath` → `resolveJavaExecutable` → `startDebugSession` → connect → `launch`, with a `compileAndLaunch` javac fallback for loose files); `python`/`javascript` → `startProgram` (snapshot breakpoints on FX, then off-thread spawn the adapter + connect + `launch`). `configure(enabled, javaPluginPath, pythonEnabled, pythonCommand, jsEnabled, jsPath)` resolves all three adapter locations synchronously; `detectPython`/`detectJs` probe `python -c "import debugpy"` / `node --version` off-thread and cache `isLanguageAvailable(lang)`. It exposes neutral records (`dap/DapModels`) so `ui`/`editor` never import lsp4j.debug; jdtls's untyped `executeCommand` results (gson `JsonElement`s) are parsed with gson (`module-info` `requires com.google.gson` + `opens com.editora.dap`). **`dap/LaunchConfig`** (pure, unit-tested) shapes the DAP arg maps: `launch` (java mainClass+classpath), `attach` (java JVM host:port — **attach stays Java-only**), and `program(type, program, cwd, runtimeExecutable, stopOnEntry)` for python/js (the interpreter goes under `python` for python, `runtimeExecutable` for node). **Both pass program args as the argv array, never a joined string** — `ProgramArgs.tokenize` already resolved the user's quoting, so re-joining on a space undoes it (`"hello world" second` → 3 args to `main()` while Run passes 2). **Breakpoints** (`config/Breakpoint` + per-project `config/BreakpointStore` in `breakpoints.json`, `ConfigSchema.BREAKPOINTS`; `editor/BreakpointManager` mirrors `BookmarkManager`, `shift`/`reanchor` pure + unit-tested — **`reanchor` resolves each marker against the lines not already claimed**, walking the list in stored-line order: it rebuilds a *line-keyed map*, so two markers landing on one line silently `put`-drop one and `restore`'s self-heal then **persists** the loss — trivially hit by two breakpoints on adjacent identical lines (`});`/`});`) plus any external edit. The same fix is in `BookmarkManager.reanchor`, where the dropped bookmark took its **note** with it) show in a **leftmost gutter strip** (`FoldManager.setBreakpointHooks` reserves `BREAKPOINT_SLOT_WIDTH` only while debug is on **and the buffer's language is debuggable** — java/python/javascript, via `DebugCoordinator.isDebuggableBuffer`; clicking toggles a bp; red dot `.breakpoint-marker`, amber/blue/hollow for conditional/logpoint/disabled). `EditorBuffer` mirrors the bookmark API + a **current-execution-line** (`setExecutionLine`/`clearExecutionLine`, `.exec-line`). **`ui/DebugPanel`** (a `ToolWindowContent`, id `debug`, `Side.BOTTOM`, `tool.debug`/`M-g d`, `Icons.debug()`) is **IntelliJ-styled**: an icon-only grouped toolbar (resume/pause/stop/restart | step over/into/out/run-to-cursor, full titles in tooltips; the state + session file right-aligned), a **thread `ComboBox`** over the call-stack `ListView` (rich `name:line, File` `TextFlow` cells), a lazy variables `TreeView` with **type-colored values** (`record VarRow(name,value,type,ref,parentRef,Kind {SCOPE,VARIABLE,WATCH,ADD_WATCH})`; the pure, unit-tested **`ui/DebugValues`** classifies a rendered value STRING/NUMBER/BOOLEAN/NULL/OTHER → `.debug-val-*` CSS), and an always-visible console with an evaluate REPL. **Watches** are merged into the variables tree IntelliJ-style: a fixed top "Watches" node above the scopes + a trailing "+ Add watch…" row; add/edit/remove via the tree context menu or double-click, prompting through the injected `OverlayInput.Prompt` (`DebugPanel.setPrompt`); each watch evaluates per stop/frame-select with context `"watch"` via `DapClient.evaluateFull` → `DapModels.EvalResult(result, variablesReference, type)` (expandable when structured); the expression list persists in **`WorkspaceState.debugWatches`** (additive field; restored at startup + on project switch, saved via `setOnWatchesChanged`). **Set Value**: context-menu "Set Value…" / F2 / double-click on a leaf variable row → prompt pre-filled with the current value → `DapManager.setVariable` on the row's `parentRef`, updating the row in place + re-evaluating watches. **The whole DAP integration lives in `ui/DebugCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `DebugPanel`, breakpoint persistence + gutter gating, the DAP event sink (`dapListener`) + panel actions (`debugActions`), the inline-values/hover/execution-line editor surfaces (`applyInlineValues`/`highlightFrame`), the start/attach/step/run-to-cursor/jump flows, `wireBuffer` (the per-buffer breakpoint-gutter + change/hover hooks), and the `debug.toggleAdapter`/`debug.setAdapterPath` pickers; reaches the window via the shared host plus an `Ops` extension for the Debug tool-window open/toggle/availability, the status-bar debug segment + loading bar, save-buffer, program-args (shared with Run), the stack-trace-link jump, open-path, buffer-for-path, the debug-watches workspace state, and the `breakpoints.json` map). The **`DapManager` stays a `MainController` field** (built on `lspManager`; `SettingsWindow` + window-dispose reach it) and is passed to the coordinator — mirroring the `lspManager`/`LspCoordinator` split; since Java debugging layers on the jdtls session, the coordinator also takes the `lspManager` + `LspCoordinator` (its `debugEffectiveFor("java")` reads `lspCoordinator.serverEnabled("java")`/`isServerAvailable("java")`; `applySupport` pushes the java-debug bundle + re-gates via `lspCoordinator.applyGating()`). `MainController` keeps the Debug `ToolWindow` (built with `debugCoordinator.panel()`), `isLocalBuffer`, the shared `programArgsFor`/`openRunLink`/`save` helpers, and the `debug.*` command registrations (delegating to the coordinator). **`DebugCoordinator`**: `applySupport()` configures all three adapters, pushes the java bundle into LSP (restart jdtls when changed), async-detects python/js (re-gating on each result), gates each buffer's breakpoint gutter via `debugSupportEnabled() && isDebuggableBuffer(b)`, and `setAvailable`s the Debug window;
