`debugEffectiveFor(language)` gates start (java = `lspSupport && javaLspEnabled && jdtls + plugin found`; python = `pythonDebugEnabled && debugpy detected`; js = `jsDebugEnabled && js-debug + node detected`); `debugStart()` reads the active buffer's language and dispatches; `ifDebug(...)` no-ops the commands when off (palette-filtered); persist/restore breakpoints on save/open. **Closed-file breakpoints are armed too**: `collectBreakpoints()` merges the open buffers' live breakpoints with `closedBreakpoints` — the persisted `breakpoints.json` entries for files with **no open tab**, computed by the pure/unit-tested `DebugCoordinator.closedFileBreakpoints(map, openPaths, isLocal, readLines)` (skips remote paths, re-anchors each file's stored breakpoints against its on-disk text via `BreakpointManager.reanchor`, keeps the stored indices when a file is unreadable/too-large, emits only enabled ones). `withClosedBreakpoints(then)` reads those files off the FX thread at every session start (a daemon thread + `Platform.runLater`) and wraps `dapManager.startLaunch`/`startAttach` so the initial `setBreakpoints` includes them — so a breakpoint in a closed file hits like VS Code/IntelliJ instead of being silently inert (#473). **Pause** (`DapClient.pause` → the `stopped` event flows through the normal path; enabled only while RUNNING) and **Run to Cursor** (`DapManager.runToCursor`: the pure, unit-tested `withTempLine` merges a temporary breakpoint into the file's set → `sendSetBreakpoints` → resume; the temp set is re-sent clean on the next stop/termination) complement the step commands. **Jump to Line** (the IntelliJ plugin's move-the-execution-pointer): DAP `gotoTargets`/`goto`, **capability-gated** via the stored `initialize` `Capabilities` (`DapClient.supportsGotoTargets`) — debugpy supports it, java-debug/js-debug don't (the command reports `status.debug.jumpUnsupported`); `DapManager.jumpToLine` teleports the suspended thread to the caret line *without executing* the code in between, and the adapter's `stopped(reason=goto)` refreshes everything. **Editor surfaces while suspended** (IntelliJ's inline values + value popup): on each stop/frame-select the controller fetches the selected frame's first non-expensive scope (capped at `MAX_INLINE_VALUES`) and pushes a name→value map to the frame's file buffer — **`editor/InlineValuesOverlay`** (a mouse-transparent `Canvas` mirroring `WhitespaceOverlay`: visible paragraphs only, coalesced per pulse, 1×1 when inactive) paints grey-italic `name: value` annotations after each visible line that mentions a frame variable (pure, unit-tested **`editor/DebugIdentifiers.matchesIn`**); hovering an identifier evaluates it with DAP context `"hover"` (`DebugIdentifiers.wordAt` → the injected `EditorBuffer.setDebugHoverEvaluator` → `DapManager.evaluateHover`, which delivers null on failure so non-variables show nothing) in a `.debug-value-tooltip`; both are gated by `setDebugHoverActive`/`setInlineValues(null)` flipped on suspend/resume, so there is zero editor hot-path cost outside a paused session. Commands (all `ifDebug`-gated): `debug.start` (`C-c C-d d`, = continue when suspended) / `debug.continue`/`stepOver`/`stepInto`/`stepOut` / `debug.pause` (`C-c C-d p`) / `debug.runToCursor` (`C-c C-d u`) / `debug.jumpToLine` (`C-c C-d j`) / `debug.stop` / `debug.restart` / `debug.attach` (Java only) / `debug.toggleBreakpoint` (`C-c C-b`) / `debug.editBreakpoint` (a 3-field `OverlayInput` form — condition / log message / enabled; a log message makes it a **logpoint**: the adapter logs and never suspends. `BreakpointManager.setLogMessage`/`setEnabled` had **zero callers** before, so both states were built-but-unreachable and the gutter's logpoint/disabled glyphs were dead) / `debug.toggleExceptionBreakpoints` / `tool.debug` (`M-g d`). The panel's data-inspection actions are also palette commands: `debug.evaluate` (open the Debug console + focus the eval field via `DebugPanel.focusEvaluate`), `debug.addWatch` (`DebugPanel.addWatch`), `debug.setValue` (`DebugPanel.setSelectedValue`). Settings → **Debugging** page is **data-driven** (`SettingsWindow.debugAdapterUis()`, mirroring the LSP page): a master enable + a per-language row group (Java/Python/JavaScript) — Python/JS each an enable checkbox + command/path field, Java a plugin-path field (no enable — gated by the Java LSP server) — each with a live green/red found status (`refreshDebugStatus` → the locators + `dapManager.detectPython/detectJs` probes). `Settings.debugSupport`/`javaDebugPluginPath`/`pythonDebugEnabled`/`pythonDebugCommand`/`jsDebugEnabled`/`jsDebugPath` (schema 15→16 additive-identity). **Adapter acquisition**: never bundled — `scripts/install-java-debug.sh` (java-debug jar from Open VSX), `scripts/install-debugpy.sh` (`pip install --target …/plugins/dap/python debugpy`), `scripts/install-js-debug.sh` (vscode-js-debug release → `…/plugins/dap/javascript/js-debug/src/dapDebugServer.js`); all honor `EDITORA_CONFIG_DIR` for `--dev`. **Dependency**: `org.eclipse.lsp4j.debug` (same version as lsp4j; moditect-patched + signed-jar-unsigned in `dist`); **no new dependency / `module-info` change** for python/js (debugpy/js-debug are external, user-installed, driven over stdio/socket; node/python come from the augmented PATH). *Deferred: browser/Chrome JS debugging, TypeScript source-map debugging, Python/JS attach (remote), more languages (Go delve, Ruby) via the registry, hit-count/data breakpoints, hot code replace, run/debug configurations, multi-session tabs, smart step-into, drop frame, the Jump-to-Line gutter-arrow drag affordance.*
- `install/` — **In-app install of language support** (LSP server + DAP adapter for Java/Python/JS, plus the Mermaid CLI), cross-platform (macOS/Linux/Windows), the Java path the bash `scripts/install-*.sh` used to be. Pure **`InstallCatalog`** (java.base only, unit-tested) maps a `Lang` (JAVA/PYTHON/JAVASCRIPT/MERMAID) → an ordered `Step` list (`Kind` NPM_GLOBAL/PIP_TARGET/VSIX/TARBALL + its prereqs + dest), with the pure URL/argv helpers (`openVsxLatestUrl`, `JDTLS_TARBALL_URL`, `JS_DEBUG_RELEASES_API`, `npmInstallGlobalArgv`/`pipInstallTargetArgv`/`tarExtractArgv`, `firstMatch` for asset-URL extraction, `forBufferLanguage`). Recipes: **pyright**/**typescript-language-server**/**mmdc** = `npm i -g` (then `npx puppeteer browsers install chrome-headless-shell` from mmdc's dir, version-matched, so the headless Chrome it renders with is present — `Kind.PUPPETEER_BROWSER`) (global); **debugpy** = `pip install --target <config>/plugins/dap/python`; **java-debug** = Open VSX `.vsix` (a ZIP) → reuse `plugin/Unzip` → `<config>/plugins/dap/java`; **jdtls** = Eclipse JDT-LS `.tar.gz` → system `tar` → `<config>/plugins/lsp/java` (then `Settings.javaLspCommand` ← `bin/jdtls`, the dir `ProcessRunner.EXTRA_PATH_DIRS` already anticipates); **js-debug** = GitHub release `.tar.gz` → system `tar` → `<config>/plugins/dap/javascript`. **`InstallService`** (the `GitService`/`MermaidService` idiom: one daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`) runs the steps off-thread reusing `ProcessRunner.run/resolveExecutable` (npm/pip/tar; Windows `.cmd`/`.exe` resolution + augmented PATH so a GUI-launched app finds them), `PluginRegistry.readCapped`+`isHttps` over `java.net.http` for bounded HTTPS downloads, and `Unzip.extract` for the vsix; `detectPrereqs` probes npm/python/tar on PATH. **`ui/InstallCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` pattern + a small `Ops` for config-dir / per-feature availability reads / re-detect): `installSupport(lang)` filters to the *missing* tools (per the existing `LspCoordinator.isServerAvailable`/`DapManager.isLanguageAvailable`/`MermaidCoordinator.mmdcAvailable` detectors), checks prereqs first (reports a missing Node/Python/tar instead of installing it — Editora never installs runtimes), runs them, then `reapplyToolSupport()` (`LspManager.invalidateDetection()` + `LspCoordinator`/`DebugCoordinator`/`MermaidCoordinator` `applySupport()` + persist) so the tools activate **without a restart**. Palette commands `install.javaSupport`/`pythonSupport`/`jsSupport`/`mermaidSupport`. **Settings → Language Servers** rows (java/python/typescript) and the **Mermaid** page also carry an **Install…** button (`SettingsWindow.setInstallActions` injected with a language-key consumer → `installSupport`; tracked in `installButtons`, flipped to "Installed"/disabled by `updateInstallButton` from the existing `refreshLspStatus`/`refreshMermaidStatus` detect callbacks; `MainController`'s `reapplyToolSupport` calls `SettingsWindow.refreshDetectionStatus()` after an install so it updates live — the JS row installs the LSP **and** js-debug, so the Debugger page needs no separate button). **In-editor install banner:** `EditorBuffer.getNode()`'s `BorderPane` top stacks (in a `VBox`, via `refreshTopBars`) a generic `.lsp-install-bar` (built lazily like `buildViewModeBar`; toolkit-only `setInstallPrompt(message, actionLabel, onInstall, onDismiss)` + `showInstallBar`/`setInstallBarBusy`, so `editor` stays decoupled) **above** the existing `.view-mode-bar`. `MainController.maybeOfferInstall(buffer)` (run on tab switch / after an install / on `reapplyAfterSharedSettingsChange`) shows it per `shouldOfferInstall`: the buffer's language has an installer, the relevant feature is **on** but its server/CLI is **confirmed missing** (`lspEnabled() && lspCoordinator.isServerMissing(...)` — tri-state, *probed-and-absent* not merely pending; or `mermaid.isEnabled() && mmdcDetected() && !mmdcAvailable()`), no live LSP session is already serving the file (`!lspCoordinator.isManaged(path)`), the user hasn't dismissed it (a `WeakHashMap` `installDismissed`, mirroring `httpUserClosed`), it's a local buffer, and the master nudge `Settings.lspInstallPrompts` (default on, schema 44→45 additive; Settings → Language Servers checkbox + `view.toggleInstallPrompts`) is on. **Install** runs `installCoordinator.installSupport(lang, ok→…)` (the callback overload spins the banner + hides on success); **Not now** dismisses for that buffer. The banner re-evaluates when LSP detection settles (`LspCoordinator.applyGating` → `Ops.onDetectionSettled` → `maybeOfferInstall`), so a late-starting server hides it without a tab switch. Downloads are HTTPS-only + capped; `Unzip` keeps its zip-slip/size guards; **no new Maven dependency / `module-info` change** (`install` is internal). **More LSP servers (server-id-centric):** beyond the 4 `Lang` bundles, `InstallCatalog.installableServerIds()` + `serverInstall(serverId)` describe the **LSP-only** servers (no DAP) keyed by their `LspServerRegistry` server id; `InstallCoordinator.installServer(serverId[, cb])` installs one (filters on `lspAvailable(serverId)`, prereq-checks, runs, re-detects). The Settings → Language Servers rows get an **Install…** button for any `installableServerIds()` entry (`SettingsWindow.setInstallServerActions`), the editor banner offers them via `LspServerRegistry.serverIdFor(language)` (in `MainController.maybeOfferInstall`'s server-id branch), and the palette `install.languageServer` picks any installable server (`QuickOpen` over `installableServerIds()`). The npm batch (needs Node): **json/html/css** (one package `vscode-langservers-extracted`), **bash**, **yaml**, **dockerfile** (`dockerfile-language-server-nodejs`), **toml** (`@taplo/cli`). The **toolchain batch** (`Kind.TOOL_COMMAND` — argv carried in the `Step.npmPackages` field; runs via the language's own package manager, gated on that toolchain being on PATH via the new `Prereq` GO/RUBY/DOTNET/RUSTUP/COMPOSER): **go** (`go install …/gopls@latest`), **sql** (`go install …/sqls@latest`), **ruby** (`gem install ruby-lsp`), **csharp** (`dotnet tool install --global csharp-ls`), **rust** (`rustup component add rust-analyzer`), **php** (`composer global require phpactor/phpactor`). The **binary batch** (`Kind.ARCHIVE` + `InstallCatalog.archiveSpec(serverId)` → an `ArchiveSpec{apiUrl, Map<Platform,assetSubstring>, binaryName, binaryPrefix, commandSuffix}`; `InstallService.installArchive` picks the asset for `currentPlatform()` (`platformKey`, pure/unit-tested), downloads it, extracts (zip via the new capped `Unzip.extract(...,maxEntry,maxTotal,maxEntries)` since clangd's binary dwarfs the plugin caps; `.tar.gz` via system `tar`), `findBinary`-walks the tree, `chmod +x`es it, and returns the path → the coordinator persists it into that server's `Settings.<id>LspCommand` via `applyServerCommand`): **clangd** (clangd/clangd), **xml**/lemminx (redhat-developer/vscode-xml, binary prefix-matched `lemminx-…`), **kotlin** (fwcd/kotlin-language-server, single `server.zip`), **lua** (LuaLS, per-OS tar.gz/zip), **terraform** (releases.hashicorp.com via the HashiCorp releases API, command suffix ` serve`). All 21 LSP servers now have an installer. *Deferred: a keymap binding for the install commands.*
- `ai/` + `agent/` — **AI features** (three Settings pages; all off by default). **This is the only feature that transmits the user's source code to a third party — treat every change to it as security-relevant.** Two independent halves: (1) **direct API** — `ui/AiCoordinator` (the `CoordinatorHost` pattern) drives `ai/AiService` (a generation-guarded facade over `ai/AiClient`, which speaks either dialect via the pure `ai/AiProvider`: **ANTHROPIC** = `x-api-key` to the Messages API, **OPENAI** = `Authorization: Bearer` to any OpenAI-compatible server — its default endpoint is deliberately **plain-http loopback** (`http://127.0.0.1:1234`, LM Studio) because `requiresApiKey()` is false for local inference, so a blanket https rule would break the feature's primary path). `ai/AiRequests` builds the bodies (capped by `truncate` at 120k chars) — it sends the **selection**, never the whole buffer, and no file path/name; `ai/SseParser`+`OpenAiSse` decode the stream; `ai/AiErrors` maps failures. Commands: commit-message-from-staged-diff, explain-selection (into a Markdown buffer), rewrite-selection (an undoable edit, re-verified against the original text before it lands), and **inline completion** (`Settings.aiInlineCompletion`, its own `AiService` so it can't cancel an explicit action) with the floating `editor/AiActionsBar`. (2) **ACP agent** — `agent/AcpClient` runs an external agent process over stdio JSON-RPC (`agent/AcpJson`, `agent/AcpAgentRegistry`), driven by `ui/AgentCoordinator`+`AgentPanel`; it correctly `ProcessRegistry.track`s + `killTree`s the process and **drains stderr past the log cap** (the undrained-PIPE deadlock documented for LSP/DAP). Gated by `Settings.aiSupport` **&&** `aiEnabled` **&&** `!simpleModeActive()`. **Credential invariants — do not regress these:** the key is **per-provider** — `Settings.aiApiKey` holds the **Anthropic** key and `Settings.aiApiKeyOpenai` the **OpenAI-compatible** one, read via `Settings.getApiKeyFor(provider)`/`setApiKeyFor(provider, key)` — because a single shared field silently sent one provider's key to the *other*'s (user-supplied) endpoint the moment you switched provider (#480; schema 77→78, `ConfigMigrations.splitAiApiKeyByProvider` moves an existing key onto `aiApiKeyOpenai` only when the saved provider was OpenAI, since Anthropic was the default and already lands in the right field). The Settings AI page's single key field shows/edits the *currently-selected* provider's key (the provider combo reloads it on switch, guarded by `loading`; the key field's listener writes to the combo's current provider). Both live in `settings.toml`, which `config/ConfigWriter` writes **owner-only (0600)** since the default umask left a billable credential world-readable in a 0755 config dir; and `AiCoordinator.effectiveKey(configured, provider, envKey)` (pure, unit-tested) **only** falls back to the `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` environment variable for the **ANTHROPIC** provider — it is Anthropic's credential by name and is exported on most dev machines, so a provider-agnostic fallback shipped it as a bearer token to the OpenAI provider's user-supplied endpoint with the Settings field empty, on every inline-completion idle pause. `AiCoordinator.apiKey()` resolves `getApiKeyFor(provider())`, so each provider only ever sees its own configured key. **The key is never sent in cleartext to a remote host:** `AiClient` refuses (via `onError`/the check-string, **before dialing**) whenever a key would be attached to a **non-loopback `http://`** endpoint — the pure/unit-tested `ai/AiEndpoints.isCleartextRemote(endpoint)` is true only when the scheme isn't https **and** the host isn't loopback (`localhost`/`127.0.0.0/8`/`::1`), so plain-http *loopback* (LM Studio/Ollama/vLLM, the intended local-inference path) and https are both allowed, and a keyless local server is unaffected (#481). A deceptive hostname that merely resolves to loopback (nip.io-style) is a remote host string and is refused — we don't do DNS. **A hanging endpoint can't wedge the AI worker:** the streaming read's response timeout only bounds the wait for the *headers*, so an endpoint that returns `200` then writes nothing would block the read forever — and since `AiService` runs on a **single-thread executor**, every later request would queue behind it permanently. `AiClient.stream` runs an **idle-read watchdog** (a shared daemon `ai-idle-watchdog` scheduler): each received line resets a `lastActivity` clock, and if no data arrives for `responseTimeout` the watchdog **closes the response stream** — the only thing that unblocks a `readLine` already blocked mid-read (`cancel()` is polled *between* lines and can't) — so the read fails fast and the worker returns to the queue. A healthy slow generation is untouched: Anthropic sends periodic ping events, so the clock keeps resetting (#482).
- `update/` — **Update notifications** (on by default, gated by `Settings.updateCheck`). On startup Editora checks GitHub for a newer release, throttled to once/day and to once/session across windows. Pure, unit-tested **`update/UpdateCheck`** (java.base + Jackson `readTree` only): `parseLatest(mapper, json)` maps a GitHub `/releases/latest` payload → `update/ReleaseInfo{version,url,name}` (strips a leading `v` via `normalizeVersion`; returns null for a `draft`/`prerelease` or a missing `tag_name`, never throws), `isNewer(current, latest)` (delegates to the shared `plugin/PluginInstaller.compareVersions`, so `0.10 > 0.9` numerically; a `0.0.0` dev fallback surfaces the real latest), and `isDue(lastCheckMs, nowMs, intervalMs)` (the once/day throttle; a future timestamp = clock-moved-back also counts as due). The impure **`update/UpdateService`** (the `GitService`/`PluginRegistry` idiom: one `update-check` daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`) HTTPS-GETs `AppInfo.LATEST_RELEASE_API` reusing `PluginRegistry.readCapped`/`isHttps` (bounded 1 MB; a `User-Agent` header — GitHub 403s a missing one), parses via `UpdateCheck`, and posts an `Outcome{available, latest, error}`. **`AppInfo`** gained `GITHUB_REPO`/`LATEST_RELEASE_API`/`RELEASES_PAGE`. **`MainController`** owns the wiring: `maybeCheckForUpdates()` at the end of `init` (guarded by a static `updateCheckStartedThisSession` so only the first window hits the network, and `UpdateCheck.isDue` off the persisted `Settings.lastUpdateCheckEpoch`, which it stamps `now` before checking so a failed check doesn't retry all day); `onUpdateOutcome(outcome, manual)` caches a newer release in a **static `latestKnownUpdate`** (shared in-process so a second window + the About dialog see it) and `refreshUpdateNotice()`s; the notice is a **status-bar segment** (`StatusBar.setUpdateAvailable`, the `.status-update` accent pill, an `update.openDownloadPage` click target — always shown even in Simple mode) gated on `latestKnownUpdate != null && version != Settings.dismissedUpdateVersion`. Commands: `help.checkForUpdates` (manual — ignores the throttle *and* the setting, echoes checking/up-to-date/failed status), `update.openDownloadPage` (opens the release page — `ReleaseInfo.url()`, else `AppInfo.RELEASES_PAGE` — **and dismisses that version** by persisting `Settings.dismissedUpdateVersion`, hiding the segment), `view.toggleUpdateCheck`. `SettingsWindow.showAbout(...)` gained a nullable `ReleaseInfo` param → an "Update available: X.Y.Z" link row. Settings → Workspace → **Updates** checkbox (+ a "contacts GitHub over HTTPS, sends no data" note). `Settings.updateCheck`/`lastUpdateCheckEpoch`/`dismissedUpdateVersion` (schema 76→77 additive ×3). i18n ×6 (`command.*`/`statusbar.update`/`statusbar.tip.update`/`settings.checkForUpdates`/`settings.section.updates`/`settings.updates.note`/`about.updateAvailable`/`status.update.*`; the `{0}`-parameterized ones avoid apostrophes for MessageFormat). **No new dependency / `module-info` change** (`java.net.http` + Jackson already required; the `update` package needs no `exports`/`opens` — it reads JSON via `readTree`, no reflection). *Deferred: in-app download/auto-update (installers are unsigned), pre-release opt-in, a periodic re-check while running (only checks at startup), per-OS installer asset deep-linking.*
- **Markdown editing** (pure cores in `markdown/`, UI/overlays in `editor/`) — an IntelliJ-style **selection format bar** + smart editing, gated to Markdown buffers (`isMarkdown()` + editable + non-huge + view mode ≠ pure PREVIEW). Pure, unit-tested cores (no toolkit) all return a `markdown/MarkdownEdit` record (`from,to,replacement,selStart,selEnd`, applied via `area.replaceText`+`selectRange`, mirroring `Commenter`): **`MarkdownInline`** (toggle wrap/unwrap of `**`/`*`/`~~`/`` ` ``; `link(...)`; `linkAround(caret)` for open-link), **`MarkdownLines`** (`continuation(line)`/`isEmptyItem`/`markerLength` for list/quote continuation + `toggleBullet`), **`MarkdownHeading`** (`apply(delta)` promote/demote + `setLevel`, clamped 0–6, multi-line), **`MarkdownTable`** (`blockBounds(caret)` — **no `Math.max(0,caret-1)` clamp**: `lastIndexOf` searches from *and including* `fromIndex`, so clamping caret 0 finds a leading `\n` and yields `substring(1,0)`, and this runs on every Enter/Tab in a Markdown buffer — + `reflow` padding/aligning pipes honoring `:--`/`:-:`/`--:`; **an escaped `\|` is content, not a separator** — cells are held *unescaped* inside the class and re-escaped on emit (`escapePipes`), widths are measured on the escaped form, and `cellIndexAt`/`cellContentOffset` skip escaped pipes, so a `fromCsv` table survives a Tab; plus **table generation/editing** — `generate(rowsTotal, cols)` builds an aligned skeleton, `addRow`/`deleteRow`/`addColumn`/`deleteColumn` and `setAlignment(…, Align)` mutate the caret's table, each returning a `Nav{block,caret}` the controller applies like `tab`; the existing `tab`/`enter` give Tab-to-next-cell + add-row-on-Enter); `MarkdownLines.toggleTask` adds/removes a GFM checkbox (`- [ ] `). The **`editor/MarkdownFormatBar`** is a non-focus-traversable, free-positioned HBox of **icon buttons** — the same `MenuIcons` glyphs the editor right-click menu uses (bold/italic/strikethrough/code/link) plus bullet-list, **task-list/checkbox**, and an **insert-table** grid button (`MenuIcons.bulletList()`/`taskList()`/`table()`) and a Normal/H1–H6 `ComboBox` — calling back into `EditorBuffer` format methods (icons instead of letter labels keep it consistent with the menu and avoid the barely-slanted italic "I"; kept in `editor`, no `ui` dependency, like `CompletionPopup`). `EditorBuffer` owns the lifecycle: a **coalesced** `selectionProperty`/scroll listener (`scheduleFormatBar`/`updateFormatBar`, pending-flag per pulse — the `scheduleBraceMatch` idiom) positions it above the selection via `getCharacterBoundsOnScreen`→`screenToLocal`→`resizeRelocate` on `root`/`root2` (the ghost-label technique), hiding on Escape/blur/empty selection; format methods (`formatInline`/`formatLink`/`formatLinkFromClipboard`/`formatHeading`/`setHeadingLevel`/`formatBulletList`/`reflowTable`/`openLinkUnderCaret`) apply the core's `MarkdownEdit`; list/quote continuation lives in the existing `addAutoIndent` Enter filter; Ctrl/Cmd-click opens a link via an injected `setOpenUrlHandler` (controller `openExternalUrl`). Commands (markdown-gated, no-op elsewhere with a status): `markdown.bold`/`italic`/`strikethrough`/`code`/`link`/`bulletList`/`taskList`/`headingPromote`/`headingDemote`/`openLink`/`reflowTable`/`toggleFormatBar` + the table commands `insertTable` (the **mouse** path — the format-bar button + right-click "Insert Table" — opens a Typora/Word-style grid size-picker overlay; the **command-palette** path is keyboard-only, prompting for an `RxC` string parsed by the pure `MarkdownTable.parseSize`; both → `EditorBuffer.insertTable`)/`tableAddRow`/`tableDeleteRow`/`tableAddColumn`/`tableDeleteColumn`/`tableAlignLeft`/`tableAlignCenter`/`tableAlignRight`, with Emacs `markdown-mode`-style chords (`C-c C-s b/i/s/c`, `C-c C-s u`/`k` (bullet/task list), `C-c C-a l`, `C-c C-h p|d`, `C-c C-o`, `C-c C-s t` — note `C-c C-t` is taken by `view.toggleFold`) + a right-click **Format** group (`EditorBuffer.markdownMenuItems`, which also carries a **Table** submenu — insert/add/delete row & column/align). Gated by `Settings.markdownFormatBar` (default on; schema 13→14 additive-identity; Settings → Editor → Markdown checkbox + `SettingsWindow.syncMarkdownFormatBarCheck`; `MainController.applyViewSettings` pushes `setFormatBarEnabled`). CSS `.markdown-format-bar`/`.md-fmt-*` in `app.css`; i18n `command.markdown.*`/`tooltip.markdown.*`/`markdown.heading.*`/`settings.markdownFormatBar`/`status.markdown.*` across the six catalogs. **No new dependency / `module-info` change.** The pure Markdown logic — the editing cores (`MarkdownEdit`/`MarkdownInline`/`MarkdownLines`/`MarkdownHeading`/`MarkdownTable`), the lint cores (`MarkdownLint`/`MarkdownLintConfig`/`MarkdownLintDirectives`/`MarkdownLintFix` — MD009 exempts a **hard line break** via the shared `MarkdownLint.isHardLineBreak` (exactly 2 trailing spaces before a non-blank line = `<br>`, allowed by upstream's `br_spaces: 2`; the fixer must use the same rule or it deletes the break)), `MarkdownOutline`, and `MarkdownImagePaste` — lives in its own **`com.editora.markdown`** package (internal, no `exports`/`opens`/`module-info` change), with their unit tests under `com.editora.markdown`; the FX `MarkdownRenderer`, the preview/lint overlays + stripes, `MarkdownFormatBar`, and the image loaders (`PreviewImageLoader`/`MermaidImages`/`MathImages`) stay in `editor/` as the editor's rendering surfaces.  Tables also convert to/from **CSV**: pure/unit-tested `MarkdownTable.fromCsv` (delimiter auto-detect comma/semicolon/tab, RFC-4180 quoting, pipe-escaping) and `toCsv` back the GFM table block to the clipboard, via `EditorBuffer.tableFromCsv`/`tableToCsv` → commands `markdown.tableFromCsv`/`markdown.tableToCsv` + the right-click Table submenu. The caret's table also **file-exports** to **CSV / Excel (`.xlsx`) / ODF (`.ods`)**: `EditorBuffer.exportTableFile(format)` renders the table via `MarkdownTable.toCsv` then hands the CSV + format to the injected `setTableFileExporter` (editor stays free of `ui`/`office`); `MainController.exportMarkdownTableFile` picks the destination (`chooseOfficeDestination`) and either writes the CSV text (`exportCsvTextToFile`) or reuses the CSV grid's `csvExportSpreadsheet` (`CsvParser.parse` → `office/OfficeExportService.exportXlsx`/`exportOds`, header row = true since `toCsv` drops the `---` divider). Commands `markdown.tableExportCsv`/`tableExportExcel`/`tableExportOds` (palette + the right-click Table submenu, `MenuIcons.download()`); no new dependency.  **Table of contents:** pure/unit-tested `markdown/MarkdownToc` (`build`/`updated`/`slug`, reusing `MarkdownOutline.headings`) generates a nested list of GitHub-anchor heading links; `EditorBuffer.insertOrUpdateToc` inserts it wrapped in `<!-- toc -->`/`<!-- /toc -->` markers at the caret, or regenerates the existing marker block in place — command `markdown.toc` (palette + the right-click Markdown menu). (Supersedes the registry `markdown-toc` plugin.) **Image insertion** (pure `markdown/MarkdownImagePaste`: `uniqueFileName`/`relativePath`/`snippet`/`imageUrlFromDrag`/`extensionForUrl`): pasting a clipboard image (`tryMarkdownImagePaste`), dropping image **files** (`EditorBuffer.installImageDrop` → `MainController.insertDroppedImages`), and dragging a **raw image / image URL out of a web browser** (`setWebImageDropHandler` → `insertWebImage`) all copy/download the bytes into a sibling `assets/` dir and insert `![](assets/…)`. The browser path resolves the source via `MarkdownImagePaste.imageUrlFromDrag` (drag URL → `<img src>` in the dragged HTML → an image-looking string) and downloads it **off the FX thread** (`PreviewImageLoader.fetchBytes`, handling http(s) + `data:`); a raw `Dragboard` image is encoded to PNG via `PreviewImageLoader.imageToPng` (headless Java2D, no `javafx.swing`); on total failure it falls back to inserting the remote URL. Requires a saved local file (`assets/` resolves next to it; else `status.markdown.imageNeedsSave`). *Deferred: reference-style links, WYSIWYG inline rendering, table auto-format-on-type, table cell-merge / move-row-or-column, format bar in plaintext.*
- **Personal Notes** — file-attached annotations stored **outside** the file (for read-only/generated/shared code), built as a *separate* feature that reuses the **Bookmarks** machinery (see the bookmarks paragraph) rather than extending it; the two coexist. **Model** (`config/`, all Jackson-serialized so they ride the existing `opens com.editora.config to jackson.databind` — no `module-info` change): `enum NoteScope{WORD,LINE,RANGE}`, `enum NoteStatus{ACTIVE,RESOLVED,ORPHANED}`, `record FileIdentity(path,canonicalPath,size,lastModified,hash)` (pure `of(Path)` sha-256 capped at `MAX_HASH_BYTES`=5 MB, pure `match(a,b)` priority **canonicalPath → contentHash → similarPath**. **A content-hash match is not identity** — `PathKeys.findKeyByIdentity` (the re-key used when a buffer's path key misses) trusts it only when the candidate's own file is **gone from disk** (injected `Predicate<String> stillExists`, so it stays pure), because two files can hold the same bytes (`cp x x.bak`, a duplicated LICENSE, a monorepo's boilerplate `index.ts`) and accepting the hash alone made *opening* such a file `remove` the other's notes and re-`put` them under the new key — deleting them from the original), `record TextAnchor(line,column,endLine,endColumn,selectedText,prefix,suffix,length)` (`MAX_TEXT`/`MAX_CONTEXT` cap the stored text/context; **`length`** is the note's *full* uncapped selection length — a 7-arg convenience ctor derives it from the raw `selectedText` before the cap — so `NoteAnchors.relocate` highlights the whole span, not just the first `MAX_TEXT` chars of a >200-char note (#454; `notes.json` schema 1→2, additive: an old anchor deserializes with `length` 0 and the relocator falls back to the needle length)), `record PersonalNote(UUID id, FileIdentity, NoteScope, TextAnchor, body, List<String> tags, NoteStatus, long createdAt, long updatedAt)` — **`long` epoch-millis timestamps deliberately** (the default `ObjectMapper` has no jsr310 module). `NoteStore` mirrors `BookmarkStore`: `schemaVersion` + per-project `Map<projectKey, Map<fileKey, List<PersonalNote>>> byProject` (fileKey = canonicalPath), static `mergePreservingOrder(prev,current)` (matches by note **id**). **Storage**: a single versioned `notes.json` (`ConfigManager.getNotesFile`/`getNotes()` = the active project's bucket via the same `currentBookmarkKey()` derivation as bookmarks / `saveNotes()` / `loadNotes()` via `ConfigMigrations.readVersioned(..., ConfigSchema.NOTES)` / `deleteNotesForProject`), kept out of `WorkspaceState` like bookmarks. **Anchoring** (`editor/`): pure, unit-tested `NoteAnchors` (`shiftOffset`/`shiftRange` interval-adjust through a `PlainTextChange`; `relocate(doc,savedStart,savedEnd,selectedText,prefix,suffix,length)` → `int[]{start,end}` or null=orphan: a level-1 exact-offset check that **also requires the stored context to still match at `savedStart`** (so an identical line shifted into the old offset isn't mistaken for the original — an old/contextless note still passes, `wantContext == 0`), else occurrence scoring by a **graded `contextScore`** (0/1/2 of prefix/suffix match, not a boolean requiring both — a one-sided match beats none) then proximity, bounded by `MAX_OCCURRENCES`. **LINE-scope notes capture prefix/suffix context too** (`EditorBuffer.captureNoteDraft`, like WORD/RANGE) — the lines a LINE note lands on (`    }`/`});`/`end`/a repeated import) are the most-duplicated, so with empty context relocation collapsed to pure proximity and re-anchored to the nearest identical line (#453). The span runs to `start + max(length, needle.length())` clamped to the doc, so the full selection is highlighted, not just the capped needle (#454); a needle occurring **more than `MAX_OCCURRENCES`** (5000) is too ambiguous to place → **orphan** (honest + recoverable) rather than pick from a truncated top-of-file list, which used to jump a note living past occurrence #5000 far up-file (#455)). `NoteManager` (per-buffer, like `BookmarkManager`): holds `Map<UUID,Tracked>` of notes + live offset ranges, subscribes to `area.plainTextChanges()` to shift ranges (does **not** fire `onChanged` on edit-shifts — only `onLinesRepaint`; persistence happens on save/tab-switch, never per-keystroke), exposes `isNoted(line)`/`notesOnLine`/`noteAt(offset)`/`activeLines`/`next`/`previous`/`activeSpans()` (for the overlay), `add/update/remove/setStatus/clear` (these fire `onChanged`), `snapshot()` (rebuilds anchors from offsets), and `restore(saved)` (relocates each via `NoteAnchors`, returns whether anything moved/orphaned so the controller self-heal-persists — the bookmark pattern). **Editor surface**: `NoteHighlightOverlay` (a mouse-transparent `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`/`WhitespaceOverlay`: coalesced per-pulse redraw, visible-spans only, soft amber wash) paints behind each note's anchored span as a **flat, contiguous fill drawn like a text selection** (`paintSpan`, clamped to `first/lastVisibleParToAllParIndex`): one square fillRect **per visible line** with no per-line outline/rounding so adjacent lines join seamlessly; intermediate lines of a multi-line range fill to the viewport's right edge (matching how a selection paints the included line break), the first line starts at the start column and the last line stops at the end column; it also draws a small **amber corner-triangle marker at the note's start character** (inline, on the note's first visible line) — the "there's a note here" indicator is now inline at the selection start, **not** a gutter slot, and is **clickable** (`EditorBuffer.setNoteMarkerClick` → edit the note — restoring the old gutter click-to-edit). A `mouse-moved` hover (guarded to only update when the hovered note id changes) shows the body in a `Tooltip` whose graphic is the body **rendered as Markdown** (`renderNoteTooltip` → `MarkdownRenderer`, in the editor's own font family/size, with `app.css`+`syntax.css` attached to the node since the tooltip lives in its own popup scene; plain-label fallback on failure); the editor right-click menu prepends "Add Personal Note"/"Add Note to Selection" (when `path != null`). `EditorBuffer` mirrors the bookmark API: `getNoteManager`, `setAddNoteHandler`, `setOnNotesChanged`, `applyNotes`, `captureNoteDraft()` (infers WORD/RANGE/LINE + prefix/suffix context), `fileIdentity()`, `setNoteIndicatorsVisible`. **UI/commands**: `NotesPanel` (a `ToolWindowContent` modeled on `BookmarksPanel`, and like it now **groups by project** — General + current + a "Show all projects" toggle over `NotesPanel.Scope` / `ui/ScopeGroups`, with real `FileIcons` + accent project-group headers, #565) groups notes per file with a filter (bold file-header rows like Find-in-Files, plus a trailing clear-(`✕`) button shown only while the filter has text, reusing `.project-filter-bar`/`.project-filter-clear`), NoteCell context menu (Edit/Resolve↔Reopen/Delete, file: Delete all), double-click/Enter to open; tool window id `notes` (`tool.notes`, `M-5`, `Icons.notes()`). **`ui/NotesCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern) owns the `NotesPanel` + the two cross-file pickers + `persistNotes`/`restoreNotes` (run on save / tab switch / project switch; re-key by hash when the path key misses but the bucket is non-empty), `addNoteFromContext`/`addNoteAtCaret`, `editNoteAtCaret` (the `notes.editNote` command — edit the note at the caret, replacing the old gutter-click), `jumpNote` (next/previous), the `notes.jump` cross-file QuickOpen (`M-g n` — matches the note's first line) + `searchNotes` (`notes.search` — the same picker but its `QuickOpen` `searchKey` matches the **full body + tags + file** via `noteSearchText`, while the displayed label stays the first line; `QuickOpen` gained an optional `searchKey` ctor arg defaulting to the label, so other pickers are unchanged), `deleteNoteAtCaret`, `exportNotes` (FileChooser → JSON), the `showNoteDialog` editor, and the gating (`applySupport`/`ifEnabled`/`migrateKey`); it reaches the window via the shared host plus a small `Ops` extension (open-path / navigate-to-line / the shared `noteKey` + open-buffer-for-key / install-emacs-keys / tool-window availability / the `notes.json` map). `MainController` keeps the `ToolWindow` (built with `notesCoordinator.panel()`), the global `promptText`/`noteKey`/`tabForKey`/`navigateToLine`/`openPath` helpers, the rename-migration call (`notesCoordinator.migrateKey`), and wires `addBuffer`'s note hooks + the `notes.*`/`view.toggleNotes` commands to the coordinator. (Resolve/Reopen is available from the panel's NoteCell menu; there's no caret command for it.) Bodies are edited via `showNoteDialog(initial, onAccept, onDelete)` — a **multi-line** `TextArea` `Dialog` (Enter = newline, Ctrl/Cmd+Enter = save) with the user's **configured keybindings** installed for caret movement + basic editing via `command/TextInputKeymap.install(textArea, keymap)` (a dialog has its own scene, so the global `KeyDispatcher` isn't there — `TextInputKeymap` adds a `KEY_PRESSED` filter that resolves the same chord token through `KeymapManager` and runs the matching `nav.*`/`edit.*` action on the `TextInputControl`, e.g. Emacs `C-a`/`C-e`/`C-f`/`C-b`/`C-n`/`C-p`/`M-f`/`M-b`/`C-d`/`C-k`/`C-w`/`M-w`/`C-y`; pure caret math `lineStart`/`lineEnd`/`lineUp`/`lineDown`/`backToIndentation` is unit-tested; reusable for any dialog text field); when editing an existing note it shows a left-aligned **Delete** button (`onDelete`) that **confirms first** (a native `CONFIRMATION` alert). The dialog also shows a muted hint (`.note-dialog-hint`) that the body supports **Markdown** (it renders as Markdown in the hover tooltip). `promptNoteBody` delegates to it with no delete. Commands: `notes.add` (`C-c n`), `notes.editNote` (`C-c e`, edit the note at the caret — also via clicking the inline marker), `notes.toggleResolved` (resolve/reopen the note at the caret), `notes.next`/`previous`, `notes.jump` (`M-g n`), `notes.search` (`M-g s`, full-text picker), `notes.delete` (deletes the note on the caret line; also in the panel + the editor's Delete button), `notes.export`, `tool.notes` (`M-5`). **Gated by `Settings.notesSupport`** ("Enable Personal Notes", Settings → Application, default **on**) — `NotesCoordinator.applySupport()` (mirrors `GitCoordinator.applySupport`, called at init + on every settings apply) hides the Notes tool window (`toolWindows.setAvailable`), sets each buffer's `setNotesEnabled` (gates the editor "Add Note" menu items), and on the off→on transition `restoreNotes` every open buffer; the `ifEnabled(...)` wrapper no-ops each `notes.*`/`tool.notes` command + keybinding, those ids are filtered from the command palette, and `persistNotes`/`restoreNotes` early-return while off. A second **view toggle** `Settings.showNoteIndicators` (default on, only effective when notes are enabled) hides just the inline start marker + highlight — `applyViewSettings` applies the effective `notesSupport && showNoteIndicators`, and the Settings "Show note indicators" checkbox disables when the master is off (autocomplete master/sub pattern). All strings localized in the six catalogs. *Deferred: fuzzy match beyond nearest-text, scrollbar/minimap markers, Markdown note bodies, team/cloud sync — the model already carries tags/status/FileIdentity so these are additive.*
- `vfs/` — **Remote file access (SFTP)**. Edit/browse/search files on a remote host over SSH/SFTP. The
  approach keeps `EditorBuffer.path` a `java.nio.file.Path` but lets it belong to a **non-default
  filesystem** (a MINA SSHD `SftpFileSystem`), so `Files.readString`/`writeString`/`list`/`walkFileTree`/
  `readAttributes` keep working over SFTP and the Project tree / search / open / save need no rewrite. The
  only local-only boundary is `path.toFile()` (used by `ProcessRunner`/LSP/DAP/run) — gated off for remote.
  **`Vfs`** (pure, unit-tested) is the seam: `isLocal(Path)` (= `path.getFileSystem() == FileSystems.getDefault()`,
  the single predicate every local-process feature gates on; a null/untitled path counts as local),
  `toStorableString`/`parseStorable` (a path↔string round-trip — local plain, remote as its `sftp://` URI,
  reconstructed through an injected resolver), `isRemoteUri`, `displayLabel`. **`SftpUri`** (pure,
  unit-tested) parses/formats `sftp://[user@]host[:port]/path` and yields the `authority()` connection key.
  **`RemoteConnection`** (record: host/port/user/`AuthMethod {DEFAULT_KEYS, KEY, PASSWORD}`/keyPath/label/
  lastPath — **no secret**) + **`config/ConnectionStore`** (schema-versioned `connections.json`,
  `ConfigSchema.CONNECTIONS`; `ConfigManager.getConnections`/`putConnection`/`removeConnection`/
  `saveConnections`/`loadConnections`). **`RemoteFileSystems`** (UI-owned, the `GitService` idiom: a daemon
  executor + `Platform.runLater`) holds one `SftpFileSystem` per `user@host:port`, `connect(conn, secret,
  cb)` (auth precedence **default `~/.ssh` keys → key file → password**; the secret `char[]` is wiped after
  use, and the password is removed from the SSH session the instant the handshake finishes —
  `RemoteFileSystems.authenticate`'s `finally` — so MINA's String-only `addPasswordIdentity` copy isn't
  retained on the session for the whole connection), `pathFor(SftpUri)`/`disconnect`/`shutdown`, and **registers itself in the `Vfs` provider registry** so remote URIs in
  recent-files reconstruct to live Paths. **Multi-window (#436):** `RemoteFileSystems` is per-window but `Vfs`'s remote hooks are `static`, so they're a **registry of `Vfs.RemoteProvider`s (one per window)**, not a single slot — `Vfs.registerRemoteProvider(this)` in the ctor, `unregisterRemoteProvider(this)` in `shutdown`. `RemoteFileSystems implements Vfs.RemoteProvider`: `resolve(uri)` returns a live Path only for an authority it has connected (`pathFor` → `byAuthority.get(authority)`, else null), and `storable(path)` returns an `sftp://` string only for a Path whose `FileSystem` it owns (else null). `Vfs.parseStorable` tries each provider until one resolves (first non-null wins); `Vfs.toStorableString` dispatches to the provider owning the path's `FileSystem`. So a second window connecting to another host no longer clobbers the first's resolution, and closing one window only removes *its* provider — the others' remote paths keep resolving. **Local-only gating** (all inert for local files, so zero
  behavior change): `MainController.isLocalBuffer` + `Vfs.isLocal` guards on LSP (`syncBufferLsp`
  eligibility), DAP/breakpoints (`isDebuggableBuffer`), run/shell-run/HTTP (`addBuffer`), git
  (`refreshGit` → `RepoState.NONE` for a remote context), and external-change polling
  (`checkExternalChanges` skips remote — a network `mtime` per focus). **Remote stays text-capable**:
  editing, highlighting, search, bookmarks, notes, preview, PDF/print. **The SFTP UI/commands live in
  `ui/RemoteCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` feature-coordinator pattern — owns the `RemoteFileSystems`
  engine + the `RemoteConnectionsPanel` + the mount state, reaching the window via the shared host plus an
  `Ops` extension for keymap / open-path / set-project-root / open-project-tool-window / active-project-root /
  error-report (reusing `GitCoordinator.gitError`) / the `connections.json` get/put/remove; `MainController`
  keeps the `remote` `ToolWindow` built with `remoteCoordinator.panel()`, queries `isMounted()` for the
  current-folder view, and wires the `remote.*`/`tool.remote` commands + the Welcome quick-connect to it).
  **UI/commands**:
  `remote.connect` (an `OverlayInput` form — host/port/user/auth + key Browse/secret/path, localized auth
  picker; on success **mounts the remote folder as the Project tree root** via `projectPanel.setRoot` +
  opens the Project tool window, and `config.putConnection`s it), `remote.manageConnections` (a `QuickOpen`
  over saved connections → re-opens the form pre-filled), `remote.openFile` (an `sftp://` URI →
  `Vfs.parseStorable` → `openPath`), `remote.disconnect` (restores the local project root). **Saved sites get
  three visible surfaces** (all over the same `connections.json` most-recent-first list — no schema/secret
  change): a **Remote Sites tool window** (`ui/RemoteConnectionsPanel`, id `remote`, `Side.RIGHT`, `Icons::remote`,
  `tool.remote`/`M-g r`, *not* buffer-gated, **registered default-hidden** via `toolWindows.register(tw, false)` —
  the stripe button is off until the user enables it (Settings → Tool Windows or `tool.remote`), and it opens on the
  right; the remote *functionality* is unaffected — a flat `ListView` of saved sites; double-click/Enter or the
  New/Connect/Remove bar → `connectRemote(c)`/`removeConnection`/`connectRemote()`, refreshed on open + after a
  mount); a **Settings → Remote master-detail page** (`SettingsWindow.remoteConnectionsEditor`, mirroring the
  External Tools page — list + label/host/port/user/auth/key-path form editing the immutable `RemoteConnection`
  record via `remoteItems.set(i, …)`, persisted through the new `ConfigManager.setConnections(list)` →
  `SharedConfig` whole-list replace; opened by `remote.settings` → `showRemote`); and a **Welcome-page "Remote
  Sites" quick-connect list** (`WelcomePane.remoteList`, shown only when non-empty, each row → `connectRemote(c)`).
  All three open the **prefilled connect form** on pick (so the secret is still prompted), never a silent
  reconnect. A remote buffer
  opens with a remote `Path`, so plain Save → `writeBuffer` → `Files.writeString` writes back over SFTP, no
  dialog; `saveAs` is guarded for remote. Recent files round-trip the `sftp://` URI (`Vfs.toStorableString`;
  a remote entry resolves only once its connection is open). **Host-key verification (do not weaken):** the client uses a `KnownHostsServerKeyVerifier` over **`~/.ssh/known_hosts`** — shared with OpenSSH on purpose. Unknown host → the injected `RemoteFileSystems.HostKeyPrompt` (trust-on-first-use; `RemoteCoordinator` marshals it to FX and blocks the SSH I/O thread, bounded + fail-closed), written to the file only on acceptance; **changed key → refused without asking** (that's the MITM — a prompt there just gets clicked through); no prompt → refuse. It shipped as `AcceptAllServerKeyVerifier`, which made every SFTP session unauthenticated and handed a password-auth MITM the password (GHSA-p4qf-p7q6-2mrw). **The host-key dialog's think-time is excluded from the handshake deadline (#486):** the trust-on-first-use prompt blocks the key exchange that gates auth, so it lands inside the auth wait — a careful "compare this fingerprint" answer would otherwise time out at `AUTH_TIMEOUT` (20s). The verifier times how long the dialog is open (`promptStartNanos` while up + `promptAccumulatedNanos` once closed; `livePromptElapsedNanos()` also counts an in-progress dialog, since the deadline is checked *while* it's up), and `authenticate` polls the `AuthFuture` in `POLL_MILLIS` steps discounting that time via the pure/unit-tested `handshakeExpired(elapsed, promptNanos, timeout)`. A genuinely stuck host still fails at `AUTH_TIMEOUT` (prompt time stays 0 when nobody is asked). The connect phase keeps a plain `verify(CONNECT_TIMEOUT)` — MINA fulfils the connect future at the transport level, before KEX, so no prompt overlaps it. `CONNECT_TIMEOUT`/`AUTH_TIMEOUT` are ctor-injectable so the FX test exercises the deadline in ~2s. Tested against a real in-process `SshServer` **and a real impostor on the same port** (`HostKeyVerificationTest` + `RemoteFileSystemsHostKeyFxTest`); the known_hosts path is ctor-injectable so tests never touch the real one. **Dependency:** Apache **MINA SSHD**
  (`org.apache.sshd:sshd-osgi` + `sshd-sftp`) — the combined **sshd-osgi** bundle (module
  `org.apache.sshd.osgi`) is used instead of sshd-common+sshd-core, which **split** the
  `org.apache.sshd.common`/`server` packages across two automatic modules (illegal under JPMS); `sshd-sftp`
  **excludes** sshd-core/sshd-common + **`jcl-over-slf4j`** (its `org.apache.commons.logging` module
  collides with pdfbox's commons-logging under jlink), and **slf4j-api is forced to 2.0.17** (a real
  module, not the automatic 1.7.36 SSHD pins). `module-info` `requires org.apache.sshd.osgi`/`.sftp` +
  `opens com.editora.vfs to com.fasterxml.jackson.databind` (the `RemoteConnection` record). **dist/jlink
  moditect:** sshd-osgi uses a hand-maintained `src/moditect/module-info-sshd-osgi.java` (jdeps's 106
  exports + a `requires org.slf4j` jdeps drops under `--ignore-missing-deps` — without it every SSHD class
  fails at load), and sshd-sftp uses a hand-written client-only `<moduleInfoSource>` (drops the unused SFTP-
  *server* `SubsystemFactory` provides that jlink rejects, keeps only the nio FileSystemProvider). The
  `-Pdist` app-image builds, links, and launches. *Deferred: OS-keychain secret storage + auto-reconnect on
  launch, true ssh-agent (SSH_AUTH_SOCK), remote LSP/DAP/git/run, remote Save-As / new-file, a status-bar
  remote indicator + tab tooltip, remote-search caps, FTP/WebDAV/cloud providers (the layer generalizes).*
- `plugin/` — **Plugin support** (off by default, gated by `Settings.pluginSupport`; **also off in Simple UI
  mode** via `pluginsEnabled()`). A plugin is a folder `<configDir>/plugins/<id>/` with a `plugin.json`
  manifest + optionally a Java jar (`*.jar`/`lib/*.jar`) + `snippets/`/`templates/` dirs. **The one hard
  constraint:** the `-Pdist` build is a **sealed jlink image with no module path at runtime** and there is no
  `ServiceLoader` infra, so plugins are discovered by **manifest** and a Java plugin's classes load via a
  child **`URLClassLoader(jarUrls, appClassLoader)`** (parent = the app module's loader → the plugin can use
  Editora's **exported** packages `com.editora.plugin`/`command`/`ui`/`editor`/`config` + the baked JDK/JavaFX
  modules via normal parent delegation; **no `ModuleLayer`**). Compile a plugin on a plain **classpath**, not
  the module path. **API (the exported `com.editora.plugin` package):** `interface Plugin {void start(ctx);
  default void stop()}`; `interface PluginContext` (`registerCommand(id,title,Runnable)`, `bindKey(chord,
  commandId)`, `registerToolWindow(id,title,ToolWindowSide,Region,commandId[,Supplier<Node> icon])` (the icon
  overload sets the stripe glyph — a `Supplier<javafx.scene.Node>`, e.g. an `SVGPath` with the `toolbar-icon`
  style class; the no-icon overload is a `default` delegating with `null` ⇒ the jigsaw `Icons.plugin()`),
  `addEditorMenuItem(label,
  Consumer<ActiveEditor>)`, `addStatusBarSegment(label,commandId)`, `activeEditor()`, `pluginDir()/dataDir()/
  configDir()`, `log/setStatus`); `interface ActiveEditor` (narrow editor facade — `filePath/text/
  selectedText/replaceSelection/insertAtCaret/setText/openPath` (`setText` = whole-buffer replace, undoable —
  for whole-file transforms like formatting), **never** exposes `MainController`); `enum
  ToolWindowSide{LEFT,RIGHT,BOTTOM}` (keeps the API package free of a hard `ui` dependency); lenient Jackson
  `PluginManifest` (`@JsonIgnoreProperties` — `id/name/version/main`, `Map keymap`, `List<DeclaredCommand>
  commands{id,title,List<String> run,dir}`) + `PluginDescriptor` (manifest/dir/enabled/classLoader/loadError).
  **`PluginManager`** is **shared, owned by `ui/WindowManager`** (created once with `(pluginsDir, isEnabled
  predicate)` + `discover()`): `discover()` scans the dir, parses each manifest (`parseManifest`, unit-tested),
  builds one `URLClassLoader` per enabled Java plugin; `instantiate(descriptor)` does `Class.forName(main,...)`
  + `newInstance` under the plugin TCCL, catching `Throwable` → null (one bad plugin never blocks others).
  **The whole plugin feature lives in `ui/PluginCoordinator`** (the `CoordinatorHost` pattern): it owns the
  per-window `PluginRegistry`/`PluginInstaller`, the started-plugin instances, the plugin-contributed tool
  windows + editor menu items, the "Browse Plugins" picker, and the two inner adapters
  (`PluginContextImpl`/`ActiveEditorImpl`). The shared `PluginManager` (owned by `WindowManager`) is passed
  in; `MainController` keeps the `pluginManager` field + thin `disposePlugins()` (the `WindowManager`
  window-close contract) and `pluginsEnabled()` delegates, and wires `applyPlugins` / the buffer-gating
  (`gateToolWindows`) / the editor-menu contributor (`editorMenuItems`) / the `plugins.*`+`view.togglePlugins`
  commands to the coordinator; `PluginCoordinator.pluginCapabilitySummary` is the public static the Settings
  page also calls. **Multi-window:** classes load **once** (shared manager), but a `Plugin` **instance + its
  tool-window content Node are built per window** (a Node can't live in two scenes) — `PluginCoordinator.applyPlugins()` (run in
  `init`, **before** `toolWindows.restore()` so contributed windows restore their visibility) registers the
  declarative bits + `plugin.<id>.<cmd>` external commands (`runDeclaredCommand` → `process/ProcessRunner`
  off-thread) + applies the shared `keymap.applyOverrides(manifest.keymap)`, then `instantiate` + `start(new
  PluginContextImpl(d))` each Java plugin; `disposePlugins()` (window close) calls each `stop()`.
  `PluginContextImpl.fullId(id)` namespaces a bare command/tool-window id to `plugin.<id>.<...>` (a dotted id
  = a built-in, used verbatim); tool windows register via `toolWindows.register` + a toggle command,
  status-bar segments via `StatusBar.addPluginSegment`, editor menu items via a `setMenuContributor` hook on
  each `EditorBuffer` (the `editor` package stays decoupled — a `Supplier<List<MenuItem>>` injected from
  `MainController.pluginEditorMenuItems`). **Buffer-gated stripe:** every registered plugin tool window is
  tracked in `MainController.pluginToolWindows` and its stripe button is gated on an open editor buffer
  (`toolWindows.setAvailable(tw, activeBuffer() != null)` at registration + in `updateBufferToolWindows()`,
  alongside the built-in Structure/File-Info/TODO windows) — plugins act on the active editor, so they're
  hidden on a non-buffer tab (e.g. Welcome). **Opt-out:** the full
  `registerToolWindow(id,title,side,content,commandId,icon,needsBuffer)` overload takes a `needsBuffer` flag
  (the icon/no-icon overloads are `default`s delegating with `true`); a plugin passes `false` for a
  self-contained tool window (scratchpad/calculator/…) so it's **not** added to `pluginToolWindows` and stays
  available on every tab. Declarative **assets**: `SnippetManager.addExtraSourceDir`/
  `TemplateRegistry.addExtraSourceDir` (generalized extra-source-dir lists, cache-clearing) merge a plugin's
  `snippets/`/`templates/` into the registries (`reload()`d once after applying). **Enabled set** lives in
  `<configDir>/plugins.json` (`config/PluginStore`, schema-versioned via `ConfigSchema.PLUGINS`, owned by
  `SharedConfig` — `getPluginStore`/`savePlugins`/`getPluginsDir`). **Gating:** `Settings.pluginSupport`
  (default off; schema 21→22 additive-identity) + `applyPlugins` early-returns when off, so `plugin.*`
  commands are never even registered when disabled (no palette filter needed). **Settings → Plugins** page
  (data-driven over `pluginManager.descriptors()`): a master *Enable plugins* checkbox + a "runs untrusted
  code, no sandbox" warning + the plugins-folder path + a **Reload** button (`discover()` + `refreshPluginList`)
  + a per-plugin enable checkbox row (writes `PluginStore.setEnabled` + `savePlugins`; load errors shown in
  red `settings-git-missing`) + a "restart to apply" note; `SettingsWindow.setPluginManager` is injected after
  construction (the page builds lazily on first `show`). Palette toggle `view.togglePlugins`
  (`togglePluginSupport` — persists + `syncPluginsCheck`, reports a restart is needed). `module-info`
  `exports com.editora.plugin;` + `opens com.editora.plugin to com.fasterxml.jackson.databind;` (the manifest
  DTO). **Plugins load at startup only** — enable/disable + the master gate take effect on the next launch (no
  hot classloader/UI unload; per-window `stop()` on close is the only teardown). **Class-loader lifecycle (#442):**
  `PluginManager` tracks every `URLClassLoader` it builds in a `live` set and ref-counts them in `pins`. Each
  window's `PluginCoordinator` `pin`s a loader per started plugin (in `applyPlugins`) and `release`s it in
  `disposePlugins`; `discover()` closes any previously-built loader that's now orphaned (unpinned and not carried
  into the new descriptor set — the Reload/install/uninstall leak that held jar handles + locked the jar on
  Windows), `release` closes a loader once its last pin drops **and** it's no longer a current descriptor's
  loader, and `WindowManager.onWindowClosed` calls `closeAll()` when the last window closes. A loader still in use
  by a plugin running in another window is never closed (pinned), so this is safe without hot-reload. **One new
  exported package; no new Maven dependency.** Plugin-API Javadoc (the author-facing surface) builds + doclint-validates via the `apidocs` profile: `./mvnw -Papidocs javadoc:javadoc` (scoped to `com.editora.plugin`, `doclint=all,-missing` so broken `@link`/HTML fail). Example: `examples/example-plugin/` (a complete Java + declarative plugin with a
  `build.sh`) + `docs/plugins.md`. **Registry / install (browse + from-disk):** a plugin is distributed as a
  **`.zip`** whose top level is the plugin folder contents. **`RegistryIndex`/`RegistryEntry`** (lenient
  Jackson, static `parse`) model a curated **`index.json`**; **`PluginRegistry`** fetches it over HTTPS
  (the `HttpClientService` idiom — JDK `java.net.http`, daemon executor + `Platform.runLater`, HTTPS-only
  guard `isHttps`, per-URL cache); **`PluginInstaller`** (off-thread) does `installFromUrl` (download →
  **mandatory sha-256 verify** → unzip → move into `<pluginsDir>/<id>/` → `pm.discover()`) + `installFromZip`
  (no checksum — the user picked it); **`Unzip`** is a hardened `ZipInputStream` extractor with a
  **zip-slip guard** (`safeEntryName`/`isUnderDir`) + per-entry/total/count caps. Pure helpers
  (`compareVersions`, `isSafeId`, `sha256(byte[])`, the unzip guards) are unit-tested (`RegistryIndexTest`,
  `PluginInstallerTest`). `Settings.pluginRegistryUrl` (default `DEFAULT_PLUGIN_REGISTRY` =
  `adriandeleon/editora-plugins` raw `index.json`, overridable; schema 22→23 additive). UI: a `QuickOpen<RegistryEntry>`
  browse picker (status = Installed / Update available / Install / Requires-newer via `compareVersions` +
  `AppInfo.VERSION`), an install **confirm `Alert`** (name/version/source + trust warning), a `FileChooser`
  install-from-disk, and Settings → Plugins **Registry URL** field + **Browse / Install-from-file / per-plugin
  Remove** buttons (`SettingsWindow.setPluginActions` injected by `MainController`). Commands `plugins.browse`/
  `plugins.installFromDisk` (palette-filtered when plugins off); `MainController.onPluginInstalled` enables the
  id in `PluginStore` + `savePlugins` + `syncPluginsCheck`; `uninstallPlugin` deletes `plugins/<id>/`. **No new
  dependency** (`java.net.http` already required). **Example plugin:** the editor repo keeps a single
  in-tree reference, `examples/example-plugin/` (a complete Java + declarative plugin exercising every
  extension point, with a generic `build.sh` that reads the id from `plugin.json` and emits `<id>.zip` + its
  sha) — this is the SDK example `docs/plugins.md` walks through. **The full plugin catalog (and the live,
  signed `index.json` registry) lives in the separate `adriandeleon/editora-plugins` repo** under
  `plugins/<id>/` — text/encode/hash/json tools, scratchpad, format-runner, regex-tester, markdown-toc,
  color-picker, word-count, calculator, run-task, slug-tools, open-on-github, box-banner, etc. They were
  *not* kept duplicated under `examples/` (that copy had already drifted); add or update a real plugin in the
  registry repo, not here.
  **Security:** consent + integrity + authenticity. (1) *Consent* — `MainController.confirmEnablePlugin` shows a
  **capability disclosure** (jar? declared external commands + argv? keybinding remaps? via
  `pluginCapabilitySummary`) before *enabling* at every arming point (install, install-from-file, the Settings
  per-plugin checkbox). (2) *Integrity/anti-OOM* — `PluginRegistry.readCapped` bounds the index + download
  reads; `RegistryIndex.parse` caps entry field lengths; HTTPS-only + no `https→http` downgrade; a
  non-default registry URL is flagged with its host. (3) *Authenticity* — `PluginSignature` verifies a
  detached **Ed25519** signature of `index.json` (fetched from `<url>.sig`) against a **bundled public key**
  (`resources/com/editora/plugin/editora-registry.pub`; JDK `java.security`, no dependency);
  `PluginRegistry.Result.signed` carries the verdict, and `Settings.pluginRequireSignature` (default on; schema
  23→24) makes `browsePlugins` **block** an unsigned/unverified registry. The registry owner signs with
  `scripts/PluginSigningTool.java` (keygen/sign/verify, Ed25519); the private key is never committed (the
  bundled `.pub` is). Signing proves *who* published — not a sandbox.
  *Deferred (full trust in v1, like VSCode/IntelliJ): sandboxing, hot reload, inter-plugin deps,
  GitHub-API/per-repo discovery, per-plugin/TOFU signing, auto-update, gutter-marker contributions.*
- `editorconfig/` — **EditorConfig (`.editorconfig`) support** (on by default, gated by
  `Settings.editorConfigSupport`; schema 29→30 additive-identity). Honors `root`, `indent_style`,
  `indent_size` (incl. `tab`), `tab_width`, `end_of_line` (lf/crlf/cr), `charset`
  (utf-8/utf-8-bom/latin1/utf-16le/utf-16be), `trim_trailing_whitespace`, `insert_final_newline`, and
  `max_line_length` (incl. `off`). All **pure + unit-tested** (java.base only, no dependency/moditect):
  **`EditorConfigProperties`** (record of nullable boxed fields + `OFF` sentinel + `EMPTY` +
  `merge(lower, higher)` where higher's non-null wins), **`EditorConfigParser`**
  (`parse(text)`→`Parsed{root, List<Section{glob, Map}>}` + `toProperties` typed conversion: keys/values
  lowercased, glob keeps case, `indent_size=tab`→null, `max_line_length=off`→OFF, lenient positive-int),
  **`EditorConfigGlob`** (`matches(glob, relPath)` glob→regex: prepends `**/` when no slash, `**/`→
  `(?:.*/)?`, `*`→`[^/]*`, `?`→`[^/]`, `[!`→`[^`, `{a,b}`→alternation, `{n1..n2}`→numeric alternation
  capped at `MAX_RANGE`), **`EditorConfigCharset`** (`charsetFor`/`writesBom`/`bomFor`/`detectByBom`
  (UTF-8 BOM, then UTF-16BE before LE)/`decode`/`encode`/`displayName`), and **`EditorConfigTransform`**
  (`transform(content, props)`: trim trailing + EOL-normalize + final-newline, idempotent, returns content
  unchanged when nothing is set so EOLs are preserved). The one impure class **`EditorConfig`** —
  `resolveFor(Path)` walks up dirs reading `.editorconfig` (per-file **mtime cache**), matches sections,
  merges nearest-dir-wins, stops at `root=true`; `clearCache()`. **Wiring** (`MainController`):
  `applyEditorConfig(buffer)` (gated `editorConfigEnabled() && path!=null && Vfs.isLocal`) resolves the
  chain and pushes per-buffer overrides — indent (`EditorBuffer.setIndentOverride` → `Indenter.smartTab`/
  `enterEdit` new `(Boolean insertSpaces, Integer size)` overloads, the legacy signatures delegating
  `(null,null)` so the no-`.editorconfig` path is byte-identical) — the **effective** indent is resolved by
  `MainController.applyEffectiveIndent(buffer, props)` with precedence **`.editorconfig` `indent_style` >
  global `Settings.indentStyle` (`detect`/`space`/`tab`, default `detect`; Settings → Editor "Indent style"
  combo + the `editor.setIndentStyle` palette picker via `chooseSetting`; schema 30→31 additive-identity) >
  per-file `Indenter.detectUnit`** (so the global preference applies even when EditorConfig is off / a file
  is remote / has no path — it runs in the early-return branch too; `detectUnit` reads the first indented
  line and **falls back to spaces** when the file has no indentation, matching VSCode/IntelliJ's
  "spaces unless detected as tabs" default), tab width (`setTabSize`), EOL
  (`setEolOverride`, `getLineEnding()` returns it; a manual `chooseLineEndings` change sets it so the
  user wins for the session), ruler column (`setRulerColumn`, OFF hides), charset
  (`setCharsetOverride`/`getEffectiveCharset`) — plus `setEditorConfigProps` for save time; called from
  `applyViewSettings`. `applyEditorConfigSupport()` (mirrors `applyGitSupport`: init + every settings
  apply; off → clear overrides + cache). **Read/write are charset-aware**: `readWithCharset` does
  `Files.readAllBytes` → BOM-detect → else EditorConfig `charset` → else UTF-8, `setDetectedCharset`,
  decode (huge-file `readCapped` stays UTF-8, documented); `saveBytes` runs `EditorConfigTransform` then
  `EditorConfigCharset.encode` (BOM-prefixed when needed) — used by `writeBuffer` (`Files.write`) and
  `autoSaveBuffer` (snapshot bytes on FX, write off-thread); **disk-only** — the live document/caret/undo
  are untouched. StatusBar shows the per-buffer tab size + `EditorConfigCharset.displayName(getEffectiveCharset())`,
  plus a clickable **EditorConfig** segment (`status-editorconfig`) shown only when the active buffer's resolved
  props are non-empty (`refresh()` checks `buffer.getEditorConfigProps()`, hidden in Simple mode); its click runs
  the `editorConfig.openActive` command → `MainController.openActiveEditorConfig` → `EditorConfig.nearestFile(path)`
  (closest `.editorconfig` walking up to `root=true`) → `openPath`. Palette `view.toggleEditorConfig` (via the
  generic `toggleSetting`) + `editorConfig.openActive`; Settings → Editor "Enable
  EditorConfig" checkbox (`viewCheck` + `syncAll`/`syncViewChecks`). The repo ships its own `.editorconfig` at the
  root (Java 4-space/120-col per Palantir, JSON 2-space, shell tabs, etc.). *Deferred: per-language indent
  profiles beyond the std keys, live re-resolve on `.editorconfig` edit (currently mtime-cache-invalidated),
  remote-file support.*
- `logviewer/` — **Server log viewer** (on by default for `.log` files, gated by `Settings.logViewer`; **suppressed in Simple UI mode** via `LogViewerCoordinator.isEnabled()`). Pure, unit-tested core: **`LogLevel`** (TRACE…FATAL with a severity `rank()`; `fromToken` maps Logback/Log4j, `java.util.logging` FINEST…SEVERE, syslog, and zerolog 3-letter forms), **`LogPatterns`** (`levelOf(line)` — an UPPERCASE level token near the line start wins, else a bracketed any-case `[error]` / a `level=…`/JSON field, else an Apache/Nginx access-log status 5xx→ERROR/4xx→WARN/2xx→INFO; deliberately prose-safe so the lowercase word "error" in a message never reclassifies a line; plus `looksLikeLog`/`hasLeadingTimestamp` content sniffs), **`LogFilter`** (`filter(text, minLevel, regex, startCarry)` keeps lines passing a level floor AND regex, where an unleveled continuation/stack-trace line **inherits the previous record's level** so an exception's whole trace survives a `WARN+` filter; `effectiveLevel`/`endCarry` make incremental appends correct), and **`LogTail`** (`readTail(file, maxBytes)` opens a huge log at its **end**, dropping the partial first line; `readAppended(file, fromOffset)` reads only the delta and holds back a trailing incomplete UTF-8 sequence — the pure `completeEnd`/`firstLineStart` byte maths are unit-tested — and flags `reset` when the file shrank = rotation). **`LogTailService`** (the `GitService` daemon idiom: one `ScheduledExecutorService` poll per followed file, ~500 ms, `Platform.runLater` callbacks) drives `tail -f` via `LogTail.readAppended` and returns a `Handle` to stop it. **Highlighting is two complementary layers:** a bundled `grammars/log.tmLanguage.json` (`source.log`, ext `log`) whose `markup.error/warning/info/debug/trace.log` + `constant.other.timestamp.log` scopes map (in `TextMateHighlighter.classify`) to `.text.log-*` classes (AtlantaFX semantic colors in `syntax.css`, so no per-editor-theme override) — inline token color for logs under the 5 MB highlight cap; **plus `editor/LogHighlightOverlay`** (a coalesced, visible-lines-only `Canvas` mirroring `SpellCheckOverlay`: a solid left-edge bar per leveled line + a faint WARN/ERROR row wash, level inheritance via a bounded upward scan, cached per line) — **size-independent**, so the huge tail-loaded logs where TextMate is off still show levels. **`EditorBuffer`** mirrors the markdown-mode bolt-on: `isLog()` (language `"log"` or forced via `setLogViewForced`), a floating `setLogControl(Node)` overlaid top-right (reusing `attachControlToCodePane`, mutually exclusive with the markdown/html controls), `setLogHighlightEnabled`, `applyLogFilter(minLevel, regex)` (keeps the full text aside in `logFullText`, shows only matching lines, re-applies incrementally on append), `appendLogText`/`resetLogContent` (follow + rotation; auto-scroll to bottom while `logFollowing`; trims past a 12 MB `LOG_FOLLOW_CAP` to bound memory). **`ui/LogControlBar`** (the floating control, the `HtmlPreviewToggle` pattern): a Follow `ToggleButton` (`Icons.arrowDown()`), a minimum-level `ComboBox`, and a regex `TextField`, reporting through callbacks to **`ui/LogViewerCoordinator`** — the first *feature coordinator* extracted from `MainController` (it owns the tail service + the per-buffer follow/offset/control maps and reaches the window only through a shared `CoordinatorHost` interface — settings, active/all buffers, status, `fileSize`, `requestSave`, overlay host, prompt; `MainController` supplies an anonymous `Host` adapter and keeps one-line delegations at each call site, and a fake `Host` makes the coordinator unit-testable — see `LogViewerCoordinatorFxTest`). It owns the wiring: `applySupport()` (init + every settings apply, mirrors `applyHtmlPreviewSupport`) (un)attaches the control + overlay on log buffers; `ensureControl` gates on `isEnabled() && isLog()`; log files **open in View mode by default** (`MainController.restoreReadOnly` adds `logViewer.isEnabled() && isLog()` — read-only with the Enable-Editing banner, since logs are for reading and follow-tail still appends programmatically while read-only); `MainController.loadInto` opens a huge `.log` at its tail (read-only, via `logViewer.handlesLogFile`/`recordLoadOffset`) instead of the first chunk; `startFollow`/`stopFollow` manage one `LogTailService.Handle` per buffer (resume from EOF on restart so a stop/start never duplicates); `applyFilter` builds the pattern via the pure `LogFilter.compileFilter` (a **case-insensitive regex**, with a **literal-substring fallback** when the query isn't valid regex — so a partial regex typed live, or a plain string with metacharacters, still filters), and the control's regex field filters **live** (debounced 300 ms) as well as on Enter. Commands `log.toggleFollow`/`log.viewAsLog`/`log.setLevelFilter`/`log.setRegexFilter`/`log.clearFilter` (palette-filtered when off via a new `log` field on `Chrome.PaletteGates`) + the master `view.toggleLogViewer`; `Settings.logViewer` (Settings → Editor → **Logs** checkbox; schema 37→38 additive-identity). Follow/tail is **local-only** (`Vfs.isLocal`); i18n in all six catalogs. **No new dependency / `module-info` change.** *Deferred: tailing remote (SFTP) logs, a multi-file merged tail, a dedicated Logs tool window, timestamp-range filtering, jump-to-next-error navigation.*
- `i18n/` — **UI localization**. `Messages` is a tiny static catalog loaded once by `App.start` (right after `config.load()`, before the command registry / FXML / UI are built) via `Messages.init(Messages.resolve(settings.getUiLanguage(), Messages.available().keySet(), Locale.getDefault().getLanguage()))`. Strings live in `resources/com/editora/i18n/messages.properties` (English **base/fallback**) plus `messages_<lang>.properties` overlays for **it/es/fr/pt/de**, read with `getResourceAsStream` + a UTF-8 `InputStreamReader` (the keymap/snippets loading style, so **no `module-info` opens** — we read our own module's resources; `ResourceBundle`'s JPMS pitfalls are avoided). `tr(key)` resolves active → English → the key itself (a missing key is visible, never throws); `tr(key, args...)` applies `MessageFormat` (e.g. `status.saved = Saved {0}`). `resolve(pref, available, systemLang)` (pure/unit-tested) picks the explicit pref if bundled, else the system language if bundled, else `en`. Bundled languages + endonyms live in `LANGUAGES` (en→English, it→Italiano, es→Español, fr→Français, pt→Português, de→Deutsch). **Command titles** come from this catalog automatically: `Command.of(id, runnable)` (the title-less overload) lazily resolves `tr("command." + id)`, so `MainController.registerCommands()` registers ids and the palette/Settings read titles fresh. **Command descriptions** work the same way: `Command.description()` (a `default` method) lazily resolves `tr("command." + id + ".desc")`, returning `""` when the key is absent (plugin/dynamic commands) so callers degrade gracefully; the command palette shows the highlighted command's description as a detail line (a `.palette-desc` `Label`) between the results list and the navigation hint, updating off the list's selection. Every `command.<id>` title has a matching `command.<id>.desc` in all six catalogs (enforced by `MessagesTest.everyCommandTitleHasAMatchingDescription`), and the website's Commands page reads the *same* `.desc` values via `website/scripts/gen-commands.py` (no separate description source). Other surfaces use explicit keys: `tooltip.*` (toolbar), `toolwindow.*` (tool-window titles), `settings.*` (the whole Settings window, incl. the language picker), `statusbar.*` (status-bar segments + tooltips), `hint.*`/`badge.*` (toolbar Switcher hint + `--dev` badge), `status.*` (the transient echo-area messages, parameterized via `MessageFormat`), `dialog.*` (every `Alert`/`TextInputDialog`/`ChoiceDialog` title/header/content + custom `ButtonType`s), `menu.*` (tab context menu), `editmenu.*` (editor right-click menu), `viewmode.*` (View-Mode banner), `find.*` (Find/Replace bar), `palette.*`/`filefinder.*`/`switcher.*` (popups), `bookmarks.*`/`project.*`/`gitpanel.*`/`branchpopup.*`/`structure.*`/`fileinfo.*` + `char.cat.*` (the tool-window panels), `markdown.*`, `autosave.*`, `branch.*`/`gitlabel.*`, `common.on`/`common.off`, `spell.lang.*`. `App.start` also calls `Locale.setDefault(...)` to the chosen language so JavaFX localizes its **own** built-in `ButtonType.OK/CANCEL/YES/NO` and locale-sensitive controls to match. The picker is a `ComboBox` at the top of Settings → Appearance (`Settings.uiLanguage`, default `""` = Automatic); changing it saves + shows a "restart to apply" `Alert` (set-once chrome is fully relabeled on the next launch). `MessagesTest` enforces **key-parity** — every bundled locale must have exactly the base's key set — so translations can't drift; add a language by dropping a complete `messages_<lang>.properties` + a `LANGUAGES` entry. Essentially **all** user-facing strings are now externalized — command palette, toolbar tooltips, tool-window titles + panel contents, Settings, status-bar segments, status/echo messages, every dialog (title/header/body/buttons), context menus, and popups. The only deliberately-untranslated tokens are technical identifiers (`UTF-8`, `LF`/`CRLF`, `Ln`/`Col`, git verbs in `gitlabel.*`, the detected language name, an example clone URL).
- **Command line** — `App.main` intercepts `--version`/`-V` and `--help`/`-h` (print via `AppInfo` + `helpText` and exit, before `launch()`, so no GUI). `App.start` parses the rest (pure/unit-tested helpers `configDirArg`/`projectArg`/`zenFlag`/`expertFlag`/`simpleFlag`/`fileTargets`/`parseTarget`/`newFileArg`/`singleWindowArg`) and calls `MainController.startup(projectDir, List<OpenTarget>, newFile)` instead of `openInitialBuffer()`: it activates a CLI `--project` (only if `projectsEnabled()`), restores the session, and opens any `--new-file[=name]` buffer and the `FILE[:line[:col]]` targets (additive, focused, `gotoInFile`) via the one-shot `pendingAfterRestore`. **A requested `FILE` is front-loaded so it's on screen from the first frame** — `openInitialBuffer` consults `startupTargets` *before* creating the restored tabs (`indexOfStartupTarget`): if the requested file is itself part of the session, **its** tab is the selected one and is filled first (the CLI action then runs right after that fill, via `runPendingStartupAction(false)` at `k == 0` in `fillSessionFiles`, so a `:line:col` jump still has content to land on); if it isn't in the session (or `--new-file` was given), the CLI action runs **synchronously before** any restored tab exists (`runPendingStartupAction(true)`) and the restored tabs are then appended with `selectIndex == -1` so none steals the selection. Running the targets only after the *whole* pulse-paced restore (the original shape) meant opening a file from the desktop — GNOME Files → "Editora Expert Mode", which passes the path as argv — showed the **session's** active file, fully rendered with its LSP starting, for a second or two before the requested file replaced it. Guarded by **`CliTargetFirstFxTest`**, which samples the selected tab *inside the build runnable* (before any `Platform.runLater` has run) via `FxWindowFixture.create(configDir, …, targets, onBuilt)` → `WindowManager.buildWindowForTest(zen, expert, simple, targets)`; asserting after the window settles would pass even with the old deferred code. `runPendingAfterRestore` (end of the fill chain) still runs the action if it somehow hasn't, then flips `restoringSession` off and reconciles the HTTP auto-show. A restored buffer's viewport is parked on its saved caret by **`scrollRestoredCaretIntoView`**, which retries across a few pulses: `replaceText` leaves the caret *and the viewport* at the **end** of the document (the reason `EditorBuffer.goToStart()` exists) and `moveTo` doesn't scroll, so this was a single `Platform.runLater(showParagraphAtTop)` whose failure was swallowed — on a freshly-added tab the viewport isn't laid out yet, that one attempt did nothing, and the file sat rendered at its **tail** until some unrelated event scrolled it (for a command-line file, `openPath`'s `requestFocus`), a visible scroll jump with the line numbers running from the end of the file back to the top.
