It now tries in the same pulse (no tail is ever painted when the tab is already laid out) and otherwise retries until the area reports a height — a not-yet-laid-out area silently no-ops rather than throwing, so height, not the exception, is the readiness test. **The chrome flags do NOT ride that deferred runnable** — `--zen`/`--expert`/`--simple` go through **`MainController.applyStartupChrome(zen, expert, simple)`**, called by `WindowManager.buildWindow` **before `stage.show()`** (after `init` — whose `toolWindows.restore()` state a focus mode stashes — and after `setWindowContext`, which selects the window's session). They shape only chrome and depend on nothing the restore produces, so deferring them made the window appear in **full chrome for the whole pulse-paced restore and then visibly strip itself** — a flash that grew with the number of restored files. Applying them pre-`show()` makes the first frame correct; files restored afterwards still pick the mode up because `addBuffer` runs `applyViewSettings` per buffer. Expert wins if both `--expert` and `--zen` are passed (the two are mutually exclusive). Guarded by **`CliChromeFirstFrameFxTest`**, which samples the chrome *inside the build runnable* (before any `Platform.runLater` has run) via `FxWindowFixture.create(zen, expert, simple, onBuilt)` → `WindowManager.buildWindowForTest(zen, expert, simple)` — asserting after the window settles would pass even with the deferred code. **`--simple`** is a *session-only* Simple-UI override (sets a transient `cliSimpleOverride`, OR'd with the saved `Settings.simpleMode` in `simpleModeActive()`); it doesn't change the saved preference, mirroring how `--zen` is session-scoped. **`--single-window[=name]`** opens exactly one window at startup instead of restoring the saved multi-window set — the named project's window, else the no-project window (an unknown name → no-project, with a logged warning); it's **session-only** (`WindowManager.launchSingleWindow` skips `markOpen`/`pm.save()`/the orphan-GC, and the `singleWindowSession` flag makes `reconcileOpenSet()` a no-op), so the persisted open-window layout is untouched and the next normal launch restores everything. `singleWindowArg` (pure/unit-tested) returns null / `""` (bare → no-project) / project-name, like `newFileArg`. **`--no-session`** (pure/unit-tested `noSessionFlag`) opens **only** the command line's files, skipping the saved session's entirely — `MainController.startup(..., noSession)` sets `skipSessionFiles`, which makes `openInitialBuffer` read an empty open-file list. It exists for a file-manager "Open With" launch, where restoring the last session's tabs is pure cost: every restored file is a buffer to load and highlight and (once shown) a language server to run, for files the user didn't ask to see. **Measured on an 8-file session opening one `.typ` file: 5 → 1 child processes, 19 s → 8 s of Editora CPU, 917 → 696 MB RSS.** It is **session-only in the strong sense**: `persistSession` returns early while `skipSessionFiles`, because this window's single tab is *not* the session and writing it back would replace the user's saved tabs with whatever they happened to open from the file manager (the file may still be rewritten by an ordinary config save — the *open-file list* is what's preserved, which is what `NoSessionStartupFxTest` asserts). The Linux `.deb` **postinst derives the Expert menu entry with it** — `Exec=… --expert --single-window --no-session %F`. **Welcome page**: when there are no files to restore (and no CLI `--new-file`/`FILE` target opened anything), `openInitialBuffer` no longer creates an empty Untitled buffer — it opens the Welcome page in its own tab via `showWelcomeIfNoTabs()`→`addWelcomeTab()` (see `ui/`). `newFileArg` (pure/unit-tested) returns null / `""` / name; `--new-file` ⇒ blank untitled, `--new-file=foo.md` ⇒ an unsaved buffer via `EditorBuffer.setDisplayName(name)` (tab title + extension highlighting, `path` stays null so Save prompts Save-As, the dialog's initial name defaulting to `getDisplayName()`). `AppInfo` (NAME/VERSION/HOMEPAGE/COPYRIGHT/LICENSE/buildTime) is the single source for `--version`, the About dialog, and the Welcome footer — **`VERSION` itself derives from `pom.xml`'s `<version>`** (Maven-filtered into `build-info.properties` alongside `build.time` and read via `AppInfo.loadVersion()`, falling back to `"0.0.0"` on an unfiltered non-Maven run), so **a release bump touches only the pom**, never a hardcoded constant — all of which show the home-page link (opened via `HostServices`), copyright, and license. `AppInfo.gitCommit()` adds the **short git commit** (read once at runtime via `git rev-parse --short HEAD`, cached, `""` when unavailable); it's shown in the About dialog and the Welcome footer **only under `--dev`** (`config.isDev() ? AppInfo.gitCommit() : ""` — passed to `SettingsWindow.showAbout(..., commit)` and `new WelcomePane(..., devCommit)`, each rendering the `about.commit` line only when non-blank), so a dev build can tell at a glance which commit it's running. Production builds pass `""` (nothing shown). **macOS "Open With" (Finder file associations):** the packaged `Editora.app` declares `CFBundleDocumentTypes` in its Info.plist so Editora shows up in Finder's *Open With* menu for text/source files. **Wiring is macOS-only + two-part:** (1) **`scripts/aot_build.java`'s `fixMacDocumentTypes`** (run on the macOS app image before the APP_IMAGE copy / DMG wrap) writes `CFBundleDocumentTypes` via `PlistBuddy` — a single entry declaring the **system UTIs `public.text` + `public.source-code`** (role `Editor`, `LSHandlerRank=Alternate` so it doesn't steal the default). **Deliberately NOT jpackage `--file-associations`:** that emits per-extension *custom* UTIs (`com.editora.txt`, …) conforming to `public.data`, which **don't work** — Launch Services never offers the app for a file already typed as a system UTI (a `.txt` is `public.plain-text`, which doesn't conform to `com.editora.txt`), so it wouldn't appear in Open With at all. Declaring the *system* types works because **every** text/source file's UTI **conforms to** `public.text`/`public.source-code`, making Editora an eligible alternate editor for all of them (verified via `lsregister -dump` → `bindings: public.text, public.source-code`). (`fixMacDocumentTypes` first `Delete`s any pre-existing `UT*TypeDeclarations`/`CFBundleDocumentTypes`, tolerating absence; it's a no-op on non-mac and best-effort — a PlistBuddy failure logs and the app still runs, just without the association.) **Two signing gotchas the plist edit exposes, both fixed in `aot_build.java`:** (a) jpackage **ad-hoc-signs** the `.app` during the app-image build, so editing `Info.plist` afterward **invalidates the code-signature seal** (the plist's hash is sealed) — macOS then rejects the app as *tampered* (`spctl`: "invalid Info.plist … modified"; the Finder dialog says it "could not verify … free of malware" with only *Move to Trash*/*Done*, a hard block). So `fixMacDocumentTypes` **re-runs `codesign --force --deep --sign -`** on the bundle after the edit to re-seal it (arm64 needs *some* signature to run; ad-hoc is fine for a locally-built, un-notarized app). (b) The APP_IMAGE-delivery `copyRecursive` **must preserve symlinks** (`Files.isSymbolicLink` → `createSymbolicLink`, not follow-and-copy): the jlink runtime dedups its `legal/*` license files as symlinks, and turning them into regular files breaks the seal in the *delivered* copy (`spctl`: "sealed resource … invalid: file modified: …/legal/…"; the DMG path is unaffected — jpackage does its own symlink-preserving copy). *(A validly ad-hoc-signed local app still shows `spctl -a -t exec: rejected` — that only means "not notarized"; a non-quarantined local app launches fine regardless. Full **notarization** (Apple Developer ID) is the outstanding follow-up for shipping downloadable installers.)* (2) Finder delivers the opened path as an AppKit **`openFiles` Apple Event, not argv**, so the `fileTargets` argv path never sees it — `App.start` (gated to macOS, after the windows build) calls **`MacOpenFiles.install(windows)`**, which sets a Glass `com.sun.glass.ui.Application.EventHandler` (`MacOpenFiles.Handler`) that forwards `handleOpenFilesAction` to `WindowManager.openExternalFiles(List<Path>)` → the focused window's `MainController.openExternalFiles` (each path `openPath`-ed; a cold-launch's buffered event lands in the just-built window). `Handler` **wraps** JavaFX's own handler (delegates every other event — quit/activate/preferences/… — to it) so Cmd-Q etc. still work; everything is `try/catch(Throwable)` so a missing internal API never breaks launch. **The handler is a standalone top-level class `com.editora.MacOpenFiles`, deliberately *not* nested in `App`:** the JavaFX launcher reflects over the `App` main class to find its methods, which eagerly loads `App`'s **nest members** — so a `com.sun.glass.ui` subclass nested in `App` gets class-loaded (and access-checked) *before* `start()` runs, **outside** any `try/catch`, and a missing `--add-exports` there is a hard launch crash (`IllegalAccessError` in `LauncherImpl`). As a separate class it loads only inside `install()`'s guarded body, so it degrades to a logged no-op instead. The internal `com.sun.glass.ui` access needs `--add-exports javafx.graphics/com.sun.glass.ui=com.editora` in **four** places: the **compiler** args (main-compile-scoped), the **`javafx:run`** options, the **dist jpackage `<javaOptions>`**, **and the AOT-training command in `scripts/aot_build.java`** (it launches the image's own `bin/java` with a hand-built option list that must mirror the launcher, else training crashes loading `MacOpenFiles.Handler` and ships no cache). `java.awt.Desktop.setOpenFileHandler` can't be used because `App.main` forces `java.awt.headless=true` (the SVG guard). **Windows/Linux need no handler** — their file associations pass the path as argv, already handled by `fileTargets` (associations there are an installer-time feature and aren't wired yet — a future add). To appear, the built app must be registered with Launch Services (drag `Editora.app` to `/Applications`, or `lsregister -f`).
- `config/` — `ConfigManager` loads/merges/saves config in the config dir, chosen by precedence **`--config-dir <path>` CLI arg (parsed by `App.configDirArg`, pure/unit-tested) > `EDITORA_CONFIG_DIR` env var > `--dev` (`~/.editora-dev/`, the `App.devFlag` flag — a separate dev config so a development instance can't disturb production; future home for extra dev-only behavior like more logging) > `~/.editora/`** (`user.home` is the user profile on every OS); the env/default fallback is the unit-tested pure `ConfigManager.resolveConfigDir(editoraHome, userHome, dev)`. Falls back to defaults on malformed input. **Preferences** (`Settings` POJO: font, theme, keymap, tab size, view options, keybindings) are **TOML** in `settings.toml` via a Jackson `TomlMapper` (jackson-dataformat-toml). **Text zoom** is `Settings.fontZoom` (1.0 = 100%) — a persisted Settings field deliberately *not* shown in the Settings window; `MainController.applyViewSettings` applies the effective size `round(fontSize*fontZoom)` to every buffer, `textZoom(±1/0)` adjusts it (status-bar `−/+`, `C-=`/`C--`/`C-0`, and the scene-level `Ctrl`+mouse-wheel filter in `App`). That wheel filter routes through `MainController.zoomFromWheel`, which zooms the Markdown **preview** (`markdownZoom`) when the active buffer is in **PREVIEW** mode (`getMarkdownViewMode() == PREVIEW`) and otherwise the editor text (Editor/Split always zoom text). **Session state** (`WorkspaceState` POJO: collapsed fold regions, tool-window layout/visibility/dividers) stays **JSON** in `workspace-state.json`, and `RecentFiles` stays JSON in `recent-files.json`; `config.save()` writes both files. **Writes go off the FX thread** via `config/ConfigWriter` (one `config-writer` daemon thread): the caller serializes a consistent snapshot to bytes on the FX thread (single-threaded → no locking) and hands the immutable bytes to the writer, which writes each file via a temp-file + atomic move (no half-written config on a crash), **coalescing per file (latest wins) and ordered through the one thread**. `cancel(file)` (used on project deletion to stop a queued session-file write from resurrecting the just-deleted file) both drops it from the pending queue **and** adds it to a `cancelled` set the drain re-checks per file just before each write — because `drain` clears `pending` under the lock but writes outside it, so a `cancel` arriving after the drain already *claimed* the bytes could otherwise not stop the write, re-creating the file (#491); a fresh `enqueue` un-cancels the file. The frequent, coalesced in-session save (`MainController.requestSave` → `config.saveAsync()`) is non-blocking; durable saves (`config.save()` — used by `persistSession()` on quit, one-off actions, and `exportConfig()`) `enqueue` + `flush()` (block until written), and `App.start` registers a JVM-shutdown flush. **A write failure is surfaced, not swallowed** (#418): the drain's atomic write now fires `ConfigWriter.setOnWriteError((file, ioe) -> …)` (default no-op) besides the SEVERE log; `WindowManager` wires `SharedConfig.setOnWriteError` once to `Platform.runLater` a `status.config.saveFailed` message onto the focused window's status bar — so a full disk / read-only `~/.editora` that used to lose a setting/session change with no sign now shows a status. (The sibling stores `saveBookmarks()`/`saveNotes()`/… still throw `UncheckedIOException` directly.) settings.toml + workspace-state.json are the only files with both an async and a sync writer, and both funnel through the one writer queue, so a stale async write can never land after and clobber a durable one (the other stores — `bookmarks.json`/`notes.json`/… — keep their direct synchronous `writeValue`). **Bookmarks** are deliberately *not* in `WorkspaceState` — they're in their own `bookmarks.json` (`BookmarkStore`), written by `config.saveBookmarks()` (independent of `save()`), but **scoped per project** (bucketed by project key; `config.getBookmarks()` returns the active project's bucket). See the bookmarks paragraph in `editor/` for the per-project model and the one-time migration out of the legacy session files. Both POJOs are `@JsonIgnoreProperties(ignoreUnknown = true)`, so `save()` rewrites with only modeled fields. The switch to TOML was a clean cut — a pre-existing `settings.json` is not migrated. (The bundled keymap `emacs.json` and the TextMate grammars stay JSON — they're app resources, not user config.) The About dialog shows the live settings path via `ConfigManager.getSettingsFile()` — don't hardcode it. **Export config** (owner-only — it copies `settings.toml`'s API key + `notes.json` into `$HOME`; see `ConfigWriter.createOwnerOnly`, the single helper every config-derived file must go through — it also backs `editora-session.log`): `ConfigManager.exportConfig()` zips the *active* config dir into a timestamped `.zip` in the user's home (`~/editora[-dev]-config-<version>-<user>-<yyyy-MM-dd_HHmmss>.zip`, embedding `AppInfo.VERSION` + `user.name`, both filename-sanitized) via the pure, unit-tested `ConfigExporter` (`zipName`/`sanitize` + `export(configDir, destDir, version, userName, now)`); surfaced as the Settings → Advanced "Export Configuration…" button (wired via the `onExportConfig` `Runnable` ctor arg → `MainController.exportConfig`, which shows the result path in a dialog) and the `config.export` command. **Projects** (`ProjectManager`, index in `projects.json`) are named single-folder workspaces; each project's session is a separate `WorkspaceState` JSON under `projects/<id>.json`. **Multi-window config split:** the config is split into a **`SharedConfig`** — the app-wide state (the `Settings` object, the bookmark/note/breakpoint/connection stores, the user dictionary, and the `ProjectManager` index) held **by reference** across every window — and a per-window **`ConfigManager`** that owns only that window's session (`WorkspaceState` + its `workspaceStateFile`) and delegates everything shared to `SharedConfig`. So a `config.save()` from any window writes `settings.toml` + that window's session file without clobbering another window's in-memory copy, and `config.getBookmarks()/getNotes()/getBreakpoints()` return the bucket for *this* window's project (keyed off its session file). `ConfigManager.setWorkspaceStateFile(...)` picks a window's session file (default = `workspace-state.json` for the no-project/global window). **Each project opens in its own window** (see `ui/WindowManager`); the open-window set is tracked in `ProjectManager.Index.openProjectIds` (`""` = the global window) — `markOpen`/`markClosed`/`isOpen` — and restored on the next launch, with `activeProjectId` as the last-focused window. `ProjectManager.Index` schema is **2** (v1→v2 `ConfigMigrations.seedOpenProjectIds` seeds `openProjectIds` from the old single `activeProjectId` so a pre-multi-window install reopens its active project as a window). **Schema versioning + migrations** (`config/migration/`): every structured config file carries a per-file integer `schemaVersion` (baseline **1**; the owning POJO's `SCHEMA_VERSION` constant — `Settings`/`WorkspaceState`/`BookmarkStore`/`ProjectManager.Index`, and `RecentFiles`), enumerated in `ConfigSchema` (SETTINGS/WORKSPACE/BOOKMARKS/PROJECTS/RECENT) with its current version, the version assumed when the field is absent (=1, the pre-versioning baseline), and an ordered map of `v→v+1` step `Migration`s. All structured reads now go through **`ConfigMigrations.readVersioned(file, mapper, defaults, schema)`**: parse to a Jackson tree → `upgrade` (apply the migration chain via `applySteps`, stamp `schemaVersion`) → merge onto defaults. It's mapper-agnostic (works for TOML + JSON since `TomlMapper` yields ordinary nodes). A file **newer** than this build (`schemaVersion > current`) throws `NewerThanSupportedException` and is **backed up to `<name>.v<n>.bak`, then defaults are loaded** — an older Editora never clobbers a newer config. `recent-files.json` was a bare JSON array (v0); the registered RECENT `0→1` step (`wrapRecentFilesArray`) wraps it into `{schemaVersion,files}` (`RecentFiles.Stored`). **To add a migration later: bump the POJO's `SCHEMA_VERSION` and add one `v→v+1` entry to that file's `steps` map in `ConfigSchema` — the read path, stamping, and downgrade backup are automatic.** The older one-off `migrateLegacyBookmarks()` (bookmarks flat→bucketed) stays as orthogonal field-level back-compat and runs before the versioned read.
- `ui/` — `MainController` (+ `main.fxml`): toolbar, tabbed `EditorBuffer`s, status bar. **Multiple windows (`WindowManager`)**: each window has its own `MainController`/`Stage`/`CommandRegistry`/`KeyDispatcher` + per-window services (all already per-instance, so no static per-window state) over the shared `SharedConfig`/`KeymapManager`. **`ui/WindowManager`** (created once in `App.start`) owns the set of open windows: `buildWindow(...)` is the per-window construction extracted from `App.start`; `openOrFocus(project)` focuses an already-open project window or builds a new one; `openOrFocusGlobal()` is the no-project window; `newWindow()` always **builds** a fresh no-project window (the palette **`window.new`** command / `C-x 5 2` — so a second window no longer requires loading a project; works regardless of the Projects feature). Each such window gets a unique **`untitled:<uuid>`** key and its **own** session file `windows/<uuid>.json` (so windows never clobber each other's open-files/layout — they are *not* all keyed `""`), is tracked in `openProjectIds` like a project window, and is **restored on the next launch regardless of the Projects feature** — the no-project windows (`""` + `untitled:*`) always restore; only saved *project* ids are dropped when Projects are off. `launch` dispatches a restore key by prefix (`""`→global/`workspace-state.json`, `untitled:`→`untitledStateFile`, else a project id) and `gcOrphanWindowSessions(toOpen)` deletes `windows/*.json` for untitled windows closed in a previous session. **Bucket:** an untitled window shares the global no-project bookmark/note bucket `""` — its `windows/<uuid>.json` session isn't under `projects/`, and `ConfigManager.currentBookmarkKey` returns `""` for anything not directly under `projects/` (only `projects/<id>.json` gets its own bucket). `launch(...)` restores the previously-open window set on startup: with Projects **disabled** that's the global window plus any untitled "New Window"s (the default stays single-window until you open one); with Projects **enabled** it's every previously-open window. A new window is **cascaded** (offset + brought to front, un-maximized if secondary) so it doesn't stack exactly on an existing one (projects carried identical saved bounds from the single-window era). `MainController.setWindowContext(wm, project)` (called right after `init`, before `startup`) binds the window to its project — sets the panel root/title/combo and auto-opens the Projects tool window — so the combo shows *this* window's project (a window switcher, not an in-place swap). **Window title** (`MainController.updateWindowTitle`): the active file's home-collapsed path with a `•` unsaved marker, then the project, then `Editora` (e.g. `~/app/Main.java — MyProject — Editora`); an untitled buffer shows its display name, a non-file/Welcome tab shows just the project/app name. Refreshed on tab switch (the selection listener) and on dirty-flip / Save-As / rename (via `updateTabMeta`, guarded to the active tab). **Current-folder mode:** in the **global ("No Project") window** the Project tool window doesn't sit empty — `MainController.updateProjectFolderView()` (called from the tab-selection listener, `setWindowContext`, and after a Save-As) roots `ProjectPanel` at the **active file's parent dir** and retitles the tool window **"Current Folder"** (`toolwindow.currentFolder`), so it tracks the focused tab like a file explorer. It no-ops when a project is open (tree stays the project root, title "Project") or while a remote folder is mounted (`activeRemoteAuthority != null` — that root is set explicitly); an unsaved/Welcome tab (or remote file) shows the placeholder + default title. Deduped against `ProjectPanel.getRoot()` so switching files in the same folder doesn't rebuild the tree. The retitle works because `ToolWindow`'s title is now a `StringProperty` the `ToolWindowPanel` header `Label` binds to. `switchToProject`→`openOrFocus`; `closeProject` closes this window; `deleteProject` closes the project's window first; the per-window close handler persists the session, **disposes that window's services** (LSP/DAP/git/search/mermaid/pdf/print/run/autosave + buffers, in a defensive `try/catch`), and notifies `WindowManager.onWindowClosed` (no per-window "Quit?" prompt; `app.quit`/`C-x C-c`/last-window-close still `Platform.exit`). A Settings change in one window broadcasts to all via `WindowManager.broadcastSettingsApplied` → each window's `reapplyAfterSharedSettingsChange`. *Window restore:* the open-window set persisted in `projects.json` (`openProjectIds`) is reconciled to the live set by a **debounced** `WindowManager.openSetReconcile` `PauseTransition` (~350 ms → `reconcileOpenSet()`; not an eager per-close `markClosed`): a genuine single-window close (the app keeps running) outlives the debounce, which then persists the reduced live set, so the closed window is forgotten; a **quit** terminates the JVM before the timer elapses, so the reduced set is never written and the full pre-quit set stays on disk ⇒ **every** window reopens next launch. The debounce delay (rather than a plain `runLater`) is deliberate: it can't elapse inside a quit's close-handler burst, so it never persists a half-drained intermediate even if those close events interleave with the FX event queue. This covers both quit paths — Cmd-Q / OS quit fire every window's close handler in a fast burst, and `app.quit`'s `Platform.exit` fires none at all. `reconcileOpenSet` also guards an empty live set (persist nothing). `ProjectManager.setOpenWindows(keys)` replaces the whole set (deduped, `null`→`""`). (Earlier this used a "remain" rule — eager `markClosed` unless it was the last window — which drained a Cmd-Q down to only the last window.) **Tab content abstraction**: a tab's `userData` is no longer always an `EditorBuffer` — it's a `editor/TabContent` (`node()`/`title()`/`icon()`/`closeable()`; lives in `com.editora.editor` so `EditorBuffer` can implement it without the editor package depending on `ui`, the same independence the completion popup keeps). `EditorBuffer` and `WelcomePane` both implement it, so the Welcome page is a **real tab** (and future diff/image/help views can be too). **Image viewer**: `ui/ImageViewerPane implements TabContent` is a **read-only** raster-image tab — opening a `.png`/`.jpg`/`.jpeg`/`.gif`/`.bmp` renders the picture instead of showing its binary bytes as text (the pure/unit-tested `ui/ImageFormats.isSupported(name)` gates which extensions route here; SVG is deliberately excluded — it's editable XML). It decodes the file's bytes (`Files.readAllBytes`, so it works for local **and** remote/SFTP paths; refused above a 64 MB cap) into a JavaFX `Image`, shows a top bar with zoom out/in/fit/actual-size + a read-only badge (Ctrl+wheel zooms; fit-mode never upscales past 100%; small images center, large scroll), and `dispose()`s the decoded `Image` on tab close (releasing its Prism texture — the per-buffer VRAM-bounding rule). `MainController.openPath` routes an image file to `openImageTab(file, select)` before the text path; `imagePaneOf(Tab)` + `tabPath(Tab)` (buffer path else image-pane path) generalize the buffer-only lookups, so image tabs round-trip through `tabForPath`/`persistSession`/session-restore (restored via `openImageTab`, a `null` placeholder in the `buffers` list keeps indices aligned — the `buffers.get(i)` reads are null-guarded) and show their path in the window title. i18n `imageviewer.*`; CSS `.image-viewer*`; **no new dependency**. **Hex viewer**: `ui/HexViewerPane implements TabContent` is a **read-only** hex tab for **binary** files — an executable/archive/`.class`/`.pdf` opens as the classic `offset | hex | ASCII` dump (pure/unit-tested `ui/HexDump.format(bytes, baseOffset)`, 16 bytes/row) instead of dumping its bytes as garbage text. **Binary detection** is by content, not extension: pure/unit-tested `ui/BinarySniff.looksBinary(sample)` (git's rule — a NUL byte ⇒ binary — plus a control-char density fallback, with a **BOM guard** so BOM'd UTF-16/UTF-8 text isn't misrouted, and bytes ≥0x80 aren't counted so UTF-8/Latin-1 prose stays text); `MainController.looksBinaryFile(path)` reads a bounded `BinarySniff.SAMPLE_BYTES` prefix. The dump sits in a read-only monospace RichTextFX `CodeArea` (selectable/copyable), reads up to `MAX_DISPLAY_BYTES` (1 MiB → a large binary shows its first slice with a truncation note, so a multi-GB file can't exhaust memory), and `dispose()`s the text on close. `openPath` routes a binary to `openHexTab(file, select)` **after** the image check + before the text load; `hexPaneOf(Tab)` joins `imagePaneOf` in `tabPath(Tab)`, so hex tabs round-trip through `tabForPath`/`persistSession`/session-restore (a `null` `buffers` placeholder, like images) and show their path in the title. Palette command **`view.openAsHex`** force-opens the active file's bytes as hex (works for a text file too). i18n `hexviewer.*`/`command.view.openAsHex`; CSS `.hex-viewer*`; **no new dependency**. **PDF viewer**: `ui/PdfViewerPane implements TabContent` opens a `.pdf` in a **read-only page viewer** (rasterized via **PDFBox**, already a dependency for PDF export) instead of the hex viewer — a top bar with `◀ Page N of M ▶` navigation + zoom (fit/actual/`Ctrl`-wheel). Pages are rasterized **one at a time, off the FX thread** on a single `pdf-render` daemon thread (PDFBox's `PDDocument` isn't thread-safe, so all document access is serialized there; only the current page's image/texture is held — the VRAM-bounding rule). `MainController.openPath` routes `PdfViewerPane.isPdf(name)` **before** the binary/hex check; `openPdfTab`/`pdfPaneOf` + `tabPath`/`tabType` mirror the image/hex viewers so a PDF tab round-trips session restore (a `null` `buffers` placeholder keeps the fill indices aligned). The PDFBox `BufferedImage`→FX conversion reuses the now-public `PreviewImageLoader.toFxImage` (no `javafx.swing`); works for local **and** remote (SFTP) PDFs, refused above 128 MB. `PdfViewerPane.isPdf` unit-tested (`PdfViewerPaneTest`); i18n `pdfviewer.*`; CSS `.pdf-viewer*`; **no new dependency** (PDFBox already bundled). *Deferred: continuous page scroll, a page-jump field, text selection/search, encrypted/password PDFs.* **Every** `tab.getUserData()` read goes through `bufferOf(Tab)` (returns the `EditorBuffer`, or `null` for a non-buffer tab via `instanceof` — a raw cast would `ClassCastException` on the Welcome tab); `activeBuffer()` delegates to it. `addContentTab(TabContent, select)` is the generic tab factory (sets content/userData/close-request, appends, optionally selects+focuses) and builds a **draggable graphic header** (icon + title `Label`, `enableTabDrag`) — so non-buffer tabs (Welcome) reorder like any other tab; the tab text is left empty, so the Switcher/pickers read the title via `TabContent.title()` (`bufferTitle`/`Switcher.tabContentTitle`). `addBuffer` calls it then overrides the header via `updateTabMeta` (drag handle, pin, dirty); buffer-only ops (pin, save, edit commands) are inert on the Welcome tab because `bufferOf`/`activeBuffer` yield null and the tab-switch consumers (status bar, Structure, File-Info, breadcrumb, git, external-change) are null-safe. **Welcome page**: `setupWelcome()` just builds the `WelcomePane` + wires its callbacks; `addWelcomeTab()` opens (or re-selects) the single Welcome tab — held in a `Tab welcomeTab` field, cleared in its `onClosed`, with a Close-only context menu; its title (`welcome.tab`) comes from `WelcomePane.title()` — shown in the draggable header and read by the Switcher/pickers (`bufferTitle`/`Switcher.tabContentTitle` use `TabContent.title()` for non-buffer tabs). Shown at startup with no session (`showWelcomeIfNoTabs`, run after CLI targets) and by the `view.welcome` command (`showWelcome`). Closing the last tab leaves the editor **empty** (VSCode-like — not auto-recreated). **Buffer disposal on close**: the `tabPane.getTabs()` `ListChangeListener` (which already drops closed tabs from `mru`/`pinned`, skipping pin/drag reorders via the `reordering` guard) calls `EditorBuffer.dispose()` on each removed buffer tab — `shutdownNow()` on the buffer's two daemon executors (`markdown-preview` + `editor-highlighter`) + `unsubscribePreview()` — so those threads don't accumulate one pair per opened file. It runs for every real close path (close, close-others/left/right, deleted-file removal, Welcome) but never on a tab switch (selection change doesn't mutate the tabs list); the split secondary view shares the buffer's executors, so one `dispose()` covers it. `WelcomePane` reuses commands (`file.new`/`file.open`/`project.open`/`git.clone`/`palette.show` — `project.open`/`git.clone` gated by `projectsEnabled()`/`gitEnabled()`, `palette.show` listed last) each labelled with its keybinding via a `KeymapManager.bindings()` reverse-lookup (`shortcutFor` — Open File deliberately shows `file.find`'s `C-x C-f`) + the `RecentFiles` list (open via `openRecent`), and a footer with `AppInfo.VERSION` + a home-page link (`AppInfo.HOMEPAGE`, opened via `App`'s `HostServices` passed through `MainController.setHostServices`/`openExternalUrl`) + `AppInfo.LICENSE` (the welcome shows the license only; the author/copyright lives in About); rebuilt on each `refresh()` (also on settings apply while the Welcome tab is open, so Open-Folder/Clone track the Projects/Git toggles); styled `.welcome-*` in `app.css`. The content sits in a `ScrollPane` (`.welcome-scroll`) over a centering `StackPane` (fit-to-width, with a min width) so it stays centered but shows a vertical/horizontal scrollbar when it doesn't fit the window. **In-scene overlays (`OverlayHost`)**: the command palette and *every* keyboard picker/popup are **in-scene overlays**, **not** `javafx.stage.Popup`s — a Popup is a separate native window that on Windows doesn't reliably take OS keyboard focus, so `input.requestFocus()` orphaned focus between the popup's scene and the main window and the keyboard went dead app-wide (mouse still worked). A single shared **`ui/OverlayHost`** (owned by `MainController`, `install(sceneRoot)`-ed into the scene-root `StackPane` from `installZenOverlay`) renders one "card" node at a time over a dim, click-to-dismiss backdrop (`.overlay-backdrop`); it owns focus capture/restore (returns typing to the editor on close), `Esc`/`C-g` dismissal, a `justHidden()` toggle guard, and `showingProperty()`. `show(content, onShown, onHidden)` centers the card near the top; `show(content, anchor, onShown, onHidden)` instead positions it just **above** an anchor node (e.g. a status-bar segment, so a dropdown "drops" from it). Each component supplies its card node (which sets `editora.ownsKeys` so its `C-n`/`C-p`/arrow nav isn't hijacked by the global dispatcher), an `onShown` hook (`input.requestFocus()`), and an `onHidden` hook (clears its own `showing` flag); `MainController.wireOverlayHost()` injects the host into all of them via `setOverlayHost(...)` (on-demand pickers — LSP references, spell/app/editor-theme — get it at their construction site; `MessageLogPopup` via `StatusBar.setOverlayHost`). Converted: `CommandPalette` (M-x; the footer legend lists `esc`/`C-g`, no separator above it), the generic `QuickOpen<T>` pickers (recent files, structure, open files, tool windows, bookmarks, notes/notes-search, snippets, projects, LSP references, themes), `FileFinder` (file + folder finders), `Switcher` (IntelliJ Ctrl-Tab), the Git `BranchPopup` (anchored), and `MessageLogPopup` (anchored). When a card is anchored to a status-bar segment, the full-scene backdrop intercepts a re-click on that segment (closes the overlay, doesn't reach the segment) — a clean click-to-toggle. (`editor/CompletionPopup` stays a `Popup` — it never calls `requestFocus()`, so it's safe.) `FindReplaceBar` (find/replace with case + regex) was already in-scene the same way. **Input dialogs** are also in-scene via **`ui/OverlayInput`** — a stateless helper that builds a form card (title + caller-supplied body + footer Cancel/OK, optional left-aligned Delete `Extra`, optional `okEnabled` validity gate) and shows it through the same `OverlayHost`; the card sets `editora.ownsKeys`, `Esc`/`C-g` cancel (host), and `Enter` accepts (or `Ctrl/Cmd+Enter` when `ctrlEnterToSubmit` for the multi-line note editor). `onAccept` runs **after** the card hides (focus already back in the editor) — flows are callback-driven, no blocking `showAndWait`. `MainController.promptText(title,label,initial,onAccept)` is the single-line convenience (installs `TextInputKeymap` for Emacs caret nav) and doubles as the `OverlayInput.Prompt` functional interface injected into `BookmarksPanel`/`ProjectPanel` (`setPrompt`) so those tool windows prompt without needing the host/keymap. Converted off native `TextInputDialog`/`Dialog`: the Personal Note editor (`showNoteDialog`, multi-line + Delete), bookmark-note edit, file rename (tab + project tree), Git **clone** (two fields + Browse + validity gate) and **new branch**, **go to line**, and **Save As from the command palette / a keybinding** (`saveAsPrompt` — a path prompt pre-filled with the current path, or the project folder + suggested name for an untitled buffer; a bare name resolves against that folder and `~` expands, via the pure/unit-tested `config/PathKeys.resolveUserInput`; overwriting a different existing file still uses a native confirm `Alert`). The **toolbar Save-As button keeps the native `FileChooser`** (its FXML `onAction="#onSaveAs"`, a mouse action) — only the `file.saveAs` command routes to the in-scene prompt, so keyboard = prompt, mouse = chooser. Deliberately left **native**: simple `Alert` confirmations (overwrite/delete/external-change) and the `ChoiceDialog` selectors (set language / tab size / line endings) + the `i18n` key `dialog.ok`. **Status-bar message log**: every echo-area message set via `MainController.setStatus`→`StatusBar.setMessage` is recorded (non-blank only) in an in-memory, **session-only** `MessageLog` (pure model, capped at `MAX_ENTRIES`=200, oldest evicted, newest-first `entries()`; unit-tested). The echo label is clickable (`view.messageLog` command) → `StatusBar.showMessageLog()` → `MessageLogPopup.toggle` (a second click on the echo **closes** it — the backdrop intercepts it; a `lastHiddenAt` guard absorbs the close-then-click race) → a `MessageLogPopup` (an `OverlayHost`-anchored scrollable `ListView` above the echo; each row an `HH:mm:ss` time indicator + the message; long messages **wrap** (the row grows in height — no horizontal scrollbar, the row width is bound to the list viewport). Rows are **multi-selectable**; a footer **Copy** button copies the selected messages (or all when none are selected, joined by newline — `⌘/Ctrl+C` also works) and a **Clear** action empties the log; Esc / `C-g` / `M-g` close it. (The popup is sized 552×280 — 20% wider than the original — and has no per-row right-click menu; the Copy button replaced it for discoverability.) Not persisted. Styled `.message-log*` in `app.css`. **Debug Log** (distinct from the echo MessageLog): `ui/DebugLog` is a static capture of the app's **`java.util.logging`** output + **uncaught exceptions** — installed in `App.main` (`DebugLog.install()`: a root-logger `Handler` at `Level.ALL` appending to a bounded ring buffer + `Thread.setDefaultUncaughtExceptionHandler`) so a packaged build (DMG/MSI/DEB, no visible stderr) can still surface errors; `App.start` calls `DebugLog.attachFile(config.getConfigDir())` to also mirror records to `editora-session.log` (truncated per session) so they survive a crash for a bug report. `ui/DebugLogWindow` shows the buffer in a read-only monospace `TextArea` (Refresh/Copy/Clear/Export…), opened by the `view.debugLog` command and the **Settings → Advanced → "Show Debug Log…"** button (wired via the `onShowDebugLog` `Runnable` ctor arg → `MainController.showDebugLog`). Pure helpers (`shortName`, the bounded `append`, `format`) are unit-tested. **Unsaved-file indicator consistency**: every surface that lists open buffers shows the same dirty marker as the tab strip (a `• ` prefix + amber-italic `.dirty-name` in `app.css`): the **Switcher** (its cell checks `buffer.isDirty()`), the **Open Files** picker (`buffer.jump` — its label adds the `• ` and `QuickOpen.setItemStyleClass(tab -> isTabDirty(tab) ? "dirty-name" : null)` colors it; the `searchKey` stays the plain name), and the **Project tool window** tree (the pre-existing `.modified-file` cell class, refreshed via `projectPanel.refreshModified()` on every dirty-flag change). **Git file coloring (IntelliJ-style):** the Project tree colors each file by its Git working-tree status — added = green, modified = blue, deleted = gray, renamed = violet, untracked = olive, and a folder containing changed descendants is tinted blue. The pure/unit-tested **`git/GitFileStatus`** enum (`of(FileEntry)` classifies porcelain-v2 index/worktree letters — deleted→renamed→added→modified precedence, untracked first; `byPath(GitStatus, root)` → `Map<Path, GitFileStatus>` keyed by absolute-normalized path) drives it; `GitCoordinator.applyState` pushes the map (or empty on non-repo / Git-off) via `Ops.setProjectGitStatus` → `MainController` → `ProjectPanel.setGitStatus`, which stores it + derives the set of changed ancestor dirs and `tree.refresh()`es. The `PathCell` adds the status's `.git-status-*` class (or `.git-status-dir-changed` on a folder) — but an **unsaved (`.modified-file`) file keeps its amber marker, which takes precedence**. Colors ride the Git feature (updated on the same tab-switch / focus / save / mutation cadence as the gutter change bars); no separate setting/command. CSS `.project-tree .git-status-*` (+ `.git-tree .git-status-*`) in `app.css` (semantic `-color-accent-fg`/`-color-success-fg` + fixed olive/violet). Each changed file also shows a **single-letter status prefix** (`GitFileStatus.letter()` → M/A/D/R/U) matching the Commit tool window, and the **Commit window's rows are colored by the same `.git-status-*` classes** (`GitPanel.GitCell` adds `GitFileStatus.of(entry).cssClass()`), so the two panels read identically; an unsaved-in-editor file keeps its amber `•` instead of a Git letter. **Project-tree Git actions** (the cell right-click **Git** submenu, `ProjectPanel.FileActions`): files offer **Stage** / **Unstage** / **Revert…** / **Add to .gitignore** + **Compare with HEAD** / **Compare with Branch…** / **Compare with Revision…** / **Annotate** / **Show File History**; folders offer **Stage** / **Revert…** of the whole subtree. The path-based ops live in `GitCoordinator` (`gitStagePath`/`gitUnstagePath`/`gitRevertPath`/`addToGitignore`, all repo-relative via `rel(...)` and refreshing through `afterMutation()`): Revert reuses the confirming `discardChanges` (untracked → `git clean`, else `git checkout`, deciding via the stored `lastStatusByPath`); Add-to-.gitignore appends the pure/unit-tested `git/GitIgnore.entryFor`/`withEntry` line to the repo-root `.gitignore`. The three navigation/inspection actions delegate to path-based entry points: **Compare with Branch** → `DiffCoordinator.diffPathVsBranch(path)` (a `QuickOpen<String>` over `GitService.branches` local+remote, diffing working ↔ `<branch>:rel`), **Compare with Revision** → `DiffCoordinator.diffPathVsCommit(path)` (the path-based extraction of `diffActiveVsCommit`, a commit picker over the file's log — `diffActiveVsCommit` now delegates to it), and **Annotate** → open the file + `GitCoordinator.annotateActive()` (enables inline blame if off, then `applyBlame`). The menu items enable/disable off `ProjectPanel`'s own `gitStatus`/`gitChangedDirs` (Revert only when the file/folder has changes; Add-to-.gitignore only for untracked), and the whole Git submenu greys out with no VCS (`FileActions.gitAvailable`). **The editor tab's right-click menu mirrors this same Git submenu** (`MainController.installTabMenu`), acting on *that tab's* file (`buffer.getPath()`) via the same path-based ops (`GitCoordinator.gitStagePath`/`gitUnstagePath`/`gitRevertPath`/`addToGitignore`/`annotateActive`, `DiffCoordinator.diffPathVs{Head,Branch,Commit}`, `gitFileHistoryForPath`) and the same `project.menu.git.*` labels; `GitCoordinator.statusFor(path)` gates **Revert** (only when the file has changes) / **Add to .gitignore** (untracked only), the submenu is hidden for an untitled buffer and greyed out with no VCS. The pre-existing tab **"Compare With…"** (any two files) + **"Open in Diff Viewer"** (`.patch`/`.diff`) stay *outside* the submenu — they aren't Git ops. **Project tree filesystem refresh**: `ProjectPanel.refreshTree()` re-scans the tree against disk (files/folders added/removed outside Editora) while **preserving the expanded folders + selection** (it collects expanded paths, `reload()`s only the expanded directories, re-expands by path, restores the selection) — no-op while filtering/no project; called on window focus-regain (alongside `checkExternalChanges`/`refreshGit`) **and by a filesystem watcher**. **Live filesystem watcher**: `ProjectPanel` runs a `java.nio.file.WatchService` (daemon `project-fs-watch` thread) over the **root + currently-expanded directories** (re-synced via `syncWatches()` on expand/collapse and after each rebuild — cheap even on huge trees; a collapsed folder isn't watched since it isn't visible, and expanding re-lists it). Disk events (create/delete/modify) are drained and coalesced by a 250 ms `PauseTransition` into a single `refreshTree()`. **Local roots only** (`Vfs.isLocal`; a remote SFTP root has no local watcher). Lifecycle: started in `setRoot` (`ensureWatchOrStop`), torn down in `ProjectPanel.dispose()` (closes the service + thread), called from `MainController.disposeWindow`. *(On macOS the JDK's WatchService is a poller, so external changes can lag a few seconds — the focus-regain refresh covers the immediate case.)* In-app rename/delete update the tree instantly via `refreshAfterChange()` → `refreshTree()` (re-list from disk **by path**, not the captured `TreeItem` — the confirm/rename dialog is a separate window, so closing it regains focus on the main window and fires the focus-regain `refreshTree()` which rebuilds the nodes, detaching the captured item; re-listing by path is immune to that) and call `markLocalChange()` so the watcher **skips its redundant ~1s-later refresh** for the app's own change (a `SELF_CHANGE_WINDOW_MS` guard in the debounce handler). **Mini file manager:** the tree is `SelectionMode.MULTIPLE` (arrow-key nav uses `clearAndSelect`, so it stays single; mouse Ctrl/Cmd- + Shift-click multi-selects), and each `PathCell` has drag handlers to **move** a file/folder (or the whole multi-selection — `actionTargets`) onto a **folder** cell (or the root): `setOnDragDetected` stores the paths in `draggedPaths` + a snapshot drag view, `setOnDragOver` accepts `MOVE` + adds `.project-drop-target` when `canDropInto` (a folder cell only, via `dropTargetDir`), and `setOnDragDropped` runs `moveInto(sources, targetDir)` — `Files.move` per source, skipping no-ops/conflicts/invalid moves (the pure, unit-tested `canMoveInto`: not the current parent, not into its own subtree), then `onFileRenamed.accept(src, dest)` per moved path. **Right-click Delete acts on the whole multi-file selection** (`deleteSelected` → `actionTargets`, one confirm; files only). `MainController.onProjectFileRenamed` was widened to **prefix-remap** every open buffer under a moved directory (not just an exact-path file match), so a moved folder's open tabs follow to the new path; a `setOnStatus(this::setStatus)` sink shows the move/delete feedback. **External change detection**: each buffer records its file's on-disk mtime+size at load/save (`EditorBuffer.setDiskSnapshot`/`diskChangedFrom`); `MainController.checkExternalChanges()` checks the **active tab's** file and, if its disk stamp changed under it, prompts (`promptExternalChange` → `reloadFromDisk`). It runs on window focus-regain (`stage.focusedProperty`) and on tab switch — so the prompt only appears for the file the user is looking at; background tabs are checked when switched to. A re-entrancy guard stops the modal prompt from re-triggering itself; "Keep" re-baselines the snapshot; deleted files are skipped; the app's own writes re-baseline so they never prompt. **`SettingsWindow`** is a scalable shell: a top search box + a left **grouped** sidebar + a per-category page (built once into a `Map<Category,Region>`), with a bottom **Reset to Defaults** + Close. The sidebar is a `ListView<Object>` of mixed rows — a non-selectable **`Group`** header (muted, `.settings-group-header`, mouse-transparent) followed by its indented **`Category`** items (`.settings-sidebar-item`), built by `sidebarItems()` in `Category` declaration order; the selection listener swaps the page only for an `instanceof Category` row. **Five groups** (`Group` enum, in order): **General** (Appearance / Interface / Workspace / Tool Windows), **Editor** (Editor = General display+indent+saving+logs+PDF / Code Completion / Snippets / Templates / TODO / Spell Check / Search), **Languages & Tools** (Language Servers / Debugger / Markdown / Mermaid / Web / External Tools), **Version Control** (Git), **System** (Keymap / Remote / Plugins / MCP / Advanced). This replaced the old flat 22-entry list: the catch-all *Editor* page was split (**Code Completion** + **TODO** are now their own leaves), the *Application* grab-bag dissolved into **Interface** (chrome: toolbar/status-bar/tab-bar/breadcrumb/tool-stripe + Simple/Zen/Expert **Modes**) + **Workspace** (Projects / show-hidden-files / Notes / Local History), the author field moved to **Templates**, and the two one-toggle *HTTP Client* + *HTML Preview* pages merged into **Web** (two sections). Each feature's master toggle now lives on one canonical page (the Tool Windows page's gated-window notes point there); the AI category grew from a "coming soon" placeholder into three real pages — **AI** / **Agent** / inline completion, see the `ai/`+`agent/` bullet (no more `placeholder` flag / `placeholderPage`). `filter()` greys non-matching categories **and** empty group headers (`searchHiddenCats` + `searchHiddenGroups`) and auto-selects the first hit. New i18n: `settings.group.*` + `settings.cat.interface/workspace/completion/todo/web` + `settings.section.modes/htmlPreview/httpClient/templatesList`. The **Snippets** + **Templates** body fields are now RichTextFX `CodeArea`s (not `TextArea`s) with live TextMate highlighting for the snippet/template language (`highlightSnippetBody` via `GrammarRegistry`+`TextMateHighlighter`, re-run on edit) + basic Emacs caret movement (`installEmacsKeys`: `C-a/C-e/C-f/C-b/C-n/C-p/M-f/M-b/C-d/C-k`, since the settings scene has no global `KeyDispatcher`). `formRow` pins each label's min width to its preferred width so a tight `GridPane` never collapses labels to "…". It keeps the **live-apply** model (each control writes its `Settings` field then `apply()` → `config.save()` + `onApply`); there is no OK/Cancel. **Search** filters via the pure/unit-tested `SettingsWindow.matches(query, keywords)` (hides non-matching rows + empty section headers, disables sidebar categories with no hits, auto-selects the first match). The **Appearance** page has a **live preview**: a read-only `CodeArea` (`editor-area`) highlighted once via `TextMateHighlighter.compute(sample, java grammar)`; the Settings `Scene` carries `app.css`+`syntax.css` and an editor-theme override sheet swapped on theme change (mirroring `MainController.applyEditorTheme`), so the preview recolors for free; font changes update its inline style. **Reset** (a single "Reset to Defaults" on the Advanced page) → **`Settings.resetToDefaults(live)`**, which copies every property Jackson persists off a fresh `new Settings()` onto the live instance **in place** (every window holds that reference), preserving only `fontZoom` + `keybindings`. **Never replace it with a list of setters** — that is what it was, and the list rotted to **23 of 181 fields**, so Reset silently left ~87% of preferences (all of AI/LSP/Debug/previews/build-tools/`simpleMode`/`keymap`/`uiLanguage`, and the `aiApiKey`) untouched; driving it off the serialized form covers a new setting the day it is added. **Tool stripe toggle**: the **Interface** page has a "Show tool stripe" checkbox (`Settings.showToolStripe`, default on, schema bumped 3→4 additive-identity) at the top with a `note(...)` warning that hiding the stripe **takes precedence** over each tool window's individual visibility toggle below. It's UI-only — `ToolWindowManager.setStripesEnabled(false)` hides the left/right/bottom stripe `Pane`s (folded into `setStripeShown`'s `stripesEnabled && !zenHidesStripes && !empty` guard) but tool windows still open via their keys (`M-1`…) and the palette. `MainController.applyChromeVisibility()` calls `toolWindows.setStripesEnabled(s.isShowToolStripe())` (re-applied on every settings apply + at init); the palette command `view.toggleToolStripe` (`MainController.toggleToolStripe`) flips the setting, saves, re-applies, and re-syncs the checkbox via `SettingsWindow.syncToolStripeCheck()`. **Simple UI mode** (`Settings.simpleMode`, default off, schema 19→20 additive-identity; Settings → Interface "Simple UI mode", a toolbar `Icons.simpleMode()` square button + `onToggleSimpleMode`, palette `view.toggleSimpleMode`, and the `--simple` CLI session-override) is a single toggle that strips chrome to a minimal surface. `applyChromeVisibility` calls **`applySimpleMode()`** (the effective state is `simpleModeActive()` = `Settings.simpleMode || cliSimpleOverride`): it hides a curated set of toolbar buttons (`newFromTemplateButton`/`recentButton`/`clearRecentButton`/`findInFilesButton`/`splitVertical`/`splitHorizontal` — the **Open** button is deliberately kept so opening a file stays one click away) then **collapses orphaned separators** via `collapseToolbarSeparators()` (a generic pass hiding any `Separator` with no visible control before+after — self-correcting, so toggling off restores them), and pushes `statusBar.setSimpleMode(...)` (hides the git/language/tab-size/line-ending/encoding segments **and the LSP server segment + loading bar** — the LSP ones are event-driven, so `setLsp`/`setLspLoading` store their state and route through `applyLspStatusVisibility()` which suppresses them while `simpleMode`; keeps echo/read-only/zoom/Ln-Col **and the file size**). The **tool-window stripe** and **breadcrumb** are hidden via effective values right in `applyChromeVisibility` (`setStripesEnabled(showToolStripe && !simple)`, `breadcrumb.setEnabled(showBreadcrumb && !simple)`). The project toolbar group is gated inside `applyProjectSupport` (`on && !simpleModeActive()`, since it runs after `applyChromeVisibility`). The minimap is hidden via an **effective value in `applyViewSettings`** (`buffer.setMinimapVisible(showMinimap && !simpleModeActive())`) so the saved pref is preserved; the **whole gutter** is removed via `buffer.setGutterVisible(!simpleModeActive())` (a flag making `refreshGutter()` set a **null `setParagraphGraphicFactory`** — no line numbers, fold chevrons, or bookmark/note/run/breakpoint/git slots), and when Simple mode is active `applyViewSettings` also calls `buffer.unfoldAll()` so collapsed regions aren't stranded behind the hidden chevrons. (`setLineNumbersVisible` is still applied for the non-simple state.) `toggleSimpleMode()` mirrors `toggleToolStripe` (clears `cliSimpleOverride`, flips + saves, `applyViewSettingsToAllBuffers`, `syncSimpleModeCheck`, localized `status.toggle.simpleMode` echo) and, when **entering** Simple mode, **closes any open tool window** (`toolWindows.getOpenToolWindows()` → `close`) since the stripe is hidden. (Toolbar layout: the **Settings** button sits just left of **About**, each set off by a small `Separator` — a general arrangement, not Simple-mode-specific.) Simple mode also **disables the heavier features**: `lspEnabled()`, `debugSupportEnabled()`, `httpEnabled()`, `gitEnabled()`, and `multiCaretEnabled()` each fold in `&& !simpleModeActive()`, and their `apply*` methods compute `on` from those helpers — so toggling Simple mode on shuts down language servers + debug adapters, gates off the HTTP ▶, disables the Git integration (status-bar VCS segment, gutter change bars, Commit window), and turns off **multiple cursors / Alt+drag column selection** (`applyMultiCaret` pushes the effective off to every buffer; `withMultiCaret` reports "disabled") — all reusing each feature's existing enable→disable path, and toggling off restores them from the untouched saved settings. The `git.*`/`lsp.*`/`http.*` palette commands (and the Commit/Problems/HTTP tool-window picker entries) are filtered out via those same effective gates while Simple mode is on. Tabs stay; the `--dev` badge stays (a deliberate dev indicator). **About** is no longer in Settings (it's on the toolbar + `help.about`; `SettingsWindow.showAbout` is still the shared dialog); the settings-file link moved to the **Advanced** page. Keep its public API (`show`/`syncThemes`/`syncProjectsCheck`/`syncToolStripeCheck`/`showAbout`/`displaySettingsPath`) — `MainController` wiring is unchanged.

## Conventions

- **Performance is a top priority.** Editora must stay fast and responsive, especially on large files. Treat the UI thread as sacred and these as the hot paths: typing/editing, scrolling, syntax highlighting, the document overlays (whitespace, minimap, 80-column ruler), and the line-number gutter. Rules to uphold:
  - **Never block the JavaFX Application Thread** with non-trivial work — tokenize/parse/search off-thread (see the `highlightExecutor` pattern in `EditorBuffer`) and apply results back on the FX thread with a generation/stale-result guard.
  - **Debounce and coalesce** — re-highlighting is debounced; overlay/ruler/minimap redraws coalesce to one per pulse (a `pending` flag + `Platform.runLater`). Don't add per-keystroke or per-scroll-pulse work that isn't coalesced.
  - **Work incrementally / only on what's visible** — highlighting re-tokenizes only from the changed line; overlays iterate just the visible paragraphs (`firstVisibleParToAllParIndex … last`) and skip folded lines. Avoid O(document) work on edits or scrolls.
  - **Don't defeat the per-node CSS style cache** — keep token rules as the compound `.text.<class>` selector (see `syntax.css`); coalesce adjacent same-style spans (`SpanMerger`) before `setStyleSpans`; never query `getCharacterBoundsOnScreen` synchronously inside a layout/viewport event.
  - **Large/huge files** already disable highlighting + minimap (≥5 MB) and go read-only with a capped load (≥50 MB); preserve those guards. There's also an **intermediate large-source tier** (`EditorBuffer.heavyFile` / `setHeavyFile` / `isHeavyFile`, set in `MainController.loadInto` when a sub-5 MB file's `lineCount()` ≥ `Settings.largeFileThreshold`, default 10000 lines, 0 = off): it **disables the minimap + LSP** (the two heaviest features for a very long single source) but **keeps syntax highlighting + editing**; `largeFile` implies the same minimap/LSP suppression. Per-buffer toggleable (`view.toggleLargeFileMode` → `MainController.toggleLargeFileMode`, which flips `setHeavyFile` then `syncBufferLsp`); threshold via `editor.setLargeFileThreshold` + Settings → Editor → Performance. Bound memory (undo history is capped; loads are capped). **Undo granularity:** `boundedUndoManager` builds the RichTextFX manager with `UndoMerge.PAUSE` as the `preventMergeDelay` (idle break) and a `plainTextChanges` subscriber calls `UndoManager.preventMerge()` at word/whitespace/newline boundaries (pure `editor/UndoMerge.breakAfter`), so one `C-z` undoes a word/line instead of the whole contiguous burst RichTextFX would otherwise merge; split views share the document so both managers are broken together. **Undo History tool window** (`ui/UndoHistoryPanel`, id `undoHistory`, `Side.RIGHT`, `tool.undoHistory`/`M-g u`, buffer-gated; **registered default-hidden** via `register(tw, false)` — the stripe button is off until the user enables it via Settings → Tool Windows or `tool.undoHistory`, since the `undoHistory.jump` popup is the primary entry point): `editor/UndoHistory` keeps a capped (50) in-session list of full-document checkpoints captured on the `UndoMerge.PAUSE` debounce (`EditorBuffer.captureUndoCheckpoint`, skipped for huge/>1 MB files); the panel lists them newest-first (time + caret-line preview) and double-click/Enter calls `EditorBuffer.restoreUndoCheckpoint` (an undoable `replaceText`). A **popup alternative** — command `undoHistory.jump` (`M-g v`; `MainController.undoHistoryPalette`, a `QuickOpen<UndoHistory.Checkpoint>` over the active buffer's `entriesNewestFirst()`, seeding a baseline when empty like the panel) — opens the same checkpoints as a filterable in-scene overlay (label = caret-line preview, detail = `HH:mm:ss`); Enter restores. Session-only, finer-grained than save-based Local History; pure bits (`UndoHistory.add`/`lineAt`/`clamp`) unit-tested.
  - **Bound retained GPU textures.** JavaFX's Prism texture pool has a fixed ceiling (default 512 MB); exhausting it makes the render thread NPE (null `RTTexture`/mask texture) → a black window — seen only in the packaged build. So don't let GPU-backed resources grow with the number of open files: a background (non-selected) tab's buffer drops its minimap snapshot via `EditorBuffer.setRenderingActive(false)` (driven from the tab-selection + tabs-added listeners; `Minimap.setRenderingActive` nulls the cached snapshot and stops rendering, regenerating on show), and the `PreviewImageLoader`/`MermaidImages` image caches are **LRU-bounded** (not unbounded `ConcurrentHashMap`s) since each holds an `Image` (a pinned texture). The `dist` jpackage app (and `mvn javafx:run`) also raise the caps as a safety net (`-Dprism.maxvram=2G -Dprism.maxTextureSize=16384`). When adding any per-buffer Canvas/Image, make sure it's released or bounded.
  - **Packaged-runtime JVM tuning (footprint + install size).** The `dist` jpackage `<javaOptions>` (mirrored into the `javafx:run` options so dev == prod) cap the heap and GC: **`-Xmx2g`** (without it, jpackage inherits the default ergonomic max heap ≈ ¼ of physical RAM — multi-GB on a high-RAM box — which lets GC-driven RSS balloon; 2g is predictable across the release matrix and safe for a 50 MB huge-file load + capped undo) and **`-XX:+UseSerialGC`** (a mostly-idle single-user editor on a small heap gets sub-ms pauses with no parallel GC-thread overhead — lower idle RSS than the default G1; if large-file GC *hitching* ever shows up, generational ZGC is the smoothness-over-footprint alternative). The jpackage `<jLinkOptions>` strip the bundled runtime (`--strip-debug --no-man-pages --no-header-files --compress=zip-6`) → smaller DMG/MSI/DEB + less mapped footprint. (`--strip-native-commands` is deliberately *omitted* from jLinkOptions — `bin/java` must survive the jlink step for the AOT training run below; the `aot_build` helper deletes `bin/` itself afterward, reclaiming the same footprint. The runtime's `bin/` is never used at launch — the jpackage native launcher starts the JVM via `libjli`, and every external tool (java/python/node/git/LSP/DAP) is resolved via the augmented PATH. **WINDOWS EXCEPTION (`aot_build.java` strips `bin/` non-Windows-only):** the Windows JDK layout puts the JVM *inside* `bin/` (`runtime\bin\server\jvm.dll` + the bootstrap `jli.dll`/`java.dll`/`jvm.cfg`/…), and `Editora.exe` loads `jvm.dll` from there — so deleting `bin/` on Windows makes the launcher die with *"Failed to find JVM in …\runtime directory"* (a shipped regression fixed by guarding the strip to non-Windows). On Windows the whole `bin/` is kept — its launcher exes are a negligible footprint.) **AOT cache (JDK 25 Leyden) — implemented, ~28%/≈300–480 ms faster cold start** (measured macOS: first-frame ~1060 ms → ~760 ms; delivered-app wall delta ~480 ms): the build does a **two-phase jpackage** — phase 1 (`prepare`) jlinks an `APP_IMAGE` into `target/aot-image` with `-XX:AOTCache=$APPDIR/editora.aot` baked into the launcher `.cfg`; then `scripts/aot_build.java` (run by `exec-maven-plugin` with the build JDK) **trains a full-GUI cache against the image's own runtime** (so archived classes match the shipped runtime, path-independently — it maps after the install-dir move because the classes live in the jlinked `lib/modules`, keyed to the runtime image not absolute paths), writes `editora.aot` into `$APPDIR`, strips `bin/`, then either copies the image (APP_IMAGE builds) or wraps it into the installer via `jpackage --app-image` (DMG/MSI/DEB). **A *headless* trainer gives ≈0 win** — the gain is JavaFX scene/control/CSS class loading, which only loads when a window renders; the training run is the real GUI driven by `-Deditora.aotTrainExit` (`WindowManager` renders the first frame, settles ~2.5 s for highlight-class coverage, then `System.exit`). On Linux the helper auto-wraps training in `xvfb-run` (release.yml installs `xvfb`+GTK/GL libs on the Linux legs); macOS/Windows runners use their session. **The trainer pins `-Dprism.order=es2,sw` (#399)** — the one launcher option it deliberately does *not* mirror. Training must not depend on the host having a **real GPU**: CI runners present virtualized ones, and once JavaFX 26 made **Metal** the macOS default, the macOS **arm64** runner's paravirtual GPU aborted the trainer outright — `-[AppleParavirtDevice newArgumentEncoderWithLayout:]: unrecognized selector`, an Obj-C `NSException`, i.e. an `abort()` that Prism's own `mtl→es2→sw` fallback chain cannot catch (a *pipeline* fallback can't rescue a process-level abort). **That shipped macOS arm64 uncached from v0.9.1 through v0.9.8** — every tagged release — while x64 (a different virtual GPU) trained fine every time; it never reproduced on real Apple silicon, which has a proper Metal device, which is exactly why device-testing missed it. *(Both premises in the original bug report were wrong: it was never "both macOS legs", and never a v0.9.4 regression — check the per-leg `[aot]` lines in the release logs before believing a summary.)* The trade: the cache then archives es2's pipeline classes rather than Metal's, but the bulk of the win (scene graph, controls, CSS, editor, highlighting) is pipeline-independent, an archived class the runtime doesn't use is dead weight rather than a correctness problem, and anything not archived just loads normally. *(The "a headless trainer gives ≈0 win" note above predates JavaFX 26's built-in Headless Glass platform, under which a scene genuinely renders into a buffer — worth re-measuring as a more portable trainer that would also drop the `xvfb-run` dependency.)* **Failure-tolerant, but no longer silent:** the build still continues and ships uncached (a missing/invalid `-XX:AOTCache` logs to stderr and starts normally under `AOTMode=auto`), but `aot_build.java` now reports the trainer's **exit code** (previously discarded, so a crashing trainer was indistinguishable from a clean run and the only symptom was the absent file), writes a per-target row into `$GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY`, and raises a GitHub **`::error` annotation** naming the target (`EDITORA_TARGET`, set from the release matrix) — a missing cache is a silent ~28% cold-start regression that nothing downstream notices. **`EDITORA_REQUIRE_AOT=1`** upgrades that to a hard build failure; release.yml wires it at `'0'` with a comment to flip it once a green tag confirms all five targets train. **Cost: the cache is ~60 MB**, so the installed image grows accordingly (the DMG/MSI/DEB compress it — the DMG download stayed ~81 MB). **Prism pipeline order is per-OS** (the `${prism.pipeline}` property set in the `os-mac`/`os-windows`/`os-linux` profiles, passed as `-Dprism.order=${prism.pipeline}` to both the dist `<javaOptions>` and `javafx:run` `<options>`): **macOS = `mtl,es2,sw`** — the **Metal** pipeline, added in **JavaFX 26**, which fixes the blank/garbled render-to-texture glitches the deprecated es2/OpenGL backend produced on Apple silicon (e.g. M-series: empty breadcrumb crumbs + tool-stripe icons); es2/sw stay as fallbacks since Metal is opt-in. **Windows = `d3d,es2,sw`** (must keep Direct3D — a blanket `mtl,es2,sw` would strip d3d and lose Windows GPU accel). **Linux = `es2,sw`**. JavaFX 26 runs on JDK 24+, so the JDK stays **25**. Still a **commented-out opt-in** in the pom (DEVICE-TEST before enabling, touches correctness): JDK 25 **compact object headers** (`-XX:+UseCompactObjectHeaders`, experimental, ~10–20% live-heap cut — note it changes the AOT cache's recorded layout, so retrain after enabling). *(Aside: `App.main` exits `--version`/`--help` via `System.exit(0)`, not a bare return — launching this `Application` subclass in module mode pre-starts the FX toolkit, whose non-daemon keep-alive thread would otherwise hang the process after `main` returns.)*
  - **Assess and report the performance cost of every change.** For any implementation or bug fix, evaluate its cost on the hot paths (allocation per keystroke/scroll, added FX-thread work, extra layout/CSS passes, memory) and tell the user about it — even if it's "negligible." If a change risks a regression, measure rather than guess — **for startup there is a permanent harness: `perf/Startup` + `scripts/measure-startup.sh`** (below).
  - **Startup timing — `com.editora.perf.Startup`.** Phase marks from launch to the **first rendered frame carrying the file's content** (`main` → `fx-start` → `config-loaded` → `fxml-loaded` → `controller-init` → `window-built` → `window-shown` → `file-loaded` → `first-paint`). **Off unless `EDITORA_PERF=1` / `-Deditora.perf`**, and when off every `mark()` is one static boolean test, so it ships inert; `EDITORA_PERF_EXIT=1` halts at first paint for a repeatable loop. Run it with **`scripts/measure-startup.sh -n 5 -c <configDir> <launcher> [args…] <file>`**, which reports the **median** (run 1 is always cold — page cache, GPU init — so a mean lies). **Two traps this harness exists to avoid, both of which produced confident nonsense first time:** (a) the timing **origin** — `ProcessHandle.startInstant()` is derived from boot time on Linux and drifted ~500 ms *early*, reporting a first paint **later than the process had existed**; the script now stamps `EDITORA_PERF_T0` (epoch millis) immediately before exec and `Startup` prefers it, labelling the output APPROXIMATE when it falls back. **Always sanity-check a reported number against externally measured wall-clock** — reported must be *below* wall. (b) `first-paint` is marked on the **second** `AnimationTimer` tick after the content load, because a tick fires at the *start* of a pulse: the second one proves the pulse that laid out and painted the content completed (≈1 frame of resolution). The mark is taken on the **first** loaded buffer and deliberately **not** gated on `buffer == activeBuffer()` — on the fresh-open path `loadInto` runs *before* the tab is added, so that guard silently never fired and the run never reported at all. **Measured baseline (Linux, packaged `.deb`, `--expert --single-window --no-session`, a 185-line file): ≈1.37 s to first paint** — 28% pre-`main` (launcher + JVM boot), 8% config, 16% FXML + `controller.init`, and **39% in the final load→paint segment** (FX layout/CSS/text render; the window is on screen ~570 ms before it shows content). **A/B results worth not re-deriving: the AOT cache is worth ~830 ms (38%) — 1.38 s with vs 2.22 s without, and almost all of that saving is class loading *after* `main`, so the 70 MB mapping is nearly free; the typst preview costs only ~70 ms and LSP startup only ~37 ms** (already off the critical path via the `lsp-start` pool) — so neither is the place to optimise, despite both being the intuitive suspects.
- **Code style — Palantir Java Format, enforced by Spotless.** All Java is auto-formatted with [Palantir Java Format](https://github.com/palantir/palantir-java-format) (a lambda-friendly, 120-col fork of google-java-format) via the `spotless-maven-plugin` (config in `pom.xml`; versions in the `${spotless.version}`/`${palantir.version}` properties). **Run `mvn spotless:apply` before committing** — `mvn spotless:check` is bound to the `verify` phase, so `mvn verify`/`mvn package`/CI fail on unformatted code (the `mvn javafx:run`/`mvn compile` dev loop is deliberately left untouched). Pipeline: `removeUnusedImports` → `palantirJavaFormat` → `importOrder` → `toggleOffOn`. **Import groups** (blank-line separated; longest-prefix wins, so `javafx` is *not* swallowed by `java`): JDK (`java`/`javax`) → `javafx` → everything else (third-party + `com.editora`) → static imports last. Escape hatch for hand-aligned code: wrap it in `// spotless:off` … `// spotless:on`. Palantir 2.72.0+ supports JDK 25. The two tree-wide mechanical reformats are recorded in `.git-blame-ignore-revs` (enable locally once with `git config blame.ignoreRevsFile .git-blame-ignore-revs`; GitHub honors it automatically) so `git blame` skips them.
- **Code size — soft limits, not hard gates.** Keep classes and methods small enough to hold in your head; these are review heuristics, not a build check. **Per class (target):** ≤ ~500 lines is ideal, ≤ ~1000 is fine; **~1000–1500** is acceptable only for a *genuinely cohesive subsystem* (e.g. `editor/EditorBuffer`, which coordinates one buffer's many overlays/managers — treat it gently); **> ~2000 lines is a refactor smell** — split it. **Per method (target):** ≤ ~50 lines ideal, **> ~100 is a smell** (extract helpers / a pure decision function). What actually matters is **responsibility count** and **cyclomatic complexity**, not raw line count — a 600-line class doing one thing is healthier than a 300-line class doing five. When a class creeps over the line, the first move is to extract the *pure* logic (a decision/format/parse helper in its own class, unit-tested) and, for a whole feature, a **`CoordinatorHost`-style coordinator** (see the `ui/*Coordinator` classes). **`ui/MainController` is the known outlier** (~12k lines) and is being incrementally decomposed one feature at a time into `ui/*Coordinator` classes (External Tools, Macros, TODO, Search, Run done; Notes, Bookmarks, LSP, Debug pending) — so **a new feature should be its own coordinator (or pure package), never bolted onto `MainController`**. No tooling enforces these numbers (JaCoCo gates *coverage*, not size); they're for human judgement during review and when deciding where new code lives.
- **Palette gating lives in `ui/Chrome`, and has two independent dimensions.** A command the palette can't run is **listed but grayed out and inert** (skipped by the selection cursor, ignored by Enter/click) rather than hidden, so the user still sees it exists and what its keybinding is (#532). `Chrome.paletteEnabled(id, gates, context)` ANDs the two halves, both pure + unit-tested in `ChromeTest`: **(a) `PaletteGates`** — the feature is switched off; driven by the `FEATURE_RULES` table (an `enabled` predicate + an id prefix + any exact `tool.*` ids), so **adding a feature is one record component + one table row**, not another `if`. **(b) `PaletteContext`** — the feature is on but there is nothing to act on right now (no buffer, wrong file type, no repo, no suspended debug session); these commands would no-op with a status message if run. `MainController.paletteGates()`/`paletteContext()` snapshot the live state, and the palette takes that snapshot **once per refresh, not once per command** (`CommandPalette`'s ctor takes a `Supplier<Predicate<Command>>`) — the predicate runs over the whole ~550-command registry on every keystroke in the query field, and the context half reads the active buffer, whose `hasPreview()` sniffs buffer text. Two invariants: a feature's **master enable toggle must not match its own gate** (they live under the never-gated `view.`/`appearance.` prefixes, or turning a feature off would gray out the command that turns it back on — `ChromeTest.masterEnableTogglesAreNeverGated` guards this), and the context rules stay **conservative** — graying a command that would in fact have worked is a worse regression than leaving one lit, so only families where *every* member needs the same context are listed (`git.clone` is the explicit carve-out from the in-a-repo rule). `PaletteContextFxTest` guards the wiring end-to-end in both directions. **A grayed row explains itself on hover**: `Chrome.disabledReason(id, gates, context)` returns a `DisabledReason{messageKey, commandArg}` — i18n **keys**, not text, so `Chrome` stays catalog-free — which `MainController.disabledCommandReason` resolves, filling `{0}` with the *localized title* of the command that would re-enable the feature (so the tooltip names something the user can type into that same palette). `paletteVisible`/`contextEnabled` are **derived from** `featureReason`/`contextReason`, so a command can never be grayed for a reason the tooltip can't state. Two subtleties: the feature reason **outranks** the context reason (telling someone to open a Markdown file when Markdown-lint is off sends them nowhere), and a feature that **Simple UI mode** forces off (`FeatureRule.simpleSuppressed`, declared via `simpleRule(...)` — git/github/lsp/http/localHistory/mcp/plugins/externalTools/log/testRunner/debug/ai/agent) points at `view.toggleSimpleMode` while Simple mode is on, since its own toggle would be a dead end.
- **Adding a feature = add a `Command`, and surface it in the command palette.** Every time we add a command or an applicable user-facing feature, it must be discoverable in the palette. Register it in `MainController.registerCommands()` and, if it needs a key, add a binding to `emacs.json`. The palette is populated from `CommandRegistry.all()`, so a properly registered command appears automatically — never add a user-facing action that bypasses the registry. Toolbar buttons and the palette both dispatch through commands; don't wire UI handlers to logic directly when a command fits.
- **Every setting also needs a palette command** — Editora is command-driven, so a Settings-window control (toggle, picker, font, path, number, …) is **not** enough on its own; it must have a command-palette equivalent too. Register a command in `MainController.registerCommands()` that flips/prompts the **same** `Settings` field, persists (`requestSave()`), re-applies the feature (`applyGitSupport`/`applyLspSupport`/`applyViewSettingsToAllBuffers`/…), and keeps an open Settings window in step via `SettingsWindow.syncAll()`. Toggles → `view.toggle*` (master feature-enable toggles use a `view.`/`appearance.`/`debug.` prefix so the palette's feature-gating filter never hides them); values → a `promptText` prompt or a `QuickOpen` picker; many per-item settings (e.g. the per-server LSP / per-adapter Debug commands) → one grouped picker command. Reuse the generic helpers `toggleSetting`/`promptStringSetting`/`promptIntSetting`/`chooseSetting`, and add `command.<id>` + `command.<id>.desc` to all six i18n catalogs (the two shared status keys `status.settingToggled`/`status.settingChanged` reuse the command's own title). The 2026-06 sweep (PR #56) closed every gap — keep parity when adding a setting.
- **Every user-facing string is localized — never hardcode UI text.** Any new label, status/echo message, tooltip, dialog title/header/body, button, menu item, prompt, or placeholder must go through the i18n catalog: `import static com.editora.i18n.Messages.tr;` then `tr("some.key")` (or `tr("key", args…)` for `MessageFormat` parameters like `Saved {0}`) — never pass a raw English literal to a JavaFX control. **Add the key to all six `resources/com/editora/i18n/messages[_<lang>].properties` files** (English base + `it/es/fr/pt/de`) with a real translation in each; `MessagesTest`'s key-parity check fails the build if any locale is missing a key. New `Command`s get their title for free via `Command.of(id, runnable)` + a `command.<id>` key. Only deliberate exceptions stay literal: technical tokens (`UTF-8`, `LF`/`CRLF`, `Ln`/`Col`, git verbs in `gitlabel.*`, detected language names, example URLs) and the pre-GUI `--help`/`--version` text. See the `i18n/` architecture bullet for the full system.
- **App icon / branding:** the source logo is `branding/editora-icon.svg`. Window-icon PNGs (16–512) live in `resources/com/editora/icons/` (loaded into `stage.getIcons()` in `App`; also the About-dialog logo). Native-installer icons `branding/editora.{icns,ico,png}` are generated from the SVG (rsvg-convert + iconutil + a small ICO writer) and passed to jpackage via `${jpackage.icon}`, set per-OS in the OS-activated profiles. Regenerate after editing the SVG.
- **Context-menu icons:** **every right-click `MenuItem` carries a leading icon** (`MenuItem.setGraphic(...)`).
